# Product Spine - Implementation Map

> **Implementation reference** for the idea-layer docs:
> [`relix-company-model.md`](relix-company-model.md),
> [`relix-execution-and-issue-design.md`](relix-execution-and-issue-design.md),
> [`relix-dashboard-design.md`](relix-dashboard-design.md),
> [`relix-agent-adapters.md`](relix-agent-adapters.md),
> [`relix-hermes-integration.md`](relix-hermes-integration.md), and
> [`relix-lexicon.md`](relix-lexicon.md). This maps the lexicon to the
> shipped code: modules, mesh capabilities, and known divergences.

## Modules

| Module | What |
|---|---|
| `coordinator/agent/store.rs` | Operatives: `reports_to` (Lead), `rig`, `monthly_allowance_cents`, runtime Keys, and the org/work Keys (`can_spawn_agents`, `spawn_route`, `can_assign_work`, `assign_scope`, `assign_allowed_agents`, `can_manage_work`, `manage_scope`, `manage_allowed_agents`, `can_configure_agents`, `configure_scope`, `configure_allowed_agents`, `secret_allowlist`, `instruction_bundle`); org-tree queries, status counts, the hire flow, and the typed spawn Clearance (`create_spawn_clearance`, `SPAWN_CLEARANCE_METHOD`). **GROUP 6 tenant isolation:** every product agent-id/approval-id read+write has a `*_for_tenant` variant (`get_agent_for_tenant`, `update_agent_field_for_tenant`, `soft_delete_for_tenant`, `list_direct_reports/peers/by_role_for_tenant`, `manager_subtree/chain_of_command/manages_for_tenant`, `committed_allowance_cents_for_tenant`, `list_pending_approvals_for_tenant`, `get_approval_record_for_tenant`). The unscoped methods remain as internal/gate helpers. |
| `coordinator/agent/keys.rs` | Pure, I/O-free Keys policy: `spawn_verdict` / `assign_verdict` → three-valued `KeyVerdict` (Allow / Clearance / Deny). Unknown scope/route values normalise to the safest option so a garbage value can never widen authority. Exhaustively unit-tested. |
| `coordinator/agent/handlers.rs` | Agent capability handlers + the actor-aware enforcement helpers (`caller_is_operator`, `enforce_spawn_key` → `SpawnGate`, `finalize_spawn`, `enforce_assign_key`), `agent.assign_check`, and the Prime flow `mandate.team_plan` / `compute_readiness` (shared by `mandate.team_readiness`) / `mandate.orchestrate` (+ `orchestration.latest` / `.list`). Operator/admin (Founder/Board) bypasses; an agent actor is gated by its Keys. Product routes pass `ctx.tenant_id_or_default()` to the tenant-scoped store. `coord.approval.decide` has a spawn-Clearance hop that activates/disables the linked pending hire. |
| `coordinator/spine/` | Mandates, Campaigns, Guilds, Allowance, the strategy gate, **persisted Mandate Team Plans** (`mandate_team_plans` + `TeamPlan`/`TeamPlanRecord`, `record_team_plan` / `latest_team_plan`), and **persisted Orchestration runs** (`mandate_orchestration_runs` + `OrchestrationRun`/`OrchestrationRunRecord`, `record_orchestration_run` / `latest_orchestration_run` / `list_orchestration_runs`; the run row records `created_brief_ids` / `existing_brief_ids` (reused) / `assigned_brief_ids` / `skipped` / `source_markers` / `blockers` / `input_signature` — additive columns, safe on existing SQLite DBs). Tenant-scoped store plus `mandate.*`, `campaign.*`, and `guild.*` handlers. The Brief store (`coordinator/mod.rs` `TaskStore`) gains the `tasks.source_kind`/`source_marker` columns + index and the `set_brief_source_marker` / `get_brief_by_source_marker` / `list_briefs_by_source_kind` / `create_brief_with_marker` lookups that back marker-based orchestration idempotency, plus a row-level `tasks.tenant_id` (Guild) column + index stamped on Brief creation (`set_task_tenant`) and `*_for_tenant` read variants (`list_briefs_by_board_for_tenant`, `board_summary_for_tenant`, `list_unassigned_briefs_for_tenant`, `list_overdue_briefs_for_tenant`, `list_blocked_briefs_for_tenant`, `list_stale_briefs_for_tenant`, `search_briefs_for_tenant`, `list_briefs_by_label_for_tenant`, `brief_detail_for_tenant`/`task_in_tenant`) that isolate the board/inbox/detail/search/label reads per Guild (`COALESCE(tenant_id,'default')`; legacy NULL rows resolve to the `default` Guild). A `deny_cross_tenant` handler guard reuses `task_in_tenant` to refuse **every** exposed Brief mutation / read on a row outside the caller's Guild (returns the same not-found a missing Brief would); the reverse-edge reads add tenant-scoped store variants (`list_blocking_for_tenant` / `parent_briefs_for_tenant`) so related ids never leak across Guilds; and `create_brief` makes the tenant stamp required (rolls back the row on stamp failure). |
| `coordinator/brief.rs` | Brief board vocabulary, priorities, reviewer field, and the `BriefCard`, `Dossier`, and `BriefFields` types. |
| `coordinator/mod.rs` (`TaskStore`) | Brief ledger: board moves with guarded side effects, two-pointer Claim fields (`checkout_run_id`, `execution_run_id`, holder, locked-at), lease/heartbeat/release, persistent Brief wakeup queue (`queued`, `running`, `coalesced`, `deferred`, `skipped`, terminal rows), Sub-briefs, Snags, Dossiers, spine fields, board/ready/blocked/stale queries, progress rollups, link listings, and Chronicle events. **Supervisory auto-wake at the transition seam (execution §1.6/§3.1):** `set_board_status` — the single board-transition choke point every done/cancel path flows through (manual `brief.move`, the apply-driven `complete_reviewed_brief`, board recovery) — now promotes first-class follow-up wakes when a Brief reaches a terminal column, event-driven (no busy-poll): `promote_blockers_resolved` (on `done`) offers every same-Guild dependent that was `blocked_on` it a wakeup, and `promote_children_completed` (on `done` OR `cancelled`) offers a same-Guild parent a wakeup once ALL of its same-Guild Sub-briefs are terminal (`done`/`cancelled`). Both route through the shared `request_brief_wakeup` enqueue (source `automation`, stable reasons `blockers-resolved` / `children-completed`), so the existing readiness/claim guards apply: a dependent still waiting on another unfinished blocker is `skipped` (not woken yet), a Brief being run coalesces/defers, and a repeated terminal transition coalesces into the live/queued wake (no duplicate run). Tenant-safe by construction (only same-Guild dependents/parents enumerated via the `*_for_tenant` reverse-edge reads + a same-Guild Sub-brief terminal count — a cross-Guild edge can neither wake nor leak another Guild's Brief). An unassigned dependent/parent invents no one to wake — it records an honest `brief.wakeup_skipped` Chronicle note (`automation:<reason>: assignee required`). |
| `coordinator/heartbeat.rs` | Dispatch loop: timer wakes ready Briefs through the persistent wakeup queue, lazily claims queued wakeups with per-Operative concurrency caps, honors timer-wake disablement, runs on Rig, advances board, parks failures, marks wakeup terminal, promotes deferred wakeups, and mints/revokes bridge-back tokens per Shift. |
| `rig/` | Universal agent-backend contract (`Rig` trait), registry, `EchoRig`, `ProcessRig`, CLI Rigs, probe/install hints, structured-output flag, bridge-back support flag, billing metadata, and per-method bridge-back token store. Hermes is currently a stdio `BoxLevel` placeholder, not the real rich Tether. |
| `macros/` | Native Macro / execute-code core: capped execution, interpreter allowlist, split `@relix-call` tool requests, scoped `cwd` and env. |
| `tradecraft/` | Keeper scaffolding: usage-clock Knack aging, provenance gate, creation trigger, post-response nudge. |
| `bench/` | Bench scaffolding: sleep/wake workspace lifecycle and idle hibernation tick. |
| `src/controller_runtime.rs` | Wiring: spine handlers, shared Rig registry, `rig.list`/`rig.describe`, `RELIX_DEFAULT_RIG`, optional live heartbeat loop, prompt composition, failure parking, and bridge-token sweep. |
| `relix-cli` `call.rs` | `relix call --method <name> --arg <pipe-delimited>`: generic operator escape hatch for the spine capability surface. |
| `relix-web-bridge` `spine.rs` | Dashboard HTTP proxy for `/v1/spine/*`, including board reads, Brief create/move/comment/due/pin/set, Mandates, Roster, Desk, search, overdue, Guild detail, and Allowance committed reads. Also exposes composite read payloads that fan out to existing capabilities only: `/v1/spine/inbox` (blocked + stale + overdue + in-review + unassigned in one bounded response), `/v1/spine/unassigned`, `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/events` (a Brief Chronicle as an array), `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/thread` (detail + Chronicle + wakeups + claim holder), `/v1/spine/keys/:agent` (the full Operative profile for the Keys panel), `/v1/spine/assign_check` (assign-Key preview), `/v1/spine/clearances` (pending Clearances parsed from `coord.approval.pending`'s TSV into TYPED objects — the runtime now appends `subject_id` / `capability_category` / `expires_at` / `task_id` after the historical 5-column prefix, append-only and back-compatible, so the Approvals hub renders a per-type payload summary without a second per-row fetch; nothing fabricated), `POST /v1/spine/clearances/:id/decide` (inline approve/reject, forwarded to `coord.approval.decide` as the bridge identity — the runtime cap still enforces the real authorisation; no per-decision TTL knob), `POST /v1/spine/mandates/:id/team_plan` (Prime team-build) + `GET` (the latest persisted plan), `GET /v1/spine/mandates/:id/team_readiness` (live team readiness), `POST /v1/spine/mandates/:id/orchestrate` (Prime Mandate-to-Brief orchestration), and `GET /v1/spine/mandates/:id/orchestration/latest` (the latest persisted run). |
| `relix-web-bridge` `bridge_back.rs` | Narrow public bridge-back API for scoped Rig tokens: comment, Sub-brief, Dossier add, Snag set, Clearance request, and claim-holder lookup. Every route validates `Authorization: Bearer brt_*` through `bridge_back.authorize` before forwarding. |
| `relix-web-bridge` `spine_dashboard.html` | Interim `/spine` company console: self-contained HTML/CSS/JS, left rail, Issues board/list, a real Desk/Inbox (sectioned Blocked/Stale/Overdue/In-review/Unassigned from `/v1/spine/inbox`), a Brief live work thread (claim holder, status/priority/assignee/reviewer editors, runs, Blockers, Sub-issues, Chronicle timeline, comment) from `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/thread`, an Operative Desk (their active Briefs + allowance/Rig summary) from `/v1/spine/desk/:agent`, a per-Operative **Keys panel** split into "enforced" (spawn + assign Keys) and "stored only" (manage/configure/secrets/charter), pending **Clearances** on the Desk (read-only, with an honest "decide via CLI" note), companion chat, Mandate hierarchy/drilldown, Org/Roster, live Allowance summary, and live Chronicle Activity tail. It follows the Paperclip-like work-object IA but is not the final React SPA from `relix-dashboard-design.md`. |
| `relix-web-bridge` `agent.rs` | Roster HTTP API for listing, reading, and patching Operatives, including the runtime Keys and the org/work Keys (`can_spawn_agents`, `spawn_route`, `can_assign_work`, `assign_scope`, `assign_allowed_agents`, `can_manage_work`, `manage_scope`, `manage_allowed_agents`, `can_configure_agents`, `configure_scope`, `configure_allowed_agents`, `secret_allowlist`, `instruction_bundle`) surfaced to / edited from the dashboard. |
| `relix-web-bridge` `companion.rs` | **Company-aware** action spine behind `POST /v1/spine/companion` (`relix-dashboard-design.md` §13). It creates/moves/searches Briefs and Mandates **and** reads live company state — `what needs attention` → `company.actions` (ranked next actions), `what is blocked` → `brief.blocked_list`, `what is running` → `brief.runs` (active Shifts), `who is on the crew` → `agent.operatives` (roster) — summarizing each in plain language (top-3 titles / counts) while keeping the raw capability JSON in `result`. It can also open a **governed plan package** from one line (`plan package <brief_id>: <body> => child: <t>; child high: <t>`) via `brief.plan_package_open`, refusing an empty body or zero children and **never** bypassing the approval-bound confirm (priorities only; no assignee hints). The deterministic parser + reply summarizers are pure, total functions with exhaustive unit tests. **An opt-in `mode:"ai"` now adds guarded model-assisted *action selection*** (see the dedicated note below): the model chooses ONE strict-JSON action from a fixed allowlist, the bridge validates it into the existing `CompanionAction` and runs the SAME governed handler, falling back to the deterministic parser (honest `ai_mode`) on any failure. **Still one turn → one validated action; not an autonomous planner.** |

## Capabilities

**Guild** - `guild.get`, `guild.counts`, `guild.set`, `guild.set_allowance`, `guild.set_billing_code` (object-level billing code, company-model §6.6 — mirrors `guild.set_allowance`; empty clears)

**Mandate** - `mandate.create/get/list/update` (`update` now accepts a `billing_code` field — object-level cost attribution, company-model §6.6), `mandate.children`, `mandate.tree`, `mandate.search`, `mandate.progress`, `mandate.briefs`, `mandate.propose_strategy/approve_strategy/reject_strategy/strategy`, `mandate.team_plan` (Prime team-build foundation: strategy + spawn-Key gated; **persists** the plan + mints identified hires with spawn Clearances), `mandate.team_plan.latest` (the newest persisted plan), `mandate.team_readiness` (live readiness combining the plan with current hire/Clearance states), `mandate.orchestrate` (Prime Mandate-to-Brief orchestration), `mandate.orchestration.latest`, `mandate.orchestration.list`

**Campaign** - `campaign.create/get/list/update` (`update` now accepts a `billing_code` field — object-level cost attribution, company-model §6.6), `campaign.search`, `campaign.progress`, `campaign.briefs`

**Brief** - `brief.create`, `brief.move`, `brief.set`, `brief.fields`, `brief.detail`, `brief.search`, `brief.set_labels`, `brief.labels`, `brief.by_label`, `brief.pin`, `brief.set_due`, `brief.due`, `brief.overdue`, `brief.board`, `brief.board_summary`, `brief.desk`, `brief.workload`, `brief.team_workload`, `brief.subbrief_progress`, `brief.comment`, `brief.ready`, `brief.children_done`, `brief.blocked`, `brief.blocked_list`, `brief.stale_list`, `brief.subbrief`, `brief.unsubbrief`, `brief.subbriefs`, `brief.parents`, `brief.snag`, `brief.unsnag`, `brief.snags`, `brief.blocking`, `brief.dossier_add`, `brief.dossier_author` (§1.8 issue-document authoring with optimistic locking / fork), `brief.dossier_lock` / `brief.dossier_unlock` / `brief.dossier_locks` (§1.8 document locking — owner-or-nobody lock/unlock + active-lock list), `brief.dossiers`, `brief.dossier_get`, `brief.dossier_latest`, `brief.interaction_create` (§1.9 idempotency-aware ask/confirm create), `brief.interaction_cancel` (§1.9 close a card without answering), `brief.wakeup`, `brief.wakeups`, `brief.claim`, `brief.heartbeat`, `brief.release`, `brief.claim_holder`, `brief.cost_rollup`

**Cost rollup / billing attribution (company-model §6.6)** - `brief.cost_rollup` → `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/cost?since=&until=` returns the cost of a Brief **and its entire same-Guild Sub-brief tree**, summed from the durable `brief_runs` ledger (real `cost_micros`, never UI data): tree `run_count` / `cost_micros` / `brief_count`, the own-vs-descendant split, and a per-`billing_code` breakdown. **Tenant-safe by construction** — the recursive `spawned`-edge descent only enters same-Guild Briefs (a cross-Guild edge + its subtree is dropped; a cross-Guild caller reads not-found). The window defaults to the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window` (current UTC calendar month, ms→secs), overridable with explicit unix-second `since`/`until`; pre-run `refused` rows are excluded. **Billing code** is an additive `tasks.billing_code` column (set via `brief.set <id>|billing_code|<code>`, surfaced on `BriefFields`) PLUS additive `billing_code` columns on **Mandate, Campaign, and Guild** (set via `mandate.update`/`campaign.update <id>|billing_code|<code>` and `guild.set_billing_code <code>`; surfaced on the Mandate/Campaign/Guild reads), and an additive `brief_runs.billing_code` **stamped at run start** (`prepare_claimed_run`, shared by manual + autonomous). The stamp resolves the **effective** code with full precedence: **Brief own → nearest same-Guild ancestor Sub-brief → linked Campaign → linked Mandate → Guild** — durable point-in-time attribution (a later change to ANY object's code never rewrites a past run's bill). The object-level steps (Campaign/Mandate/Guild) resolve through a tenant-safe `ObjectBillingResolver` (implemented by the spine `SpineStore`, injected into the `TaskStore` once at boot in `controller_runtime`): `effective_billing_code` walks the Brief tree, then consults the resolver with the Brief's OWN Guild + its `mandate_id`/`campaign_id` links — so a Brief in one Guild can never inherit another Guild's object code, even with a bad/cross-Guild link (the resolver only reads objects in the Brief's own Guild). Store: `brief_cost_rollup_for_tenant`, `effective_billing_code`, `brief_object_links`, `stamp_run_billing_code`, `set_object_billing_resolver` (`coordinator/mod.rs`); `SpineStore::set_guild_billing_code` + `update_mandate_field`/`update_campaign_field` `billing_code` + the `ObjectBillingResolver` impl (`coordinator/spine/store.rs`). **Frontend (now shipped, partial):** the Costs page (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Costs.tsx`) consumes this via the typed `briefCost.rollup` client — own/descendant split, tree counts, window, and the per-`billing_code` breakdown table (see the Lattice + Costs frontend slice below).

**Delegation-depth counter + guard (company-model §6.6 — BACKEND SHIPPED)** - the runaway-recursion safety backstop that complements the cost rollup. A Brief's **delegation depth** = the LONGEST same-Guild `spawned` parent chain up to a root (a root is `0`, its Sub-brief `1`, a grandchild `2`, …), computed by `brief_delegation_depth` / `delegation_depth_in_tenant` (`coordinator/mod.rs`). The central cap is `MAX_SUBBRIEF_DELEGATION_DEPTH = 1024` (named once; the doc-LOCKED "≥1024 runaway backstop, not a product limit" from relix-execution-and-issue-design.md Part 7 item 2). **Guard:** `link_subbrief` — the single choke point for **every** Sub-brief link — refuses a link whose child would land past the cap (`depth(parent)+1 > MAX`), creating no edge; an idempotent re-link of an already-existing edge skips the guard. Because `link_subbrief` backs **all three** create/link paths (direct `brief.subbrief`, the `suggest_tasks` accept materialization, and Mandate orchestration), all three are guarded. The `suggest_tasks` accept additionally **pre-checks up front** (before claiming the card or creating any child) so an over-cap accept refuses cleanly with **no partial child creation** and the card stays open. **Tenant-safe by construction:** depth is computed over same-Guild `spawned` edges only, in each Brief's OWN Guild — a cross-Guild edge can neither inflate nor reveal another Guild's depth. **Read visibility:** `brief.detail` (`BriefDetail`) now carries `delegation_depth` + `max_delegation_depth` so a UI can show how deep a cascade sits without inventing the value. *Honest gap:* Mandate orchestration links via `let _ = link_subbrief(...)` (it swallows the result), but its tree is structurally only 2 deep (parent → role track → subject Brief), so the cap can never fire there; a hypothetical over-cap orchestration link would skip silently rather than abort — a negligible gap given the fixed shallow shape. *Deferred:* the **frontend** Costs + Lattice surfaces are now shipped (see the Lattice + Costs frontend slice below), but neither yet renders `delegation_depth` — that read-visibility field is still unsurfaced in the UI.

**Operative / Roster** - `agent.create/get/list/update/delete/keys`, `agent.request_hire`, `agent.request_hire_for_mandate`, `agent.approve_hire`, `agent.reject_hire`, `agent.reports`, `agent.branch`, `agent.line`, `agent.peers`, `agent.by_role`, `agent.manages`, `agent.assign_check`, `agent.roster_summary`, `agent.allowance_committed`, hire status flow. `agent.create` is operator-only; `agent.request_hire`/`agent.request_hire_for_mandate` enforce the spawn Key for agent actors. `agent.update` edits all stored Keys (validated).

**Company / Action Center** - `company.status` (first-run + Prime/crew shape), `company.bootstrap_founder`, `agent.operatives` (Crew roster), and **`company.actions`** → `GET /v1/spine/company/actions` — the READ-ONLY Action Center (company-model §5.4/§8.2): one ordered, deduped feed of the operator's next actions (approval / hire / **budget** / failed_or_refused / needs_review / ready_to_start / blocked / stale) computed from existing live state, tenant-scoped, mutating nothing. Ordering + dedupe live in the pure `agent/action_center.rs`.

**Rig / execution** - `rig.list`, `rig.describe` (name, label, governance, bridge-back + structured-output support, billing, and a **live readiness probe** + hint); per-Operative `rig`; `dispatch_batch` runs ready Briefs on their Rig via the timer loop. **Structured CLI readiness:** `ProcessRig::probe()` returns one of six honest statuses — `available` (binary present + a noninteractive `--version` ran clean) / `missing_binary` (not on PATH) / `not_authenticated` (the probe output carries a login nudge) / `unsupported_version` (the binary rejected `--version`) / `interactive_only` (the probe hung past an 8s timeout → needs a TTY) / `probe_failed` (spawn error or other failure). `classify_readiness` is a pure function over `ReadinessSignals`, unit-tested with mocked CLI outputs; the hint is the login hint for `not_authenticated`, the install hint otherwise. **Windows-safe resolution:** `resolve_program` resolves a CLI through `PATH` + `PATHEXT` into a `Spawnable` — a `Direct` `.exe`/`.com` (spawned straight) or a `BatchShim` `.cmd`/`.bat` (run via `%SystemRoot%\System32\cmd.exe /C <shim> <args…>` with **discrete argv**, no shell string) — preferring a real `.exe`, and treating an extensionless file as non-spawnable (so an npm `claude` *sh* shim sharing the PATH dir with `claude.cmd` is skipped, not spawned into `os error 193`). `probe()` and `run()` resolve identically, so the probe can never report a binary the runner can't launch; ProcessRig `fallback_paths` add the npm real launcher (`%APPDATA%\npm\node_modules\@anthropic-ai\claude-code\bin\claude.exe`). **Claude readiness is two-step:** `claude --version` then `claude auth status --text`, so `available` means installed AND logged in, an installed-but-logged-out CLI is `not_authenticated` (hints `claude auth login`), and an auth-check hang is `interactive_only`. **Codex readiness is also two-step:** `codex --version` then `codex login status` ("Logged in using ChatGPT" → `available — …; logged in`; "Not logged in" → `not_authenticated`). Gemini keeps the `--version`-only check (auth surfaces at run). **Honest limit:** for `--version`-only adapters `available` means "binary runs noninteractively", not necessarily "logged in". **Claude run behavior:** the Claude rig spawns `claude --print --output-format stream-json --verbose` with the Brief prompt on **stdin** (noninteractive; no TTY). The CLI emits JSONL — hook/system/assistant noise then a terminal `type:"result"` event carrying the real answer, `is_error`, and `permission_denials`. `parse_claude_stream_json` (`RigOutputFormat::ClaudeStreamJson`) extracts that event off the **raw, pre-redaction** stdout (so the JSON parses), then redacts + caps only the answer: `is_error` → a clear non-retryable failure (`subtype` + text); otherwise `Done` with the model's answer, where the summary **leads with `⚠ N tool permission(s) denied`** when Claude wanted a tool it couldn't run — Relix runs Claude **noninteractively and does NOT auto-approve tool use** (no `--dangerously-skip-permissions`), so file/command actions are blocked unless Claude itself already trusts the working directory. No terminal result event → fall back to exit-code handling (never a faked success). The result event is authoritative over the exit code. **Codex run behavior:** the Codex rig spawns `codex exec --json --sandbox workspace-write --skip-git-repo-check -` with the prompt on **stdin** (noninteractive). `--json` emits JSONL (`thread.started` → `turn.started` → `item.completed`* → `turn.completed`); `parse_codex_jsonl` (`RigOutputFormat::CodexJsonl`) takes the LAST `item.completed` of `item.type=="agent_message"` as the clean answer (no raw-JSONL dump) and maps an `error`/`turn.failed`/`thread.error`/error-item event to a non-retryable failure; no terminal event → exit-code fallback. `--sandbox workspace-write` confines the model's shell-command writes to the working directory — Relix pins that to the scoped run workspace — so **real coding work happens confined to the sandbox, never the repo**; `--skip-git-repo-check` because a scoped workspace is not a git repo. **Honest Codex-on-Windows caveat:** Codex's *shell-command* sandbox can fail to spawn on Windows (`windows sandbox: spawn setup refresh`), so shell tools (e.g. `ls`) may not run, though Codex's direct file-write tool does; this surfaces honestly inside Codex's own final message (captured in the run summary), not hidden. **Scoped per-run workspace:** every run now executes inside a dedicated sandbox folder — `<workspace_root>/<run_id>` (root = `<db_parent>/workspaces/runs`, overridable via `RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_ROOT`) — NOT the coordinator/repo CWD. `preflight_run` creates it after winning the Claim (`prepare_run_workspace`: the path is derived ONLY from the validated single-segment `run_id`, never from Brief content, so a prompt can't choose it and traversal is impossible; it drops a small trusted `BRIEF.md`), pins it as the child's `working_dir`, and persists it in the run ledger (`brief_runs.workspace`, surfaced in `/v1/runs` + the dashboard). A workspace-creation failure refuses cleanly (`workspace_error`) — releases the Claim, opens NO run record, and never falls back to repo-wide execution. `RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_MODE=inherit` is the only (explicit) opt-out back to coordinator-CWD execution. **Workspace context modes** (`RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_CONTEXT`, persisted in `brief_runs.workspace_context`/`_files`/`_bytes` + surfaced in `/v1/runs` + the dashboard, read via `run.workspace_config` → `GET /v1/spine/run-config`): **`empty`** (default, safest) gives the workspace only `BRIEF.md` — no project files; **`copy_repo`** copies a **capped, filtered** snapshot of the project (`RELIX_RUN_PROJECT_ROOT`, default coordinator CWD) into the sandbox so real coding work can happen WITHOUT repo-CWD execution. `copy_repo` is hard-bounded (`RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_MAX_FILES`/`_BYTES`, defaults 2000 files / 32 MiB — **exceeding either aborts and removes the partial copy**, so the prior 150GB local-bloat class of incident can't recur), and excludes dangerous/huge/generated dirs at any depth (`.git`, `target`, `target-audit`, `node_modules`, `dev-data`, `workspaces`, `worktrees` (covers `.claude/worktrees`), `dev-keys`, build caches) + secret/key files (`.env*`, `*.key`/`*.pem`/`*.p12`/`*.pfx`/`*.aic`, `id_rsa*`, `bridge-token`, `dashboard-admin.json`, `*secret*`/`*credential*`/`*password*`), respects top-level `.gitignore` names (best-effort) on top of those, and **skips symlinks** (no escaping the root / no loops). The project root is validated (real dir, never a filesystem/drive root) and is **operator config — the Brief prompt never chooses the root or any include path**. A context/cap failure refuses `workspace_context_error` (Claim released, no run record); basic-creation failure is `workspace_error`. (`git_worktree`/`git_checkout` context is **deferred / future** — only `empty` + `copy_repo` ship now, to keep scope + disk safe.) **Why repo-CWD execution stays unsafe + explicit-only:** running in the live repo lets an agent read/modify real source + tracked secrets and (for Claude) inherits the repo's tool-trust; `copy_repo` instead operates on a throwaway, secret-free COPY, so even a permitted write only touches the sandbox. **Honest caveat:** whether a tool action is permitted is decided by **Claude's own project-trust config**, not Relix — because a fresh scoped workspace is an untrusted Claude project, file/command tool use is **denied + surfaced via the `⚠` caveat** there (proven live: a "create a note" Brief in its scoped workspace left the repo untouched and recorded the denial), whereas a dir Claude already trusts would let the tool run. **Async dispatch:** `brief.run` is split into `preflight_run` (resolve adapter, refuse clearly without spawning, win the Claim, open the run record — all fast + synchronous) and `execute_ready` (the blocking `rig.run` + board advance + Chronicle + close record). The bridge handler pre-flights inline then hands `execute_ready` to a background thread, returning immediately with `status:"running"` + the `run_id`, so a long Claude/Codex Shift never freezes the bridge; the synchronous `run_brief_now` (heartbeat + tests) still runs both halves in-line. The `RunReport` status distinguishes accepted (`running`) + real outcomes (`done`/`failed`/`continued`) from clear pre-run refusals (`not_found`/`unassigned`/`no_adapter`/`adapter_unavailable`/`already_running`). **Run ledger:** a durable `brief_runs` table (one row per Rig execution: `run_id`/`brief_id`/`agent_id`/`rig`/`status`/`started_at`/`finished_at`/`duration_secs`/`summary`) is opened on commit and closed on terminal; a pre-flight refusal records **no** row. `brief.runs` lists recent runs (empty arg) or a Brief's history (id arg). **Run transcript:** a focused, capped `run_events` table (event_id / run_id / ts / kind / source / message / payload_json / redacted) records *what happened* in a run — the lifecycle (relix source: `accepted` → `workspace_prepared` → `process_started` → `process_exited` → terminal `result`/`failed`/`continued`/`cancelled`) PLUS parsed adapter events (`claude_events`: assistant_message / tool_use / result / permission_denied / usage cost / error; `codex_events`: thread/turn lifecycle / agent_message / command / file_change / error; raw adapters: a compact `output`/`stderr` event). It is **never the raw JSONL** — every text field is secret-redacted + length-bounded, `append_run_event` enforces a per-run cap (`MAX_RUN_EVENTS=400` → one `truncated` marker then drop) and a per-field byte clamp. The `Rig` contract gains an additive `run_transcript` (default wraps `run` with no events); `ProcessRig` shares one `execute` body. **Cancellation (real):** a global `CancelRegistry` (run_id → `AtomicBool`) is registered at pre-flight; `ProcessRig`'s wait loop polls the flag (lock-free) and **kills the child** on cancel; `execute_ready` then reports the run `cancelled` (not failed). `run.cancel` flips the flag, records a `cancel_requested` event, and returns `active` truthfully (a live process was signalled vs already finished) — no fake cancellation. **ProcessRig** spawns with safe argv (no shell), a hard timeout + child-kill (timeout + cancel), streamed capture, a validated working directory, and **secret redaction** of captured output. **Reviewable run results (artifacts + review):** after a run finishes, `execute_ready` detects WHAT THE AGENT CHANGED by diffing a BEFORE manifest (captured at pre-flight) against an AFTER scan of the scoped workspace into `created`/`modified`/`deleted` rows in a `run_artifacts` table — **metadata + path references only, never file content in SQLite** (run_id/brief_id/workspace/rel_path/kind/size/hash/is_text/captured_at). The scan reuses the workspace copy filters (no `.git`/`target`/`node_modules`/`dev-data`/secrets/`.env`/key files), **skips symlinks**, content-hashes only files ≤ 1 MiB (deterministic `DefaultHasher`), caps the walk + the recorded count (`MAX_RUN_ARTIFACTS=1000`), and **NEVER scans the repo** — `inherit` (non-scoped) runs are skipped entirely. `BRIEF.md` / copied context only appear if the agent actually edited them. Failures surface as `artifacts.scan_failed` (alongside `artifacts.scan_started` / `artifacts.detected` with counts) — never swallowed. **Review state:** a `done` run opens `pending_review` (`brief_runs.review`/`review_note`/`reviewed_at`); `set_run_review` records `accepted`/`rejected` (only for `done` runs) + a `review` transcript event. **Safe apply (SHIPPED):** an `accepted` run's changed files can now be applied back into the configured project root (`RELIX_RUN_PROJECT_ROOT`, the same operator-config root `copy_repo` snapshots from) — guarded, path-safe, conflict-checked, idempotent, tested. `build_apply_plan` produces a **pure preview** (`run.diff` → `GET /v1/runs/:id/diff`, never mutates files): a per-file plan (`action` = `create`/`overwrite`/`delete`/`noop`/`refuse`, `can_apply`, `conflict`, `reason`) plus whether the run is **apply-eligible** (`run_apply_eligibility`: `done` + `accepted` + a scoped workspace — `inherit`-mode / legacy / unreviewed / rejected runs are refused, with nothing of theirs ever applied). **Conflict detection** compares each target against the run's BEFORE-run baseline: a new `run_artifacts.baseline_hash` (the before-scan content hash, persisted for `modified`/`deleted`; `None` for `created` / files > 1 MiB) lets apply confirm the project-root file still matches what the run started from. The rules are conservative — *better to refuse than overwrite blindly*: `created` applies only if the target is absent (or already byte-identical → `noop`), and **refuses if the target exists with different content**; `modified` applies only if the target still equals the baseline hash (or already equals the new content → `noop`), and **refuses if the target is missing, diverged, or the baseline is unverifiable** (incl. files too large to hash); `deleted` removes only if the target still equals the baseline (or is already absent → `noop`), else refuses. Paths are re-validated at apply time (reject absolute / `..` / drive-letter / UNC / empty-component paths and the same excluded dirs/files the copy filter uses — `.git`/`target`/`node_modules`/secrets/…), and the resolver **refuses any path that escapes the root or crosses a symlink** (no traversal, no symlink-target overwrite). `apply_run` (`run.apply` → `POST /v1/runs/:id/apply`) **refuses the WHOLE apply if ANY file is unsafe/conflicted** (no partial apply, no `force`), otherwise copies `create`/`overwrite` files (creating parent dirs) + removes `delete` files, and is **idempotent** (re-applying an already-applied plan is all-`noop` → 0 writes, no corruption). A durable apply ledger on `brief_runs` (`apply_status` = `not_applicable`/`blocked`/`ready`/`applied`/`failed`/`conflicted`, `applied_at`, `apply_note`, `applied_files`, `failed_files`) records each attempt; transcript events `apply.plan` / `apply.started` / `apply.applied` / `apply.conflicted` / `apply.failed` narrate it. A zero-artifact accepted run is a clear `applied` no-op. Bridge: `GET /v1/adapters` (rig.describe), `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/run` (brief.run), `GET /v1/runs` (recent run ledger), `GET /v1/runs/:id` (one run), `GET /v1/runs/:id/events` (the chronological transcript), `POST /v1/runs/:id/cancel` (cancel a running run), `GET /v1/runs/:id/artifacts` (changed files), `GET /v1/runs/:id/artifacts/:aid/preview` (a safe text preview — server-resolved path verified UNDER the workspace, binary/large/missing refused, secret-redacted, size-limited to 64 KiB), `POST /v1/runs/:id/review` (accept/reject), `GET /v1/runs/:id/diff` (the safe-apply plan + eligibility), `POST /v1/runs/:id/apply` (apply an accepted run's changes), `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/runs` (a Brief's Shift history). The artifact/preview/review/diff/apply endpoints are **tenant-scoped** (`run_belongs_to_tenant` — a run whose Brief is in another Guild reads as not-found, no existence leak). The dashboard Active Runs rows expand to show the transcript, a **Changes** section (created/modified/deleted files with size + per-file text Preview), a **Review** row (accept/reject for `done` runs, with a ✓/✕ status marker), and — for an `accepted` run — an **Apply** section (the per-file plan with refusal reasons, the apply target root, the durable `apply_status`, and an Apply button enabled only when the plan is fully applicable with ≥1 change). The boot policy generators grant `chat-users` the rig/run/`brief.runs`/`run.get`/`run.events`/`run.cancel`/`run.artifacts`/`run.artifact_preview`/`run.review`/`run.diff`/`run.apply`/`task.events` methods so the operator console reaches them. **Unified execution (manual + autonomous share ONE pipeline):** the opt-in heartbeat timer no longer runs the Rig inline with events-only recording — it now commits + executes each claimed Brief through the SAME path a manual dashboard run takes, so an autonomous run produces the IDENTICAL durable output: a `brief_runs` ledger row, a `run_events` transcript, scanned artifacts, `pending_review` review state, apply eligibility, `/v1/runs` dashboard visibility, and tenant-safe access. The shared seam is `prepare_claimed_run` (workspace prep → board move → ledger row → cancel-register → lifecycle transcript events → bridge-back token → pre-run baseline snapshot) followed by `execute_ready` (run the Rig + transcript, scan artifacts, advance board, chronicle, close the run row, release the Claim). `preflight_run` (manual, after `claim_brief_for_run`) and `dispatch_batch_with_policy` (autonomous, after `claim_queued_wakeups_with_caps`) BOTH call it; there is exactly one execution system, not two. **Trigger field:** every run record carries `brief_runs.trigger` (`manual` / `heartbeat` / `scheduled`; `unknown`/NULL for legacy rows), surfaced in `RunRecord` → `/v1/runs` → a **Trigger** column + a trigger filter on the dashboard Active Runs table — autonomous runs are visually marked (`auto`) but live in the same list. **Autonomous safety:** the heartbeat path keeps all the manual guards (same `probe()` readiness check — an unavailable adapter is refused with a `brief.dispatch_failed` chronicle and NO run row, never spawned; scoped workspaces — never `inherit` unless explicitly configured; never auto-applies — a `done` autonomous run stops at `pending_review`, identical to manual) PLUS its autonomous-only admission gates (per-Operative `wake_on_timer` + `active` status, `max_concurrent_runs` concurrency caps, and the Allowance/budget hard-stop). The single-owner Claim still guarantees no duplicate run (a live-claimed Brief is not `ready`, so no second worker/tick dispatches it). **Failure/retry behavior:** a Rig failure opens a `failed` run row + a `failed` transcript event; a non-retryable failure parks the Brief in `blocked` (so it is NOT re-dispatched in a retry storm — the cooldown is structural: `blocked` ≠ `ready`), a retryable failure stays `in_progress` for the next tick, a refusal (no adapter / unavailable / workspace-prep failure) finishes the wakeup `failed`, chronicles WHY, releases the Claim, and opens NO run row. **Honest limit:** within one tick the heartbeat runs claimed Briefs sequentially on the dispatch thread (a slow adapter delays the rest of that batch); the live timer loop is still gated behind `RELIX_HEARTBEAT_ENABLED` (off by default). **Dashboard surfacing:** `run.workspace_config` → `GET /v1/spine/run-config` additionally returns `inherit` (the unsafe coordinator-CWD opt-out), `heartbeat_enabled`, and `heartbeat_interval_secs` (read from the coordinator's env) so the **Command Center** (Overview) can show actionable system warnings (no Founder → first-run setup CTA, no available adapter, unassigned/blocked Briefs, unsafe `inherit` mode, missing project root) with next-action buttons + a company/runtime snapshot + latest-runs list, the **Settings** page can show heartbeat status + an `inherit`-mode warning, and a first-time operator can follow the whole loop (initialize company → create Brief → assign → run → review → apply) without reading the code. **Run deep links:** the Runs page is URL-driven (`/runs?run=<run_id>`) — a Brief card's latest-run link opens that exact run (labelled *Review run* / *Apply run* / *View run* by its state), which auto-expands and loads the transcript + changes + apply plan; refresh and back/forward preserve it, an unknown id falls back to the list, and a *Copy link* button shares it.

**Bridge-back** - `bridge_back.authorize` plus public HTTP routes under `/v1/bridge-back/*`, including Brief-local Clearance requests

**Chronicle** - `brief.created`, `brief.board_moved`, `brief.assigned`, `brief.reviewer_assigned`, `brief.comment`, `brief.subbrief_added`, `brief.subbrief_removed`, `brief.snagged`, `brief.snag_cleared`, `brief.dossier_added`, `brief.dossier_authored` / `brief.dossier_revised` / `brief.dossier_forked` (§1.8 authored Dossier revision / revise / fork), `brief.dossier_locked` / `brief.dossier_unlocked` (§1.8 document lock/unlock), `brief.interaction_opened` / `brief.interaction_resolved` / `brief.interaction_rejected` / `brief.interaction_cancelled` / `brief.interaction_expired` (§1.9 thread-interaction lifecycle), `brief.clearance_requested`, `brief.shift_done`, `brief.continued`, `brief.dispatch_failed`, `brief.budget_refused`, `brief.run_refused` (durable manual + heartbeat refusal), `brief.run_recovered` (stale run → `interrupted`), `brief.claim_reclaimed` (a dangling live Claim released by terminal-run evidence — stale-run adoption, §1.4/§7.1), `brief.run_discarded` (operator discarded a run's output)

## Governance And Security Carried Through

- Default-deny agent gate; a pending hire is inert.
- Heartbeat Rig resolution now refuses non-active Operatives before dispatch, so pending/suspended/disabled hires cannot run through the default-Rig path.
- Heartbeat wake admission now checks the assigned Operative's `wake_on_timer` flag and `max_concurrent_runs` cap before claiming queued work.
- Tenant-scoped spine reads for Mandates/Campaigns/Guild state.
- Org tree is cycle-guarded.
- Thin Rigs are governed at the box boundary and through scoped bridge-back tokens.
- Bridge-back tokens are scoped per Shift, Brief, Operative, and method; tokens are checked by `bridge_back.authorize`, exposed only through narrow HTTP routes, and revoked when the Shift ends.
- Thin Rigs can raise a real Brief-linked Clearance through `brief.clearance_request`; the handler derives subject/approver metadata from the stored Operative profile, parks the Brief in `awaiting_input`, and writes a pending `approval_requests` row.
- Macro execution is allowlisted and `ProcessRig` stdout is capped.
- Hard dispatch failures park the Brief in `blocked` and Chronicle the reason.
- Strategy gate is queryable and tenant-guarded. The explicit `agent.request_hire_for_mandate` team-build path refuses until the Mandate strategy is approved; it now *also* applies the spawn Key. `agent.create` is operator-only (an agent actor is refused). Legacy/manual `agent.request_hire` does not check a Mandate but does enforce the spawn Key.
- Spawn Key (company-model §5.2A) is **enforced**: an agent actor calling `agent.request_hire` / `agent.request_hire_for_mandate` is allowed only with `can_spawn_agents`; the hire is always pending-inert (never live). The Founder/Board (operator/admin) bypasses. An actor with no Operative profile in the Guild is security-denied. `agent.create` (live creation) is operator-only.
- **Route-differentiated spawn Clearance** (company-model §5.2A): `spawn_route=lead/founder` now mints a real typed Clearance (`approval_requests` row, `method = agent.activate_hire`, `agent_id = the pending hire`) linked to activating the hire. The hire stays pending-inert until the Clearance is decided: `coord.approval.decide` activates the hire on approve (`approve_hire`) and disables it on reject (`reject_hire`). `route=lead` widens the deciders to the actor's Lead (operator/admin always allowed); `route=direct` and operator hires mint NO Clearance.
- Assign Key (company-model §5.2B/§5.3) is **enforced at every assignment path**: `brief.set` (field=assignee), `brief.create` (initial assignee), and `brief.move` (into `in_progress`/`in_review`, against the Brief's current assignee). `enforce_assign_key` is the single tenant-scoped chokepoint with three layers: (1) the non-operator caller must have an Operative profile in this Guild; (2) **assignee validity** — the assignee must exist in this Guild and be `active`, so cross-tenant/unknown ids and disabled/pending/suspended hires can no longer receive executable work; (3) the actor's `can_assign_work` + `assign_scope` (any / branch via the tenant-scoped org tree / specific). Short-circuits to allow for: empty assignee (clearing), the Founder/Board (operator/admin, sovereign), and assignee == actor (claiming/progressing one's own work). `agent.assign_check` exposes the verdict read-only.
- **Tenant isolation (GROUP 6)** on the product agent/governance surface: `agent.get/keys/update/delete`, `agent.reports/peers/by_role/branch/line/manages`, `agent.assign_check`, `agent.allowance_committed`, and `coord.approval.pending/get/decide` all scope by the caller's verified tenant. A known agent_id/approval_id from another Guild resolves to not-found — never a cross-tenant read/write. The bridge forwards the tenant; the unscoped store methods remain only as internal/gate helpers.
- **Inline Clearance decide**: `POST /v1/spine/clearances/:id/decide` forwards to `coord.approval.decide` as the bridge's own verified identity (same path as `/v1/approvals/:id/decide`); the runtime cap enforces `authorized_approvers` ∪ operator/admin, so this never fabricates approval. The runtime refuses to re-decide a terminal approval (`decide_approval` requires `status='pending'`) and the decide handler returns before the spawn-Clearance activation hop, so side effects (activating a pending hire) apply **exactly once**. A cross-tenant `approval_id` resolves to not-found. There is intentionally no per-decision `ttl_secs` knob — the minted token's TTL is controller-configured.
- **Prime team-build foundation** (`mandate.team_plan`): a single governed step (NOT an autonomous loop). Requires an approved Mandate strategy + the actor's spawn Key; **persists** the plan (`mandate_team_plans`) and returns a structured JSON plan (`plan_id`, `status`, `proposed_roles`, `adopted`, `pending_hires`, `clearance_ids`, `denials`, `next_steps`). **Crew is reused before it is hired (company-model §12.5A/§12.5B):** for each required role the planner first looks for an already-active, runnable (Rig-bound) same-role Operative in this Guild — the **oldest** such match, tenant-scoped, never cross-tenant (`adopt_active_operative` over `AgentStore::list_active_for_tenant`, canonical-role matched via `prime::try_canon_role` so the apex Founder is never mistaken for an Operative). When one exists the role is **adopted** onto it (surfaced in `adopted`, no hire minted — so the starter engineer/designer staffs a build plan instead of being duplicated as a pending hire); only a role with **no** active same-role Operative mints a pending hire (with a spawn Clearance) when an identity is supplied, or is left `proposed`. `mandate.team_plan.latest` reads the newest persisted plan; `mandate.team_readiness` recomputes live readiness (missing roles / pending clearances / active agents / pending hires / blocked roles / next action) from the current hire and Clearance states — and **re-resolves each persisted required role to its active Operative on every call**, so an adopted role reports as an active agent (readiness `ready`) and approving a spawn Clearance that activates a hire makes the Mandate view show the team becoming active without mutating the plan row. Because adopted Operatives stay `active` (never a `pending` hire), the Action Center surfaces a hire card only for genuinely missing roles. All three are tenant-scoped.
- **Prime Mandate-to-Brief orchestration** (`mandate.orchestrate`, company-model §4.6): the Brief **skeleton** (roles, agents, assignments, ids, markers, gates) is deterministic, non-LLM; the Brief **text** (titles / dossiers / checklists) is deterministic by default and **opt-in model-authored** on the autonomous/manual Prime tick only (see *Prime Orchestration Authoring v1* below). Arg `mandate_id|mode?|max_briefs?|dry_run?` with modes `plan_only` (default; report-only) / `create_briefs` / `assign_ready`. Gate 1 = approved strategy (without it **nothing** is materialised). Materialisation is then **per-role**, not whole-team: with the strategy approved and a building mode (`create_briefs`/`assign_ready`), orchestration lays down a parent + a role-track Brief for **every** planned role, and an executable subject Brief only for the roles that are actually **active**. An **idempotent, three-tier** Brief tree: one parent `Execute Mandate: <title>` → one **role-track** Brief per role (known roles get a named track, e.g. `Engineering track: …`; unknown roles get `Execute <role> track for <mandate>`) → one **subject-execution** Brief per active agent under its (active) role track (e.g. `Engineering execution: <agent_id>`). Role tracks link under the parent and **stay unassigned**; subject Briefs link under their role track and are the items `assign_ready` assigns. **Placeholder role tracks:** a role that is **missing / pending-hire / pending-clearance / denied / blocked** still gets a durable role-track Brief under the parent — titled `… track blocked: <reason>` (e.g. `crew not ready`, `pending hire`, `pending clearance <approval_id>`), tagged `placeholder:true` + `reason` on its run entry, given a `blocker` Dossier explaining why — but **no** subject execution Brief and **no** assignee. **Role-keyed clearances:** a spawn Clearance records the pending hire's `agent_id`; `compute_readiness` maps that back to the seat's role (via the plan's pending hires) and stamps `role` + `agent_id` onto each `pending_clearances` entry, so a Clearance-blocked seat gets its own placeholder (reason naming the approval id) rather than only an unattributed JSON blocker. The most specific reason wins per role (pending clearance → pending hire → missing → blocked). A placeholder shares the role marker, so when the role later becomes active the **same** role track is reused and gains its subject Brief (the placeholder→active transition). **Placeholder title lifecycle:** on that transition the role-track title is **auto-promoted** from `… track blocked: <reason>` to the normal `… track: <mandate>` title — but only when the current title is still the machine-written placeholder form (detected by the `… track blocked:` prefix); a hand-edited title is detected as non-auto and **preserved**. The whole-team `ready` flag still drives the reported `status` (`blocked` while any gap remains) and next-actions. **max_briefs overflow visibility:** role tracks are capped at `max_briefs - 1` (parent counts as one) with active tracks prioritised; any placeholder role that does not fit is **not** silently dropped — it is reported in `placeholder_tracks_omitted` (`{role, reason, omitted:"max_briefs"}`), mirrored into the persisted `skipped` list, and surfaced as a next-action + a dashboard warning. (If active roles alone exceed the cap, the surplus active roles are still dropped — a documented edge for very large teams under a tiny cap.) Mandate-link is preserved on every tier and a newly-created parent gets an orchestration Dossier. `assign_ready` assigns each active agent's subject Brief through `enforce_assign_key` (the real assign gate — operator bypasses, an agent actor is gated); a denial/failure is recorded in `skipped`, never panics. **Idempotency (stable, subject-aware source markers):** every orchestrated Brief carries a `source_kind = "mandate_orchestration"` + a `source_marker` (the `tasks.source_kind`/`source_marker` columns). Markers are derived from the Mandate id, **not** from title text: parent `mandate:{mandate_id}:parent`, role track `mandate:{mandate_id}:role:{role_key}`, subject execution `mandate:{mandate_id}:role:{role_key}:subject:{agent_id}`. A rerun looks up each Brief by marker (`get_brief_by_source_marker`), reuses the marked tiers, and creates only the missing ones (`create_brief_with_marker`); a reused Brief's **title is left untouched** so a manual rename is never clobbered. This makes orchestration robust to a **Mandate rename**, a **manual Brief-title edit**, and a **partial crash** (any missing tier — parent-only or parent+role-track — is filled on rerun). A **changed active agent** for a role yields a new subject Brief (its agent-keyed marker) while the role track above is reused; the same agent on a rerun reuses its subject Brief. **Back-compat:** the previous slice's role-only marker (`…:role:{role_key}`) *is* the role-track marker, so legacy role-only children are reused as role tracks with no duplication. The deterministic `input_signature` (`DefaultHasher`, fixed seed) is computed over all markers (parent + role + subject) + mode + plan id, so it is rename-stable and reflects staffing changes. Every run persists via `record_orchestration_run`; `mandate.orchestration.latest` / `.list` read them back (tenant-scoped). The response carries the tiered view `{parent_brief, role_tracks_created, role_tracks_existing, placeholder_tracks_created, placeholder_tracks_existing, placeholder_tracks_omitted, subject_briefs_created, subject_briefs_existing, assigned_briefs, skipped, blockers, source_markers, next_actions}` plus the backward-compatible flat `created_briefs` / `existing_briefs` (unions, each entry tagged with its `marker`, and placeholder entries additionally tagged `placeholder:true` + `reason`). The run record persists `created_brief_ids` / `existing_brief_ids` (reused) / `assigned_brief_ids` / `skipped` / `source_markers` / `blockers` / `input_signature` — each created/existing entry keeps its `marker` (and `placeholder` flag), so the tier (parent / role / subject / placeholder) is recoverable from the persisted run without extra columns. **Tenant note:** the `tasks` table now carries a row-level `tenant_id` (Guild) column. Product-spine Briefs are stamped at creation (`create_brief` → `set_task_tenant`); legacy rows and non-Brief Tasks are NULL and resolve to the `default` Guild via `COALESCE(tenant_id,'default')` in the tenant-scoped reads, so existing single-tenant DBs keep seeing every row while a *named* Guild sees only its own. The product **board / inbox / detail / search / label** read capabilities (`brief.board`, `brief.board_summary`, `brief.blocked_list`, `brief.stale_list`, `brief.overdue`, `brief.unassigned`, `brief.search`, `brief.by_label`, `brief.detail`) call `*_for_tenant` store variants with the caller's `ctx.tenant_id_or_default()`, so a known Brief id from another Guild reads as not-found and never appears on another Guild's board/inbox. **Same-tenant ownership on every exposed Brief surface:** a `deny_cross_tenant` guard (built on `task_in_tenant`) runs **before** the Brief-row mutations and relationship/Dossier operations. **All** Brief row reads and mutations currently exposed through the product-spine handlers now enforce same-tenant ownership: the mutations `brief.set`, `brief.move`, `brief.comment` (communication is not authorization-free across Guilds — a cross-Guild comment is refused and **no** Chronicle event is appended), `brief.set_labels`, `brief.set_due`, `brief.pin`, `brief.snag` / `brief.unsnag` (both the blocked Brief AND its blocker), `brief.set_snags`, `brief.dossier_add`, `brief.dossier_author` (§1.8), `brief.subbrief` / `brief.unsubbrief` (both endpoints); and the reads `brief.detail`, `brief.fields`, `brief.labels`, `brief.due`, `brief.blocked`, `brief.snags`, `brief.dossiers`, `brief.dossier_latest`, `brief.dossier_get` (resolved via the Dossier's owning Brief), `brief.subbriefs`, `brief.subbrief_progress`, plus the reverse-edge reads `brief.blocking` / `brief.parents` which use tenant-scoped store variants (`list_blocking_for_tenant` / `parent_briefs_for_tenant`, a JOIN on `tasks` filtered by Guild) so a related Brief from another Guild is never leaked even if a legacy edge crosses tenants. A cross-Guild target returns the **same not-found** a genuinely-missing Brief would, so the row's existence in another Guild is never leaked. Brief creation treats the tenant stamp as **required**: `create_brief` rolls the freshly-created row back and returns an error if `set_task_tenant` fails, so a stamp failure can never silently leave an unscoped Brief (the human-ref `assign_brief_ref` stays fail-soft — it is a display-only `REL-N` id whose absence does not make a Brief unusable). **Remaining honest caveats:** `mandate.briefs` / `list_briefs_by_mandate` still rely on the globally-unique, tenant-validated `mandate_id` (not a row tenant filter); and the marker-based orchestration dedup remains keyed on the `mandate_id` embedded in the marker (also tenant-validated upstream).

- **Prime guided driver v1** (`prime.next_step` + `prime.advance`, company-model §5.4/§8.2 + §12.5/§12.5B): a bounded one-step guide over the EXISTING governed routes - the manual guided surface. `prime.next_step` is READ-ONLY: given a `proposal_id` **or** a `mandate_id` (JSON arg, tenant-scoped — an unknown/cross-Guild target reads as not-found) it classifies the single next governed step by joining the proposal/strategy gate, `compute_readiness` (team plan + live hire/Clearance state), the Brief board (reusing `prime.status`'s exact `brief_status_row` bucketing), and the run ledger. It returns `{phase, label, reason, route, action_api, can_advance, advance_action, proposal_id, mandate_id, plan_id, strategy_status, missing_roles, pending_hires, pending_clearances, counts}` where `phase ∈ needs_approval | needs_team_plan | needs_hire_approval | needs_orchestration | ready_to_start | running_or_done | blocked | unknown`. `prime.advance` executes **at most one** explicitly-requested step: `create_team_plan` (calls the existing `handle_team_plan` with the Mandate's distinct active **work-role** crew, via `prime::try_canon_role` over `list_active_for_tenant` — so it **adopts** active Operatives and mints **no** hires/Clearances; an empty roster records an inert plan shell) or `orchestrate_assign_ready` (calls the existing `handle_orchestrate` in `assign_ready` mode). Both auto-advance steps are gated on `strategy_approved` (so a step the orchestration/team-plan gate would refuse is never offered as a button — proposal-origin Mandates, which have no strategy-gate row, show the route but no button). Safety: `prime.advance` **re-reads** state and runs the step ONLY when the requested `advance_action` still equals the current `next_step.advance_action` and `can_advance` is true — otherwise it returns `{advanced:false, refused:"stale_action", next_step}` with **no side effects** (the bridge maps this onto a **409**). It runs through the same governed handler + the caller's identity/Keys as the manual route (a sub-`InvocationCtx` only swaps the args; the caller is never elevated), and a governance refusal from the underlying handler is propagated honestly. It **never** implements `approve_strategy` / `approve_hires` as auto-advance actions (those stay human), and `start_work` is deliberately routed to the existing explicit `prime.start` button (no real adapter is auto-run). Bridge routes: `GET /v1/spine/prime/proposals/:id/next-step` + `GET /v1/spine/mandates/:id/next-step`, `POST /v1/spine/prime/proposals/:id/advance` + `POST /v1/spine/mandates/:id/advance` (stale → 409, bad input → 400). Dashboard: the Chat Shift Room renders the next step + a restrained **Advance one step** button when `can_advance`, else the route to take by hand. **The Overview now surfaces the same guided next-step driver** as a top-level **"Company operating status"** cockpit (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Overview.tsx` → `OperatingStatus`, using the `primeDriver.{nextStep,advance,mandateNextStep,mandateAdvance}` clients over the existing routes — **no new backend authority**): it picks the most relevant active object (latest Prime proposal, else the latest loaded Mandate via the twin route), shows `phase`/`label`/`reason`, the payload's board/run counts, a deep link to the relevant route, and a live Action-Center pressure strip (approvals / hires / budget / recovery / review / ready). The **Advance one step** button runs exactly one governed step through the same gated route (proposal or Mandate twin), then refreshes the Overview + Action Center; a stale `409` shows an honest banner and reloads the fresh step; a refusal shows its reason. It is **best-effort** (a missing/unavailable next step degrades to an honest calm empty state and never blanks the Overview) and remains the manual one-step surface; the separate autonomous Prime driver v1 below can drive those same approved-work steps on a bounded timer. Six runtime tests pin the doc semantics (proposed→needs_approval/no-advance; approved-no-plan→create_team_plan advances + next step changes; pending hire→human/no-advance; ready team→orchestrate_assign_ready creates+assigns through the existing path; stale request refuses with no side effects; tenant isolation) + a bridge 409-mapping test.

## Shipped This Roadmap

- Phase 5 materialize-work: rule-based companion plus command-bar operations through `/v1/spine/*`.
- Phase 6 interim dashboard: `/spine` work-object console over the live spine API.
- Execution invariant pass: reviewer guard for `in_review`, assignee/no-Snag guard for `in_progress`, two-pointer Claim fields, lock clearing on assignee/status ownership changes, persistent Brief wakeup queue with queue/coalesce/defer/skipped audit rows, lazy claim stamping, deferred promotion on lock release/status unlock, scoped bridge-back HTTP routes.
- Strategy-gated hire slice: `agent.request_hire_for_mandate` blocks team-build hires until the target Mandate has an approved strategy, then creates only a pending inert hire.
- Bridge-back Clearance slice: `/v1/bridge-back/briefs/:id/clearance` plus `brief.clearance_request` creates a pending approval from a scoped Rig token.
- Runtime Keys slice: Operatives persist timer-wake permission, on-demand wake permission, and max concurrent Brief runs; heartbeat dispatch enforces timer wake and concurrency caps, `brief.wakeup` records skipped rows when wake admission is disabled, and the dashboard can edit those values from the Roster panel.
- Costs panel slice: `/spine` reads `guild.get` and `agent.allowance_committed` through browser-safe spine proxies and shows configured Guild cap, committed Operative allowance, remaining headroom, and over-cap warning. The panel now states the dispatch-level enforcement state (see the Allowance hard-stop slice below); the Guild-cap figures themselves remain visibility only.
- Allowance hard-stop slice (Brief dispatch): the heartbeat dispatcher now refuses to run a Brief when the assigned Operative is over its Allowance. `heartbeat::allowance_admits(monthly_allowance_cents, spend_micros)` is the pure verdict; `dispatch_batch_with_policy` takes an `admit_budget` closure, and the live loop (`controller_runtime.rs`) builds it from the Operative's `monthly_allowance_cents` plus its current UTC calendar-month spend read from the metrics ledger (`MetricsQuery::cost_since(agent_id, since_ms)`). A refused Brief is parked in `blocked` (not silently skipped), gets a `brief.budget_refused` Chronicle event (`budget_refused: agent_id=… allowance=…c used=…u reason=…`), its wakeup is closed `failed`, and its Claim is released. **Honest limits:** (1) an Operative allowance of `0` is a deterministic hard-stop; a positive cap is **best-effort** — it only counts priced AI calls whose recorded `agent_name` matches the Operative's `agent_id` in the metrics ledger (`cost_micros`), so missing/unattributed spend fails open. (2) ~~The window is a trailing 30 days, not a calendar month with reset bookkeeping.~~ *(Superseded by the Allowance calendar-month windowing slice below: the window is now the current UTC calendar month via the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window`, with implicit reset at month start.)* (3) Guild-level Allowance is **not** spend-enforced at dispatch (no tenant-scoped spend query, and Briefs carry no tenant at the dispatch site) — it remains visibility/commitment only. *(Superseded by the Guild-level spend hard-stop slice below: the autonomous dispatch path now resolves each Brief's own Guild and enforces the Guild budget against that Guild's current UTC calendar-month spend.)*
- Guild-level spend hard-stop slice (autonomous) — company-model §6/§6.6: the Guild budget now **binds autonomous spend**, mirroring the per-Operative Allowance hard-stop and additive on top of it (per-Operative enforcement is unchanged and authoritative — a per-Operative refusal takes precedence and is never weakened). `heartbeat::guild_allowance_admits(budget_cents, guild_spend_micros)` is the pure verdict; `heartbeat::dispatch_budget_admits(card, task_store, agent_store, spine, metrics, now_ms)` composes the two gates and is what the live heartbeat loop (`controller_runtime.rs`) calls as its `admit_budget` closure. **Tenant isolation:** the Guild gate resolves the Brief's OWN Guild (`TaskStore::task_tenant`, now `pub`) and sums **only that Guild's active Operatives'** current UTC calendar-month `cost_since` (never a cross-tenant `cost_since(None, …)`) against `Guild.monthly_allowance_cents` — the exact figure + window the Action Center's `company_spend_item` reports, so the gate and the feed never disagree. A Guild-refused Brief is parked in `blocked` (not silently skipped), gets a **`guild.budget_refused`** Chronicle event (`guild_budget_refused: tenant=… brief=… assignee=… budget=…c guild_used=…u reason=…`) distinct from the per-Operative `brief.budget_refused`, opens a durable refused run (status **`over_guild_budget`**, distinct from `over_allowance`), its wakeup closes `failed`, and its Claim releases. The Action Center's "Guild spend over budget" card copy now states the autonomous dispatch gate refuses (manual runs stay sovereign). **Manual sovereignty preserved:** `preflight_run` / `brief.run` / `prime.start` take **no** budget gate (the Board is sovereign), so a manual run of the same over-budget Brief still commits — pinned by a test that the autonomous gate refuses while `preflight_run` returns `Ready` for the same Brief. **Tests:** pure `guild_allowance_admits` verdicts; `dispatch_budget_admits` over-Guild-budget refused + under-budget allowed + no-budget allowed; per-Operative stop takes precedence over Guild; cross-tenant spend does not trip another Guild's cap; the dispatch path parks + chronicles a Guild stop as `guild.budget_refused` (not the per-Operative event); manual run sovereign over the Guild gate. **Honest limits (unchanged from the per-Operative gate):** ~~the window is a trailing 30 days, not a calendar month with reset bookkeeping (roadmap §5 slice 9)~~ *(now the current UTC calendar month — see the Allowance calendar-month windowing slice below)*; spend is best-effort (only priced AI calls whose recorded `agent_name` matches an Operative's `agent_id`, so unattributed spend fails open); there is still **no issue-tree cost rollup and no billing-code attribution** (company-model §6.6 — deferred, roadmap §5 slice 10); the Guild gate is inert when the SpineStore or the metrics ledger is unavailable (per-Operative gate still applies). A Guild budget of `0`/unset is "no cap" here (the Action Center only signals a positive budget), deliberately distinct from the per-Operative `0` = hard-stop.
- Allowance calendar-month windowing slice (autonomous spend window) — company-model §6/§6.6 (roadmap §5 slice 9): the per-Operative Allowance hard-stop, the additive Guild-budget hard-stop, AND the Action Center live-spend feed now bill against a single canonical window — the **current calendar month in UTC** — replacing the trailing-30-day approximation. `heartbeat::allowance_window(now_ms) -> AllowanceWindow { start_ms, cutoff_ms, resets_at_ms }` is THE window function: `start_ms` is the month's first instant (00:00:00.000 UTC, **inclusive** — matching `MetricsQuery::cost_since`'s `timestamp_ms >= since` bound), `cutoff_ms` is the supplied now, and `resets_at_ms` is the next month's first instant (the reset edge). It uses zero-dependency Hinnant civil-date math (`civil_from_days`/`days_from_civil`, `div_euclid`-safe). **One source of truth:** `dispatch_budget_admits` derives `since_ms` from it (was `now − 30·86_400·1000`), and the Action Center's `MetricsSpendSource::current_month` (renamed from `trailing_30d`, used by `controller_runtime`'s `company.actions` wiring) derives its window from the same function — so the dispatch gate and the Desk can never disagree by computing the window two ways. **Reset bookkeeping is implicit:** there is no stored counter to clear; spend is always re-summed from the live month start, so a new month is a fresh window by construction (`resets_at_ms` is the value an operator surface can show as "resets at …"). **UTC is deliberate and fixed:** the mesh carries no per-Guild billing timezone, so a single stable zone keeps gate + feed + tests in agreement (a future per-Guild zone would change only this one function). Action Center operator copy changed "in the last 30 days" → "this month". **Tests:** the canonical window (inclusive month start, next-month reset edge, 1ms-before-boundary belongs to the previous month, leap Feb 2024 = 29 days, Dec→Jan rollover); the metrics-seeded budget tests now pin their rows to the window start so they stay deterministic at a month boundary; the real-ledger live-spend tests seed relative to the window (in-month counted / pre-month excluded). **Honest limits / still deferred:** spend remains best-effort (only priced AI calls whose recorded `agent_name` matches an Operative's `agent_id`); there is still **no issue-tree cost rollup and no billing-code attribution** (company-model §6.6 — roadmap §5 slice 10); only the autonomous heartbeat path passes through this gate (manual `brief.run`/`prime.start` stay sovereign, no window/budget gate); the metrics `BudgetEnforcer`'s separate Daily/Hourly windows are unrelated and untouched.
- Activity slice: `/spine` renders the existing `/v1/tasks/events/recent` Chronicle tail instead of a dead placeholder.
- Goals slice: `/spine` renders the tenant Mandate hierarchy and side-panel drilldown through `mandate.list` and `mandate.tree`.
- Desk/Inbox + live-thread slice: a new `brief.unassigned` capability lists active Briefs with no Operative; the bridge composes `/v1/spine/inbox` (blocked + stale + overdue + in-review + unassigned), `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/thread` (detail + Chronicle + wakeups + claim holder), `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/events`, and `/v1/spine/unassigned` from existing capabilities only (no new runtime queries, no fabricated data; all bounded by limit). `/spine` now renders the Inbox as a sectioned Desk, the Brief detail as a live work thread (claim holder + Chronicle timeline), and an Operative Desk (their active Briefs + allowance/Rig summary). **Honest limits:** the page is still the interim single-file shell with no realtime/websocket — the thread refreshes only on open/comment, not via push.
- Adapter metadata pass: Rig descriptions expose probe status, install hints, structured-output support, bridge-back support, and subscription billing metadata for Claude/Codex/Gemini.
- Operative Keys + governance slice (company-model §5.2): Operatives gained the product-level org/work Keys (`can_spawn_agents`, `spawn_route`, `can_assign_work`, `assign_scope`, `assign_allowed_agents`, `can_manage_work`, `can_configure_agents`, `configure_scope`, `secret_allowlist`, `instruction_bundle`), all default-deny and validated. Pure policy helpers (`agent/keys.rs`) decide spawn/assign. **Enforced:** the spawn Key on agent-originated hires (`agent.request_hire` / `..._for_mandate`), `agent.create` made operator-only, and the assign Key at `brief.set` (assignee) using live Branch membership. `agent.assign_check` exposes the assign verdict; the dashboard gained a Keys panel (enforced vs stored-only) and a pending-Clearances surface on the Desk (`/v1/spine/clearances`, read-only). **Stored/displayed only at the time of this slice:** `can_manage_work`, `can_configure_agents` + `configure_scope`, `secret_allowlist`, `instruction_bundle`. *(Superseded by the stored-only Keys enforcement slice below: all four are now enforced.)*
- Tenant-safe governance + inline Clearances + Prime team-build slice: (1) **GROUP 6 tenant isolation** — every product agent-id/approval-id read+write gained a `*_for_tenant` variant and the handlers now pass the verified tenant, so a known id from another Guild resolves to not-found (proven by store + handler isolation tests). (2) **Inline Clearance decide** — `POST /v1/spine/clearances/:id/decide` + Approve/Reject buttons on the Desk, forwarded to `coord.approval.decide` as the bridge identity (the runtime cap still enforces authorisation; no fabricated approval). (3) **Route-differentiated spawn Clearance** — `spawn_route=lead/founder` mints a real typed Clearance linked to the pending hire; approving it activates the hire, rejecting disables it; direct/operator hires mint none; the mandate strategy gate still runs first. (4) **Prime team-build foundation** — `mandate.team_plan` (strategy + spawn-Key gated) returns a structured plan and mints identified hires with spawn Clearances, plus a "Plan team" action in the Mandate panel. **Honest limits (at the time of this slice):** no autonomous Prime loop. *(Superseded by the spine-hardening slice below: team plans now persist through `mandate_team_plans` with `mandate.team_plan.latest` + `mandate.team_readiness`, and the misleading `ttl_secs` field was removed from the clearance-decide API.)*
- Spine hardening slice (assignment gates + persistent team plans + readiness): (1) **Assignment-gate closure** — `brief.create` (initial assignee) and `brief.move` (into `in_progress`/`in_review`) now run the same tenant-scoped assign gate as `brief.set`, and the gate gained an **assignee-validity** layer (must exist in-Guild + be `active`) so cross-tenant / unknown / disabled / pending assignees are refused; self-assignment and the Founder/Board path are allowed. (2) **Persistent Mandate Team Plans** — `mandate.team_plan` writes a `mandate_team_plans` row; `mandate.team_plan.latest` reads it back; both tenant-scoped. (3) **Live team readiness** — `mandate.team_readiness` recomputes staffing from current hire/Clearance states, so a Clearance approval activating a hire makes readiness flip to `ready`. (4) **Clearance decide hardening** — removed the misleading accepted-but-ignored `ttl_secs`; pinned exactly-once side effects (a re-decide is refused) and cross-tenant decide rejection with tests. Dashboard: the Mandate panel renders the persisted plan + readiness. **Honest limits:** no autonomous Prime loop; readiness is computed on read (the plan row's `status` is a coarse creation-time label, not live); plan persistence is best-effort (a DB error surfaces `persisted:false` rather than failing the already-minted hires).
- Stored-only Keys enforcement slice (company-model §5.2): the four previously stored/displayed-only Keys now enforce. (1) **`can_manage_work`** + new `manage_scope` / `manage_allowed_agents` columns + `manage_verdict` gate `brief.move` / `brief.set` (non-assignee) / `brief.set_due` / `brief.pin` / `brief.snag` / `brief.unsnag` on a Brief owned by another Operative (`enforce_manage_key`; self-progress, unowned, and Founder bypass; tenant-scoped; non-active owner fails closed). (2) **`can_configure_agents`** + new `configure_allowed_agents` (+ `configure_scope` extended with `any`) + `configure_verdict` gate `agent.update` / `agent.delete` (`enforce_configure_key`); self-config denied (no self-escalation); cross-tenant target fails closed. (3) **`secret_allowlist`** gates `credentials.get` for Operatives (`enforce_secret_allowlist` + `secret_allowed`) on top of the vault's owner/tenant gate — exact id, empty = deny-by-default, disabled denied, non-Operative passes through; denials are `tracing::warn`-logged. (4) **`instruction_bundle`** is composed into the agent prompt as a trusted charter section (`compose_brief_prompt_with_charter`) ahead of the Brief body; editing it is configure-gated. The dashboard Keys panel moves all four into the enforced section with scope/allowlist editors. **Honest limits:** the secret gate is only on the explicit `credentials.get` read (no runtime auto-injection path exists to gate); `brief.comment` is intentionally ungated; every per-agent gate is bypassed by the sovereign Founder/Board and skipped when no agent store is wired.
- Prime Mandate-to-Brief orchestration slice (company-model §4.6): `mandate.orchestrate` (modes `plan_only` / `create_briefs` / `assign_ready`, with `dry_run`) turns an approved-strategy Mandate + a ready team into a deterministic, idempotent three-tier Brief tree (parent → role track → per-agent subject execution, linked + mandate-tagged + Dossier'd), assigning each active agent's subject Brief through the real `enforce_assign_key` gate and recording the run in `mandate_orchestration_runs` (read back via `mandate.orchestration.latest` / `.list`). Readiness logic was extracted into a shared `compute_readiness` so `team_readiness` and orchestration agree. Bridge: `POST /v1/spine/mandates/:id/orchestrate` + `GET .../orchestration/latest`; the Mandate panel gains Orchestrate (Plan / Create briefs / Create + assign) buttons and renders the latest run. **Honest limits:** the Brief breakdown is **rule-based, not LLM** — a fixed three-tier tree (parent → role track → per-agent subject execution) with a fixed role→title map, no task decomposition, dependencies, or content authoring; idempotency uses **stable, subject-aware source markers** (Mandate-id + role + agent-derived, rename-safe — see the orchestration entry above), superseding the old title-keyed and role-only schemes; missing/pending/blocked roles now get **durable placeholder role tracks** (no subject Brief, no assignee) so staffing gaps are visible work objects; orchestration is still operator/Prime-initiated per call, not an autonomous loop. Each active role currently produces exactly one role track and one subject Brief per active agent — there is no multi-subject fan-out per role beyond the active staffing, and no inter-Brief dependency edges yet. **Placeholder honesty:** a placeholder role track keeps its `… blocked: <reason>` title even after the role becomes active (titles are never clobbered), so the live placeholder-vs-active distinction comes from the run's tier buckets / the presence of a subject Brief, not from the role-track title.
- Production execution slice (real, safe, observable Claude/Codex): (1) **Structured CLI readiness** — `ProcessRig::probe()` returns six honest statuses (`available` / `missing_binary` / `not_authenticated` / `unsupported_version` / `interactive_only` / `probe_failed`) from a noninteractive `--version` probe with an 8s anti-hang timeout; `classify_readiness` is a pure, mocked-output-tested function; the Crew + Settings pages render the friendly label + probe detail + install/login hint, with a "Refresh probes" button and a confirm-before-assigning-an-unavailable-adapter guard. (2) **Async dispatch** — `run_brief_now` split into `preflight_run` + `execute_ready`; the `brief.run` handler pre-flights inline then runs the blocking Shift on a background thread, returning `status:"running"` + `run_id` immediately (a long Claude/Codex run no longer freezes the bridge).
