(3) **Durable run ledger** — a new `brief_runs` table + `brief.runs` capability + `GET /v1/runs` / `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/runs`; the dashboard Active Runs reads the stable records (status filter + duration + result) instead of parsing event strings. **Live validation (fresh debug binaries, mock provider, 2026-06):** the mesh booted, `/dashboard` served the current bundle, and `/v1/adapters` reported **real** readiness — `codex` `available` (`codex-cli 0.136.0` via the live `--version` probe), `claude` `probe_failed` (genuinely not installed on the box — honestly refused, not faked), `gemini`/`hermes` `missing_binary`, `echo` available; `/v1/runs` + the per-Brief runs route returned stable empty ledgers. **Honest limit:** an end-to-end real run (a populated `brief_runs` row) was **not** exercised live because creating the assignable Operative requires the pre-existing operator-gated hire flow (`agent.create` is operator/admin-only; the dev bridge identity is operative-role and no Founder is seeded in fresh data) — orthogonal to this slice; the run model + async split are covered by unit tests (record open/close, refusal-records-nothing, preflight→execute parity). **Update:** the manual + autonomous paths are now UNIFIED — the heartbeat timer commits + executes through the same `prepare_claimed_run` → `execute_ready` pipeline as a manual run, so an autonomous run opens the same `brief_runs` ledger row / transcript / artifacts / `pending_review` state, stamped with a `heartbeat` trigger; covered by unit tests (heartbeat run opens a ledger row, records events + artifacts, enters review, appears in `list_runs`, refuses an unavailable adapter without a run row, never auto-applies, correct trigger, tenant-scoped).
- First-run company bootstrap slice (usable from zero): close the gap where a fresh install had **no way** to create the first assignable Operative (the dashboard/bridge identity is operative-role, and `agent.create` is operator/admin-gated, so with no Founder seeded the dashboard dead-ended at "No Operatives yet"). (1) **`company.bootstrap_founder`** — an owner-gated, idempotent first-run capability that ensures the Guild's single **Founder** Operative (role `founder`, `active`, full Org/Work Keys = `any`, apex of the org, rig defaulting to `echo`). Atomic check-then-insert under one lock, so two concurrent calls cannot both create a Founder; a repeat returns the existing Founder (`created:false`), never a duplicate. The **owner gate** admits a real operator/admin AIC **or** the boot-seeded `allow-all` operator-console identity (the trusted dashboard/bridge owner); a normal Operative or an unknown caller is refused (`SECURITY_DENIED`). (2) **`company.status`** (initialized / founder / operative_count) + **`agent.operatives`** (tenant-scoped Crew roster that **excludes** the infra operator-console). (3) **Console owner authority** — boot now calls `grant_console_authority` (idempotent, self-healing) to give the operator-console identity the full Org/Work Keys (`assign`/`manage`/`spawn`/`configure` = `any`) so the dashboard owner can assign Briefs to the Founder + stand up the first team. It UPDATEs **only** the `allow-all` console profile (matched by subject + profile), never a normal Operative, and is a separate enforcement axis from the admission gate (no gate weakening). (4) **Bridge:** `GET /v1/spine/company`, `GET /v1/spine/operatives`, and `POST /v1/spine/company/init` — the init route is **session-gated** (requires a logged-in dashboard session, not merely a bearer) as defence-in-depth over the runtime owner gate. Policy generators allow the three methods. (5) **Dashboard:** Crew shows a first-run "Initialize Company" state (Founder name + default-adapter picker, `echo` recommended) when uninitialised, else the real roster (now from `/v1/spine/operatives`, Founder badged) instead of the wrong access-broker list; the Briefs board gains an inline per-card Operative assignee picker (create → assign → run in one place) and a "no Operatives → initialize" hint; the Assign page uses the real roster. **Live validation (fresh debug binaries, clean empty data dir, mock provider, 2026-06):** from a truly empty install — admin setup → login (session) → `company.status` `initialized:false` → `POST /v1/spine/company/init` created the Founder (`created:true`, role `founder`, rig `echo`) → `/v1/spine/operatives` showed it → created a Brief → assigned the Founder (the console-owner assign gate **passed**) → ran it on `echo` → **`/v1/runs` recorded a real row** (`status:done`, `echo: …`) and the per-Brief runs route returned it, with **no 401/502s**; re-`init` returned `created:false` (no duplicate); a bearer-without-session `init` was refused **401** (session gate). This closes the previous slice's honest limit (the operator-gated hire flow blocking an end-to-end live run). Codex probed `available` but a real Codex Shift was **not** forced (only its `--version` was verified noninteractive-safe). **Honest limit:** the Founder is a distinct Operative with its own generated `subject_id` (not the owner's AIC) — it is `created_by` the owner subject but does not share an identity bundle, which is sufficient for `echo`/subscription-CLI runs but not for a Founder that must itself present an AIC to the mesh.
- Windows CLI-resolution + Claude auth-readiness slice: fix Claude (and Codex/Gemini) being misreported `probe_failed` on Windows, where the CLI is an npm shim (`claude.cmd`) that Rust `Command::new` can't spawn directly. (1) **`resolve_program` / `Spawnable`** — resolve through `PATH`+`PATHEXT` to a `Direct` (`.exe`/`.com`) or `BatchShim` (`.cmd`/`.bat` → `%SystemRoot%\System32\cmd.exe /C` with discrete argv, no shell-string injection from a Brief), preferring a real `.exe`; an extensionless file is non-spawnable on Windows (skips the npm `claude` sh shim that otherwise spawned into `os error 193`). `probe()` + `run()` resolve identically; a missing program is now a clear non-retryable "not found" (pre-spawn), not a retryable spawn blip. ProcessRig `fallback_paths` add the npm real `claude.exe`. (2) **Two-step Claude readiness** — `claude --version` then `claude auth status --text` via `classify_readiness_with_auth` (available = installed + logged in; not_authenticated = logged out; interactive_only = auth hang; available-with-note = older CLI lacking `auth status`); hints use `claude auth login` / `claude auth status --text`. **Live validation (this machine, real Claude Code 2.1.159 installed + Claude Max login):** `/v1/adapters` now reports `claude available — installed: 2.1.159 (Claude Code); Login method: Claude Max account` (was `probe_failed`); `codex available`, `echo available`, `gemini`/`hermes` `missing_binary`. Tests: `.cmd`-shim resolution, direct-`.exe` preference, extensionless-shim skip + real-`.exe` fallback, classify-by-extension, unix bare-name, Claude auth parsing (logged-in/logged-out/hang/auth-absent), spawn-failure-is-probe_failed-not-missing.
- Claude execution-path slice (parse stream-json, surface permissions): the full Claude run — not just readiness. `claude --print --output-format stream-json --verbose` (prompt on stdin) emits JSONL whose terminal `type:"result"` event holds the real answer + `is_error` + `permission_denials`; Relix used to store the raw ~8KB JSONL as the run summary. `RigOutputFormat::ClaudeStreamJson` + `parse_claude_stream_json` now extract the result event (off raw pre-redaction stdout, then redact + cap only the answer): `is_error` → non-retryable failure (subtype + text); else `Done` with the answer, leading with `⚠ N tool permission(s) denied` when Claude wanted a tool Relix's noninteractive run didn't approve (no `--dangerously-skip-permissions`); no result event → exit-code fallback (never a faked success). **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** Founder on the `claude` rig, Brief "Create a short plain text note saying Relix Claude test passed." → `brief.run` dispatched **async** (returned `status:running`, the bridge stayed responsive throughout) → completed in **9s** → `/v1/runs` + `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/runs` recorded `done`/`claude`/`9s` with the **clean** summary `Created relix-claude-test.txt with the text "Relix Claude test passed."` (no JSONL noise), `/v1/adapters` still `claude available`. In this run the working dir was the coordinator CWD (the repo, which the local Claude config trusts) so the Write was permitted; a manual probe in an untrusted temp dir instead returned 1 permission denial, surfaced via the `⚠` caveat — both honest. Tests: terminal-result extraction, permission-denial count, no-result→None + junk tolerance, and outcome mapping (clean answer / denial caveat / is_error failure / none-falls-through). **Honest limits:** no scoped per-Brief workspace yet (Claude runs in the coordinator CWD unless overridden) — *superseded by the scoped per-Brief run workspace slice below*; tool-permission grant is Claude's own project-trust decision, not Relix's.
- Scoped per-Brief run workspace slice (safe execution boundary): a Brief run no longer executes in the coordinator/repo CWD — each run gets a dedicated sandbox `<root>/<run_id>` (root = `<db_parent>/workspaces/runs`, env-overridable). `TaskStore` resolves the root; `prepare_run_workspace` validates strictly (path derived ONLY from the generated `run_id` — a prompt can never choose it; `run_id` checked to a safe single segment with no `.`/`..`/separators; a direct-child guard), creates the dir + a trusted `BRIEF.md`. `preflight_run` pins it as `working_dir` and persists it (`brief_runs.workspace` + additive migration, in `/v1/runs` + the RunReport + the dashboard Active Runs "Workspace" column + the Brief Run banner); a creation failure refuses `workspace_error` (Claim released, no run record, no repo-wide fallback). `RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_MODE=inherit` is the explicit opt-out. **Live-validated:** an echo run recorded its workspace + wrote `BRIEF.md` there; a Claude "create a note" Brief ran **inside** its scoped workspace (an untrusted Claude project) so the Write was **denied + surfaced** (`⚠ 1 tool permission(s) denied`) and **the repo root was untouched** (previously Claude wrote into the repo) — the core safety win. Tests: workspace created, traversal run_ids rejected, run uses the workspace as cwd (via a pwd ProcessRig + the ledger), creation-failure → clean `workspace_error`, concurrent same-Operative runs get distinct non-colliding workspaces. **Honest limits:** the workspace is created empty (a trusted `BRIEF.md` only) — no project context is copied/checked out yet; tool-permission grant remains Claude's own project-trust decision (a scoped workspace is untrusted by default).
- Run-workspace context modes slice (intentional, capped, observable context): let a run receive project context without repo-CWD execution. `RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_CONTEXT` = **`empty`** (default — only `BRIEF.md`) or **`copy_repo`** (a capped, filtered project snapshot). `copy_repo` has hard file-count + byte caps (`RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_MAX_FILES`/`_BYTES`, defaults 2000 / 32 MiB; exceeding either aborts + removes the partial copy — no 150GB-bloat recurrence), excludes dangerous/generated dirs (`.git`/`target`/`node_modules`/`dev-data`/`workspaces`/`worktrees`/`dev-keys`/caches) + secret/key files (`.env*`/`*.key`/`*.pem`/`*.aic`/`bridge-token`/`dashboard-admin.json`/`*secret*`…), respects top-level `.gitignore` names, skips symlinks, and validates the project root (real dir, never a drive root). The Brief prompt never chooses the root or include paths (operator config only). Persisted in `brief_runs.workspace_context`/`_files`/`_bytes` (+ migration) and surfaced in `/v1/runs`, the new `run.workspace_config` capability → `GET /v1/spine/run-config` (Settings), the Active Runs Context column, and the Brief Run banner. A context/cap failure → `workspace_context_error` (Claim released, no run record). **Live-validated:** echo `empty` → only `BRIEF.md`; echo `copy_repo` of a tiny project → copied `hello.txt`+`notes.md` (files=2) while `.git`/`node_modules`/`.env` were **excluded**; a Claude `copy_repo` read-only run listed `BRIEF.md, hello.txt, notes.md`, modified nothing, and never saw the excluded entries; Settings `/v1/spine/run-config` reported the active mode + caps. **Honest limits / future:** `git_worktree`/`git_checkout` context is deferred (only `empty` + `copy_repo` ship); the `.gitignore` honoring is best-effort (top-level single-segment names, not full glob semantics) — the hardcoded excludes are the real safety net.
- Real Codex execution slice (parity with Claude): made Codex as real/safe/observable/honest as Claude. Investigated the live CLI (codex-cli 0.136.0): `codex exec` runs noninteractively, `--json` emits JSONL whose answer is the last `item.completed` `agent_message`, and `codex login status` reports auth. Command shape `codex exec --json --sandbox workspace-write --skip-git-repo-check -` (prompt on stdin, no shell strings); `RigOutputFormat::CodexJsonl` + `parse_codex_jsonl` give a clean summary (no raw JSONL) + error mapping; two-step readiness (`--version` + `codex login status`). **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** Founder on `codex`, `/v1/adapters` → `codex available — installed: codex-cli 0.136.0; logged in`; an `empty`-mode Brief ran async (running → **done** in 9s) with the clean summary `Relix Codex test passed` (no JSONL noise) in a scoped workspace; a `copy_repo`-mode Brief read the copied `app.py`/`README.md` (`.git`/`.env`/`node_modules` **excluded**) and **wrote `codex-summary.txt` confined to the scoped workspace** — the original project (files before=5/after=5) and the repo root (0 codex files) were **untouched**. The run also honestly surfaced a Codex-on-Windows quirk (shell sandbox couldn't spawn so `ls` failed, but the file-write tool worked) inside the summary. Tests: JSONL extraction (last agent_message), error-event mapping, none-without-events fallthrough, outcome mapping (clean answer / error failure), no-raw-JSON summary, the rig wiring (sandbox flags + auth probe). **Honest caveats:** on Windows, Codex's shell-command sandbox may not spawn (file-write tool still works) — surfaced, not hidden; auth is detected via `codex login status` text.
- Run transcript + cancellation slice (observability + control): click a run, see what it did, stop it. (1) **Transcript** — a capped, redacted `run_events` table (kind/source/message/payload_json) holding the run lifecycle (relix) + parsed adapter events (`claude_events` / `codex_events`, never raw JSONL) + a compact raw-adapter `output` event; per-run cap (400 → one `truncated` marker) + per-field byte clamp; the `Rig` trait gains an additive `run_transcript` (default no events) sharing `ProcessRig::execute`. (2) **Cancellation** — a global `CancelRegistry` (run_id → AtomicBool) polled by `ProcessRig`'s wait loop, which **kills the child**; `execute_ready` reports `cancelled` (not failed); `run.cancel` is truthful about whether a live process was signalled. (3) **Endpoints** — `GET /v1/runs/:id`, `GET /v1/runs/:id/events`, `POST /v1/runs/:id/cancel` (+ capabilities + policy); existing `/v1/runs` summary unchanged. (4) **Dashboard** — Active Runs rows expand to a chronological transcript + Cancel button (no redesign). **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** echo run → 5 lifecycle events; Claude run → `assistant_message`/`result`/`usage cost $…` (clean, framed by lifecycle); Codex run → `thread_started`/`turn_started`/`file_change`/`agent_message`/`turn_completed`; and a **real cancellation** — a Codex run was killed mid-flight (cut off at `turn_started`, `active:true`), reported `status:cancelled` with `cancel_requested` + `cancelled` transcript events, no repo-root writes, no 401/502. Tests: claude/codex event extraction, redaction+truncation bounds, CancelRegistry lifecycle, raw `run_transcript` output event, store event-cap + truncated marker, lifecycle transcript end-to-end, cancellation → `cancelled`. **Honest limits:** the registry is per-process, so `run.cancel` only kills a process running on THIS coordinator (a multi-node deploy would need to route the cancel) — reported via `active:false`; reasoning/internal items are intentionally not transcribed (noise reduction).
- Reviewable run result slice (artifacts + review): answer "what did the agent change, and do I accept it?". (1) **Artifacts** — `execute_ready` diffs a pre-flight BEFORE manifest against an AFTER scan of the scoped workspace into a `run_artifacts` table (metadata only — created/modified/deleted, path/size/hash/is_text; NO content in SQLite). The scan reuses the copy filters (no .git/target/node_modules/dev-data/secrets), skips symlinks, hashes only ≤1 MiB files, caps the count, NEVER scans the repo (inherit mode skipped), and surfaces `artifacts.scan_started`/`detected`/`scan_failed` in the transcript. (2) **Review** — a `done` run opens `pending_review`; `set_run_review` records accepted/rejected (done-only) + a transcript event. (3) **Endpoints** (tenant-scoped via `run_belongs_to_tenant`): `GET /v1/runs/:id/artifacts`, `GET …/artifacts/:aid/preview` (server-resolved path verified under the workspace, binary/large/missing refused, secret-redacted, 64 KiB cap), `POST /v1/runs/:id/review`. (4) **Dashboard** — the run expansion gains a Changes section (per-file preview) + a Review row (accept/reject + ✓/✕ marker). **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** an echo run recorded 0 artifacts + opened `pending_review` and accepted cleanly; a Codex "create a file" Brief detected `created result.txt (22 bytes)`, its preview returned the real content `artifact review works`, `artifacts.detected: 1 created` fired, and **the repo root was untouched** (the file landed only in the scoped workspace). Tests: created-file detection (BRIEF.md excluded), exclusion of .git/target/node_modules/dev-data/.env/*.key, created/modified/deleted diff, preview redaction + binary/truncation/traversal refusal, review done-only + invalid-decision reject, and tenant isolation. **Safe apply (SHIPPED):** applying an accepted run's changes back into the configured project root is implemented — `run.diff` (`GET /v1/runs/:id/diff`, a pure apply-plan preview) + `run.apply` (`POST /v1/runs/:id/apply`): whole-or-nothing, idempotent, conflict-checked against a persisted `baseline_hash`, path-safe (refuses absolute / `..` / drive / UNC / excluded paths + symlink traversal), and review-gated (only a `done` + `accepted` + scoped-workspace run; `inherit` / unreviewed / rejected refused; no `force`). The full refusal rules are in the safe-apply paragraph above. **End-to-end coverage:** the `run.diff` / `run.apply` capability bodies are extracted into `execute_run_diff` / `execute_run_apply` (the bridge routes call them verbatim), and an in-process integration test drives the WHOLE loop on a real file-writing adapter (a `cmd`/`sh` one-liner registered as a test Rig — no fake product adapter): a real `copy_repo` run modifies a copied file → `run.diff` previews the pending change while review-gated (`eligible=false`) → accept flips it `eligible=true` → `run.apply` writes the change into the configured project root AND review-to-dones the Brief (board `done`, the dependent Brief unblocks) → a second apply is a no-op (idempotent, 0 writes); a divergence written into the project root after the run is refused as a conflict that writes nothing and leaves the Brief in review. This is the deterministic equivalent of the live HTTP smoke (no paid/interactive CLI). **Honest limits:** change detection is hash/size-based (a same-content rewrite reads as unchanged); deleted files have no preview; `run.diff` returns a structured per-file apply plan (action / conflict / reason), not a unified text diff, because file CONTENT is never persisted — only the `baseline_hash` for conflict detection.
- Local dashboard admin recovery + authenticated smoke slice: unblock testing the real browser flow when the local admin password is forgotten. (1) **Reset path** — `relix-web-bridge reset-admin` (wrapped by `scripts/relix-dashboard-admin-reset.ps1` / `.sh`) rewrites `dashboard-admin.json` with a fresh **Argon2id** credential using the SAME storage as first-run setup. It resolves the admin file the same way the server does (`--admin-file` → `--config`-derived bridge-token dir → `~/.relix/dashboard-admin.json`), keeps the existing username unless `--username` is given, and generates + prints a strong password when `--password` is omitted (never prints/reads the old secret). **Security properties:** there is NO network/unauthenticated reset — it is a local CLI/filesystem operation requiring write access to the admin file; it does not weaken session auth, does not touch any other dev-data, and does not invalidate live sessions itself — a **bridge restart** applies the new credential AND drops the in-memory sessions (documented in the command's own output). (2) **Login UX** — the dashboard sign-in screen gains a collapsible "Forgot the local admin password?" hint pointing at the reset script (guidance only, no secrets, no remote-reset button). (3) **Tests** — reset changes the password (old fails / new works after reload), can set/keep the username, creates when absent, validates (empty username / short password refused), and stores only the Argon2id PHC hash (never plaintext). **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** reset to a known temp credential → booted the mesh → **logged in** (`/v1/auth/login` + `/v1/auth/me`) → company already initialized → created a Brief → assigned the Founder (rig set to echo) → ran it (running → **done**, trigger `manual`, `pending_review`) → `/v1/runs/:id/events` returned the 7-event transcript (the deep-link target) → `/v1/runs/:id/diff` reported not-yet-eligible with `no artifacts — nothing to apply` → **accepted** the review → post-accept diff `eligible=true`; every authenticated endpoint returned 2xx (no 401/502). The original admin credential was backed up and **restored** afterward, the mesh torn down, and no generated dev-data/smoke files are tracked. **Honest caveats:** the reset requires a bridge restart to take effect (sessions are in-memory, so a restart is the revocation); a custom `[bridge] token_path` needs `--config`/`--admin-file` so the reset targets the right file.
- Operator maintenance + cleanup slice (production hygiene): keep Relix from silently filling disk + give operators a storage view. (1) **Summary** — `maintenance.summary` → `GET /v1/maintenance/summary`: a bounded, symlink-skipping scan of the run-workspace root (count / bytes / oldest / newest, graceful on a missing root, capped dir + file budget so a huge tree can't stall) joined with cheap `brief_runs`/`run_events`/`run_artifacts` counts + review/apply breakdown, plus actionable warnings (large storage, too many workspaces, unsafe `inherit`, missing project root). (2) **Prune** — `maintenance.prune` → `POST /v1/maintenance/prune`: **dry-run by default**; a real delete is explicit (`dry_run:false`). Rules: never deletes a `running` run's workspace, keeps the newest `keep_latest` + anything newer than `older_than_days`, only deletes DIRECT children of the validated workspace root (refuses a shallow / filesystem root), never follows symlinks; optional conservative DB-log prune removes only `run_events`/`run_artifacts` rows of pruned runs, **never** the `brief_runs` ledger row. (3) **Dashboard** — Settings gains a *Maintenance & storage* panel (counts + warnings + dry-run preview listing exactly what would be deleted + an Execute action gated behind typing `DELETE`); the Command Center surfaces storage warnings. (4) **Backup** — `scripts/relix-local-backup.ps1`/`.sh`: a local-only zip/tar of DBs + configs, excluding build output / `.git` / run workspaces / logs / secrets by default. **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** logged in via the reset path, `GET /v1/maintenance/summary` returned root + 3 workspaces / 897 B + 3 runs / 33 events; a 10-year-backdated disposable workspace was created under the root, a `dry_run` prune (`older_than_days=3000`) listed **only** that disposable (deleted 0, kept the 2 real recent workspaces), and the real prune removed exactly it (`deleted_workspaces=1`, real workspaces untouched, post-count unchanged) — no user data harmed, mesh torn down, admin restored. Tests: scan handles a missing root / skips loose files / counts bytes; prune dry-run deletes nothing, refuses a shallow root, keeps running + recent and deletes only old, and `keep_latest` protects the newest even when old. **Honest limits:** maintenance is operator-global (single bridge admin), not tenant-scoped; log-row pruning targets only runs whose workspace is eligible; the audit is a tracing log line (a durable maintenance table is future work). See `docs/operations.md`.
- Scheduled cleanup + durable maintenance audit slice (operations hardening): make cleanup observable + automatable, not just manual. (1) **Durable audit** — a bounded `maintenance_audit` table (last 500 rows; clamped note/payload; no secrets) + store helpers; a shared `execute_prune` engine records a row for EVERY prune attempt (dry-run / refusal / failure / success) with the trigger (`manual` / `scheduled`), counts, status, and a compact payload. `maintenance.prune` routes through it; new `maintenance.audit` → `GET /v1/maintenance/audit?limit=N` (newest-first, auth-gated). (2) **Scheduled cleanup** — `RELIX_MAINTENANCE_AUTOPRUNE_*` config (off by default; **dry-run by default even when enabled**); `resolve_autoprune_config` + `autoprune_tick` run the same safe engine on an opt-in controller timer loop (skips the boot tick). (3) **Summary + dashboard** — `maintenance.summary` now reports the autoprune config + the last prune and warns on REAL-DELETE scheduled mode / a failed-or-refused last cleanup; the *Maintenance & storage* panel shows scheduled-cleanup policy/status + a Cleanup-history table; the Command Center surfaces the new warnings. (4) **Backup/restore** — the backup scripts print local restore guidance (mesh-down → expand/extract → mesh-up; never auto-restores), add `-ListContents`/`--list-contents`, and document what's excluded by default. **Live-validated end to end on this machine:** logged in via the reset path, `GET /v1/maintenance/audit` was empty, a dry-run prune recorded a `manual` dry-run audit row (deleted 0), a backdated disposable workspace was real-deleted (audit row `status=ok`, `deleted_workspaces=1`), and `summary.last_prune` reflected it — real workspaces untouched, mesh torn down, admin restored, no tracked junk. Tests: audit row for dry-run / real / refused prune; audit newest-first; autoprune config defaults disabled + dry-run; tick disabled → None + no audit; real-delete removes only eligible. **Honest limits:** maintenance stays operator-global (not tenant-scoped); only prune attempts are audited (not summary reads); log-row pruning still targets only runs whose workspace is eligible. See `docs/operations.md`.
- Mandate orchestration dashboard slice (goal → Brief tree, UI over the existing engine): surface the already-tested `mandate.orchestrate` backend so an operator can turn a high-level goal into work, without duplicating it. **Frontend-only** over existing endpoints (`POST/GET /v1/spine/mandates`, `…/:id/briefs`, `…/:id/orchestrate` body `{mode,max_briefs,dry_run}`, `…/:id/orchestration/latest`). (1) **Mandates page** (nav + route) — create a Mandate (title + spec), then orchestrate with a mode (`plan_only` / `create_briefs` / `assign_ready`), `max_briefs`, and a dry-run preview; renders the latest orchestration result (created / existing / assigned / skipped / blockers / next-actions) + per-Mandate Brief progress (column counts + a done bar). Empty state: "Create a Mandate to turn a big goal into Briefs." (2) **Briefs board** — cards show a `◎ <mandate>` chip when they belong to a Mandate + a filter-by-Mandate dropdown. (3) **Command Center** — a no-Mandates next-action prompt + an Active-mandates card. (4) **Policy fix** — the mesh-up generators were missing `chat-users` allow rules for `mandate.orchestration.latest` / `.list` / `team_plan.latest`, so the dashboard's latest-plan read was default-denied; added them. **Live-validated on this machine:** created a Mandate, listed it, ran a dry-run (`status=blocked`, **created 0**, blockers `strategy_not_approved` + `no_team_plan` surfaced) and a real `create_briefs` (same gate, honest blockers + next-actions), read `mandate.orchestration.latest` (denied → **allowed** after the policy fix), and `team_readiness`. **Honest limits:** actual Brief materialization is governance-gated (strategy approval + a team plan must exist first — Phase 4 flow); the dashboard surfaces those blockers clearly but doesn't drive the approval flow yet; orchestration decomposition is the existing rule-based role-track engine, not LLM planning.
- Mandate governance workflow dashboard slice (blocked → ready → Briefs): make the Mandates page guide an operator through the existing governance gates instead of just reporting blockers — WITHOUT bypassing them. (1) **Strategy capabilities (new, thin)** — `mandate.strategy.status` / `.propose` / `.approve` / `.reject` over the already-tenant-guarded `SpineStore` strategy methods + bridge `GET /v1/spine/mandates/:id/strategy` and `POST .../strategy/{propose,approve,reject}` (propose body `{doc?}`, deterministic default if omitted) + precise `chat-users` policy allow-rules (no wildcard). Team-plan (`mandate.team_plan` POST), `team_plan.latest`, `team_readiness`, and clearances (`coord.approval.pending` / `.decide` via `/v1/spine/clearances`) already existed and are reused — no duplication. (2) **Guided Mandate workflow UI** — the selected-Mandate panel is now a numbered workflow with a "Next:" banner: **Strategy** (status + propose/approve/reject, default doc from the title), **Team & readiness** (Plan team once strategy approved; live readiness — active / pending hires / pending clearances / missing / blocked roles + `next_action`), **Pending clearances** (approve/reject via the existing endpoint, shown only when present, reloads readiness after a decision), **Decompose** (blocker-aware Create Briefs / Create + assign — disabled-with-reason until `readiness=ready` — + dry-run preview + the latest orchestration result/blockers), and Brief progress with a board link. Nothing fakes readiness; errors + blockers surface honestly. **Live-validated on this machine:** created a Mandate, `propose` → `proposed`, `approve` → `approved=true`, `team_plan` → `planned`, readiness `staffing` (honest `next_action`), 0 pending clearances; orchestration moved from **fully-blocked (created 0** with `strategy_not_approved`+`no_team_plan`) **to created 1 Brief** after the strategy was approved + the team planned — no policy-denied errors (new strategy rules active). Tests: `propose→approve` flips `strategy_approved`; `reject` blocks it; propose requires a doc + mandate id; tenant isolation on propose. **Honest limits:** deeper role-track Briefs still require the team plan to identify + staff roles (hire / clearance), so a bare Mandate with only a Founder yields a single parent Brief and `readiness=staffing` — the UI shows exactly why + the next action; strategy/team are governance state, not LLM planning.
- Macro RPC-to-tools parse layer; Hermes stdio placeholder; Keeper in-memory scaffold.
- Backend execution-reliability slice (make the run spine survive restarts + observable, no UI redesign): six backend hardenings on the existing unified `prepare_claimed_run` → `execute_ready` pipeline. (1) **Usage/cost capture (TG6)** — `RunUsage` is parsed from the adapter's structured output (`parse_claude_usage` off the terminal Claude `result` event: input/output/cache-read tokens, `total_cost_usd`→`cost_micros`, model, `session_id`; `parse_codex_usage` off Codex `turn.completed.usage` + `thread.started` thread-id, no cost) and persisted on additive `brief_runs` columns (`provider`/`model`/`input_tokens`/`output_tokens`/`cached_input_tokens`/`cost_micros`/`session_id`, surfaced on `RunRecord`/`GET /v1/runs`); **null when the adapter (echo/raw) emits nothing — never faked**, and malformed JSON lines are skipped without panicking. (2) **Persistent adapter runtime state (TG2)** — a new `agent_runtime_state` table keyed `(tenant_id, agent_id, rig, brief_key)` stores the resumable `session_id`, latest provider/model, accumulated token/cost totals, `last_run_id`/`last_status`/`last_error`, an opaque `runtime_state` JSON blob, and timestamps; `record_run_runtime_state` UPSERTs after every run (latest-wins for session/status, accumulates usage, clears `last_error` on success), with `get`/`list`/`list_for_tenant(limit)`/`reset(agent)`/`reset(agent+brief)`. Capabilities `rig.runtime_state.get` / `.list` / `.reset` (tenant-scoped) + bridge `GET /v1/runs/runtime-state?agent_id=…`, `GET /v1/runs/runtime-state/list[?limit=N]` (the global Guild-wide session list, `{rows:[...]}`, newest first, clamped to 200), and `POST /v1/runs/runtime-state/reset`. (3) **Boot recovery (TG3; recovery state hardened to `interrupted` in the Execution Reliability Pack)** — `recover_stale_runs(live, min_age_secs)` reconciles any `brief_runs` row left `running` after a crash/restart whose `run_id` has no live in-process handle (the `CancelRegistry` is empty on a fresh boot, so all leftover rows are stale): mark terminal **`interrupted`** (honest; not `failed`) with the reason "Run interrupted: the executing process is gone …", append a `recovered` transcript event + a `brief.run_recovered` Chronicle note, and release the Brief Claim **only if it still points to that run** — live + terminal runs untouched; wired into coordinator startup (`min_age_secs = 0`) and an opt-in periodic heartbeat sweep (lease + grace). See the Execution Reliability Pack bullet for the full recovery semantics. (4) **Cancel/timeout hardening (TG4)** — confirmed the existing `ProcessRig` cancel/timeout already kills the child without a pipe-hang (detached reader threads, bounded grace) and reports an honest non-success outcome (cancel → non-retryable `Failed`, timeout → retryable `Failed`, **never `Done`**); added tests for idempotent double-cancel and a genuine mid-flight cancel (kill + non-success + no hang). (5) **Execution event stream (TG5)** — `GET /v1/runs/events/stream`, a tenant-scoped SSE feed of execution transitions. A new `recent_run_events` coord query JOINs `task_events`→`tasks` (so a Guild only tails its own Briefs) and filters to `RUN_STREAM_EVENT_TYPES`; the bridge handler re-applies the resolved tenant on every poll (the SSE body is polled outside the auth middleware's task-local scope) and re-labels chronicle types to normalized SSE event names (`run_started`/`run_finished`/`run_cancel_requested`/`brief_moved`/`review_changed`/`apply_changed`), with keep-alive pings. The cancel/review/apply transitions now also emit `brief.run_cancel_requested`/`brief.run_reviewed`/`brief.run_applied` Chronicle events so they surface on the stream. (6) **Chokepoint audit (TG7)** — see the refined divergence note below. Tests: usage parse (claude/codex/malformed/empty), runtime-state upsert+accumulate / unknown-run no-op / reset scoping, stale-run recovery (releases claim + records events, leaves live/terminal alone, idempotent), cancel idempotency + mid-flight kill, run-events tenant isolation + type filter + cursor, SSE event-name mapping. **Honest limits:** allowance/cost is captured on the ledger + runtime state but the dispatch-time Allowance gate still reads the *metrics* ledger (now summed over the current UTC calendar month — see the Allowance calendar-month windowing slice below), not these per-run columns (no new spend-enforcement wiring); the run-events stream is a 750ms poll over the chronicle (not push), and fine-grained per-transcript `run_event` frames remain on the existing per-run `/v1/runs/:id/events` endpoint (now with an optional `?since=<event_id>` incremental cursor that the dashboard transcript polls to live-tail an in-flight run cheaply — see the Run transcript renderer note below), not the global execution stream.
- **Full Brief detail API (IMPLEMENTED).** `brief.detail` → `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id` returns the complete Brief product object in one tenant-scoped read. Sections returned: `title`; `fields` (task_id, human_ref, board_status, priority, assignee_agent_id, reviewer_agent_id, mandate_id, campaign_id); `subbriefs` (child Briefs), `parents`, `snags` (blockers), `blocking` (reverse) — **each relation JOIN-filtered to the Brief's own Guild** so a cross-tenant parent/child/blocker id can never leak; `dossiers`; `labels`; `pinned`; `due_at`; `blocked`; `claim` (current lease holder + expiry, or null); `wakeup_count`; `chronicle` (total event count + the newest 5 entries); and **`latest_run`** (the Brief's most recent Shift summary — see below). **Tenant isolation:** a missing OR cross-Guild id reads as not-found (no existence leak); the relation graph is filtered via `list_brief_edges_for_tenant` / `list_*_for_tenant`; dossiers/wakeups/chronicle/runs belong to the Brief's own Task row (`brief_runs.brief_id == task_id`), gated by the existence+tenant check. Tests: full-view assembly (incl. title/claim/wakeup_count/chronicle), latest-run surfacing (null→first run→newest run, bounded summary, cross-tenant), cross-tenant relationship filtering, cross-tenant + missing not-found. The React **Brief detail panel** (opened from a card on the Briefs board) consumes this endpoint directly (replacing the `…/thread` composite) and renders title, fields, claim, relations summary, labels, due, the **Latest Shift** block, the Chronicle tail, and a comment box. **Not embedded (by design, available on dedicated routes):** the full paginated Chronicle timeline (`…/events`), the live thread composite (`…/thread`), the full wakeup ledger (`…/wakeups`), and the full per-Brief Shift history (`…/runs`); Briefs carry no separate free-form `body` field today — the title + Dossiers + comment Chronicle are the description surface.
- **Brief run lifecycle in the detail (`latest_run`, IMPLEMENTED).** The Brief detail embeds a bounded summary of the Brief's most recent Shift (run from the `brief_runs` ledger) so the operator sees execution state without a second fetch. Fields: `run_id`, `rig` (adapter), `status` (`running` while in flight, then terminal `done` / `failed` / `continued` / `cancelled`), `trigger` (`manual` / `heartbeat` / `scheduled`), `started_at` / `finished_at` / `duration_secs`, a **bounded** `summary` (already secret-redacted, capped to a 280-char snippet — no huge logs embedded), `review` (`pending_review` / `accepted` / `rejected`), `apply_status`, `artifact_count` (changed files), and `total_runs` (Shift count on the Brief); `null` when the Brief has never run. Store: `latest_run_for_brief` (index-backed `LIMIT 1` on `brief_runs_by_brief`) + `run_count_for_brief` + `run_artifact_count`. The dashboard panel shows the status badge, adapter, trigger, start/finish/duration, review/apply, changed-file count, the summary snippet, and an **"Open in Runs →"** deep-link (`/runs?run=<id>`); the full per-Brief history stays on `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/runs`.
- **Durable refused Shift attempts (IMPLEMENTED).** A MANUAL run (`brief.run` / `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/run`) that is refused before any adapter spawns now persists a durable `brief_runs` row with **`status = "refused"`** + a machine **`refusal_reason`** (`unassigned` / `no_adapter` / `adapter_unavailable` / `workspace_error` / `workspace_context_error`), a bounded redacted `summary`, `trigger = "manual"`, and `finished_at == started_at` (instant) — so the Brief detail and run history can later answer "why didn't this run?". A `brief.run_refused` Chronicle event (reason + Rig, redaction-safe) is appended. `RunRecord` and `LatestRun` gained a `refusal_reason` field; refused rows flow through `latest_run`, the per-Brief `…/runs` history, and `/v1/runs`. **Decisions:** (1) **`already_running` is NOT persisted** — a run is already in flight, so a refused row on a double-click would be pure noise; the live run is the answer. (2) **`not_found` is NOT persisted** — there's no Brief to attach to. (3) **Tenant isolation:** the refusal row is written only when the Brief belongs to the caller's Guild (`record_manual_refusal_for_tenant` gates on `task_in_tenant`), so a cross-Guild or missing Brief never gets a row — a refusal can't leak a Brief's existence. Store: `record_manual_refusal_for_tenant` + `refusal_is_durable`; additive `brief_runs.refusal_reason` column/migration. Dashboard: the Latest Shift block + Runs page render the `refused` status and the reason. **`queued` was NOT implemented** — the manual path attempts the claim/spawn immediately (a run is created directly at `running`), so there is no honest queue state to model in this slice; inventing a fake `queued` was explicitly avoided. (Autonomous refusals are now ALSO durable — see the Execution Reliability Pack bullet below.)
- **Execution Reliability Pack — durable autonomous refusals, stale-run recovery, live updates (IMPLEMENTED).**
  - **Durable autonomous/heartbeat refusals.** The four heartbeat dispatch refusal sites in `dispatch_batch_with_policy` now ALSO persist a durable `brief_runs` row (`status = "refused"`, `trigger = "heartbeat"`, machine `refusal_reason`, bounded redacted `summary`, `finished_at == started_at`) in addition to their existing board-park / Claim-release / wakeup-finish behavior: the **Allowance hard-stop** → `over_allowance` (newly added to `refusal_is_durable`), **no Rig** → `no_adapter`, **adapter unavailable** → `adapter_unavailable`, and **workspace-prep failure** → `workspace_error` / `workspace_context_error`. The shared writer `record_refused_run(brief, agent, rig, reason, summary, trigger)` is guarded by `WHERE EXISTS (tasks)` so a vanished/missing Brief never gets a row (no existence leak); `record_manual_refusal_for_tenant` now delegates to it after the tenant gate. A `brief.run_refused` Chronicle note is appended (same as manual). So `latest_run`, the per-Brief `…/runs`, and `/v1/runs` now explain WHY an autonomous run didn't happen — not just a chronicle line. (The pre-existing `brief.dispatch_failed`/`brief.budget_refused` chronicle + `blocked` park are unchanged.)
  - **Stale running-run recovery → `interrupted`.** `recover_stale_runs(live, min_age_secs)` now marks a stale `running` Shift terminal **`interrupted`** (honest — matches the task-level `recover_interrupted` convention; NOT `failed`, which means the run actually ran and errored). It takes an **age threshold**: boot recovery passes `0` (every leftover `running` row is stale — the in-memory `CancelRegistry` is empty after a restart), while a **periodic heartbeat sweep** passes the lease + grace and uses `CancelRegistry::live_ids()` so a genuinely in-flight, long-running Shift (registered live, or younger than the threshold) is never mistaken for stale. The Brief Claim is released **only when it still points to that run** (`release_claim_for_run`), so a newer run that already re-claimed the Brief is left alone. A `recovered` transcript event + a `brief.run_recovered` Chronicle note are recorded; the run surfaces in `latest_run` as `interrupted`. Tests: stale → interrupted (+ claim released + events), age threshold skips young runs, conditional claim release, live/terminal runs untouched, idempotent.
  - **Live dashboard run updates (SSE).** `brief.run_refused` is now forwarded on the `/v1/runs/events/stream` execution feed (mapped to `run_finished`). The React dashboard subscribes once via `subscribeRunEvents` (cookie-authed, same-origin `EventSource`, capped-backoff reconnect, honest connection state): the **Runs page** debounce-refreshes the runs list + the open run's transcript on any execution transition and shows a **live-status chip** (connecting / live / reconnecting / unavailable); the **Brief detail** panel refreshes `latest_run` + Chronicle when an event for that Brief arrives. The new terminal states `interrupted` + `refused` render with a blocked-tone badge on the Runs table, Brief detail Latest Shift, Briefs cards, and Overview; Runs gains an `interrupted` filter. The per-run transcript / artifacts / review / apply depth (scope D) was already complete from the prior execution-reliability slice and now also covers these rows.
  - **Remaining execution gaps.** (1) The autonomous refusal still ALSO parks the Brief `blocked` + chronicles `brief.dispatch_failed`/`brief.budget_refused` (the refused Shift is additive, not a replacement). (2) Still **no `queued` state** — runs are created directly at `running`; there is no pre-claim queue to model honestly. (3) **`already_running` / `not_found` are still NOT persisted** (noise / no Brief). (4) The live feed is a 750 ms chronicle **poll** re-broadcast as SSE, not a true push, and the dashboard refresh is a debounced re-fetch (not a per-row patch). (5) The periodic stale-run sweep only runs when `RELIX_HEARTBEAT_ENABLED` is on; boot recovery always runs.
- **Workspace Review/Apply Pack — inspect → diff → apply/discard → cleanup (IMPLEMENTED).** Implementation map for the run-workspace product loop:
  - **Already shipped (this slice did NOT rebuild):** scoped per-run workspaces (`<root>/<run_id>`, `RELIX_RUN_WORKSPACE_ROOT`) with context modes **`empty`** (default — only `BRIEF.md`) and **`copy_repo`** (capped/filtered project snapshot; `git_worktree`/`git_checkout` still deferred), persisted on `brief_runs.workspace`/`workspace_context`/`_files`/`_bytes`; the **`run_artifacts`** changed-file ledger (created/modified/deleted + size/hash/`baseline_hash`, metadata-only, symlink-skipping, hash-capped); a **safe text preview** (`GET /v1/runs/:id/artifacts/:aid/preview` — canonicalize-under-workspace, binary/large refused, secret-redacted, 64 KiB cap); **safe apply** (`run.diff` PLAN + `run.apply` — per-file action/conflict, baseline-hash conflict detection, no-traversal/no-symlink, refuse-the-whole-apply-if-anything-unsafe, idempotent, durable `apply_status`; **and a clean apply is the operator's review-to-done — it advances the run's Brief from `in_review` to `done` (company-model §12.5B/§12.6), so dependents unblock without a manual `brief.move done`**); **review** (`pending_review`/`accepted`/`rejected`); and the **storage maintenance** surface (`maintenance.summary` workspace usage + warnings, `maintenance.prune` dry-run-first safe prune that never deletes a `running` workspace, `maintenance.audit`, scheduled autoprune) with a dashboard MaintenancePanel.
  - **Closed in this slice:** (1) a **per-file unified diff** — `read_artifact_diff` + `run.artifact_diff` → `GET /v1/runs/:id/artifacts/:aid/diff`. The "after" side is the run's workspace output (same canonicalize-under-workspace guard as preview, secret-redacted); the "before" side is the LIVE project-root file **only when it still hashes to the run's recorded `baseline_hash`**, else an honest `available:false` ("diff unavailable; preview instead"). `created` diffs against empty, `deleted` against empty; binary / traversal / excluded paths / moved baseline never dump content; both sides byte-bounded BEFORE diffing and the output is capped + redacted. (2) an explicit **discard** — `discard_run` + `run.discard` → `POST /v1/runs/:id/discard`: marks a TERMINAL run `apply_status = "discarded"` (and rejects a `done` run's review so it can never be applied), records a `discarded` transcript event + a `brief.run_discarded` Chronicle note (forwarded on the SSE feed as `apply_changed`), and leaves the scoped workspace for the normal prune — **no immediate delete**; refuses a still-`running` run. (3) **Dashboard Runs loop:** per-file `diff` button (honest "unavailable → preview" fallback), a `Discard` button on terminal non-applied runs, the `discarded` apply badge, and a **storage-warning banner** surfacing the `maintenance.summary` workspace warnings (disk/count) with a link to the cleanup panel.
  - **Tenant/auth safety:** every run-scoped read/write (`run.artifacts`/`artifact_preview`/`artifact_diff`/`review`/`diff`/`apply`/`discard`) is gated by `run_belongs_to_tenant` — another Guild's run reads as not-found (no existence leak). Artifact paths are server-resolved from the stored row (never user-supplied); preview/diff/apply re-validate against traversal, symlinks, and the excluded-dir/secret-file filter.
  - **Remaining workspace/review gaps.** (1) Discard does NOT delete the workspace synchronously — disk is reclaimed only by the prune/autoprune (by design, but a discarded workspace lingers until then). (2) The unified diff needs the live project-root baseline to still match `baseline_hash`; for `empty`-context runs (no project copy) a `modified`/`deleted` baseline is usually unavailable → preview only. (3) Diff/preview are byte-capped (64 KiB) — a very large changed file is truncated, not paged. (4) No multi-file "review all then apply" batch UI; apply is still whole-run all-or-nothing (intentional). (5) `git_worktree`/`git_checkout` workspace context remains deferred.
- **Prime / Company Flow Pack — Founder → Prime → Crew → Briefs as a governed company (IMPLEMENTED).** Implementation map for the company-model product loop:
  - **Already shipped (this slice did NOT rebuild):** the full governance backend — `company.status` / `company.bootstrap_founder` (Founder first-run), `agent.operatives` (Crew roster, infra-console-excluded), `agent.request_hire` / `agent.request_hire_for_mandate` (gated hires), the Mandate **strategy gate** (`mandate.strategy.propose`/`approve`/`reject`/`status`), `mandate.team_plan` (+ `.latest`), `mandate.team_readiness` (`compute_readiness`: plan + `active_agents` / `pending_hires` / `pending_clearances` / `missing_roles` / `blocked_roles` + a `readiness` state ∈ `ready`/`staffing`/`awaiting_clearance`/`not_planned` + `next_action`), `mandate.orchestrate` (`plan_only` / `create_briefs` / `assign_ready`, idempotent via source markers, persisted `OrchestrationRun`) + `.latest`/`.list`, and spawn-**Clearances** (`coord.approval.pending` list + `coord.approval.decide` which activates/disables the linked pending hire). The React **Mandates** page already drove the whole workflow (strategy propose→approve, plan team, readiness counts, clearance approve/reject, orchestrate dry-run + create, Brief progress) and the **Crew** (Agents) page already had the Founder card, per-Operative Keys, Guild Allowance, adapter/readiness, and workload.
  - **Closed in this slice:** (1) `company.status` (`GET /v1/spine/company`) was a bare head-count; **extended** (no new route) with **`prime`** (the role-`prime` Operative, the Founder's planning lead, or null) and **`crew`** = `{ total, active, pending, by_status, by_role }` — a real company shape, tenant-scoped via `find_founder` / `list_operatives_for_tenant`. (2) **Crew page:** a distinct **Prime** card when a role-`prime` Operative exists, else an honest **"Prime — planning surface"** card (NOT a "no Prime yet → hire one" prompt — see the Prime-naming note below), **pending hires** broken into their own section (separate from active Operatives), and a **Reports-to** column resolving each Operative's boss to a name. (3) **Overview Command Center:** the Company card shows the **Prime** + a pending-hire badge. (4) **Mandates page:** the readiness step now lists **who is on the team** (active-crew name·role chips), not just a count.
  - **Tenant/auth safety:** company.status + the roster are read through the existing tenant-scoped agent store, so a different Guild sees an empty company (no Founder/Prime existence leak); the Mandate strategy/team/orchestrate/clearance handlers were already tenant-scoped (`ctx.tenant_id_or_default()`). Tests: company.status surfaces Prime + crew by_role/by_status after hiring; tenant isolation (a non-owning Guild sees `initialized:false` / `prime:null` / `total:0`).
  - **Prime-naming ambiguity (honest divergence).** "Prime" is **overloaded** across the docs and this is unresolved. `relix-lexicon.md` (the "apex AI agent | CEO | Prime | role `prime`" row) defines Prime as a *rostered Operative role*, yet `relix-company-model.md` uses "Prime" primarily for the **planning/orchestration loop** (`prime.propose`/`approve`/`start`, §12.5) that the **Founder/operator drives** — and **no bootstrap path creates a `prime`-role Operative**: `ensure_founder` makes only the Founder, and the §12.6 starter crew is **Engineer + Designer**. So on every real fresh company `company.status.prime` is `null` even though the Prime *function* is fully alive (the loop reads the roster and files role-track hires — never a `prime` role). The backend still **supports** a `prime`-role Operative (`handle_company_status` resolves it) — it is simply never auto-created. **UI stance (this slice):** the Crew page no longer frames the empty state as a missing hire ("No Prime yet → hire one"); it presents Prime as the **planning surface the Founder operates from Chat**, notes a dedicated Prime Operative is optional and not part of the starter crew, and keeps the rich Prime *Operative* card for when one is genuinely hired. The roster strip's leadership tier shows "Founder + Prime" only when a Prime Operative exists, else "Founder (leadership)". **Open doc question:** reconcile the lexicon (Prime = role) with the company model (Prime = the loop) — either bless a first-class Prime Operative in a bootstrap path, or demote `role prime` in the lexicon to an optional standing planning lead. No code change should silently pick one until the docs decide.
  - **What is still rule-based vs autonomous.** The Prime flow is **deterministic/rule-based**, not LLM-driven: `mandate.team_plan` derives roles from the strategy doc by rules, `compute_readiness` is a pure state machine, and `mandate.orchestrate` decomposes a Mandate into role-track + per-subject Briefs by **templated titles** (`role_track_title` / `subject_exec_title`), not by a planning model. A human operator still drives every gate (propose/approve strategy, greenlight Clearances, choose the orchestration mode). The autonomous heartbeat only **executes** assigned Briefs; it does not plan teams or author strategy.
  - **Remaining company-model gaps (what still blocks Paperclip-level feel).** (1) No **LLM Prime** — strategy + team plan + Brief decomposition are rule/template-based, so a Mandate becomes generic role-track Briefs, not a model-authored project plan. (2) **Operator-in-the-loop at every gate** — there is no "auto-pilot" that proposes+approves+staffs+orchestrates a Mandate end-to-end. (3) **Hire is request→approve only** — no model-driven "who to hire" suggestion. (4) **CLOSED** — the company summary was the **agent/identity dimension** only, with mandate/clearance/brief counts composed dashboard-side; `company.status` now folds in a read-only, tenant-scoped **`operations`** object (see the Operations-summary note below), so the Overview reads as one coherent snapshot. (5) No org-graph visual beyond the shallow reports-to list.
  - **Company operations summary (IMPLEMENTED — read-only, additive).** `company.status` (`GET /v1/spine/company`) now carries an additive **`operations`** object alongside the unchanged initialized/founder/prime/crew fields — closing gap (4) above. Shape: `briefs` (`total` + `by_board` board buckets + `in_review` / `ready_to_start` / `unassigned` / `blocked` / `stale`), `runs` (a bounded recent `window` of 200 classified into `running` / `failed_or_refused` / `pending_review`), `approvals` (`pending_clearances` / `pending_hires`), and `mandates` (`total` + `by_status` + `strategy_proposed`). It is computed in `handle_company_status_with_ops` (the live registration wires the spine + task stores; an agent-only fallback `handle_company_status` omits `operations` when the spine is absent) from the **same existing tenant-scoped store helpers the Action Center uses** (`board_summary_for_tenant`, `list_ready/unassigned/blocked/stale_briefs_for_tenant`, `list_runs_for_tenant`, `list_pending_approvals_for_tenant`, `list_mandates` + `strategy_status`) — so the snapshot and the Action Center can never disagree and nothing is fabricated. **No new authority, route, or policy.** Best-effort: a transient sub-read degrades that bucket to `0`, never failing the core status read. The bounded Brief/run/strategy lists (≤ 50 / 200) are a *glance* summary, not an audit (they match what the Action Center surfaces). **Tenant-safe by construction** — every read is scoped to `ctx.tenant_id_or_default()`, so another Guild's Briefs/runs/approvals/mandates never count. Tests: the summary reports the seeded company's Brief/hire/Mandate counts; a non-owning Guild's summary is all zeros (tenant isolation); an empty company returns calm zeros/empty maps. The Overview renders it as a flat **Operations snapshot** card in the cockpit (work-in-flight / needs-attention / governance glance groups, each a deep link), leaving the Action Center + Company operating status card intact. *Still open from this gap line:* (5) the org-graph visual; and the deeper company-model gaps (no LLM Prime / no autopilot / no provider quota polling) are unchanged.
- **Prime Assistant Pack — governed "describe what you want → plan" (IMPLEMENTED).** The product-loop entry point: a user describes a goal and Prime returns a structured, GOVERNED plan that creates nothing until explicitly approved. Capabilities (tenant-scoped, registered with the agent + spine + task stores):
  - **`prime.propose`** → `POST /v1/spine/prime/propose` `{message}` — interprets the request into a structured plan: `intent` (build/fix/research/generic), a proposed Mandate (`mandate_title` + `mandate_brief`), the crew `roles` it needs, a `crew` array (each role marked `have`/missing with the matched active Operative), suggested `hires` for any missing role, a `briefs` breakdown (one role-track per role + an integration Brief depending on all tracks, each with `depends_on` keys), `risks`, and `next_actions`. **READ-ONLY:** it writes only the proposal record — no Mandate, Brief, or Operative. The message is **secret-redacted** (`rig::redact_secrets`) before it is interpreted or persisted. Returns `{proposal_id, status:"proposed", proposal}`.
  - **`prime.approve`** → `POST /v1/spine/prime/approve` `{proposal_id}` — the ONLY path that materializes a proposal (from the PERSISTED plan, never client input). Creates the **Mandate**, the **Briefs** (idempotent per-key source markers `prime:<proposal_id>:<key>`) + their **blocked-on dependency edges** (`add_snag`), **assigns** each track to an EXISTING eligible active Operative whose role family matches (`set_brief_field` assignee) — never a fake agent — and files a **`pending` hire request** (`request_hire`, status `pending` — needs a separate Clearance / `approve_hire` to activate) for each missing role. It **NEVER** runs an adapter, applies a workspace, reviews/discards artifacts, or changes budget. Records the approval on the proposal row + a **Team Plan** + an **Orchestration run** (the existing Mandate-history surfaces) + a `prime.brief_created` Chronicle event on each created Brief. **Idempotent:** a re-approve returns the existing Mandate (`already_approved:true`).
  - **`prime.proposals`** / **`prime.proposal`** → `GET /v1/spine/prime/proposals[?limit]` / `…/:id` — the proposal history / one proposal (tenant-scoped — a cross-Guild proposal reads as not-found).
  - **Storage:** a new tenant-scoped `prime_proposals` table (SpineStore: `record_prime_proposal` / `get_prime_proposal` / `mark_prime_proposal_approved` / `list_prime_proposals`) — the durable audit of *what Prime suggested → what was approved → what objects were created*; no Mandate FK (the Mandate doesn't exist until approval).
  - **Governance (no hidden mutations):** the FIRST response is always a proposal (creates nothing). The risky actions stay behind their existing gates — a suggested hire is a `pending` (inert) Operative needing a Clearance; nothing runs an adapter / applies a workspace / changes budget automatically. The dashboard **Chat** page renders the proposal as a card (intent, Mandate, crew filled-vs-missing, Brief breakdown, risks, next actions) with an explicit **"Approve & create"** button + a banner that hires file pending Clearances and nothing runs automatically; on approve a result card links to Mandates + the board. **Overview** gains a **"Start work — Plan with Prime →"** entry point.
  - **LLM behavior (honest).** No language model is wired into a coordinator capability — the AI node is a separate mesh peer, not synchronously callable from a handler — so the plan is **deterministic/rule-based** and says so via `ai_used:false` + an `ai_status` string; it is NEVER silently presented as model output. The generator (`agent/prime.rs::generate_proposal`) is a PURE, unit-tested function with a clean seam where a model can later replace the interpretation step while reusing the same governed `prime.approve` execution path. **AI-unavailable is honest, not silent.**
  - **The exact workflow:** user types a request in Chat → `prime.propose` returns a plan (nothing created) → operator reviews the card → clicks **Approve & create** → `prime.approve` creates the Mandate + Briefs (+ deps) + assigns existing crew + files pending hire requests for missing roles → result card links to the new Mandate/Briefs; the operator then greenlights any Clearances (Mandates page) and starts a Brief from the board when ready.
  - **Remaining gaps.** (1) Rule-based by default; a model can now draft the plan **opt-in** (`mode:"ai"`, validated server-side — see the AI Prime Planner pack below), but the default stays deterministic and the coordinator handler never calls a model; (2) a partial `prime.approve` failure mid-sequence leaves the proposal `proposed` and a retry would create a second Mandate (the per-key Brief markers are idempotent, the Mandate is not); (3) no streaming/conversational refinement — one message → one proposal; (4) assignment is a single best-match by role family (no load-balancing / Keys-aware routing).
- **Prime Intelligence + Start-to-Shift Pack — request-aware planning + the closed product loop (IMPLEMENTED).** Implements `docs/relix-company-model.md` §12.5. Two slices that make the Prime flow feel like a product without faking model output or bypassing a gate:
  - **§12.5A — request-aware deterministic planner.** `generate_proposal` still says `ai_used:false` + an honest `ai_status` (no LLM is synchronously callable from a coordinator handler), but the plan now reflects the request instead of one templated shape. The new pure `build_briefs` makes the breakdown **intent-shaped**: `fix` → a sequential *reproduce → fix → verify* chain (verify routes to a QA role when the request implies one); `research` → an *investigate → synthesize* chain; `build`/`generic` → role tracks + an *integrate & ship* Brief depending on every track. Each Brief title carries the extracted **subject** (deliverable-aware). Crew/hires are derived from the roles the breakdown **actually uses**, so every suggested hire maps to a Brief (no orphan hire). The generator stays a single PURE function — the seam where a model can replace the interpretation step while reusing the same governed approve/start path. **That seam is now wired (opt-in):** the AI Prime Planner pack below lets a model draft the plan and validates it server-side before storage; the default path remains this deterministic generator. Tests pin: fix/research chains + deps + QA-verify routing; build vs fix of the same noun yield different shapes; hires only cover used roles.
  - **§12.5B — `prime.start` (Start-to-Shift).** → `POST /v1/spine/prime/start` `{proposal_id, max?}` — turns an **approved** proposal's **ready** Briefs into real **Shifts**, the satisfying "I described it and watched it run" moment. It invents NO new execution path: every Brief funnels through the SAME run chokepoint as `brief.run` — the extracted `heartbeat::preflight_and_spawn` (`preflight_run` → `prepare_claimed_run` → `execute_ready`, then the blocking adapter run on a background thread), so a Prime-started Shift is byte-identical to a manual run (ledger row, transcript, artifacts, Claim, `trigger=manual`). **Approved-only** (a non-approved / unknown / cross-Guild proposal is refused — no existence leak) and **ready-only**: a created Brief runs only when it is assigned + unblocked + not already claimed/complete; every other Brief is returned with an **honest reason** (unassigned / blocked / complete / cancelled / missing / not-ready) via the pure `prime::partition_start`. A per-call start cap reports the remainder skipped (no silent drop). **Assignment reconciliation (completes the loop past a hire):** `prime.approve` assigns each track only to the Operatives that were active THEN and files the missing roles as `pending` hires; so when the operator later greenlights one (`agent.approve_hire`: pending → active), its planned track was still unassigned and would skip as *unassigned* forever, leaving any dependent Brief (the *integrate* track) blocked. So before it reads the ready set, `prime.start` now **completes the assignment `prime.approve` already planned** — it parses the persisted plan, looks up each planned Brief by its stable `prime:{proposal_id}:{key}` source marker, and for any STILL-unassigned track whose role now has an active Operative it assigns that Operative via the SAME `set_brief_field` path + the identical `prime::canon_role` match (never clobbering an existing assignee). This is the operator's sovereign completion of the approved plan (the flow is operator-initiated; it hires/approves/creates no one and assigns nothing not already greenlit as a hire for that role). Reconciled Briefs are returned in `assigned` and get a `prime.assigned` Chronicle event. **Operator-initiated + sovereign:** like `brief.run` it is a deliberate manual action (the single-owner Claim prevents double-work; per the chokepoint audit below, operator-initiated runs are not Allowance-gated). It creates no Mandate/Brief/hire and changes no budget. **Audited:** an Orchestration run (`mode:"start"`) on the Mandate + a `prime.work_started` Chronicle event per started Brief. Returns `{proposal_id, mandate_id, assigned:[brief_id], started:[{brief_id,run_id,rig,status}], skipped:[{brief_id,reason}]}`. Granted to `chat-users`. **Honest note on dependents:** a dependent Brief unblocks only when EVERY blocking track reaches board `done`; a finished Shift opens its *run* review (`pending_review`) but does not move the Brief to `done` on its own. `prime.approve` now **stamps the Founder/Board as each Brief's reviewer** at materialization (company-model §5.4/§12.6; the same-tenant, deterministic `find_founder`) — so the heartbeat's best-effort `Done → in_review` succeeds and a completed track lands in **`in_review`** (review-ready), not `blocked`. The role tracks AND the dependent `integrate` Brief get the same reviewer-aware lifecycle. Unblocking the *integrate* track is still gated on the operator's **review-to-`done`** — but that review-to-done is now a single governed action, not a separate manual board move: a clean, accept-gated **`run.apply`** advances the run's Brief from `in_review` to `done` (resolving its dependents' blockers) via the same `set_board_status` path a manual `brief.move` uses. The new `TaskStore::complete_reviewed_brief` carries that narrow semantics (only an `in_review` Brief advances; any other column is left untouched), the `run.apply` handler calls it on a clean apply (the zero-artifact echo no-op included) and returns `brief_id` + the resulting `brief_status`, and a `conflicted`/`failed` apply never advances the board. So the §12.6 positive local loop closes on the **board** (dependents unblock without a manual `brief.move done`), not just the run ledger. Pinned by `complete_reviewed_brief_is_the_review_to_done_that_unblocks_dependents` (mod.rs) and the extended `starter_crew_closes_the_positive_local_loop_through_prime_start` (handlers.rs). A finished Shift still never auto-advances on its own — only the operator's apply does. **Honest fallback:** if no Founder exists (company never bootstrapped) the reviewer is left unset and the old "parks in `blocked` until a reviewer is set" behaviour holds — we never fabricate or borrow a cross-tenant/arbitrary reviewer. Pinned by `prime_approve_stamps_same_tenant_founder_as_reviewer`, `prime_approve_no_founder_leaves_reviewer_unset`, `prime_approve_reviewer_is_never_cross_tenant`, and `completed_shift_with_founder_reviewer_reaches_in_review_not_blocked` (handlers.rs).
  - **Dashboard.** The Chat approved-plan card gains a **"Start the work"** action (→ `/v1/spine/prime/start`) that renders the started Shifts (Brief → run_id on a Rig, with a board link to watch them finish) and the not-started Briefs with their reasons; the proposal card footer states the real flow (approve → Start the work). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **The closed loop:** describe in Chat → `prime.propose` (request-aware plan) → **Approve & create** (`prime.approve`) → **greenlight the hires** (approve the pending hire / spawn Clearance) → **Start the work** (`prime.start` — reconciles the now-active hires onto their waiting tracks, then runs every ready Brief) → review each Shift to board `done` → its dependents unblock and run on a repeat Start. Every step is a governed gate. Pinned by `prime_start_reconciles_a_greenlit_hire_so_dependent_work_unblocks` (handlers.rs): a missing-role track skips `unassigned` → approve the hire → `prime.start` assigns + runs it → reviewing the tracks to `done` unblocks the dependent `integrate` Brief, which then runs.
  - **What it is NOT.** `prime.start` is itself a deliberate operator action — as a *capability* it does not propose hires, approve hires, or loop on its own (the reconciliation only completes assignments the operator already authorised by approving the hire). Not an LLM — the plan is request-aware but deterministic. Honesty is preserved end to end. **(Update: the opt-in *autonomous Prime driver* — see "Opt-in autonomous Prime driver (bounded v1)" below — now drives this same governed `prime.start` path on a timer for already-approved work, default OFF, never auto-approving a human gate; the capability's own governance is unchanged.)**
- **Live Shift Room + Prime session observability (IMPLEMENTED).** After `prime.start` the operator needs a command center, not just object creation — "what started, what is running, what finished, what is blocked, what needs review, what next." A focused READ-ONLY status capability + a live dashboard surface, sourcing truth ONLY from the existing proposal row + Brief board + run ledger (no new state, no new event bus).
  - **`prime.status` (capability).** Arg `proposal_id` → `GET /v1/spine/prime/proposals/:id/status`. READ-ONLY: starts/applies/mutates **nothing**. Returns `{proposal_id, status, message, mandate_id, mandate_title, briefs:[…], counts:{…}, recommended_next_actions:[…], updated_at}`. Each `briefs[]` row joins the **Brief card** (title / board status / assignee / the assignee's Rig), its **open blockers** (unresolved Snags → `{brief_id,title,status}`, read **tenant-scoped** via `list_snags_for_tenant` so a legacy `blocked_on` edge that crosses Guilds can never surface a cross-tenant blocker), its **Start readiness** (the shared pure `prime::classify_start_readiness` — `ready`/`unassigned`/`blocked`/`complete`/`cancelled`/`not_ready`/`missing`; a Snag-blocked Brief reads `blocked` even when its board column is still `todo`, since a Snag keeps it out of the ready-set without moving the column), its **latest Shift** (`latest_run`: run_id / status / rig / trigger / review / apply_status / refusal_reason / bounded summary from `latest_run_for_brief`), a `needs_review` flag (a `done` run still `pending_review`), and the single most-useful **`next_action`** for that Brief. The roll-up `counts` tally one bucket per Brief (`total_briefs` / `running` / `done` / `blocked` / `needs_review` / `refused` / `failed` / `ready` / `unassigned` / `not_ready` / `missing`) and `recommended_next_actions` derive from those counts (each line appears only when its count is non-zero — no fabricated state). **Tenant-gated**: an unknown / cross-Guild `proposal_id` reads as the same not-found a missing one would (no existence leak). Registered only when the spine store opened; granted to `chat-users`. Idempotent w.r.t. `prime.start` (it shows the existing run state; a re-start that finds nothing newly ready leaves the status coherent). The pure readiness classifier is now **shared** with `prime.start` (one source of truth for "what runs" vs "what to show").
  - **Dashboard (Live Shift Room).** The Chat **approved-plan card** now embeds a live **Shift Room** panel (`ShiftRoom`, keyed by `proposal_id`): roll-up count chips, one row per Brief (state badge, assignee → Rig, latest Shift id+status, open-blocker count) and a concrete **next-action control** per row — **Run** (ready → `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/run`), **Inspect / Review / Apply** (deep-link to `/runs?run=<run_id>` by the run's state), **Hire** (unassigned → `/mandates`), or **Open** (→ `/briefs`) — plus the session's recommended next actions. It now **prefers a dedicated per-session SSE stream** (see the Hardening Pack below) and **falls back to polling** the snapshot only when the stream isn't connected, plus a manual Refresh. The **Overview** Command Center gains a compact **"Active work"** card sourced from the same API (newest approved proposal → its `prime.status` counts + next actions + a link to the full Shift Room on `/chat`); it stays a page-load snapshot by design (the live room lives on `/chat`). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **What it is NOT.** The status endpoint never runs, applies, or discards — those stay the existing explicit routes. If a missing relation makes a field unknowable it returns honest partial data (e.g. `latest_run:null`), never a fabricated state.
- **Shift Room Hardening Pack — dedicated realtime stream + tenant-scoped blockers + bridge coverage (IMPLEMENTED).** Closes the three honest gaps the Shift Room shipped with: no dedicated session stream, no bridge test for `prime.status`, and a non-tenant-scoped blocker read.
  - **Dedicated status stream (PART B).** `GET /v1/spine/prime/proposals/:id/status/stream` (`spine::prime_status_stream`) — a tenant-scoped SSE stream that captures the resolved tenant at open time and re-applies it (`CURRENT_TENANT.scope`) to every downstream coord call. It emits the initial `prime.status` snapshot **immediately** as `event: status`, then **reuses the existing run-event feed** (`run.events.recent`, the same source as `/v1/runs/events/stream`) **only as a cheap change-trigger** — when a run event arrives it re-fetches the status within ~1 s — plus a **low (~3 s) forced refresh** so the room converges even if an event is missed or the bridge has no task-recorder (then it degrades to pure forced polling). Identical frames are **de-duped** (`last_emitted`) so the loop never spins (keep-alive `ping` only). A tenant-gated / unknown proposal emits a **terminal `event: not_found`** and stops cleanly (no existence leak); transient mesh errors emit `event: error` and keep trying. It stops cleanly on disconnect (the stream future drops, releasing the `StreamMetrics` guard). **No new persistent state or event table** — it composes the same read capability the polling route uses. The pure `scan_run_events_for_change` helper (the change-trigger) is unit-tested.
  - **Tenant-scoped blockers (PART A).** New `TaskStore::list_snags_for_tenant` (JOIN on `tasks` filtered to the Guild) backs the Shift-Room open-blocker read in `brief_status_row`; a coordinator test forces a legacy cross-tenant `blocked_on` edge and proves `prime.status` filters the foreign blocker id + title. Not-found / no-existence-leak behavior is unchanged.
  - **Dashboard (PART C).** `subscribePrimeStatus` (in `api.ts`) opens the dedicated stream (cookie auth), applies the pushed snapshot + every change, reports honest connection state, and surfaces the terminal `not_found`. `ShiftRoom` **prefers the stream**, keeps one immediate fetch for instant data, and **polls the snapshot every 4 s ONLY while the stream isn't `live`** (connecting / reconnecting / SSE-unsupported). A compact header badge reads **`live`** only when the stream is connected and **`polling`** otherwise — it never claims realtime when the stream is unavailable. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Bridge coverage (PART D).** Lower-level: `scan_run_events_for_change` unit tests + the route-construction/conflict test extended with the `…/status` + `…/status/stream` patterns (matchit panics on a conflict). Full **mini-mesh** test (`prime_status_mini_mesh_test.rs`): a canned coordinator returns a `prime.status` snapshot for a known proposal and a "not found" error otherwise; it proves the **normal JSON route** (200 + snapshot), **not-found** (404, no leak), the **stream initial snapshot** (`event: status`), and the **terminal `not_found` stream event**.
  - **Honest coverage caveat.** The mini-mesh test exercises the bridge HTTP→mesh→coordinator path with a **single tenant** (the bridge tenant middleware is not stood up in the mini-mesh harness), so the **cross-Guild not-found at the HTTP layer is proven via the not-found path**, while the **true tenant-scoped blocker isolation is pinned at the coordinator layer** (the forced-cross-tenant-edge test). Both layers are covered; a single end-to-end multi-tenant HTTP isolation test would need the tenant middleware wired into the mini-mesh, which is disproportionate here.
- **AI Prime Planner — model-assisted proposal via a server-authoritative validator (IMPLEMENTED, opt-in).** Realizes the §12.5A seam: a model can now draft the *interpretation* while the coordinator stays the sole authority on validation, crew, and governance. No invariant from the deterministic path is weakened, and nothing is faked.
  - **Architecture audit (PART A — why it is shaped this way).** AI/model work in Relix runs on a **separate `ai` mesh peer** (`ai.chat`); the coordinator's capability handlers are synchronous-bodied and hold **no dispatcher/MeshClient** — so a coordinator handler *cannot* call a model inline without new wiring, and §12.5A LOCKS that invariant ("no LLM is synchronously callable from a coordinator handler"). The proven coordinator→AI pattern (delegation/cron/memory executors) calls `ai.chat` from a **background** task via an injected `…AiDispatcher` cell, never from a request handler. The **bridge**, by contrast, already orchestrates request-time AI (the chat flow's `remote_call("ai", …)`) and depends on `relix-runtime` (so it can reuse the `PrimeProposal` type + the validator). The safe, deadlock-free seam is therefore **bridge-orchestrated**: the bridge does the slow model call; the coordinator validates + persists. Secrets are redacted by `rig::redact_secrets` (bridge-side before the model sees them, and again coordinator-side before storage).
  - **`prime.propose` (extended, back-compat).** Accepts EITHER the legacy raw-text arg OR a JSON object `{message, model_output?, model_unavailable_reason?}`. The new **`agent/prime_plan.rs::validate_model_plan`** is a PURE validator/sanitizer (PART D): it bounds the raw output (≤16 KiB), parses the strict JSON plan contract, canonicalizes intent + roles, sanitizes + **secret-redacts every field**, bounds every length, enforces **unique Brief keys** and dependency edges that reference only **known keys** with **no self-edge and no cycle**, and returns a `ValidatedPlan` or a typed `PlanValidationError`.
