The handler runs it **server-side** (authoritative) and turns the result into a proposal via the shared `finalize_proposal`, so crew matching, hire suggestions, and governance risks/next-actions are computed from the **live roster — never from the model**. New honest provenance on `PrimeProposal`: `ai_mode` ∈ {`deterministic_only`, `llm_used`, `fallback`, `unavailable`} (exhaustive + mutually exclusive), `ai_used` (true only for `llm_used`), and an optional `ai_reason`. **Any** failure — model unreachable, empty/oversized output, malformed JSON, a validation error — degrades to the deterministic plan with an honest mode + reason. The only mutation remains the proposal record.
  - **Bridge `mode=ai`.** `POST /v1/spine/prime/propose {message, mode}` — `mode:"ai"` builds a **bounded (4000-char), secret-redacted, pipe-safe** prompt of the **request + crew roster only** (no repo dump; pure `build_prime_ai_prompt`, unit-tested), calls `ai.chat` on the `ai` peer (`RELIX_PRIME_AI_PEER` override) via the JSON arg form, and forwards the RAW reply (or an `model_unavailable_reason`) to the coordinator. A best-effort `agent.operatives` roster fetch is non-fatal. Any other `mode` (or none) is byte-for-byte the historical deterministic path.
  - **Dashboard.** The Chat input gains an off-by-default **"Use AI"** checkbox (sends `mode:"ai"`); the proposal card shows a compact **AI-provenance badge** keyed on `ai_mode` (AI-drafted·validated / AI rejected→rule-based / AI unavailable→rule-based / rule-based) with the full `ai_status` + fallback reason on hover.
  - **Tests.** Validator unit tests pin valid/oversized/empty/malformed/duplicate-key/unknown-dep/self-dep/cycle/secret-redaction/role-normalization; coordinator handler tests pin the valid→`llm_used`, cyclic→`fallback`, and `unavailable` paths plus back-compat raw text; the bridge prompt-builder is unit-tested. **No test calls a real provider.**
  - **What it is NOT (honest limits).** The coordinator handler still **never calls a model** (the §12.5A invariant holds) — the model call lives in the bridge, so a deployment without the `ai` peer simply reports `unavailable`. The live bridge→`ai.chat`→coordinator round trip is **not integration-tested in CI** (it needs a real `ai` peer + provider, out of scope per "no paid/model calls in tests"); the validator + fallback + mode handling that bound its blast radius ARE fully tested with fake model output. One message → one proposal (no conversational refinement). The model influences only the plan *interpretation*; it can never set crew, hires, governance, or bypass the validator.
- **Guarded AI companion action selection — opt-in model-chosen action, bridge-validated, governed-path executed (IMPLEMENTED, opt-in).** Extends `POST /v1/spine/companion` with the same honest AI peer pattern as the Prime planner, while preserving the deterministic parser and every governance check. The model **selects** an action; it never executes anything.
  - **Why the bridge validates (not the coordinator).** Unlike Prime (where the coordinator is the authoritative validator of a model-drafted *plan*), the companion's allowlist maps directly to the existing in-bridge `CompanionAction` enum + its governed handlers, so the validation seam is **bridge-side**: `validate_model_action` is the single chokepoint and the handler that runs it is byte-identical to the deterministic path. No new coordinator capability is introduced; the model's only influence is *which* already-governed action runs and with what (re-validated) fields.
  - **`companion.rs` (extended, back-compat).** `CompanionRequest` gains `mode: Option<String>` (`#[serde(default)]`; absent / non-`"ai"` = the historical deterministic path exactly). `CompanionResponse` gains optional `ai_mode` (`llm_used` / `fallback` / `unavailable`), `ai_used`, and a SAFE `ai_reason` (the bridge's own validator/transport strings — never raw model text). Execution is factored into one `execute_action(state, action, message)` helper shared by both paths.
  - **`mode:"ai"` flow.** The bridge redacts secrets (`rig::redact_secrets`) BEFORE anything reaches the provider, gathers a **bounded, secret-redacted** company context (roster counts + action-center top items + a compact `key=count` board line — never a JSON dump; pure `build_companion_ai_prompt`, ≤4000 chars, pipe-scrubbed, unit-tested), calls `ai.chat` on the `ai` peer (reusing `spine::call_ai_chat`, now taking a `session_id`; companion session = `companion-actions`, `RELIX_PRIME_AI_PEER` override shared), then runs the **pure** `validate_model_action` over the reply.
  - **The validator (`validate_model_action`, PURE + exhaustively tested).** Bounds the raw output (≤8 KiB → unusable), strips an optional ```/```json fence, parses STRICT JSON, reads `action` against the fixed allowlist (`attention|blocked|running|roster|overdue|board|help|search|create_brief|create_mandate|move|assign|pin|comment|plan_package`), and validates each action's fields into `CompanionAction` with the **same constraints as the parser**: no `|` in titles/agent, board statuses normalized + checked against `BOARD_STATUSES`, priorities checked against `PRIORITIES`, `plan_package` requires a non-empty body + ≥1 child (via the shared `plan_package_problem`), and plan-package children are **priorities-only** — a smuggled `assignee`/`agent`/`assign` key is refused. Anything unknown/invalid/unsafe returns a safe reason → **deterministic fallback**.
  - **Honest failure (never faked).** Model unreachable → `unavailable`; model answered but the choice was unusable → `fallback`; both run `parse_command` and execute that deterministically. `ai_used` is true only for `llm_used`, and on a non-`llm_used` path a short note is appended to the reply ("…I used the rule-based parser."). The deterministic path is byte-for-byte unchanged (no `ai_*` fields emitted).
  - **Dashboard.** `Chat.tsx`'s existing off-by-default "Use AI" checkbox now also drives the **Command** button (sends `mode:"ai"`); "Plan with Prime" is unchanged. No redesign. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Pure prompt-builder tests (pipe-safety, hard length bound even with a pathologically huge context, allowlist/schema present, empty-context path) + pure validator tests (every zero-arg + field action → `CompanionAction`; move-status normalization + bad-status reject; plan-package with children + empty-body/zero-children/bad-priority/smuggled-assignee reject; pipe/empty-field/unknown-action reject; non-JSON/non-object/oversized reject; code-fence strip) + the `ai_fallback_note` provenance helper. The existing deterministic parser tests still pass. **No test calls a real provider** (the live `ai.chat` round trip is out of scope per "no paid/model calls in tests", same as Prime).
  - **What it is NOT.** One chat turn → one validated action; **no autonomous planner/agent loop**, no multi-step tool use, no model-executed text. The model can only pick from the allowlist; it can never reach a capability the deterministic parser can't, nor bypass approvals (the plan-package confirm is still operator-approved).
- **Companion chat console — persistent local session + command chips + result cards (IMPLEMENTED, frontend only).** Makes the Chat surface feel like a usable company operating console (`relix-dashboard-design.md` §13) without touching the backend: it reuses the SAME governed `POST /v1/spine/companion` (and Prime propose/approve/start) routes — **no new mutation path, no new client API method.** All in `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Chat.tsx` + small scoped CSS in `styles.css` (rebuilt `dashboard-dist`).
  - **Persistent local session.** The chat log is hydrated from / written to `localStorage` under a **versioned key `relix.chat.v1`**, so a refresh no longer wipes the conversation. Only safe UI data already shown on the page is stored (ids/titles/counts/replies + the proposal/approved/started cards) — **never tokens/passwords/secrets**; a hard cap of the latest **50 entries** bounds growth, and a corrupt/foreign value (parse error or wrong shape, guarded by `isEntry`) **resets cleanly** to the Prime greeting. A **Clear chat** control (confirmed) discards the local log and restores the greeting. This is **local browser history only — NOT the server/audit record** (every governed action still lands in the Chronicle); the bar above the log says so.
  - **Command discoverability.** A compact, B&W chip row sits above the input. Safe **read** chips (*what needs attention / what is blocked / what is running / who is on the crew*) dispatch straight through the governed companion route; **write** templates (*create brief / plan package*) only **populate** the input so the operator edits the real ids/text before sending — the chat never fires a write blind.
  - **Companion result rendering.** A companion response now renders as a compact **`CompanionCard`** (a flat `.panel`, no nested cards): an action-name chip, the reply text, an honest **AI-provenance** chip when present (`llm_used` → *AI-selected* / `fallback` / `unavailable`, hidden on the deterministic path), a SAFE inferred **route hand-off** to the board (attention → The Desk, blocked/board/search/create_brief/move/assign/pin/comment/plan_package → Briefs, running → Runs, roster → Crew/Agents, create_mandate → Mandates), and the **raw result behind a `<details>` disclosure** for debugging — replacing the old raw-JSON dump in the bubble. Errors/unknown shapes still fall back to a plain-text bubble.
  - **Input behavior.** **Enter still = Plan with Prime** (the established default is preserved); **Ctrl/⌘+Enter = Command** (mirrors the existing Command button). The "Use AI" toggle still drives both. Busy state and the button row are unchanged/stable; chips disable while busy.
  - **What it is NOT.** Frontend product polish only — no backend route, capability, or governance change; the persisted log is **browser-local** (not synced, not the audit trail), and the companion is still **one turn → one validated action** (see the AI action-selection note above). Verified: `tsc -b` + `vite build` green, `scripts/check-dashboard-dist.ps1` parity after rebuild.
- **Boot + Dashboard Auth + Product Smoke Pack — make the system bootable, loginable, recoverable, and verifiable from the CLI/dashboard without weakening auth (IMPLEMENTED).** Closes the basic-usability failures (stale-looking dashboard, "spine unavailable" confusion, 401 on tasks/jobs/providers, forgotten admin password, opaque boot) **diagnostically** — no protected API is made public and auth is unchanged.
  - **Already shipped (this pack did NOT rebuild):** the dashboard operator login itself — first-run `POST /v1/auth/setup` (single admin, Argon2id PHC in `dashboard-admin.json` next to the bridge token), `POST /v1/auth/login` → HttpOnly `relix_session` cookie (12h, in-memory), `logout`/`me`/`status`, and the `auth` middleware that admits a valid session cookie exactly like the bridge bearer; the LOCAL `relix-web-bridge reset-admin` recovery (Argon2id, generates+prints a password once, never reads the old secret, no network reset) + `scripts/relix-dashboard-admin-reset.{ps1,sh}`; `relix doctor` (bridge `/v1/health`); and the dist-parity gate (`scripts/check-dashboard-dist.ps1`). All retained as-is.
  - **PART B — `relix dashboard` CLI (new, `crates/relix-cli/src/dashboard.rs`).** (1) **`relix dashboard doctor`** — a READ-ONLY health/auth + product-loop probe that mutates nothing and needs no logged-in session. It checks the bridge is reachable (`/health`), reports the **auth status** from the public `/v1/auth/status` (admin configured? → login hint; `needs_setup`? → "create the admin / `relix dashboard reset-admin`"), confirms the **SPA bundle is served** (`/dashboard` returns the SPA HTML) and that `dashboard-dist` is present locally, and probes the **product routes** `/v1/spine/board` + `/v1/spine/prime/proposals` — the crux being `classify_route_probe`, which maps a **401/403 with no token to WARN ("auth is ENFORCED, not that the spine is down — pass --token")**, a 401/403 *with* a token to FAIL (token rejected), a 404 to FAIL (route not mounted / wrong build), and a 503 to WARN (backend down). It honestly states the CLI carries no browser cookie so it cannot confirm a session, and resolves the bearer like `relix doctor` (`--token` → `RELIX_BRIDGE_TOKEN` → `~/.relix/bridge-token`). `--json` for scripts; exits non-zero on any FAIL. (2) **`relix dashboard reset-admin`** — a thin passthrough that locates the sibling `relix-web-bridge` binary and forwards `reset-admin` (the Argon2id reset is NOT reimplemented in the CLI — single source of truth stays in the bridge crate so the on-disk format can't drift).
  - **PART C — boot output clarity.** `relix boot` (`mesh.rs`) now prints, after the bridge token, a login/setup block via the pure `dashboard_login_lines(admin_exists, url)`: the dashboard URL, **first-run "create the admin" vs. "log in"** (detected from `~/.relix/dashboard-admin.json`), the `relix dashboard reset-admin` recovery, and "verify the product loop: `relix dashboard doctor`". The boot scripts' banners were corrected the same way: `relix-mesh-up.{ps1,sh}` previously told operators to **paste the setup token into the dashboard's "Authentication Required" screen** — misleading, since the browser dashboard logs in with the admin username/password and the setup token only gates the curl-only `/v1/auth/token` bootstrap. The banner now shows the real first-run/login/reset path and a `dashboard doctor` pointer, reframes the setup token as advanced/curl-only, and adds a **Controllers** summary line (tool/coordinator/telegram/discord/slack/plugin_host = started vs disabled) stating that channels are opt-in and **never block boot** (a missing token just stays offline).
  - **PART D — dashboard 401 → reauth (no route made public).** `api.ts` adds a tiny session-expired pub/sub (`onSessionExpired`): when a **protected** API call returns 401/403 (the auth endpoints `/v1/auth/*` are excluded, so a wrong password on the login form is NOT treated as an expiry), it fires once. `auth.tsx` listens, sets `sessionExpired`, and re-probes `/v1/auth/status` — which flips `authenticated:false`, so `<App>` renders `<Login>` with a clear **"Your session expired — sign in again"** banner instead of leaving every page on a broken "Could not load…" card. A successful login clears the flag. This is a **client-side reaction only**; it never makes a protected route public. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **PART E — tests.** `dashboard.rs`: `classify_route_probe` (401-no-token = WARN not FAIL; 401-with-token = FAIL; 200 = PASS; 404 = FAIL; 503 = WARN), `evaluate_auth_status` (needs_setup → reset hint; configured → login hint; login-required is INFO never FAIL), bundle HTML/non-HTML/missing verdicts, platform-correct bridge-binary name, and unknown-field tolerance. `mesh.rs`: `dashboard_login_lines` first-run-vs-existing-admin hints (both surface `relix dashboard doctor`). The existing `dashboard_auth` reset tests (old password fails / new works after reload; never stores plaintext) still pass, as do the `auth` middleware 401 tests. `cargo clippy` clean on `relix-cli` + `relix-web-bridge`; `cargo check --workspace` green; `tsc -b` + `vite build` green.
  - **Honest limits.** `relix dashboard doctor` is a CLI probe — it cannot see a browser session (no cookie), so a logged-in check still requires opening the dashboard; without `--token` the authenticated product-route probe is a WARN, not a confirmation. The reset still needs a bridge restart to take effect (sessions are in-memory). The 401→reauth flow routes the user to login but does not transparently retry the failed request. No sample/demo data is created by any of this (the smoke is read-only); `--seed-demo` was therefore not added.
- **Founder Action Center Pack — one place for what needs the operator (IMPLEMENTED).** Implements `docs/relix-company-model.md` §5.4 / §8.2 (the Board's home — *a single action center showing only what needs you, in priority order, computed from live state, not a notification table*) and `docs/relix-dashboard-design.md` §5. It composes EXISTING state into one ordered, deduped, READ-ONLY feed — **no new notification table, no new event bus, no new stored state.**
  - **`company.actions` (capability)** → **`GET /v1/spine/company/actions`**. No args, tenant-scoped. Returns `{actions, counts:{total, by_category, by_severity}, truncated}`. Registered only when the spine store is wired (needs the agent + spine + task stores); granted to `chat-users` (mesh-up policy `spine_company_actions`).
  - **Categories implemented (all from existing reads):** `approval` (pending Clearances via `list_pending_approvals_for_tenant` — a spawn Clearance targets the pending hire it activates — **plus** proposed-strategy Mandates via `list_mandates`+`strategy_status`); `hire` (Operatives `pending` via `list_operatives_for_tenant`); **`budget`** (Completion Pack — allowance-backed, from existing tenant-scoped state only: **(a)** committed Allowance over/near the Guild budget via `committed_allowance_cents_for_tenant` vs `spine_store.get_guild().monthly_allowance_cents` — fires only when the Guild has a positive budget set, *over* at >100% [High] / *near* at ≥90% [Medium]; **(b)** an active Operative hard-stopped by a `0`/negative Allowance — `heartbeat::allowance_admits` semantics — that has runnable/blocked work assigned [High]; **(c)** *live actual spend* (Live Spend Telemetry Pack) when the metrics ledger is wired — per-Operative spend over/near its Allowance **+** Guild spend over/near budget, read READ-ONLY through the `action_center::SpendSource` seam from the SAME `MetricsQuery::cost_since` source + **current UTC calendar-month** window (the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window`) the dispatch gate enforces (`over_allowance` / `heartbeat::allowance_admits`), carrying the real `spent / limit / percent` in the reason; *over* = at/over the cap (the gate's refusal threshold) [High], *near* = ≥80% [Medium]; emits **no** spend item at all when metrics are disabled — committed (capacity reserved) and actual spend (money spent) stay DISTINCT items, never double-counted); `ready_to_start` (new `list_ready_briefs_for_tenant` — assigned-to-active + unblocked + unclaimed); `blocked` (`list_unassigned_briefs_for_tenant` = missing assignee + `list_blocked_briefs_for_tenant` = dependency-blocked); `needs_review` (a `done` + `pending_review` latest run); `failed_or_refused` (a `failed`/`refused`/`interrupted` latest run, now a **recovery-decision card** — see below) — both off the tenant-scoped `list_runs_for_tenant`, taking only the **latest run per Brief** so an old failure + a new done run don't both show; `stale` (`list_stale_briefs_for_tenant`, 1-day idle, lowest priority).
  - **Recovery-decision cards (Completion Pack, Part B)** — `failed_or_refused` items now carry a plain-language root cause + a **stable recommended action and the existing governed route that fixes it**, mapped from the existing durable refusal taxonomy (`refusal_is_durable`): `unassigned` → *Assign an Operative* (`/briefs`), `no_adapter`/`adapter_unavailable` → *Configure the Rig* (`/settings`), `over_allowance` → *Raise the Allowance* (`/agents`), `workspace_error`/`workspace_context_error` → *Review runtime settings* (`/settings`), `interrupted` → *Inspect the run* (auto re-claimed), `failed` → the redacted summary + *Inspect the run* (`/runs?run=…`). It mints **no** new retry/apply mutation (the read-only Inbox form of dashboard-design §5.2 / execution §3.3b). **Update:** the card now prefers the durable per-run diagnosis metadata (failure-class / retryable / retry-budget / recovery-action / recovery-route) when stamped, and falls back to this refusal-taxonomy map for legacy rows — see the **Brief/Shift recovery diagnosis** pack below.
  - **Ordering + dedupe (Part B)** live in a PURE, unit-tested module `agent/action_center.rs` (`ActionItem` / `ActionCategory` / `ActionSeverity` + `finalize`). Rank: approval(0) < hire(1) < **budget(2)** < failed_or_refused(3) < needs_review(4) < ready_to_start(5) < blocked(6) < stale(7) — so approvals/hire blockers sit on top, **budget governance follows (a hard-stop blocks ALL of an Operative's work; over-commitment is a Board §5.4 sovereign-control concern), above a single broken Shift**, failed/refused precede informational stale, and ready_to_start precedes generic blocked. Severity is per-category by default but an item may override it (a *near*-budget warning is Medium while *over*-budget is High). `finalize` sorts by `(rank, created_at oldest-first, id)` (deterministic) then **dedupes by underlying object** `(target_type, target_id)` keeping the most-urgent.
  - **Governance (Part C):** READ-ONLY — it approves/runs/applies/mutates **nothing**; every mutation stays on its existing governed route (the item carries the dashboard route to act). Tenant-scoped on every contributing read (a cross-Guild approval / hire / Brief / run never surfaces — no existence leak); needs no new permissions.
  - **Dashboard (Part D):** the **Overview** Command Center gains an **Action Center** card (sourced from `/v1/spine/company/actions`) at the top of the operational surfaces: each row shows a severity-toned category chip, the title + plain-language reason, and a button to the existing action route (approve hires/clearances → `/agents`·`/mandates`, review/apply → `/runs?run=…`, start/assign/unblock → `/briefs`, budget → `/agents`); a calm empty state ("Nothing needs you right now…") when the feed is empty, and an honest "unavailable" state if the endpoint is down. **Refresh (Completion Pack, Part C):** the card subscribes to the EXISTING run-event SSE (`subscribeRunEvents` → `/v1/runs/events/stream`) as a cheap change-trigger (debounced ~1.2 s) and falls back to a low-frequency poll (20 s) so approval/hire/prime changes still converge; it refreshes **only** the Action Center feed (never the page load state), updates **only on a successful fetch** (a transient blip never blanks it), and stays stable if the stream is unavailable — **no new event bus**. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Pure module: rank ordering (incl. budget(2) < failed_or_refused(3)), severity mapping, `fmt_cents`, budget over-vs-near severity + singleton dedupe, recovery-card refusal→stable-action/route mapping + failed/interrupted/unknown reasons, sort, dedupe-same-object (hire+Clearance), dedupe-brief-across-categories, targetless-never-deduped, id-tiebreak determinism. Handler: empty-is-calm; surfaces hire+ready+blocked with the ordering guarantee; needs_review after a real echo Shift; hire+spawn-Clearance dedupe; proposed-strategy approval; **budget over-Guild-budget alert (+ tenant isolation), no-fake-alert-without-a-budget-source, Allowance hard-stop with assigned ready work (+ budget-before-ready ordering)**; tenant isolation (a different Guild sees `total:0`, no title leak). **Live Spend Telemetry tests:** `fmt_micros`, company-spend over/near severity + distinct-from-committed id/dedupe-key (pure); handler-level live spend over-AND-near-Allowance severity (via a fake `SpendSource`), Guild-spend-over-budget DISTINCT from the committed item, NO `budget:spend:*` item when the source is empty (no fabricated spend), and **live-spend tenant isolation** (a foreign Guild's Operative spend never leaks into this Guild's feed). **Real-ledger live-spend tests** (production `MetricsSpendSource` over a real in-memory `MetricsStore`/`MetricsQuery`, not a fake): `company_actions_live_spend_from_real_metrics_store` (sums multiple priced rows, EXCLUDES a stale row outside the current calendar-month window, renders the real over[High]/near[Medium] figures) and `company_actions_live_spend_real_metrics_is_tenant_isolated` (two Guilds sharing one ledger, neither's spend leaks into the other — isolation via the handler roster). Bridge: the route-construct test covers `/company`, `/company/init`, `/company/actions` (matchit no-conflict).
  - **Honest limits / deferred categories.** Budget alerts now carry **live spend** when the metrics ledger is wired (Live Spend Telemetry Pack): the read-only handler reads the **authoritative month-to-date spend the dispatch gate itself enforces** — `MetricsQuery::cost_since` over the **current UTC calendar month** (the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window`), the `over_allowance` refusal source — through the `action_center::SpendSource` seam (`handlers::MetricsSpendSource::current_month`, wired in `register_agent_capabilities` from the `MetricsBundle.query`). There is **no second budget truth**: the feed reads the same store + window the gate does, so it cannot disagree, and when metrics are **disabled** the seam is `None` and the feed shows **no spend item** (never a fabricated "$X of $Y"). The committed-Allowance planning signals (capacity reserved) remain and stay **distinct** from actual-spend items (money spent) — never double-counted. Remaining real-spend gaps: the near band is a fixed 80%; the production `MetricsSpendSource` is now tested against a **real** in-memory `MetricsStore`/`MetricsQuery` — `company_actions_live_spend_from_real_metrics_store` seeds priced rows (keyed by `agent_id`, the gate's attribution contract), proving the handler SUMS the window, EXCLUDES rows outside the current calendar-month window, and renders the real over/near figures; `company_actions_live_spend_real_metrics_is_tenant_isolated` proves a foreign Guild's recorded spend never leaks (isolation via the handler roster, since `cost_since` does not filter by tenant). What remains *not* covered end-to-end is only the cross-process bridge→coordinator HTTP transport carrying that spend (the spend SOURCE itself is no longer a fake), and `cost_since` attribution still depends on production recording `agent_name == agent_id` (the same best-effort assumption the heartbeat Allowance gate relies on). The `blocked` reason still distinguishes only *missing-assignee* vs *dependency-blocked*. Strategy approvals are a bounded scan of `list_mandates` + `strategy_status` (50), not a dedicated index. Recovery cards now carry a true **retryable-vs-not** verdict from the durable per-run diagnosis layer (failure-class/retryable/retry-budget on `brief_runs` — see the **Brief/Shift recovery diagnosis** pack below), preferring the run's stamped action/route and falling back to the refusal-taxonomy map for legacy rows; what remains is autonomous retry/recovery (the diagnosis informs, it does not act) and provider quota polling. The feed is capped at 60 with an honest `truncated` flag; the Overview refresh is low-latency event-trigger + poll, not hard-realtime push of every field.
- **Dashboard Invalidation Bus — first real slice of surgical cache invalidation (IMPLEMENTED).** Implements the seed of `docs/relix-dashboard-design.md` §11 ("surgical cache invalidation keyed by a centralized invalidation-key factory — not blanket refetches … adopt it early") in its smallest honest, dependency-free form — **no query library, no new socket, no optimistic state.**
  - **`apps/dashboard/src/invalidate.ts` (new).** A tiny client bus over a single `EventTarget`: `invalidate(keys, {briefId?})` emits AFTER a mutation is confirmed server-side; `onInvalidate` / the `useInvalidate(keys, cb, {match, debounceMs})` React hook subscribe and refetch. Five coarse keys — one per live data-surface — `briefs` (Issue board / Brief lists / inbox), `brief` (one Brief's detail: conversation / requests / chronicle / latest Shift, scoped by `briefId`), `runs` (the Shift ledger), `actions` (Overview Action Center + readiness), `mandates` (Mandate governance / orchestration). The hook coalesces a multi-key burst into one refetch (~150 ms) and rides a callback ref so the subscription never churns.
  - **Honesty contract.** The bus carries NO data and applies NO optimistic state — it only says "this key changed, refetch from the server", so a surface can never diverge from the backend (CLAUDE.md / §11). It **complements** the existing run-event SSE (`subscribeRunEvents`, left untouched): the SSE keeps pushing run-lifecycle transitions to the surfaces that subscribe to it; the bus carries the mutation outcomes the SSE stream does NOT (comments, interaction/suggestion answers, assignment, hiring, orchestration, governance) and keeps **co-mounted** surfaces — the Issue board and the open Brief detail panel beside it — in lockstep.
  - **Wired surfaces.** `BriefDetail` subscribes `brief` (scoped to its id) so a board **assign/move** on that card mirrors into the open panel without a manual Refresh; its `comment` / interaction / suggestion / run / review / apply / cancel handlers emit the keys the board + Runs + Action Center need (replacing the old `onChanged` prop-drill). The **Briefs board** subscribes `briefs` (so a `suggest_tasks` accept that materializes Sub-briefs, or a Shift started/reviewed/applied from the panel, refreshes the columns + run badges) and emits `brief`/`actions`/`runs` on assign/move/create/run. The **Overview Action Center** adds a bus subscription (`actions`/`briefs`/`mandates` → the same success-only `refreshActions`) on top of its existing SSE-trigger + 20 s poll, so non-run mutations converge without waiting for the poll. **Runs** review/apply/cancel/discard and **Mandates** strategy/clearance/hire/orchestrate emit the cross-surface keys (keeping their own local reloads). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **What it is NOT (honest limits).** This is the **client invalidation-key discipline only** — not the full §11 engine: there is still no per-tenant WebSocket of its own (it rides the existing run-event SSE for backend pushes), no hierarchical query-key *factory* (five flat keys, growable when a query library lands), no route-aware cache hydration (it refetches rather than splicing a new comment into a cache), and no rate-limited toasts. Cross-**route** convergence is still mount-time (the SPA mounts one route at a time, so a board mutation only live-updates surfaces co-mounted with it — today that is the board ↔ open Brief panel pair); the emits to non-co-mounted surfaces are correct + future-proofing. No backend change; no new npm dependency.

- **First-Run Company Bootstrap + Starter Crew Pack — the empty-company on-ramp to a positive Shift (IMPLEMENTED).** Implements `docs/relix-company-model.md` §12.6. Closes the honest first-run dead-end: on a brand-new Guild, `prime.approve` files Mandate + Briefs but every track lands **unassigned** (no active work-role Operative), so `prime.start` correctly skips everything and the operator never sees a single Shift run. This pack adds a governed way to populate **safe, local** crew so the Prime loop closes without any external coding-agent auth.
  - **Already shipped (this pack did NOT rebuild):** `company.status` (`GET /v1/spine/company`, `initialized` ⇔ a Founder exists), `company.bootstrap_founder` (`POST /v1/spine/company/init`, owner-gated, idempotent Founder via `ensure_founder`, defaults `echo`), the **`echo`** built-in safe-local Rig (`rig/mod.rs::EchoRig` — no external calls), the gated hire/Clearance path, and the dashboard first-run cards on Overview + Crew (Agents).
  - **`company.starter_crew` (capability)** → **`POST /v1/spine/company/starter-crew`** `{rig?, roles?}`. Wire arg `rig|roles_csv` (defaults `echo` + `engineer,designer`). **Owner-gated** (`caller_is_owner`: operator/admin or the boot-seeded `allow-all` console identity); a normal Operative is refused (`SECURITY_DENIED`). At the bridge it additionally requires a logged-in dashboard session (defence in depth, like `/company/init`). Idempotently ensures the **Founder** (`ensure_founder`) then **one active safe-local starter Operative per role** via the new `AgentStore::ensure_starter_operative` (atomic check+insert under one lock, idempotency keyed on the `STARTER_CREATED_BY = "relix-starter"` marker + canonical role). Starters are plain **workers** (active, `low` risk ceiling, NO spawn/assign Keys), bound to `rig` (echo by default), and **clearly labelled local/safe** (`"Starter Engineer (local · echo)"`, dept `Starter Crew`, team `Local/Safe`) — never presented as Claude/Codex. Roles are canonicalised + de-duped (`prime::canon_role`) and capped (`STARTER_MAX_ROLES=6`). Returns `{founder, founder_created, rig, safe_local, crew:[{agent_id,role,name,created}]}` (`safe_local` true only for echo). It hires no one behind a Clearance, runs no adapter, and changes no budget — it only **provisions** the crew; the single-owner Claim + per-Operative Allowance hard-stop (autonomous path) are unchanged.
  - **The positive local loop (no external auth):** *starter crew* → `prime.propose` (a "build …" → engineer/designer tracks + integrate) → `prime.approve` (the tracks assign to the active starter Operatives) → `prime.start` (the ready Briefs run through the echo Rig and reach `done`/`pending_review`) → the Shift Room + Action Center reflect it. Direct active creation is acceptable HERE only because it is the Board's sovereign first-run action (§5.4), the same trust basis as `ensure_founder` and operator-only `agent.create`.
  - **Tenant/auth safety:** Founder + every starter are created in the caller's Guild via the tenant-scoped store; a second Guild gets its own independent crew (no cross-tenant leak). Tests prove acme's crew never appears for globex.
  - **Dashboard (Part D):** the Crew (Agents) first-run card adds a second action **"Set up starter crew (local · echo)"** (`starterCrew()` → `/v1/spine/company/starter-crew`) with an explanatory line that the workers are safe local/demo crew (not Claude/Codex); the **Overview** first-run card surfaces the same path ("Set up a starter crew") and the next-steps list mentions it. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Store: `ensure_starter_operative` idempotent/active/rigged/worker-Keys + per-tenant. Handler: starter crew creates Founder + default engineer/designer safe-local crew (active, echo, labelled, no Keys, `initialized` after); idempotent (no dup on re-run); explicit roles canonicalise + de-dup; tenant-scoped; non-owner refused; **the positive local loop** — from an empty company, starter crew → propose → approve (tracks assigned) → `prime.start` runs at least one real echo Shift with a `run_id` on the echo Rig.
  - **Remaining gap (honest).** This closes the loop for **safe local (echo)** work only. Real Claude/Codex-authenticated execution still requires installing + logging in to a coding-agent CLI (Settings) and switching an Operative's Rig to it — `company.starter_crew` deliberately provisions/authenticates no external adapter. The default roster is engineer+designer; other roles (researcher/writer/qa/ops) still come from real hires/Clearances unless requested explicitly.
  - **Live-HTTP smoke finding + fix (boot policy).** The original pack added the capability, the `POST /v1/spine/company/starter-crew` route, and the runtime owner-gate — but **not** a mesh policy allow rule. Because the only loop test calls `handle_starter_crew` in-process (bypassing mesh admission), the gap stayed green in `cargo test` while a real boot returned `deny:default_deny:no allow rule for method company.starter_crew` over HTTP, making the on-ramp unreachable. The boot policy is generated **only** by `scripts/relix-mesh-up.ps1` / `scripts/relix-mesh-up.sh` (the CLI emits no policy; `relix boot` spawns these), so both scripts now emit the `spine_company_starter_crew` allow rule alongside `spine_company_bootstrap_founder`. The full propose → approve → `prime.start` → echo Shift loop is now verified end-to-end over live HTTP (see `docs/live-smoke.md`).

- **Dashboard first-run on-ramp — the safe-local first Shift, discoverable in the UI (roadmap §6 DoD "Time-to-first-success < 5 min … discoverable in the UI"; company-model §12.6; dashboard-design §5) — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** Closes the DoD gap that the live-smoke *proves the first-success path exists* but it was reachable only over HTTP/docs, not from the dashboard, once the company was past the `!initialized` welcome card. A compact **"Run your first Shift"** on-ramp card now renders on **Overview** (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Overview.tsx`, `FirstRunOnRamp`) when the company **is initialized but has no work yet** — no Briefs and no Mandates, guarded on a clean core read so a down coordinator never masquerades as fresh. One click chains **three existing routes** end-to-end on the built-in safe **echo** Rig: (1) `company.starter_crew` (`POST /v1/spine/company/starter-crew {rig:"echo"}`) ensures a safe-local crew and returns the Operative ids; (2) `brief.create` (`POST /v1/spine/briefs`) creates a plainly-titled Brief ("First Shift — local echo demo") **assigned in the same call** to a starter Operative via the route's existing `assignee` field; (3) `brief.run` (`POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/run {rig:"echo"}`) runs it. Each step shows honest live progress (todo/…/done/failed badges); on success the card deep-links to the run (`/runs?run=`), the Brief (`/briefs?brief=`), and the crew (`/agents`). **No fake success:** a run refusal/failure surfaces the real status (+ any `install_hint`) and a recovery hint; a thrown step marks itself failed with the real error. The panel **latches open** once started so the result + deep links survive the post-run reload, then disappears for an established company; while shown it suppresses the now-redundant "No Mandates / No Briefs yet" warning nudges (design §5: one scannable card, not a tower of banners). It also offers **Plan with Prime** (Chat) as the richer real-goal alternative. **No backend change** — no new route/capability/policy/mutation; it reuses `company.starter_crew` + `brief.create` (with `assignee`) + `brief.run`, all already admitted. **Honest scope:** this proves the local execution loop (governed crew → Brief → scoped run → transcript → review/apply) is reachable from the UI; it does **not** call a real model provider (echo is the built-in no-spend stand-in). The `!initialized` Overview welcome card + the Crew (Agents) first-run card are unchanged. Verified: `npm run build` green; `crates/relix-web-bridge/dashboard-dist` rebuilt + committed (dist-parity gate); `git diff --check` clean. No Rust touched → no Rust test required. Docs: `docs/getting-started.md` ("Your first Shift (from the dashboard)") + this entry.

- **Canonical Guild month-to-date spend route (company-model §6/§6.6; dashboard-design §10; roadmap §5 slice 11) — SHIPPED.** Closes the Costs-page caveat that canonical Guild MTD spend had no numeric route. A shared helper `heartbeat::guild_spend_micros(agent_store, metrics, tenant, since_ms)` is now THE single source of truth for "Guild month-to-date spend" — the SUM of the tenant's own active Operatives' `cost_since` over the canonical `allowance_window`; `dispatch_budget_admits` (the autonomous Guild hard-stop) was refactored to call it, so the gate and any operator surface compute spend ONE way. New handler `handle_guild_spend` (registered as `guild.spend`, wired to the same `MetricsQuery` the Action Center uses) returns `{tenant_id, guild_id, display_name, spent_micros, spent_cents, budget_cents, remaining_cents, over_budget, window_start_ms, resets_at_ms, now_ms, source, computed_from}`. Tenant-safe by construction (only the caller's own Guild's active roster; never `cost_since(None, …)`); honest-null `budget`/`remaining`/`over_budget` when no positive budget is set; null `spent_*` when no metrics ledger is wired (never a faked 0). Bridge route `GET /v1/spine/guild/spend` (`spine.rs` + `main.rs`, passthrough to `guild.spend`); admitted in both boot scripts + the boot-policy coverage manifest. 4 handler tests pin: current-month-only (stale row excluded) + over-budget + negative remaining + window/reset fields, no-budget honest-null, no-metrics null spend (budget still resolves), and tenant isolation. The dashboard Costs **Guild budget** card reads this route (`apps/dashboard/src/api.ts` `guildSpend`/`GuildSpend`, `Costs.tsx`). Verified: `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` (3970, +4) + `cargo test -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code; `npm run build` + dist parity + boot-policy coverage PASS; `git diff --check` clean.

- **The Lattice + Costs frontend surfaces (dashboard-design §9/§10; roadmap §P2 slices 4/5) — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** Two net-new React pages on data that already exists, no backend change beyond a typed client helper. (The Lattice's previously-deferred full pan/zoom/pinch + Fit/Reset is now shipped — see below.)
  - **The Lattice (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Lattice.tsx`, route `/lattice`, ORG nav).** Renders the live `reports_to` forest from `/v1/spine/operatives` (apex order — Founder → Prime — resolved from `/v1/spine/company`) as an SVG-edge layer + absolutely-positioned node cards on a **transformed pan/zoom stage**. Each node shows the Operative's name, a semantic status dot (active/pending/other), an optional title line, role + rig chips (the rig chip reads `… · not ready` when the bound adapter doesn't probe available — honest readiness, never invented), a direct-report count, and a **live** pill when `/v1/runs` shows a running Shift for it. Click → a per-Operative detail panel (the existing `.context-panel`): role/status, rig + readiness (`/v1/adapters`), reports-to, direct-report + running counts, a **clickable direct-reports list** (walk the tree without losing the panel), and the §9 governance face read-only — Keys + monthly Allowance + risk ceiling lazily fetched from `/v1/spine/keys/:id` + `/v1/agents/:id`. B&W aesthetic; color reserved for status (§12). **Now SHIPPED (gap closed): full pan/zoom/pinch.** The whole stage is one CSS `transform: translate() scale()` over the fixed layout space, driven by native `PointerEvent` (drag-pan on one pointer, two-finger pinch-zoom around the gesture midpoint) and a **non-passive** `WheelEvent` (cursor-anchored zoom, so `preventDefault` actually suppresses page scroll), with explicit −/+/**Fit**/**Reset** controls, an **auto-fit-once** on first render (guarded so the chart never jumps while hovering/clicking), drag-vs-click disambiguation (a pan past a 4px threshold swallows the trailing node click), and `touch-action:none` on the viewport so mobile gestures route to the handlers. Still CSP-clean and dependency-free (no SVG-pan lib). The layout DFS is defensive: a `reports_to` cycle (visited set) or an orphan pointer (parent not in the set) falls back to a root, and an edge to a missing parent is simply not drawn — no crash. **View state now persists:** the viewport (scale + pan x/y) is saved to `localStorage` under the versioned key `relix.lattice.viewport.v1` (reusing the Chat page's local-session pattern, §13). The write is debounced (~250ms) so a drag/pinch/wheel gesture persists once it settles, not per frame; storage mirrors the live view, so **Fit** persists the fitted view and **Reset** overwrites the saved viewport with the canonical default. Every read is hard-validated (finite numbers, scale within `ZOOM_MIN..ZOOM_MAX`, pan within a sane bound) and resets cleanly on any corrupt/foreign value — when no valid saved viewport exists the chart falls back to the default + the one-time auto-fit; a restored viewport suppresses that auto-fit so it is never clobbered. Only viewport numbers are stored — the selected Operative is deliberately left in-memory. **Honest remaining nuance:** `brief.detail`'s `delegation_depth` is still not rendered anywhere.
  - **Costs (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Costs.tsx`, route `/costs`, ORG nav).** Real-data sections: **Guild budget** — now budget vs **canonical month-to-date spend** vs remaining from the dedicated `guild.spend` route (`GET /v1/spine/guild/spend`), with an actual-spend progress bar (over-cap = red bar + "over budget" chip), the reset date, and the committed Allowance kept as a clearly-DISTINCT *capacity-reserved* line; **budget & over-cap signals** (the `budget`-category items from `/v1/spine/company/actions`); **Operative allowance & spend** (per-Operative monthly cap from each one's Keys + best-effort observed spend joined from metrics by agent name/id); **observed spend by agent** (`/v1/metrics/agents?hours=` with a 24h/7d/30d window selector, per-agent invocations/tokens/cost + a total); and the **Brief-tree cost rollup** (a Brief search → `brief.cost_rollup` via the typed `briefCost.rollup` client → own/descendant split, tree counts, window, and the per-`billing_code` breakdown; optional since/until date inputs, blank = current calendar month). All figures are real (ledger micros / configured cents); every section degrades to an **honest unavailable state naming the route + reason** rather than a fabricated zero. **Caveat closed:** the canonical month-to-date **Guild** spend now has a numeric route and the Guild budget card reads it (not the old metrics approximation). **Honest remaining nuance:** the per-agent "observed spend" table is still **operational telemetry** from the observability metrics window (explicitly labelled distinct from the governance calendar-month), and its metrics↔Operative join stays best-effort (an unmatched agent shows "no data").
  - **Client/wiring + verification.** `apps/dashboard/src/api.ts` gains the typed `briefCost.rollup(briefId, since?, until?)` helper (over `tryGetReport`, so the Costs page surfaces an honest error). `App.tsx` routes, `nav.ts` ORG entries (`Lattice` / `Costs`), `Layout.tsx` titles, and `styles.css` lattice styles updated. `npm run build` green; `crates/relix-web-bridge/dashboard-dist` rebuilt + committed (dist-parity gate); `git diff --check` clean. No backend route/policy changed, so no Rust test was required for this slice.

- **Briefs goal-facing Plan view (dashboard-design §6 "workflow checklist" / §7; roadmap DoD "Work reads as a goal-facing plan") — FRONTEND SHIPPED (bounded).** Closes the DoD gap that the Briefs surface "still mostly feels like cards in columns." A frontend-only slice over data that already exists (`/v1/spine/board/:col`, `/v1/spine/briefs/:id`, `/v1/runs`) — **no backend route, capability, policy, or mutation added**, and the existing `BriefDetail` panel is unchanged.
  - **Board / Plan toggle (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Briefs.tsx`).** A segmented control in the Briefs section header drives a URL-state `?view=plan` (Board is the default; an absent/unknown value falls back to Board), preserving the existing `?brief=<id>` selection and the mandate filter. **Board is untouched** — drag/drop, assign, run/echo buttons, latest-run badges, the mandate filter, and the contextual `BriefDetail` panel all behave exactly as before.
  - **Plan view.** Builds a flat visible-card index from ALL loaded board columns AFTER the mandate filter, then renders a **numbered workflow checklist** (`1`, `1.1`, `1.2`; depth-driven indent) with parent/child **nesting** assembled from a bounded relation cache. Each row shows status/priority/assignee/mandate chips, a **blocker chip** (the board card's unresolved same-Guild `blocked_by`, else a loaded Snag count), the **latest-run** state + a deep link to `/runs?run=<id>`, and on any row with visible children a compact **progress strip** (done / running / blocked / remaining / total) — all computed ONLY from the visible loaded window. Clicking a row opens the same detail panel via `?brief=<id>` and highlights + scrolls to the row (the shared `selectedRef`).
  - **Bounded, honest detail fetch.** On entering Plan view (and on board reload / mandate-filter change) it lazily fetches `/v1/spine/briefs/:id` relation detail for the **first 80 visible cards** (`PLAN_DETAIL_CAP`), via `tryGetReport` and the SAME cache + in-flight-guard pattern `Agents.tsx` uses (a present entry — even null/error — means "loaded", so nothing re-fetches; no duplicate loops). Cards beyond the cap render **flat** with a capped note; a card whose detail failed renders flat and the view raises **one** inline warning; a parent whose `subbriefs` extend past the loaded window shows "+N child Brief(s) not in this view" — it never fabricates hidden children or progress. Relation edges are taken from BOTH directions (`parents` + `subbriefs`) but only when both ends are visible, deduped, and cycle-guarded (a relation cycle or multi-parent child renders once).
  - **Board-card progress cue.** A parent board card shows a tiny `▣ done/total done` cue **only once the Plan-view relation cache already exists** (board cards never fetch detail themselves) — computed from the same visible-subtree counts as the Plan view.
  - **Style.** Dense, B&W, no hero/gradients/nested cards; reuses existing `badge`/`muted`/`mono`/`link` classes with a small scoped block in `styles.css` (`.seg`/`.seg-btn`, `.plan-list`/`.plan-row`/`.plan-num`/`.plan-main`/`.plan-progress`/`.plan-cue`). Rows wrap/truncate (no overlap on narrow widths); indent is inline + depth-capped.
  - **Honest limits.** Coverage is the **visible board window** only — there is no whole-tree (beyond the loaded columns) rollup, no cross-route/realtime progress push (Plan is request/response off the existing loads + the run badge map), and relation detail is **cached per session** (a relation added mid-session surfaces on the next board reload of new ids, not instantly). `delegation_depth` is typed/read from the detail but not yet surfaced in a row. No new test was required (frontend-only, no backend authority); `tsc -b` + `vite build` green, dist-parity gate run, `git diff --check` clean.

- **URL-driven Operative deep links — Lattice/Crew land on the exact Operative (dashboard-design §9; roadmap §P2 slice 4) — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** Makes the Lattice's "click a node → govern this Operative" feel like a real product: the Crew (Agents) governance panel is now URL-driven and the Lattice links straight to it. **No backend change** (no new route/authority) — pure frontend on the per-Operative reads that already exist.

- **Operative detail workbench — tabbed employee-record surface on the Crew page (dashboard-design §9; roadmap §P2 slice 4) — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** Promotes the per-Operative detail from an inline row/card expansion into a real product surface: a prominent, tabbed **workbench** for the selected Operative. **No backend change** (no new route/authority) — every tab reads data the page already fetches.
  - **Workbench panel (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Agents.tsx`).** When an Operative is selected (any **Open** button on the Founder/Prime cards or the Operatives table, a Lattice deep link, or `/agents?agent=<id>`), a single bordered panel renders at the top of the Crew page (not a row expansion) with an identity header (name/role/status, mono id, clickable reports-to, adapter) + **Copy link** + **Close**, a tab bar, and a tab body. The panel carries the `selectedRef` and is **scrolled into view** (`block:"nearest"`); the matching roster row/card keeps the `selected` highlight for visual linkage. The old inline `operativeDetail` expansions (Founder card, Prime card, table `colSpan` row) are removed; the table's `Fragment` wrapper + per-row Copy-link are gone (Copy link now lives in the workbench header).
  - **Seven tabs.** **Overview** — role/title/status/adapter/readiness summary, reports-to + a clickable **direct-reports** list (each selects that Operative), a pressure line (open · running), **open assigned Briefs** (filtered from the board-column fetch the page already does, with title + column + a `/briefs` link), and the 3 most recent **Shifts**. **Instructions** — the Operative's **charter / instruction bundle** (company-model §4.5), surfaced **read-only** from the full-profile `agent.keys` read (`/v1/spine/keys/:agent` serializes the whole `AgentProfile`, so it carries `instruction_bundle` even though the pipe-delimited `/v1/agents/:id` detail does not). Rendered (view mode) as bounded, scrollable **preformatted text — never parsed as HTML/markup** — with a small summary (char + line count, and a note that the charter is injected into this Operative's Shifts as a trusted section); an **honest empty state** when no charter is stored yet. **Now editable** (Paperclip-parity employee slice): an **Edit** button opens a bounded textarea (`.op-charter-edit`) pre-filled with the last loaded value; **Save** writes through the existing configure-gated `PATCH /v1/agents/:id { instruction_bundle }` (runtime `agent.update` → `update_agent_field` "instruction_bundle", which preserves `|` via `splitn(3)`, caps at `MAX_BUNDLE = 64*1024`, and **allows an empty value = clear**), **Cancel** restores the last loaded value, and a live char counter guards at `MAX_CHARTER = 64*1024` (no silent truncation — Save is blocked and says why). On success the page **force-refetches** this Operative's detail (`loadDetail(id, true)`) so the new charter + the Configuration tab's `updated_at` render immediately, emits the `actions` invalidation key, and shows an honest result banner; an empty save is reported as a clear. A configure-power denial (or any backend refusal) is surfaced verbatim — **the gate is never bypassed**. **Skills** — the Operative's **procedural memory** (reusable recipes) relevant to it, surfaced **read-only** from the existing `memory.skill_*` catalogue via `GET /v1/skills?agent=<id>&q=<query>&limit=20` (the bridge's `skills::list` → `memory.skill_search`). Each entry renders defensively: name (name/title/id) + status/version/confidence/usage chips when present + a bounded **3-line** description preview + source/updated/id/tags footer (every field optional). A small **filter box** refetches on **Enter / Search only** (never per-keystroke). Robust to a disabled deployment (the bridge's `{available:false, reason}` shell → calm unavailable state), an empty catalogue (honest empty state), and a varied list shape (parsed defensively for `results`/`items`/`skills`/`rows`/raw array via `skillsApi.search`). This is the one tab that fetches beyond the page's shared loads — but it hits an **existing route** (no new backend/authority) and is **tab-gated** (loads only while Skills is open; refetches on Operative/tab change), so closed tabs cost nothing. **No create/update/deprecate UI and no per-Operative skill-assignment editor** — read-only by design. **Permissions** — reuses the intact `operativeDetail(id)` (Keys + capability powers + standing approvals); **nothing governance was removed**. **Runs** — this Operative's Shifts from the page's `/v1/runs` payload (filtered by `agent_id`, newest first): status/trigger/rig/brief/duration/started/result + a deep link to `/runs?run=<id>`; honest note that the list is bounded to the recent `/v1/runs` window. **Budget** — committed monthly Allowance / risk ceiling / max-concurrent / approval-timeout from the cached `/v1/agents/:id` (+ Keys fallback), **explicitly labelled *committed* (capacity reserved), not spent**, with live month-to-date spend routed to the Costs page — **never fabricates a spend figure**. **Configuration** — adapter (the existing editable `rigSelect`) + readiness, autonomy flags (scheduled heartbeat / wake-on-assignment), max-concurrent, org placement (title/department/team/reports-to), identity (subject), created/updated timestamps; the charter is now linked to the Instructions tab as **viewable/editable**, Skills are linked to the Skills tab as **viewable (read-only)**, and a **per-Operative model preference** lane (model name + reasoning/effort) is now **viewable + editable** and consumed by supported CLI adapters (see the dedicated model-preference execution ledger entry below).
  - **State + data behavior.** The active tab is URL-driven (`&tab=<tab>`, default **overview**; an **unknown value falls back to overview without rewriting the URL** — param safety) and **Copy link captures the non-default tab**, so refresh/back/forward and shared links restore the exact view. Selection still resolves the Founder/Prime even when they're carried only on `company.{founder,prime}`, so leadership opens the workbench too; an unknown `?agent=<id>` still renders the honest "no Operative matches …" banner (no crash). All tabs but **Skills** reuse the page's existing fetches — the shared per-Operative detail cache (`loadDetail`, guarded by the cache + in-flight `Set`), `/v1/runs`, and the board columns; the **Skills** tab adds one bounded, **tab-gated** fetch to the **existing** `/v1/skills` route (no new route, no fetch loop) — so there is still **no new fetch loop**. The `AgentDetail` / `Card` / `RunRow` TS interfaces were widened to type fields the same endpoints already return.
  - **Scoped CSS (`apps/dashboard/src/styles.css`).** Small additive, B&W classes only — `.op-wb`/`.op-wb-wrap`/`.op-wb-head` (the panel + header), `.op-tabs`/`.op-tab`/`.op-tab.active`/`.op-tab-n` (underline-style tab bar), `.op-tab-body`, `.op-line` (compact Brief/Shift rows), and `.op-charter` (the bounded, scrollable read-only charter `<pre>` on the Instructions tab) + `.op-charter-edit` (the matching bounded, monospace, vertically-resizable charter editor textarea on the same tab) + `.op-skills`/`.op-skill`/`.op-skill-body` (the read-only Skills tab list + per-skill row + the 3-line-clamped description preview).   - **Standing-approval scope made obvious (roadmap §Phase 3 "make that scope obvious in the dashboard") — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** Where an operator sees the live scope of every standing authority **before** enabling autonomy: open **Agents → an Operative → Permissions tab → Standing approvals**. Each grant now renders its full scope as compact B&W columns instead of just category/used/expiry — **Status** (active / expired / exhausted / spent, derived from `expires_at` + `max_calls`/`calls_used` + `max_cost_micros`/`cost_used_micros`, since the bridge keeps spent/expired rows until revoked), **Unlocks** (the capability `match_category` + the operator note), **Scope** (a friendly `scope_kind` label — category / task / session / method / workspace — plus the concrete bound ref: `task <id>` / `session <id>` / `method*` / a workspace-path glob), **Calls** (`used / max`, `∞` when uncapped), **Spend** (`used / cap` in dollars from the micro-USD fields), **Expires**, and **Granted by**. No backend change — the bridge `StandingRow` already serialized every field (`task_id`/`session_id`/`method_prefix`/`workspace_path_glob`/`max_cost_micros`/`cost_used_micros`/`note`); the dashboard's `Standing` interface + table were simply widened to show them. The backend `agent.standing_approval.revoke` gate stays the authority on who may revoke. This is per-grant revoke for the **arbitrary individual grants** listed on an Operative — it does **NOT** duplicate the **synthetic autonomous-Prime authority** grant/revoke controls, which remain on the Settings → Prime standing-authority panel (a different, special authority id). **Verification:** `npm run build` green (tsc + vite); `powershell -File scripts/check-dashboard-dist.ps1` (dist-parity) clean after rebuild + commit; `git diff --check` clean.   - **Per-Operative model preference lane — stored adapter hint (dashboard-design §9 "model lane"; adapters §3.2/§3.3/§7) — SHIPPED (storage slice; execution now wired — see the consumption pack below).** Closes the §9 model-lane gap *honestly*: an Operative can now carry an optional **model preference** and **reasoning/effort** tier on its profile, viewable + editable on the Configuration tab. *(At the time of this storage slice, execution did NOT consume them — that gap is now closed by the **model-preference execution** pack immediately below; the historical "stored preference only" notes in this entry are superseded by it.)*
    - **Runtime (`crates/relix-runtime/src/nodes/coordinator/agent/store.rs`).** `AgentProfile` gains `model_preference: Option<String>` + `reasoning_effort: Option<String>` (both `#[serde(default)]`, nullable). Two SQLite columns added the same way as every other profile field — `CREATE TABLE` cols + idempotent `ensure_column(... "model_preference"/"reasoning_effort", "TEXT")` so **existing DBs keep working** (legacy rows read NULL → None). Appended last in all SELECTs (`SELECT_AGENT`/`_FOR_TENANT`/`_BY_TENANT` + the two inline `get_by_subject*` reads) and read at positional indices 40/41 in `row_to_agent` (existing indices unchanged). `update_agent_field` gains `model_preference|model` (free text, empty clears, 128-char cap) and `reasoning_effort|effort` (empty clears; else constrained to `minimal/low/medium/high` via the new `is_known_effort`). Both ride the existing `agent.update` → `enforce_configure_key` gate (configure-Key required, self-config denied, tenant-scoped) — **authorization unchanged**.
    - **Serialization.** `agent.keys` (`/v1/spine/keys/:agent`) carries them automatically (serde over the full `AgentProfile`); the pipe-delimited `agent.get` (`/v1/agents/:id`) appends `|model_preference=…|reasoning_effort=…`.
    - **Bridge (`crates/relix-web-bridge/src/agent.rs`).** `AgentDetail` + parser gain both fields; `UpdateAgentRequest` accepts them and forwards via the existing `agent.update` commit loop (empty string clears).
    - **Frontend (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Agents.tsx`).** Configuration tab replaces the "model config not exposed" copy with a compact editor — model free-text input (empty clears) + reasoning/effort `<select>` (default/minimal/low/medium/high) + Save/Cancel + the shared banner — writing through the governed `api.patch('/v1/agents/:id', …)` and force-refetching detail on save. Adapter/Rig selection unchanged. The later execution pack below wires these stored values into supported CLI adapter runs.
    - **Tests.** Runtime: `model_preference_defaults_none_then_set_read_and_clear`, `reasoning_effort_rejects_unknown_tier`, `model_preference_aliases_and_length_cap` (store) + `model_preference_mutation_is_configure_gated` (handlers). Bridge: `update_request_parses_model_prefs_and_empty_clears`, `parse_agent_detail_model_prefs_absent_default_none`, and the round-trip parse test extended.
    - **Honest caveat / remaining work.** *(Superseded.)* This was the remaining work; it is now implemented — see the **model-preference execution** pack below.

- **Per-Operative model preference — CONSUMED by supported CLI adapters (adapters §3.2/§3.3) — SHIPPED.** Closes the prior slice's caveat: the stored `model_preference` / `reasoning_effort` now flow from the assigned Operative's profile into the actual Rig run and onto the supported subscription CLIs' argv. No faked CLI behavior; echo / Gemini / generic Rigs are untouched.
  - **Run contract (`crates/relix-runtime/src/rig/mod.rs`).** `RigRunRequest` gains optional `model_preference` + `reasoning_effort` (with `with_model_preference` / `with_reasoning_effort` builders that normalize empty/whitespace → `None`). Both default to `None`, so every existing construction site stays backward-compatible. A pure `model_flag_args(format, model, effort)` maps the hints to argv **keyed on the Rig's existing `RigOutputFormat`** (the safe Claude-vs-Codex discriminator): `ClaudeStreamJson` → `--model <m>` (Claude Code exposes no headless effort flag, so effort is not mapped); `CodexJsonl` → `--model <m>` + `-c model_reasoning_effort=<effort>`; `Raw` (echo / Gemini / generic) → nothing. `argv_with_model_flags` splices the flags in so a trailing stdin marker (`-`, Codex) stays LAST. `ProcessRig::execute` builds the effective argv via these helpers — **argv arrays only, no shell string**; a value that is empty or contains whitespace/control chars is skipped (defense in depth atop the store's pipe/tab/newline write-time guard), so a malformed preference can never become a stray flag. Timeout / cancellation / secret-redaction behavior is unchanged.
  - **Dispatch wiring (`crates/relix-runtime/src/nodes/coordinator/heartbeat.rs`).** New `RunModelPrefs { model, effort }` (Default = neither). `prepare_claimed_run` (the ONE place a run request is built — shared by manual + autonomous) takes a `RunModelPrefs` and applies it to the request. `preflight_run` stays a backward-compatible wrapper (default prefs); `preflight_run_with_prefs` carries them; `preflight_and_spawn` gains a `prefs` param. The autonomous `dispatch_batch_with_policy` gains a `resolve_model_prefs` closure (the caller owns the agent lookup, mirroring `resolve_rig` — dispatch stays decoupled from the agent store); the simple `dispatch_batch` wrapper passes the default.
  - **Both run paths load the assignee's profile (`controller_runtime.rs`, `agent/handlers.rs`).** The synchronous `brief.run` handler and Prime's Start-to-Shift read `agent.model_preference` / `agent.reasoning_effort` (already loading the profile for the Rig + charter) and pass them into `preflight_and_spawn`; the autonomous heartbeat tick's `resolve_model_prefs` closure loads the same from the agent store. So a configured preference reaches the Rig request on **every** start path.
  - **Adapter availability + refusal unchanged.** An unavailable adapter still refuses before spawn exactly as before (the probe gate is untouched); prefs only affect the argv of a run that was already going to spawn.
  - **Tests.** Rig: `run_request_normalizes_model_and_effort_prefs`, `model_flag_args_maps_per_format`, `model_flag_args_skips_malformed_values`, `claude_argv_appends_model_flag_safely`, `codex_argv_inserts_flags_before_trailing_stdin_marker`, `argv_with_model_flags_is_noop_without_prefs`, `process_rig_run_request_with_prefs_does_not_break_echo_path`. Heartbeat: `dispatch_passes_operative_model_prefs_into_run_request` (a capture Rig proves the stored pref reaches the request through the dispatch chokepoint) + `dispatch_omits_model_prefs_when_operative_has_none`.
  - **Frontend (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Agents.tsx`).** The Configuration-tab copy + save banner now state the preference is **consumed at run time by the supported CLI Rigs** (Claude / Codex map it to `--model`, Codex also `-c model_reasoning_effort`) and that echo / Gemini / generic Rigs ignore it; committed dashboard dist rebuilt.
  - **Honest caveats.** (1) **Claude effort is not mapped** — Claude Code has no documented headless reasoning-effort flag, so only `--model` is applied for the Claude Rig (Codex gets both). (2) The guarded operator retry path (`run.retry` → `open_retry_child`) **now inherits the prefs too** — see the *Retry inherits model prefs + live execution/action streams* entry below; it threads them through `preflight_run_with_prefs`. (3) Mapping is keyed on `RigOutputFormat`, so a custom operator Rig only receives flags if it adopts `ClaudeStreamJson` / `CodexJsonl`; a `Raw` Rig never does. (4) The model name is free text — an invalid model is the CLI's error to report at run time (Relix passes it as a discrete argv value, never a shell token).

- **Approvals hub + real Settings hub (dashboard-design §10; roadmap §P2 slice 8) — FRONTEND SHIPPED (partial).** Net-new operator-control surface + Settings recovery section on data/routes that already exist; no backend change beyond typed client helpers.
  - **Approvals (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Approvals.tsx`, route `/approvals`, Workspace nav + ⌘K palette).** The one place to decide the company's pending governance gates, all REAL and now **typed**: **pending Clearances** from `/v1/spine/clearances` (the unified `coord.approval.pending` queue, now carrying the typed fields `subject_id` / `capability_category` / `expires_at` / `task_id` the bridge preserves from the runtime approval row) are **grouped by type** (Hire/Spawn · Strategy · Budget/Allowance · High-risk/Other) with a per-type **payload summary** (requesting actor, affected subject, capability category, age + expiry window, and the parked-Brief target route), a **filter/search bar**, and a per-group **decision-impact** line. Inline **Approve/Reject** goes through `/v1/spine/clearances/:id/decide` (forwarded under the bridge's verified identity; the runtime cap enforces the real authorisation, applies each side effect exactly once, and refuses re-deciding a terminal approval — surfaced as honest 4xx); **sensitive groups (strategy/budget/high-risk) require a short operator note** before deciding, while hire approvals stay fast. **Direct pending hires** (the `route=direct` `hire` items from `/v1/spine/company/actions`, which carry no Clearance) are approved with the safe-local Rig via `/v1/agents/:id/approve-hire` or declined via `…/reject-hire` (reusing the Action Center's exact wiring), and the card shows the suggested Rig + runnable/needs-Rig + target route. **Budget alerts** (the `budget`-category items) are shown read-only, **labelled by kind** (spend alert vs committed-Allowance plan vs hard-stop, derived from the stable action id) with the embedded percent chip and links to **Costs** + the item's own route — never labelled "decide". Each decision emits the `actions`/`mandates`/`briefs` invalidation keys and reloads. Calm real empty state; an unavailable backend renders an honest state naming the route + reason (never a fabricated row). `Layout.tsx` adds a pending-Clearance count badge on the Approvals nav entry. **Live Clearance stream (follow-up slice).** The hub is now **live**: a dedicated **polling-backed SSE** — `GET /v1/spine/clearances/stream` (bridge `clearances_stream`) — tenant-scopes exactly like the list route by proxying the SAME `coord.approval.pending` capability (captured tenant re-applied per call — no new privilege, no cross-Guild leak), emits an initial `event: clearances` snapshot (the same JSON array the list route returns), then pushes again **only when the parsed queue's fingerprint changes** (pure, unit-tested `clearances_fingerprint`; transient `event: error` keeps retrying; keep-alive `ping`). `Approvals.tsx` subscribes via `subscribeClearances` on mount, renders the Clearance list directly from stream snapshots, shows an honest **live/reconnecting/unavailable** header chip, and **falls back to a bounded ~7s refresh** when the stream can't connect — the existing Refresh button and the decide→invalidate→reload flow are unchanged. The company action feed (direct hires + budget alerts) still uses refresh/polling (no live backend source was fabricated for it). *Honest caveat:* polling-backed SSE (~2.5s, fingerprint-gated) like the interaction/Prime-status streams — NOT a true event bus / websocket. **Honest limits (no new authority):** the typed summary is limited to the fields the runtime records (no free-form resource/scope/payload editor — the runtime stores none); budget alerts have **no inline decide route**, so they only link out; the spawn-Clearance decide **cannot bind a Rig** (only the direct-hire approve can — the card says so and routes to the Operative page); the `approval`-category items of `company.actions` are intentionally NOT re-rendered (they duplicate the Clearance list, which carries the real `approval_id` + decide route).
  - **Settings — Admin · session recovery (`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx`).** A control-plane recovery section that **auto-loads the global runtime-state list** (`GET /v1/runs/runtime-state/list`, capability `rig.runtime_state.list` → store `list_runtime_state_for_tenant(tenant, limit)`): a tenant-scoped table of **every** persisted adapter session in the Guild across ALL Operatives (Operative, Rig, Brief, **masked** session id, status, tokens, cost, updated), newest first, clamped to 200. A client-side filter narrows by Operative/Rig/Brief/status/session fragment; a per-row **guarded Reset** (`POST /v1/runs/runtime-state/reset`) forgets a wedged session — brief-scoped for a row carrying a `brief_key`, behind a typed-confirm (`RESET`) for the dangerous agent-level reset — the durable run ledger/transcripts/artifacts are untouched. This sits on top of the already-real Settings sections (System health, Maintenance & storage, Account, Bridge info `/v1/info`, AI providers `/v1/config/providers`, run-execution sandbox + autonomous heartbeat `/v1/spine/run-config`, Adapter readiness `/v1/adapters`). The per-agent lookup (`GET /v1/runs/runtime-state?agent_id=…`) + reset routes are unchanged. **Honest remaining:** the session id is surfaced only as a masked/truncated summary; Codex now replays same-scope sessions while Claude remains stored-not-replayed; and the per-SESSION reset has no diagnosis of its own (it forgets the row). *(The separate run-level Brief/Shift diagnosis on `brief_runs` — failure-class/retryable/retry-budget — has since shipped; see the **Brief/Shift recovery diagnosis** pack below.)*
  - **Client/wiring + verification.** `api.ts` gains `clearances.list/decide`, `companyActions.list` (typed `CompanyActionItem`/feed), and `runtimeState.get/reset` (all over `tryGetReport`/`api.post` with honest error surfacing). `App.tsx` route, `nav.ts` Workspace entry (`/approvals`, auto-listed in the ⌘K palette via `ALL_NAV`), `Layout.tsx` title + nav badge. `npm run build` green; `crates/relix-web-bridge/dashboard-dist` rebuilt + committed (dist-parity gate); `git diff --check` clean. No backend route/policy changed, so no Rust test was required for this slice.

- **Brief/Shift recovery diagnosis (v1) — first bounded diagnosis layer (IMPLEMENTED).** Implements `docs/relix-execution-and-issue-design.md §3.3b` (Stage-1 *classify* — instant, no LLM, free) for the durable `brief_runs` / Brief-Shift surface. Closes the honestly-tracked gap that recovery cards mapped the refusal taxonomy to an action/route but did **not** classify a true retryable-vs-not and carried **no** per-run failure-class/retry-budget. It is **diagnosis + operator guidance ONLY** — **no** autonomous retry orchestration, **no** blind auto-retry loop, **no** provider quota polling, **no** new branch.
  - **Schema (additive, nullable).** Five columns on `brief_runs` (CREATE + additive `ALTER`): `failure_class TEXT`, `retryable INTEGER` (1/0/NULL), `retry_budget_remaining INTEGER`, `recovery_action TEXT`, `recovery_route TEXT`. Legacy/`running` rows carry NULLs. Surfaced on `RunRecord` (all 4 run SELECTs + `from_row`), `brief.runs`, and the Brief detail `latest_run` (`brief::LatestRun`).
  - **Pure classifiers (`RunDiagnosis::for_terminal` / `for_refusal`, unit-tested).** `for_terminal(status, rig_retryable, run_id)`: a clean `done`/`continued` carries NO scary metadata (`retryable=false`, `recovery_action="none"`, no class/route); `failed` uses the `RigOutcome` retryable signal — `Some(true)` → `transient` + retryable + budget 1 + `retry_later`, `Some(false)` → `permanent` + non-retryable + `inspect_run`, `None` → conservative `unknown`/non-retryable; `cancelled` → `cancelled`/non-retryable; `interrupted` → `interrupted`/retryable (re-claimed automatically) + budget 1. `for_refusal(reason, brief_id, run_id)`: `unassigned` → `precondition`+`assign_agent`+`/briefs?brief=…`, `no_adapter`/`adapter_unavailable` → `adapter_unavailable`+`configure_rig`+`/settings`, `over_allowance` → `budget`+`raise_allowance`+`/agents`, `over_guild_budget` → `budget`+`raise_allowance`+`/costs`, `workspace_error`/`workspace_context_error` → `workspace`+`review_runtime`+`/settings`, unknown → `unknown`+`inspect_run`+`/runs?run=…`; a refusal is **never** retryable (it needs an operator fix first). `failure_class` buckets: `precondition` / `governance` / `budget` / `adapter_unavailable` / `workspace` / `timeout` / `cancelled` / `interrupted` / `transient` / `permanent` / `unknown`.
  - **Stamping at the run chokepoints (no new path).** `record_run_finish` stamps the status-derived terminal diagnosis (so the stale-run-recovery `interrupted` close and `cancelled` get it for free), and the dispatch **finalize** (`execute_ready_inner`) **re-stamps** a real `failed` with the `RigOutcome` retryable signal via `set_run_diagnosis`. `record_refused_run` stamps the refusal diagnosis after the durable row is written — and `over_guild_budget` is now in `refusal_is_durable` (so an autonomous Guild-budget stop earns a durable, diagnosed refused row, matching the per-Operative `over_allowance`). No `done`/`continued` gets fabricated recovery metadata beyond `retryable=false`/`recovery_action="none"`.
  - **Action Center.** `failed_item` now **prefers the durable diagnosis metadata** (`recovery_action` → humanized label, `recovery_route`) when stamped and **falls back** to the older refusal-reason map for legacy rows; it rides `failure_class` + `retryable` + `retry_budget_remaining` on the `ActionItem` (new optional fields) so the dashboard renders an honest recovery-class chip + retryable badge + budget. Conservative: a refusal is never marked retryable; no retry button is minted.
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Runs.tsx`: the `RunRecord` type gains the five fields; the collapsed row shows a failure-class chip (for non-refused terminal failures), and the expanded run shows a restrained **Recovery** strip — failure-class + retryable/not-retryable badge + remaining budget + the recommended action, with a **Fix setup ↗** link to the governed route only when the action is a setup fix (never a fake retry button; `inspect_run`/`none` show no button). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Runtime: `diagnose_refusal_maps_each_reason_to_stable_class_action_route` + `diagnose_terminal_retryable_vs_not_and_clean_success` (pure classifier), `record_refused_run_persists_diagnosis_metadata` + `record_run_finish_stamps_terminal_diagnosis` (persistence + the finalize re-stamp), and the existing tenant-isolation run-read tests are unchanged. Action Center: `failed_card_uses_durable_diagnosis_metadata_when_present` + `failed_card_falls_back_to_refusal_mapping_without_metadata`. Full `relix-runtime --lib` green (4019); `relix-web-bridge spine::tests` green; `cargo clippy` clean on the touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated warnings only); `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** Stage-2 (auto-retry lane + a cheap LLM diagnostic pass + the one-click Inbox decision card) is NOT built — this is the free, instant Stage-1 classification only. The per-SESSION reset still has no diagnosis of its own (it forgets the row). No provider quota polling; the finer `blocked` sub-reasons are still not classified. *(Bounded follow-ups have since shipped: guarded operator Shift retry, and Codex same-scope session resume. This is still NOT a blind auto-retry loop and NOT an LLM diagnostic pass.)*

- **Guarded operator Shift retry (Stage-2, bounded v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Implements the operator-triggered slice of `docs/relix-execution-and-issue-design.md §3.3b` (the Stage-2b *Retry now* choice) on the durable `brief_runs` surface. It turns the Stage-1 retryable verdict into a real, **one-click** recovery action — **NOT** a blind auto-retry loop, **NOT** a company planner, **NOT** an LLM diagnostic pass, **NOT** provider quota polling. The runtime **refuses** if a retry is unsafe or stale.
  - **Schema (additive, nullable).** Two columns on `brief_runs` (CREATE + additive `ALTER`): `retried_from_run_id TEXT` (the source run a retry CHILD was started from) and `retry_attempt INTEGER` (the child's attempt = source + 1; a fresh run is NULL). Legacy rows stay NULL. A **partial UNIQUE index** `brief_runs_retry_lineage(retried_from_run_id) WHERE retried_from_run_id IS NOT NULL` (created AFTER the ALTER so upgraded DBs migrate cleanly) enforces **at-most-one child per source** at the DB level. Surfaced on `RunRecord` (all 4 run SELECTs + `from_row`).
  - **Pure guard (`TaskStore::retry_precheck`, unit-tested).** Tenant-scoped EXACTLY like other run reads (a cross-Guild / unknown id → `NotFound`, no existence leak). The duplicate check runs FIRST (`existing_retry_child` → `AlreadyRetried{child}`).
