Eligibility requires ALL of: terminal **failure-like** status (`failed`/`interrupted` — a `done`/`continued`/`cancelled`/`refused`/`running` refuses), `retryable == true`, `retry_budget_remaining > 0`, a non-empty `brief_id` that still names a Brief in the SAME Guild. Whether the Brief is currently claimed/running is NOT decided here — the shared preflight Claim enforces single-owner (`already_running` → 409).
  - **Orchestration reuses the existing run path (`heartbeat::open_retry_child`).** On `Eligible` it calls the SAME preflight chokepoint as `brief.run` (same assignee/adapter resolution, Claim, workspace prep, ledger row, governance, bridge-back token) — never duplicating Rig execution. *(Update: it now calls `preflight_run_with_prefs` so the retry child inherits the assignee's stored model/effort — see the streams entry below.)* Only AFTER the child's Claim is won + its row opened does it stamp the lineage (`link_retry_child`) and chronicle `brief.retry_requested` (Brief) + a `retry_started` run event (child) carrying the source id + attempt. A child row is never created without a won Claim.
  - **Capability + bridge.** `run.retry` (arg: source run id) is registered in `controller_runtime.rs`, composes the assignee's Rig/charter prompt exactly like `brief.run`, and on a committed retry returns `{status:"running", run_id:<child>, retried_from_run_id, retry_attempt}` immediately while the blocking adapter runs on a background thread. `POST /v1/runs/:run_id/retry` (`spine::run_retry` + `retry_response`) maps outcomes honestly: started/`already_retried` → **200** (idempotent already-retried returns the EXISTING child id so the dashboard can navigate to it), `already_running` Claim conflict → **409** (never retry blindly), every precondition refusal (`not_failed`/`not_retryable`/`no_retry_budget`/`no_brief`/`brief_missing`/adapter/workspace) → **400** with the reason, not-found/cross-tenant → **404** (no leak). No new policy/boot allow rule was needed (the run-control capabilities are not in a method allow-list).
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Runs.tsx`: `RunRecord` gains `retried_from_run_id`/`retry_attempt`; the expanded Recovery strip shows a **Retry Shift** button only when `retryEligible` (terminal failed/interrupted + `retryable` + budget) **and** no child is already surfaced in the list (`retriedSources`); an already-retried source links to its child instead, and a child run's header shows a "retry of <source> · attempt N" link. On success it banners the child id + navigates to it; a refusal surfaces honestly (no hidden failure).
  - **Action Center recovery card (cockpit) — IMPLEMENTED.** The Overview Action Center now surfaces the SAME guarded retry from the cockpit, so recovery no longer routes only to Runs (Paperclip-style control plane: act where the backend already knows the safe action). `agent/action_center.rs` `failed_item(r, has_retry_child)` carries the source `run_id` + `action_api = "POST /v1/runs/<run_id>/retry"` **only** when the run is retry-eligible from its OWN durable diagnosis — terminal failure-like (`failed`/`interrupted`) + `retryable == true` + a positive `retry_budget_remaining` — **and** `has_retry_child == false`. This **mirrors `retry_precheck`** so the card never offers a retry the route would refuse. **Approach chosen for the duplicate guard:** the Action Center DOES know whether a child exists — the handler builds `retried_sources` (every `retried_from_run_id` in the tenant's run list, like the Runs page's `retriedSources`) and passes `has_retry_child`, on TOP of the existing latest-run-per-Brief dedupe (a retried source's newer child is the latest row, so the source is never surfaced anyway). So `action_api` is emitted only when genuinely safe — not "always emit, let the route return `already_retried`". A refused / non-retryable / no-budget / already-retried / no-run-id item carries NO retry metadata. The deep link to Runs is **kept intact**. The model addition is one conservative optional field (`run_id`); `company.actions` is a `json_passthrough` in the bridge, so the new field rides along with **no bridge source change**. `apps/dashboard/src/api.ts` `CompanyActionItem` + the Overview local `ActionItem` gain `run_id` (+ recovery fields); `Overview.tsx` `ActionCenter` renders a compact **Retry Shift** button next to the existing inspect link for `failed_or_refused` items with `run_id`, reusing the Runs page's retry client style — on success it banners the child id with an "Open run →" link (and says so for `already_retried`); a refusal surfaces honestly. No global state library; no blind auto-retry.
  - **Tests.** Runtime (`heartbeat::tests`): `retry_opens_exactly_one_child_and_links_lineage`, `duplicate_retry_returns_existing_child_without_spawning_another`, `non_retryable_failed_run_refuses_retry`, `cross_tenant_retry_denied_as_not_found`. Action Center (`agent::action_center::tests`): `failed_card_carries_guarded_retry_action_when_retry_eligible` (retryable failed/interrupted run carries `run_id` + `POST …/retry`), `failed_card_omits_retry_action_when_not_eligible` (non-retryable / no-budget / non-failure-like carry none), `failed_card_suppresses_retry_action_when_a_child_already_exists` (duplicate guard), `failed_card_falls_back_to_refusal_mapping_without_metadata` (a refusal carries no retry action). Bridge (`spine::tests`): `retry_response_maps_each_outcome_to_an_honest_status`. `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** Still **no blind auto-retry loop** (the Action Center card exposes the run id + a safe action, but every retry is one explicit operator click through the governed route that re-checks all preconditions), **no LLM diagnostic pass / Inbox decision card** (the other Stage-2b choices — Block/Reassign/Investigate — are not built), **no provider quota polling**, and **no auto-retry on the autonomous heartbeat path** (this is operator-triggered only). A retry-of-a-retry is allowed per-run (each source can be retried at most once), bounded by the same eligibility guard.

- **Retry inherits model prefs + live execution/action streams — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked retry-preference caveat AND extends the live-snapshot pattern (already shipped for Clearances / interactions / Prime status) to the execution + action surfaces. No new data semantics, no new event table, no new privilege — every stream composes an EXISTING read capability under the same auth/session/tenant scope, polling-backed + fingerprint-gated like the others.
  - **Retry inherits model prefs (`relix-execution-and-issue-design §3.3b` / adapters §3.2/§3.3).** `heartbeat::open_retry_child` now takes a `RunModelPrefs` and calls `preflight_run_with_prefs` (was `preflight_run`), so a retry child runs on the SAME model the original Shift would. The `run.retry` capability (`controller_runtime.rs`) resolves the retry child's assignee with a **tenant-scoped** Operative lookup (`get_agent_for_tenant`, the caller has a tenant) and threads `model_preference` / `reasoning_effort` in — exactly like `brief.run`. Retry **eligibility semantics are unchanged** (the `retry_precheck` guard is untouched); only the child's run request gains the prefs. An Operative with no preference stays clean (default `RunModelPrefs`).
  - **`GET /v1/runs/stream?limit=N` (`spine::runs_stream`).** Snapshot stream for the Active Runs feed — proxies the SAME `brief.runs` read the `/v1/runs` list route serves (tenant captured at open, re-applied per tick via `CURRENT_TENANT.scope`), truncates to the most-recent `limit` rows (`truncate_runs_snapshot`, default 50, clamp 1..=100; `brief.runs` already caps at 100), emits `event: runs` immediately + on every fingerprint change, safe with zero runs, `event: error` keeps retrying, keep-alive `ping`. Registered before `/v1/runs/:run_id` (static path wins in matchit).
  - **`GET /v1/spine/company/actions/stream` (`spine::company_actions_stream`).** Snapshot stream for the Action Center — proxies the SAME `company.actions` read the list route serves (tenant re-applied per tick), emits the feed verbatim as `event: actions` on every change. Takes **no `limit`** on purpose: the feed has its own internal cap + honest `truncated` flag, so client-side truncation would falsify that flag — it mirrors the endpoint exactly.
  - **Policy.** No boot-policy change — `brief.runs` and `company.actions` are already in `scripts/check-boot-policy-coverage.ps1`; the streams reuse the identical capabilities under the same auth.
  - **Dashboard.** `api.ts` gains `subscribeRuns` + `subscribeCompanyActions` (EventSource, capped-backoff reconnect, honest conn states, same shape as `subscribeClearances`). `Runs.tsx` renders the pushed run snapshot directly while the stream is `live` (no re-fetch), falling back to the mount-load + manual Refresh otherwise; the existing live chip now reflects the runs stream. `Overview.tsx` subscribes the Action Center to `subscribeCompanyActions` (replacing the run-event change-trigger), keeping the bounded 20s poll + invalidation-bus as the convergence fallback so the feed never regresses. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Runtime (`heartbeat::tests`): `retry_child_inherits_operative_model_prefs` (a capture Rig proves the pref reaches the retry child's request) + `retry_child_stays_clean_when_operative_has_no_prefs`; the existing retry tests (`retry_opens_exactly_one_child_and_links_lineage`, etc.) are updated for the new arg. Bridge (`spine::tests`): `truncate_runs_snapshot_keeps_the_most_recent_rows` + `truncate_runs_snapshot_is_safe_with_no_runs_and_non_arrays`. Bridge mini-mesh (`runs_stream_mini_mesh_test`): boots a fake coordinator and asserts `/v1/runs` passthrough + the two streams emit their initial `event: runs` (truncated to `limit=1`) / `event: actions` snapshots over real SSE.
  - **Honest scope.** Polling-backed SSE (~2.5s, fingerprint-gated) like the Clearances / interactions / Prime-status streams — **NOT** a true websocket / event push. The runs stream re-applies the captured tenant per tick and the runtime recent-run ledger now filters by that tenant, so the Active Runs feed does not surface another Guild's Shift rows. Claude reasoning-effort is still unmapped (no headless flag).

- **Codex subscription session resume — same-scope only — IMPLEMENTED (Claude stays caveated).** Closes the honestly-tracked "captured `session_id` is stored but not replayed" gap (adapters §3.3) for the Codex Rig, narrowly and safely. **Lookup (`TaskStore::resume_session_for`, `coordinator/mod.rs`).** At run-commit time `prepare_claimed_run` (`coordinator/heartbeat.rs`, the ONE shared chokepoint every start path funnels through — manual `brief.run`, Prime Start-to-Shift, the autonomous heartbeat, and the guarded `run.retry` child) looks up the stored `session_id` for the EXACT `(tenant, Operative, Rig, Brief)` pairing — the same 4-tuple `agent_runtime_state` is keyed on, with the **tenant resolved from the Brief itself** via the same `COALESCE(t.tenant_id,'default')` expression `record_run_runtime_state` writes with, so a session stored under a different tenant / Operative / Rig / unrelated Brief can never cross in, and an unknown Brief resolves to no tenant → no match. Best-effort: any miss/error simply runs fresh. It threads the id onto the new optional `RigRunRequest.resume_session_id` (builder `with_resume_session_id`, normalized empty→None — backward-compatible default `None`). **Argv mapping (`rig::argv_with_resume`).** Keyed on `RigOutputFormat` like `model_flag_args`: **Codex (`CodexJsonl`)** maps `codex exec resume [OPTIONS] <session> -` — `resume` is spliced in right after the leading `exec`, existing flags remain before the session id, the trailing stdin `-` marker stays last (so the prompt still reads from stdin), and it composes with the model/effort flags (model flags also remain before the session id). It only transforms a recognizably-Codex `exec …` argv. **Claude (`ClaudeStreamJson`) is intentionally NOT mapped** — Claude Code resolves a `--print --resume` session from the run's working directory and Relix runs every Shift in a fresh per-run scoped workspace, so a resumed Claude session would not reliably resolve; the Claude Rig still captures + persists its `session_id` (so the recovery table shows it) but does not replay it. **Raw / echo / Gemini / generic ignore resume.** **Security.** The session id is treated as **adapter state, not user input**, but is still validated before becoming a discrete argv element (`clean_session_id`: trim, reject empty / any whitespace-or-control char / a leading `-` flag-injection shape) → an invalid id is skipped and the run starts fresh rather than spawning malformed argv; it is never logged or surfaced beyond the existing masked runtime-state recovery table; timeout / cancel / redaction / model-preference behavior is unchanged. **Tests.** Rig (`rig::tests`): `run_request_normalizes_resume_session`, `resume_argv_maps_codex_after_exec_keeping_stdin_marker`, `resume_argv_unmapped_for_claude_and_raw`, `resume_argv_skips_absent_or_malformed_session`, `resume_and_model_flags_compose_for_codex`. Store (`coordinator::tests`): `resume_session_for_isolates_tenant_agent_rig_brief` (exact match resumes; different Operative/Rig/Brief, a NULL session, and cross-tenant all yield None). Heartbeat (`heartbeat::tests`): `dispatch_resumes_a_stored_compatible_session` (a capture Rig proves a compatible stored session reaches the dispatch request) + `dispatch_ignores_incompatible_stored_sessions` (a different-Operative / different-Rig session does not). **Honest scope / still a gap.** It is **adapter-thread continuation, not SOL durable replay** (the SOL VM is still synchronous; no flow snapshot/replay) — resume hands the *agent* its prior conversation thread, it does not replay Relix's own flow; **Claude resume stays unmapped** until a stable per-line-of-work workspace exists for the Claude Rig; no provider quota polling; no new wire/dashboard surface (the field is internal adapter state).

- **Opt-in autonomous retry lane (Stage-2a, bounded v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Implements the autonomous side of `docs/relix-execution-and-issue-design.md §3.3 / §3.3b` (the Stage-2a *auto-retry lane* — "re-wake the same agent … bounded by a generous but finite cap … infinite try-until-it-works is disallowed") + the §7 LOCKED decision #4 (conservative recovery). It moves toward Paperclip-style self-healing **without** becoming a blind runaway loop, and **without inventing a second retry path** — it drives the SAME guarded `open_retry_child` chokepoint the operator one-click uses. **Default OFF.**
  - **Opt-in switch (default OFF + bounded).** `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_RECOVERY` (off by default; `1`/`true`/`yes`/`on`), paced by `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_RECOVERY_INTERVAL_SECS` (default 30), bounded per tick by `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_RECOVERY_MAX` (default 1, clamp `1..=10`). Parsed by pure helpers `heartbeat::parse_autonomous_recovery_enabled` / `parse_autonomous_recovery_max` (unit-tested: `None` ⇒ disabled, max clamps to 1..=10). The loop is spawned in `controller_runtime.rs` only when enabled, **independent of `RELIX_HEARTBEAT_ENABLED`**.
  - **Selection (`TaskStore::list_autonomous_retry_candidates`, tenant-aware, bounded).** A cheap SQL pre-filter whose WHERE **mirrors `retry_precheck` exactly**: `status IN (failed, interrupted)`, `retryable = 1`, `retry_budget_remaining > 0`, a non-empty `brief_id` whose Brief still exists (`JOIN tasks`), NOT operator-`discarded`, and **no existing retry child** (`NOT EXISTS` — the durable idempotency guard). `tenant=Some(g)` scopes to one Guild; `tenant=None` returns all Guilds, each candidate carrying its OWN Brief's tenant. Ordered oldest-first (FIFO), clamped to a small page. A companion pure predicate `heartbeat::autonomous_retry_eligible(run, has_child)` documents the same rule DB-free for unit tests.
  - **Orchestration reuses the operator path (`heartbeat::autonomous_recovery_tick`).** Selects up to `max` candidates and, for each the caller approves, calls the SHARED `open_retry_child_with_provenance(…, RetryProvenance::Autonomous)` — the same `retry_precheck` gate, Claim, workspace prep, ledger row, model prefs, **Codex same-scope session resume**, duplicate-child guard, and budget/refusal semantics as the operator retry — then executes the committed child synchronously (the tick runs inside `spawn_blocking`, exactly like `dispatch_batch`). `open_retry_child` was refactored into a thin operator-provenance wrapper over `open_retry_child_with_provenance` (the one shared body); the only behavioral difference is the chronicled provenance — an autonomous retry writes a **distinct `brief.autonomous_retry`** Brief event (vs the operator `brief.retry_requested`) + a provenance-tagged `retry_started` run event.
  - **Per-candidate policy stays in the controller (decoupled, like `dispatch_batch`'s closures).** The tick takes a `decide` closure returning `Skip` / `Proceed(RetryInputs)`. The production closure resolves the assignee's Rig + charter-aware prompt + model/effort prefs IDENTICALLY to `run.retry`, and **skips quietly** (no retry, no event — never per-tick spam) when the Operative is not `active`, its `wake_on_timer` is off, or it is over budget per the SAME `heartbeat::dispatch_budget_admits` gate (per-Operative Allowance + additive Guild budget) the autonomous **dispatch** enforces — so the autonomous lane can never spend past a budget hard-stop. `tenant=None` in production (recover all Guilds), each candidate retried under its own derived tenant (no cross-Guild leak).
  - **Observable.** `open_retry_child` chronicles the child on the Brief + the child run transcript (now provenance-tagged); the controller logs an INFO with `opened`/`considered` counts only when a child is opened. Skips/refusals are in-memory `RecoveryRecord`s (returned for logging/tests), NOT durable per-tick events.
  - **Dashboard / API.** `run.workspace_config` (passthrough → `GET /v1/spine/run-config`) gains `autonomous_recovery_enabled` + `autonomous_recovery_max`; `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx` renders an enabled/disabled badge + per-tick bound + an honest description next to the heartbeat status. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Runtime (`heartbeat::tests`): `autonomous_recovery_switch_is_off_and_bounded_by_default` (default-off + max clamp), `autonomous_recovery_selection_only_includes_eligible_runs` (includes retryable failed + interrupted; EXCLUDES non-retryable / exhausted-budget / refused / discarded / clean-done / already-retried), `autonomous_recovery_tick_opens_one_child_and_is_idempotent` (one child, distinct `brief.autonomous_retry` chronicle, second tick opens none), `autonomous_recovery_disabled_lane_creates_no_retry` (default-off ⇒ no retry while an eligible candidate exists), `autonomous_recovery_is_tenant_isolated` (a guild-a tick retries only guild-a's run, guild-b untouched). The existing operator-retry tests are unchanged (operator path still chronicles `brief.retry_requested`). `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `relix-runtime --lib` retry/heartbeat green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (pre-existing `maintenance.rs` warnings only); `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** **No LLM diagnostic pass** (Stage-2b's cheap diagnostic + Inbox decision card are NOT built — a run lacking durable diagnosis or with an ambiguous verdict is simply not retried; the diagnosis is still the pure Stage-1 classifier and the lane never reclassifies) and **no provider quota polling**. A source is retried **at most once** by the lane (the small `retry_budget_remaining` is not an auto-retry tally), so there is no growing-backoff escalation chain yet. The retry **child** is committed through the shared preflight, so it carries the shared run trigger like the operator retry child — the autonomous provenance lives in the Chronicle event, not a distinct run-trigger value.

- **Opt-in autonomous Prime driver (bounded v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the old manually-driven Prime/company-flow caveat (company-model §5.4/§8.2 the Action Center "next governed step"; §12.5/§12.5B the Prime planner + `prime.start`). It turns the **guided** driver (operator clicks "Advance one step" repeatedly) into an opt-in **autonomous loop** that drives already-**approved** work forward on a timer — **without** becoming a self-approving strategist, and **without inventing a new runner**: every action goes through the SAME governed handler the operator click uses. **Default OFF.**
  - **Opt-in switch (default OFF + bounded).** The first slice used boot-time `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME` (off by default; `1`/`true`/`yes`/`on`, case-insensitive, trimmed), paced by `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_INTERVAL_SECS` (default 30, min 1), bounded per tick by `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX` (default 1, clamp `1..=10`). The later **Prime Runtime Autonomy Switch** below supersedes the env-only UX: the loop is now spawned as a dormant watcher when `SpineStore` exists, and it wakes per Guild from the persisted runtime toggle or globally from the env override.
  - **Discovery (`SpineStore::list_approved_prime_proposals` + `list_active_mandates`, tenant-aware, bounded).** Each tick discovers candidates with bounded tenant-scoped queries (clamped, oldest-first, never an unbounded scan): standing-approvable `proposed` proposals first (offered only with a live `prime.proposal.approve` grant), then approved Prime proposals that materialised a Mandate (these carry Start), then live (`planned`/`active`) Mandates not already covered by a proposal. This **deterministic discovery order is the default**, and is preserved byte-for-byte as the FALLBACK whenever the opt-in **Prime Executive Prioritization v1** layer (below) is off, unavailable, or returns invalid output. `tenant=None` spans all Guilds (each row carries its own `tenant_id`); `tenant=Some(g)` scopes to one Guild. The controller passes `None` (drive all Guilds), each candidate processed under its **own** derived tenant.
  - **Tick (`prime_driver::autonomous_prime_tick`, pure of sleeping — unit-testable).** Re-classifies each candidate with the SAME `compute_next_step` logic `prime.next_step` serves and applies at most `max` safe actions, returning one `PrimeAutonomyRecord` (target id / kind, phase, action, outcome `advanced`/`started`/`skipped`/`blocked`, reason) per candidate considered. It executes the same two safe steps as `prime.advance` — `create_team_plan` / `orchestrate_assign_ready` — by building the SAME advance call (`handle_prime_advance`, which re-reads + stale-guards), and for an already-approved proposal at `ready_to_start` it starts ready Briefs through the **existing `handle_prime_start`** path. The synthetic caller is a `prime_driver::autonomous_prime_ctx` (role `operator`, scoped to the candidate's tenant) — the **Board's sovereign automation** over already-approved work, granting no new authority: the handlers' own gates (strategy approved, ready team, no pending hires/Clearances, active assignee, adapter, Claim) all still apply, exactly as when the operator clicks.
  - **Budget safety on auto-start (the documented narrowing).** `prime.start` is the sovereign **manual** path and deliberately takes **no** budget gate (the Board can always run an over-budget Brief by hand). To honor "do not bypass budget gates" at the **autonomous** boundary, `prime_driver::start_budget_admitted` re-imposes the SAME per-Brief autonomous gate the heartbeat applies (`heartbeat::dispatch_budget_admits` — per-Operative Allowance + additive Guild budget, same metrics ledger + canonical calendar-month window) over the proposal's currently-ready Briefs **before** calling `handle_prime_start`; if **any** ready Brief is over budget the whole autonomous start is refused (`blocked`, recorded) and left to the operator's sovereign manual Start (and the heartbeat, which gates per Brief). Inert (allows) when metrics/spine are unavailable, mirroring the heartbeat.
  - **Default approval behavior.** A candidate at `needs_approval` (proposal/strategy), `needs_hire_approval` (pending hire/Clearance), or `blocked` is recorded `blocked`/`skipped` and **left untouched** unless the later standing-authority layer has a live matching grant for that exact category. With no grant the loop greenlights no proposal, strategy, hire, spawn Clearance, budget, or arbitrary approval, and writes **no** event for a skipped gate (so an idle loop never spams the Chronicle). A **bare Mandate** (one reached `ready_to_start` with **no** owning Prime proposal) now has its ready same-tenant Briefs **started by the loop itself** (action `start_mandate`) through the **same shared guarded run pipeline** the heartbeat dispatcher and `prime.start` use (`heartbeat::preflight_and_spawn_with_trigger` → `preflight_run_with_prefs_trigger` → `prepare_claimed_run` → `execute_ready`): claims, the duplicate-run guard, the live adapter probe, scoped workspace prep, the durable `brief_runs` ledger, bridge-token minting, board advancement, and Chronicle (`prime.autonomous_mandate_start` on the Mandate's root Brief, with the count of Shifts started). No second run system is invented — the run is stamped as an **autonomous/heartbeat** trigger (not dashboard `manual`); the ready set is read tenant-scoped via `TaskStore::list_ready_briefs_for_tenant` and filtered to the Mandate (no cross-Guild Brief is selected); the **same autonomous budget hard-stop** (`heartbeat::dispatch_budget_admits` against each ready Brief) blocks the **whole** start with **zero** runs if any ready Brief is over budget; an already-claimed/running Brief is never double-started (it is excluded from the ready set and the single-owner Claim/duplicate-start guard backstops it); and it counts exactly **one** tick action only when at least one run actually starts.
  - **Idempotent + tenant-safe + observable.** Each tick re-classifies live state, so `create_team_plan` only fires while unplanned, `orchestrate_assign_ready` reuses Briefs by source marker (no duplicate tree), and an already-claimed/running Brief is never double-started (the Claim excludes it from the ready set). A real action chronicles a distinct `prime.autonomous_advance` / `prime.autonomous_start` event on the Mandate's parent Brief (only when a Brief exists). The controller logs an INFO with `advanced`/`started`/`considered` counts only when something actually happened.
  - **Dashboard / API.** `run.workspace_config` (passthrough → `GET /v1/spine/run-config`) gains `autonomous_prime_enabled` + `autonomous_prime_max` + `autonomous_prime_interval_secs`; `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx` renders an enabled/disabled badge + per-tick bound + interval + an honest description next to the heartbeat + recovery rows. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Runtime `heartbeat::tests`: `autonomous_prime_switch_is_off_and_bounded_by_default` (default-off + truthy spellings + max clamp). `prime_driver::tests`: `autonomous_tick_with_zero_bound_does_nothing` (no action at the lower bound), `autonomous_tick_advances_needs_team_plan` (records a Team Plan through the governed route), `autonomous_tick_advances_needs_orchestration` (creates + assigns the Brief tree), `autonomous_tick_orchestration_is_idempotent` (repeated ticks never duplicate the tree), `autonomous_tick_does_not_auto_approve_pending_hire` (records `blocked`, hire stays `pending`, no Briefs), `autonomous_tick_is_tenant_isolated` (a tick for Guild `other` never touches a `default` Mandate), and `autonomous_tick_starts_ready_approved_proposal` (end-to-end starter-crew → propose → approve → the loop starts ready Shifts through `prime.start`, and a second tick does not double-start). `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `maintenance.rs`/cleanup-log warnings only); `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** **Constrained reasoning only** — by default the autonomous driver only executes the deterministic next governed step over already-approved work (and, with the opt-in **Prime Deliberation v1** layer below, a model may *choose among* the already-computed governed actions — confirm-or-hold — but never invent a goal or call a tool; with **Prime Strategy Authoring v1** below, a model may author only the *text* of a `proposed` strategy doc; and with **Prime Executive Prioritization v1** below, a model may choose only the *order* in which a bounded tick spends its budget across the already-computed legal candidates — or hold the queue); it does **not** approve a strategy, decide which person/identity to hire, greenlight a Clearance, choose the action, or take a goal from raw intent to done on its own. Proposing, approving, hire/Clearance greenlights, and the Guild-budget ceiling stay the human/Board's. The autonomous **start** is the documented narrowing of "use `prime.start`": it reuses that exact governed path but adds the autonomous budget pre-gate (since `prime.start` itself has none), and a single over-budget ready Brief conservatively blocks the whole proposal's auto-start (the heartbeat still gates per Brief). The default Prime is still rules; a model shapes only the *interpretation* of a propose request.

- **Prime standing authority (bounded v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Adds a SECOND, grant-gated autonomy layer on top of the approved-work driver above (company-model standing-approval semantics): the autonomous Prime loop may take a specific governed **approval** action on the Board's behalf — but ONLY when the Board has granted a bounded `standing_approvals` row for it. **Not a loop-toggle bypass: the runtime toggle / env override only wakes the loop; each approval category acts only while a standing grant exists for that Guild.** With no grant, every approval gate stays human exactly as before — the normal approval system is unchanged.
  - **Synthetic authority subject + categories (`prime_driver`).** Constant `AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_AUTHORITY = "__relix_autonomous_prime__"` (a stable ASCII id used only as the `agent_id` of `standing_approvals` rows — never a real Operative) and seven narrow categories: `CATEGORY_PROPOSAL_APPROVE = "prime.proposal.approve"`, `CATEGORY_HIRE_APPROVE = "prime.hire.approve"`, `CATEGORY_CLEARANCE_APPROVE = "prime.clearance.approve"`, `CATEGORY_STRATEGY_APPROVE = "prime.strategy.approve"`, `CATEGORY_RUN_REVIEW_ACCEPT = "prime.run.review_accept"`, `CATEGORY_RUN_APPLY = "prime.run.apply"`, `CATEGORY_PLAN_PACKAGE_APPROVE = "prime.plan_package.approve"` (all in `STANDING_AUTHORITY_CATEGORIES`, so the `prime.standing_authority` read surface + dashboard see them). The Board grants/revokes via the EXISTING `agent.standing_approval.*` routes (`POST`/`DELETE /v1/agents/__relix_autonomous_prime__/standing-approvals`), which already accept any `agent_id`/category — no new mutation route was needed. Standing semantics reused as-is: tenant-scoped, expiry, `max_calls`/`max_cost_micros`; the loop **consumes** one call per autonomous action via `consume_active_standing_for` (an unlimited grant returns `Some` without decrementing).
  - **Proposal approval (`autonomous_prime_tick` Pass 0 + `SpineStore::list_proposed_prime_proposals`).** A new bounded, oldest-first, tenant-aware query lists `status='proposed'` proposals. For each whose **own** Guild has active `prime.proposal.approve`, the tick calls the existing `handle_prime_approve` (no duplicate materialization) and consumes the grant. Status-filtered + tenant-stamped ⇒ a rejected/already-approved/cross-Guild proposal is never approved; once approved it leaves the proposed set ⇒ a re-tick neither re-approves nor double-consumes. Chronicles `prime.autonomous_approve` on a created Brief.
  - **Hire activation (`process_candidate`, `needs_hire_approval`).** A pending hire surfaced by the Mandate's own Team Plan (`compute_readiness.pending_hires` — attributable to Prime/company planning by construction) is activated via the EXISTING `AgentStore::approve_hire_with_rig` (atomic, tenant-scoped, no-clobber) bound to `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_HIRE_RIG` (default `echo`, `prime_driver::configured_autonomous_hire_rig`). The Rig is validated against the known-Rig allowlist **in the tick**; an unknown Rig is `skipped` (hire left pending, grant not consumed), never silently bound. Requires active `prime.hire.approve`; chronicles `prime.autonomous_hire_approve`.
  - **Spawn-Clearance greenlight (`handlers::autonomous_approve_spawn_clearance`).** A pending spawn Clearance referenced by the Mandate's Team Plan (`compute_readiness.pending_clearances`) is approved by REUSING the store decide path: `AgentStore::decide_approval(Approved)` plus a runnable hire-activation hop (`approve_hire_with_rig`) bound to the same configured safe Rig as bare hires. It refuses any **non-`SPAWN_CLEARANCE_METHOD`** approval (never a tool/budget/high-risk row), validates the Rig allowlist in the tick, is tenant-scoped (no existence leak), and is idempotent. Requires active `prime.clearance.approve`; clearances are handled before bare hires (mirrors `classify_mandate` priority). Chronicles `prime.autonomous_clearance_approve`.
  - **Strategy approval (`process_candidate`, `needs_approval` + `mandate.strategy.approve`).** When the classified next step is a **proposed** Mandate strategy (`step.phase == "needs_approval"`, `step.action_api == "mandate.strategy.approve"`, `strategy_status == "proposed"`) and the candidate's **own** Guild has active `prime.strategy.approve`, the tick approves it through the EXISTING `handlers::handle_strategy_approve` (`SpineStore::approve_strategy`, **no** new handler, **no** store bypass) and consumes one grant call (action `approve_strategy`, outcome `advanced`). The store's approve is `UPDATE … WHERE status='proposed'`, so a **rejected or missing** strategy is refused (left as-is, grant not consumed) and never re-proposed — a human rejection stays final. Without the grant the step is recorded `blocked` and the proposed strategy is untouched. Bounded (skips with no consume when the per-tick action budget is spent) and idempotent (post-approval the next step is no longer `needs_approval`). Drafting (`propose_strategy`) and approving are **separate** per-candidate actions, so a bare Mandate drafts on one tick and approves on the next. Chronicles `prime.autonomous_strategy_approve` when a Brief exists.
  - **Tenant isolation + bounding.** The standing check is per the candidate's **own** Guild, so a grant in Guild A never approves Guild B's proposal/hire/Clearance/strategy. All standing actions count against the same `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX` per-tick bound; at most one governance action per candidate per tick (the next tick re-classifies the rest).
  - **Dashboard / API (read surface + operator grant/revoke control).** READ-ONLY capability `prime.standing_authority` (`prime_driver::handle_prime_standing_authority`, agent-store + tenant) → `GET /v1/spine/prime/standing-authority` (bridge `spine::prime_standing_authority`): reports `authority_id`, legacy env-derived `driver_enabled`, `hire_rig`(+`hire_rig_valid`), and per-category `{category, active, description}` for the caller's Guild — now including `prime.strategy.approve`. **`apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx` is now an operator CONTROL surface, not read-only:** the "Prime standing authority" card shows each category (with a human label — `prime.strategy.approve` → "Approve proposed strategies" — above the wire name) enabled/disabled with a **Grant** (when disabled) / **Revoke** (when enabled) button, plus the hire Rig and a "standing approvals, not loop toggles" note. The categories render straight from the backend list, so the new strategy category appears automatically once `prime.standing_authority` returns it. The card now keys its loop-off/on hint from `prime.autonomy_state.effective_enabled` (the runtime/env effective state), not the legacy env-only `driver_enabled` field. **Grant** drives the EXISTING `POST /v1/agents/__relix_autonomous_prime__/standing-approvals` with a bounded default (`expires_at = now + 24h`, `max_calls = 25`, no cost cap, `granted_by = operator`); **Revoke** lists the synthetic authority's standing approvals (`GET …/standing-approvals`) and `DELETE /v1/standing-approvals/:standing_id`s every row for that category; both refresh the read surface and show a success/error banner. **No new mutation route was added** — the synthetic authority reuses the same `agent.standing_approval.*` routes real Operatives use (the bridge's `agent::create_standing`/`list_standing`/`revoke_standing`, tenant-scoped via the verified `InvocationCtx` path). The same bounded grant is also scriptable via the CLI (`relix-cli agent standing-approval-grant --agent-id __relix_autonomous_prime__ --category prime.proposal.approve --expires-in 24h`) and bare `curl`. `apps/dashboard/src/api.ts` gains a `del` method. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.
  - **Tests (`prime_driver::tests`).** `autonomous_tick_without_standing_leaves_proposal_proposed`, `autonomous_tick_with_standing_approves_proposal_bounded` (approves through `prime.approve`, max honored, bounded grant consumed), `autonomous_tick_proposal_approval_is_idempotent` (no duplicate Mandate/Briefs, no double-consume), `standing_authority_is_tenant_isolated` (Guild-A grant never approves Guild B), `standing_hire_approve_activates_pending_hire_on_configured_rig`, `standing_hire_approve_refuses_unknown_rig` (skipped, stays pending, no consume), `standing_hire_approve_requires_grant`, `standing_clearance_approve_greenlights_attributable_clearance_only` (an unrelated non-spawn approval stays pending), `standing_authority_surface_reports_live_state`, and `standing_authority_grant_list_revoke_through_handlers` (the dashboard control path: create → read surface active → list-by-category → revoke → inactive, all through the EXISTING `agent.standing_approval.*` handlers for the synthetic authority). **Strategy-approval (added with `prime.strategy.approve`):** `autonomous_tick_drafts_strategy_but_does_not_approve_without_grant` (drafts proposed, never approves without the grant), `autonomous_tick_with_standing_approves_proposed_strategy` (approves a proposed strategy through `handle_strategy_approve`, consumes the bounded grant, next step off `needs_approval`), `standing_strategy_approve_is_tenant_isolated` (a Guild-A grant never approves Guild B's strategy), `standing_strategy_approve_never_approves_rejected` (a rejected strategy is never auto-approved/re-proposed, grant untouched), `standing_strategy_approve_respects_action_budget` (the per-tick bound caps approvals; the budget-blocked strategy stays proposed and consumes no call), and `autonomous_tick_drafts_then_approves_strategy_across_two_ticks` (documents the draft-then-approve two-tick granularity). The pre-existing approved-work autonomous tests are unchanged + still green.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** The strategy *body* is the **deterministic** draft by default (and **opt-in model-authored** under `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_STRATEGY_DRAFT` — Prime Strategy Authoring v1, below), but the model only authors the *text* of a `proposed` doc — approval is still a governed `proposed → approved` flip, never a model judging or approving the strategy; **raw goal creation still starts from a submitted goal/proposal** (Prime never invents a goal from nothing). Strategy approval is **not automatic by default** — it acts only when the loop is effectively ON **and** `prime.strategy.approve` is granted, and a **strategy rejection stays final** (only a human proposing a fresh strategy reopens it). The loop does not decide *which* identity to hire, and acts on an approval gate ONLY inside an explicit standing grant for an item attributable to Prime/company planning — never an arbitrary approval, never a budget gate. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`standing`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; clippy clean on touched code; dashboard rebuilt + parity; `git diff --check` clean.

- **Prime Shift Disposition (bounded v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the "a completed Shift (`brief_runs.status = done`, `review = pending_review`) waits on a human to accept the review and apply it" autonomy gap (company-model §12.6, the review→apply tail). The autonomous Prime loop may now **accept** a completed Shift's review and **apply** an accepted run on the Board's behalf — but ONLY under two SEPARATE, default-OFF, grant-gated standing authorities, through the EXISTING review/apply code paths and all their safety, never a hand-rolled copy. **Not combinable into one superpower:** review and apply are distinct grants and distinct ticks.
  - **Two categories (`prime_driver`).** `CATEGORY_RUN_REVIEW_ACCEPT = "prime.run.review_accept"` and `CATEGORY_RUN_APPLY = "prime.run.apply"`, added to `STANDING_AUTHORITY_CATEGORIES` (so the `prime.standing_authority` read surface + dashboard Settings grant/revoke them like the other categories — no new mutation route; the synthetic authority reuses `agent.standing_approval.*`). Both default OFF; each acts only while a live `standing_approvals` row exists for `__relix_autonomous_prime__` in that Guild.
  - **Deterministic candidate selection (`disposition_candidate` + `classify_mandate`).** Over a Mandate/proposal's OWN Brief set (the same `brief_ids` `classify_mandate` already roll up — tenant-scoped by construction, plus an explicit `run_belongs_to_tenant` guard so a cross-tenant run is **invisible**), the classifier finds the next disposition step. **APPLY takes precedence** over a fresh review acceptance (finish already-accepted work first); within each kind the **oldest** eligible run wins, stable by `(started_at, run_id)`. Eligible for `review_accept`: the Brief's latest run is exactly `done` + review exactly `pending_review` (excludes failed/refused/interrupted/running/cancelled/continued and any rejected/discarded/accepted/applied run by construction). Eligible for `apply_run`: latest run `done` + review `accepted` + apply status NOT already `applied`/`discarded`/`conflicted`/`failed` + `heartbeat::run_apply_eligibility` passes. The chosen run id is carried on `NextStep.run_id` and re-validated at execution time. New phases `PHASE_NEEDS_REVIEW`/`PHASE_NEEDS_APPLY` are grant-AGNOSTIC; `attemptable_action` gates the action on the matching grant, so with no grant the step stays a human review/apply gate.
  - **Autonomous actions (`process_candidate_inner` (B4)).** `review_accept` accepts through the EXISTING review path (`TaskStore::set_run_review(run_id, "accepted", "accepted by autonomous Prime under standing authority")` — the same store call the manual `run.review` accept makes, recording `brief.run_reviewed`); acceptance does **not** apply or advance the Brief. `apply_run` applies through the EXACT manual apply path `controller_runtime::execute_run_apply(store, run_id, tenant)` — re-running `run_apply_eligibility`, the baseline-hash / conflict / artifact-safety plan, and (only on a clean `applied`) the review-to-done `complete_reviewed_brief`. A conflicted/failed apply records `blocked`, **never** marks the Brief done, consumes no grant, and is not retried in the same tick (the next tick's classifier excludes the now-terminal apply run, so no blind retry loop). Each successful action consumes one bounded grant call and chronicles a distinct `prime.autonomous_review_accept` / `prime.autonomous_apply` event on the Mandate's parent Brief. `PrimeAutonomyRecord` actions `review_accept` / `apply_run` with outcomes `advanced`/`blocked`/`skipped`.
  - **LLM seam.** `review_accept`/`apply_run` are added to `KNOWN_ACTIONS`; the optional Prime Deliberation / prioritization layers may only confirm/hold/order these already-computed legal actions — the model never decides eligibility, invents a run id, bypasses a grant, or bypasses apply safety. A `none`/hold causes zero side effects.
  - **Tests (`prime_driver::tests`).** `disposition_review_accept_with_grant_accepts_run` (accepts, consumes grant, no apply), `disposition_apply_with_grant_applies_and_advances_brief` (applies through `execute_run_apply`, advances Brief to `done`), `disposition_no_grant_leaves_completed_shift_untouched` (blocked, run unchanged), `disposition_skips_rejected_failed_running_and_applied_runs`, `disposition_candidate_is_tenant_scoped` (cross-tenant invisible), `disposition_apply_conflict_blocks_and_does_not_mark_brief_done`, `disposition_llm_hold_causes_zero_side_effects`, and `disposition_review_then_apply_over_two_ticks` (separate ticks). `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; clippy clean on touched code; dashboard rebuilt + parity.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** Disposition acts only over runs attributable to the candidate Mandate/proposal through its Brief set — never an arbitrary Action Center run. It does not resolve apply conflicts, does not discard, does not reject a review (a human rejection stays final), and applies only through the existing all-or-nothing safe-apply (no merge/force). Default OFF; both grants are required and separable.

- **Prime Runtime Autonomy Switch (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the "autonomous Prime can only be toggled at boot via `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME`/restart" UX gap. The autonomous Prime LOOP (the approved-work driver above) is now controllable **from the product at runtime** — per-Guild, persisted, no restart — while the env var stays a **global boot override**. **Not an approval bypass:** turning the loop ON only wakes the driver over already-approved work; each governed approval still requires its own live standing grant (above). Safety, bounds, idempotency, and tenant-isolation of the tick are all unchanged.
  - **Persistence (`SpineStore` `runtime_settings`).** A new generic, tenant-scoped key→value table `runtime_settings(tenant_id, key, value, updated_at, updated_by, PRIMARY KEY(tenant_id,key))` in the coordinator spine DB (additive `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` in `init_schema`, indexed by `key`). Methods: `get_runtime_setting` / `set_runtime_setting` (raw string), `get_runtime_setting_bool` / `set_runtime_setting_bool` (canonical `1`/`0`, any truthy spelling read back), and `list_tenants_with_runtime_bool(key)` (the watcher's per-Guild enable set; only truthy rows). The one exposed key today is `RUNTIME_KEY_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME = "autonomous_prime_enabled"`; the table is deliberately generic for future runtime switches. No existence leak — an unset tenant+key reads `None`.
  - **Capabilities (`prime_driver`).** READ-ONLY `prime.autonomy_state` (`handle_prime_autonomy_state`) → the caller's Guild's `runtime_enabled` / `env_enabled` / `effective_enabled` / `source` (∈ `env`/`runtime`/`off`) + the live `autonomous_prime_max` / `autonomous_prime_interval_secs` / `hire_rig` knobs + `env_override` + a standing-grant caveat note. Mutation `prime.autonomy_set` (`handle_prime_autonomy_set`, JSON `{enabled:bool}`) persists the tenant-scoped runtime bool — **role-gated** to operator/admin via the shared `caller_is_operator` (a worker subject is `POLICY_DENIED`; `policy_denied` made `pub(crate)`), records `updated_by` = caller subject, and returns the fresh state. A malformed body is `INVALID_ARGS`. Pure, unit-tested helpers `effective_autonomy(env, runtime) -> (bool, source)` and `plan_autonomy_drive(env, enabled_tenants) -> AutonomyDrive` (env ON → `AllGuilds`; else the runtime-on `Tenants(..)`; else `Dormant`) keep the loop policy out of the controller.
  - **Runtime loop = dormant watcher (`controller_runtime.rs`).** The autonomous-Prime task is no longer spawned only when env is set; it is spawned whenever the `SpineStore` exists and runs as a **dormant watcher**. Each tick (inside `spawn_blocking`) re-reads the env override and, when env is off, `list_tenants_with_runtime_bool(RUNTIME_KEY_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME)`, then `plan_autonomy_drive`: env ON ⇒ `autonomous_prime_tick(tenant=None)` (drive ALL Guilds, the legacy behaviour); env off + runtime-on Guild(s) ⇒ `autonomous_prime_tick(Some(g))` per Guild (bounded per Guild, never a runtime-off Guild); neither ⇒ do nothing (one cheap SQL read, sleep). Interval/max/hire-Rig knobs are the SAME env defaults; the per-tick action bound is unchanged.
  - **Bridge / API.** `GET /v1/spine/prime/autonomy` (`spine::prime_autonomy` → `prime.autonomy_state`) + `PUT /v1/spine/prime/autonomy` body `{enabled:bool}` (`spine::prime_autonomy_set` → `prime.autonomy_set`), registered as one `get(..).put(..)` route. Tenant context is forwarded by `call_peer`'s verified-tenant envelope like every spine route; a permission denial maps to **403** and a malformed body to **400** via the shared `coordinator_err_status` / JSON extractor.
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx` gains an **Autonomous Prime loop** card with a live **Turn ON / Turn OFF** control (`PUT /v1/spine/prime/autonomy`), the effective state + source badge, the per-tick/interval knobs, an **env-override** banner (the OFF control can only clear the persisted row while env keeps it ON), and cross-hints with the standing-authority panel (ON but no grant ⇒ "awake, cannot approve"; OFF but grants live ⇒ "permission but asleep"). The heartbeat card's "Autonomous Prime" rows now reflect the effective runtime state (not just the env knob). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.

- **Prime Deliberation (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Makes the autonomous Prime loop no longer a hardcoded deterministic state machine: behind an opt-in switch a model may **choose among the already-computed governed actions** for a candidate, while the security invariant holds — **the model is NOT the permission system** (company-model §12.5/§12.5A, the Prime planner / model-assisted seam, applied to the loop's per-tick choice). **Default OFF.**
  - **Pure deliberation module (`nodes/coordinator/agent/prime_deliberation.rs`).** Dependency-light snapshot → prompt → parse, fully unit-tested without a mesh/provider. `PrimeDeliberationMode` (`deterministic_only`/`llm_used`/`fallback`/`unavailable`); `PrimeDeliberationInput` (a bounded, **secret-free** snapshot built from the already-computed `NextStep` + safe candidate metadata: tenant, kind, ids, phase, the single `computed_action`, the step reason, strategy status, Brief counts, missing-roles/pending-hires/pending-clearances counts — no secrets, tokens, or big text dumps); `PrimeDeliberationDecision`; the `PrimeAiDecider` trait (sync, so the loop can inject scripted decisions in tests and the live impl can bridge the async mesh call). `KNOWN_ACTIONS` enumerates every choosable action (`none`/`approve`/`propose_strategy`/`approve_strategy`/`create_team_plan`/`orchestrate_assign_ready`/`start`/`start_mandate`/`hire_approve`/`clearance_approve`); the per-candidate allowed set is always `[<computed action>, none]`.
  - **Strict validator (`parse_prime_decision`).** STRICT JSON `{"action":"…","reason":"…"}` only: rejects empty / over-long output (`MAX_MODEL_OUTPUT_CHARS`), non-object JSON (arrays, scalars), malformed JSON, a missing/non-string `action`, an unknown action, an action **not in the candidate's allowed set**, and a non-string / over-long (`MAX_REASON_CHARS`) / control-char reason; strips a single markdown code fence safely; sanitizes pipes/control chars in the accepted reason. Any rejection → deterministic fallback. So the model can never invent an action or widen the legal set.
  - **Prompt builder (`build_prime_deliberation_prompt`).** Instructs the model to choose EXACTLY ONE action from the allowed list or `none`, explain briefly, and never invent a tool; renders only the secret-free snapshot; sanitizes pipes/control chars and clamps to `MAX_PROMPT_CHARS`. Bounds + schema unit-tested.
  - **Loop integration (`prime_driver`).** `process_candidate` is now a thin wrapper: it computes the SINGLE legal next governed action (`intended_action`), and — when `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_DELIBERATION` is on and a decider is wired — consults the model as an advisory pre-pass. A `none` skips the candidate this tick with **zero side effects** (`skipped`, `ai_mode=llm_used`); a confirm (or any malformed/disallowed/unavailable output) runs the UNCHANGED deterministic `process_candidate_inner`, whose governed handler + standing authority + budget + Claim + adapter + tenant gates are byte-for-byte as before. `PASS 0` (standing-authority proposal approval) is gated the same way. The model can only reduce or confirm — never widen — the action, and approvals still require their live standing grant + budget. `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `ai_mode`/`ai_reason`, surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`.
  - **Live decider (`prime_driver::MeshAiDecider`) + env controls.** The controller loop builds the live decider only when the switch is on AND the coordinator's EXISTING outbound mesh client (the one the alert sink wires from `[peers]`) is populated; it performs ONLY the existing `ai.chat` mesh call (same `{session_id,prompt,history}` shape as the bridge's `call_ai_chat`), bridging the async call into the `spawn_blocking` tick via a captured `Handle`, deadline clamped to 5–60s. **No provider key enters the coordinator / web bridge / dashboard.** Env: `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_DELIBERATION` (`1|true|yes|on`, default OFF), `RELIX_PRIME_AI_PEER` (default `ai`), `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_SESSION` (default `prime-autonomy`). A missing mesh / AI peer ⇒ `unavailable` ⇒ deterministic fallback. The **manual** tick (`prime.autonomy_tick_now`) now builds the SAME `MeshAiDecider` from the coordinator's populated outbound mesh client (the alert mesh cell) via `handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`, and the controller registration runs the tick inside `spawn_blocking` (capturing a `Handle` on the async thread) so the decider's `block_on` never executes on an async worker — so **Run Prime now** exercises live deliberation when the mesh AI peer is reachable, falling back to `unavailable` + deterministic only when the mesh cell is unpopulated or the peer is unreachable.
  - **Tests.** `prime_deliberation::tests` (16): parser accepts a valid allowed action + `none`, rejects unknown/disallowed/malformed/array/scalar/non-string-action/over-long-output/over-long-reason/control-char-reason, strips a code fence, and bounds the prompt. `prime_driver::tests` (loop-level, scripted decider): `deliberation_none_holds_with_zero_side_effects`, `deliberation_confirm_executes_governed_action_llm_used`, `deliberation_malformed_output_falls_back_deterministically`, `deliberation_disallowed_action_falls_back`, `deliberation_unavailable_runs_deterministically`, `deliberation_enabled_without_decider_is_unavailable`, `deliberation_off_is_deterministic_only`, `prime_llm_deliberation_flag_parsing`. All pre-existing tenant-safety / budget / standing-authority tests unchanged + green. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; dashboard rebuilt + parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This is **constrained deliberation over the existing action menu**, NOT freeform tool-calling Prime: the model confirms-or-holds the ONE computed governed action and attaches a reason; it does not author strategy, invent goals, pick identities to hire, or call tools, and it can never bypass a permission/budget/Claim/adapter gate. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip is **not** integration-tested in CI (it needs a real provider; the validator + deterministic fallback that bound it are fully tested with scripted output).
  - **Tests.** Store (`spine::store::tests`): `runtime_setting_persists_and_reads_bool`, `runtime_setting_is_tenant_isolated`, `list_tenants_with_runtime_bool_returns_only_truthy`. Driver (`prime_driver::tests`): `effective_autonomy_resolves_source`, `plan_autonomy_drive_decides_what_to_run`, `autonomy_state_read_and_set_roundtrip` (default off → set on/off, tenant-scoped), `autonomy_set_is_operator_only` (worker `POLICY_DENIED`, nothing persisted), `autonomy_set_rejects_malformed_body` (`INVALID_ARGS`). `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`standing`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `maintenance.rs`/cleanup-log warnings only); dashboard `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This switches the **loop**, not the approvals — with no standing grant every approval gate stays human exactly as before. The env var remains a **global** override (no per-Guild env), and while it is set the runtime OFF control cannot fully disable the loop until the env is unset + the coordinator restarts (surfaced honestly). The env-derived `run.workspace_config` knobs (`autonomous_prime_enabled` etc.) are unchanged; the authoritative effective/runtime state is the new `prime.autonomy_state`.

- **Manual Autonomy Tick (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the "the background loop can run, but there is no operator control to *run a Prime tick now* and no returned tick records" legibility gap. Adds an operator-triggered single bounded autonomous Prime tick for the caller's Guild that returns the `PrimeAutonomyRecord` list — so an operator can wake the loop **once** and **see** exactly what it considered / advanced / started, instead of only trusting a background timer. **Still governed autonomy, not a new power:** it calls the SAME `autonomous_prime_tick` path the timer uses, so every action goes through the same standing-authority gates, the autonomous-start budget hard-stop, the Rig-readiness check, and the per-tick `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX` bound. It does **not** require the runtime autonomy switch (or the env override) to be ON — an explicit operator wake-up — but grants no new authority (with no live standing grant every approval gate is still left to the human).
  - **Capability (`prime_driver`).** `prime.autonomy_tick_now` (`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now`, args ignored) — **role-gated** to operator/admin via the shared `caller_is_operator` (a worker subject is `POLICY_DENIED` with no mutation, exactly like `prime.autonomy_set`). **Tenant-scoped:** it runs `autonomous_prime_tick(.., Some(ctx.tenant_id_or_default()), ..)`, so it drives ONLY the caller's own Guild — never all Guilds, even when the env override is on. It reads the LIVE `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX` (via `heartbeat::parse_autonomous_prime_max`) for the bound and `configured_autonomous_hire_rig()` for the standing-authority hire Rig, and uses the current wall-clock millis. Returns `{ tenant, max, records:[…], advanced, started, considered }` where each record carries `{ tenant, target_kind, target_id, mandate_id, phase, action, outcome, reason }` (built by the secret-free `prime_autonomy_record_json` helper; `PrimeAutonomyRecord` was not given `Serialize`). An `autonomous_prime_tick` error surfaces honestly as `RESPONDER_INTERNAL`.
  - **Registration (`controller_runtime.rs`).** Registered in the same block as `prime.start` (the only one with the Rig registry + metrics query + agent/spine/task stores in scope) — it composes the existing handler, duplicating none of the background-loop logic. The metrics query (`metrics.map(|m| m.query.clone())`) feeds the autonomous budget gate exactly as the timer path does. **Live deliberation (caveat closed):** the registration also captures `metrics.map(|m| m.alert_mesh_cell.clone())`, `prime_ai_peer()`, and `prime_llm_session()`, and — inside the async handler — captures `tokio::runtime::Handle::current()`, then runs the tick in `tokio::task::spawn_blocking` via `handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`. There it builds the SAME `MeshAiDecider` the background timer does (only when `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_DELIBERATION` is on AND the alert mesh cell is populated; tenant-scoped to the caller's Guild, deadline 30s) and passes it as `Option<&dyn PrimeAiDecider>`. Running from a blocking thread is required because `MeshAiDecider::deliberate` does a `Handle::block_on`, which would panic on an async-runtime worker. A `spawn_blocking` join error surfaces as `RESPONDER_INTERNAL`.
  - **Bridge / API.** `POST /v1/spine/prime/autonomy/tick` (`spine::prime_autonomy_tick`) proxies `prime.autonomy_tick_now` with empty args via the verified-tenant `call_peer` envelope. A permission denial (non-operator caller) maps to **403** via the shared `coordinator_err_status` — no special bypass. The static `…/autonomy/tick` segment does not collide with the sibling `…/autonomy` GET/PUT (matchit gives the longer static path priority; pinned by `spine_routes_construct_without_conflict`).
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx`'s **Autonomous Prime loop** card gains a **Run Prime now** button (`POST /v1/spine/prime/autonomy/tick`) beside the Turn ON/OFF control, a concise banner (`considered X, advanced Y, started Z`), and a restrained latest-records table (target / phase / action / outcome / reason, capped at 5 with an "N of M" note). The copy is honest: the button wakes **exactly one** bounded tick for this Guild and does **not** require the loop to be on or bypass standing approvals / budgets. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.
  - **Tests.** Driver (`prime_driver::tests`): `tick_now_is_operator_only_no_side_effect` (worker `POLICY_DENIED`, no Team Plan recorded), `tick_now_is_tenant_scoped` (an `other`-Guild tick never touches `default`'s bare Mandate / proposed proposal, even with a `default` proposal-approve grant live), `tick_now_advances_same_tenant_approved_mandate` (advances a same-Guild approved Mandate at `needs_team_plan` via the existing logic), `tick_now_honors_action_budget` (with `max + 1` advanceable Mandates exactly `max` advance — the bound is never exceeded). **Live-deliberation helper** (`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`, scripted sync decider): `tick_now_with_decider_hold_is_llm_used_zero_side_effects` (scripted `{action:"none"}` + `llm_enabled` ⇒ `ai_mode=llm_used`, `skipped`, no Team Plan), `tick_now_with_decider_confirm_executes_llm_used` (scripted confirm ⇒ `advanced`, `ai_mode=llm_used`, Team Plan recorded), `tick_now_no_decider_llm_enabled_is_unavailable_runs_deterministically` (no decider + `llm_enabled` ⇒ `ai_mode=unavailable`, deterministic action still runs), `tick_now_with_decider_worker_denied_no_side_effect` (role gate unchanged with a decider wired). The **bridge route only proxies**, so behavior is covered in the runtime; the bridge side adds route-construction coverage in `spine_routes_construct_without_conflict`. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`standing`/`heartbeat` + `relix-web-bridge --bins` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `controller_runtime.rs`/`maintenance.rs` warnings only); dashboard `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** v1 is deliberately simple: **no** separate max/body argument (it always uses the live env `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX`), and the tick is the existing per-tick bounded discovery (≤ `max` actions across the discovered candidates), so the over-budget candidate is simply left unprocessed rather than emitting a per-candidate "budget reached" skip record. It runs synchronously inside the request and returns the in-memory tick summary; durable provenance of any real action still lives in the Chronicle event the underlying handler writes. It changes **none** of the loop's safety: still standing-grant-gated for approvals, budget-hard-stopped on autonomous start, Rig-validated for hires, and bounded per tick.

- **Prime Strategy Authoring (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked "the strategy Prime drafts is deterministic-only; there is no model-backed strategy reasoning" gap. When the operator opts in, the *body* of a PROPOSED Mandate strategy can be model-authored, while the security invariant holds — **the model is NOT the permission system** (company-model §12.5/§12.5A, the Prime planner / model-assisted seam, applied to the strategy DRAFT body). **Default OFF.** Strategy stays only **proposed**, never approved or executed by the model; all existing approval / standing-authority gates are unchanged.
  - **Pure strategy module (`nodes/coordinator/agent/prime_strategy.rs`).** Dependency-light snapshot → prompt → validate, fully unit-tested without a mesh/provider. `PrimeStrategyDraftMode` (`deterministic_only`/`llm_used`/`fallback`/`unavailable`); `PrimeStrategyDraftResult { doc, mode, reason }`; `PrimeStrategySnapshot::new(...)` builds a bounded, **secret-free** snapshot (Mandate title / status / description bounded to `STRATEGY_DRAFT_DESC_CAP` / active work roles / optional Brief total-ready-running counts — **no** secrets, credentials, tokens, repo/file content, or large dumps). `build_strategy_draft_prompt` renders a length-capped (`MAX_STRATEGY_PROMPT_CHARS`), pipe-/control-sanitized prompt instructing the model to write plain Markdown, state the doc is a non-approved DRAFT, and never include secrets/tool-calls.
  - **Strict validator/sanitizer (`validate_strategy_draft`).** Rejects empty / over-long (`MAX_STRATEGY_OUTPUT_CHARS`) output and obvious prompt-injection boilerplate (`INJECTION_MARKERS`); strips a surrounding markdown code fence; sanitizes the pipe to `/` and non-whitespace control chars (keeping `\n`/`\t`); appends a standard `GOVERNANCE_FOOTER` ("DRAFT / not approved") when the model omits the language; bounds the final doc to `STRATEGY_DRAFT_BODY_CAP` with the footer preserved. Any rejection → deterministic fallback. So the proposed doc is always non-empty, pipe-safe, bounded, and carries the non-approved governance language.
  - **Drafting + loop integration (`prime_driver`).** `draft_strategy_doc(ai, mandate, roles, counts, strategy_llm_enabled) -> PrimeStrategyDraftResult`: with the flag off → deterministic `draft_mandate_strategy` (`deterministic_only`); with no decider → deterministic (`unavailable`); else builds the snapshot+prompt, calls the SAME `PrimeAiDecider` the deliberation layer uses, validates the reply (`llm_used`) or falls back deterministically (`fallback` on bad output / `unavailable` on a model error). In the autonomous tick's safe-advance path (`process_candidate_inner`, block A1), when the classified safe action is `propose_strategy` the body is drafted here and proposed through the EXISTING `handle_strategy_propose` — the classifier only yields `propose_strategy` for a Mandate with **no** strategy, so an existing `proposed`/`approved`/`rejected` strategy is **never overwritten** (a human rejection stays final). `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `strategy_ai_mode`/`strategy_ai_reason` (distinct from the action-choice `ai_mode`), surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`. The deliberation pre-pass still governs the *action choice*: if it holds (`none`), no strategy is drafted; if it confirms/falls back to `propose_strategy`, the body layer runs. The action choice and the body author are independent, so a Guild can run deterministic action selection with a model-authored body, or vice versa.
  - **Env controls + wiring (`controller_runtime.rs`).** `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_STRATEGY_DRAFT` (`1|true|yes|on`, default OFF, `parse_prime_llm_strategy_draft`). Both the background timer and the manual `prime.autonomy_tick_now` (Run Prime now) re-read it each tick and thread it through `autonomous_prime_tick`/`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`. The live `MeshAiDecider` (the SAME one the deliberation layer builds, reusing `RELIX_PRIME_AI_PEER` / `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_SESSION` and the populated coordinator outbound mesh client) is now built when **either** switch is on — so strategy authoring works even with deliberation off. **No provider key enters the coordinator / web bridge / dashboard.**
  - **Explicit click stays deterministic.** The operator one-click `prime.advance {action:"propose_strategy"}` route (`handle_prime_advance`) is left **deterministic** by design — it never builds a decider — so model-backed strategy authoring is constrained to the autonomous/manual-tick Prime loop. Documented, not half-wired.
  - **Read accessor (`SpineStore::strategy_doc`).** A small tenant-guarded read returning the proposed/approved/rejected strategy body text (mirrors `strategy_status`), used to surface the proposed strategy for review and to assert authoring provenance in tests.
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx`: the Prime-LLM copy now documents **two** opt-in switches — Deliberation (chooses/holds the legal action) and Strategy Draft authoring (authors the proposed strategy text), both fall back deterministically and never approve a gate. The Run-Prime-now tick table gains a **Provenance** column showing `act:<ai_mode>` and, on a `propose_strategy` row, `strat:<strategy_ai_mode>` (with the reason on hover). Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.
  - **Tests.** Pure (`prime_strategy::tests`): prompt is bounded/pipe-free/steers and clamps a huge description; validator accepts good Markdown + keeps/append governance language, sanitizes pipe + control chars (keeps newlines/tabs), strips a code fence, rejects empty/over-long/prompt-injection, and bounds the final doc with the footer preserved. Loop (`prime_driver::tests`, scripted strategy drafter): `strategy_llm_authors_proposed_strategy_body` (good draft ⇒ proposed contains model content + `strategy_ai_mode=llm_used`, never approved), `strategy_llm_bad_output_falls_back_deterministically` + `strategy_llm_overlong_output_falls_back` (`fallback`), `strategy_llm_no_decider_is_unavailable` (`unavailable`), `strategy_llm_off_is_deterministic_only`, `strategy_llm_does_not_overwrite_a_rejected_strategy` + `strategy_llm_does_not_overwrite_an_existing_proposed_strategy` (no overwrite, model never consulted), `prime_llm_strategy_draft_flag_parsing`. All pre-existing Prime deliberation / standing-authority / bare-Mandate-start tests unchanged + green. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `controller_runtime.rs`/`maintenance.rs` warnings only); dashboard rebuilt + parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** Model-backed authoring covers only the *body* of a **proposed** strategy in the **autonomous/manual-tick** loop; it never approves or executes, never chooses the action, never picks a hire/identity, and never invents a goal from raw intent. The explicit one-click `prime.advance` strategy route remains deterministic. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip is **not** integration-tested in CI (it needs a real provider; the prompt builder + validator + deterministic fallback that bound it are fully unit/loop tested with scripted output). Reuses the deliberation layer's `MeshAiDecider`/session rather than a separate `RELIX_PRIME_STRATEGY_SESSION`.

- **Prime Executive Prioritization (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked "candidate discovery/order is still deterministic — when `RELIX_AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_MAX=1` the loop spends its tick on the first deterministic candidate even if another legal candidate is more important" gap. When the operator opts in, a model may choose the **ORDER** in which a bounded tick spends its action budget among the candidates the deterministic classifier has ALREADY computed as legal/attemptable — while the security invariant holds: **the model is NOT the permission system** (company-model §5.4/§8.2 the Action Center "next governed step"; §12.5/§12.5A the Prime planner / model-assisted seam, applied to the loop's per-tick candidate order). **Default OFF.**
  - **Pure prioritization module (`nodes/coordinator/agent/prime_priority.rs`).** Dependency-light summaries → prompt → parse, fully unit-tested without a mesh/provider. `PrimePriorityMode` (`deterministic_only`/`llm_used`/`fallback`/`unavailable`); `PrimePriorityCandidate { key, tenant, target_kind, target_id, mandate_id, phase, computed_action, reason, strategy_status, briefs counts, missing_roles/pending_hires/pending_clearances }` — a bounded, **secret-free** summary with a stable, opaque per-tick `key` (`cand-1`, `cand-2`, …); `PrimePriorityOrder { order, reason }`. `build_priority_prompt` renders a length-capped (`MAX_PRIORITY_PROMPT_CHARS`), pipe-/control-sanitized prompt that lists the offered candidate keys and asks the model to return strict JSON `{"order":["cand-2","cand-1"],"reason":"…"}` (most-important-first) or `{"order":[],"reason":"…"}` to hold the whole queue — never inventing a key or an action.
  - **Strict parser/validator (`parse_priority_order`).** Accepts ONLY keys from the offered list; rejects unknown keys, duplicates, a non-array / missing `order`, more keys than offered, non-string keys, non-object/array/scalar/over-long (`MAX_PRIORITY_OUTPUT_CHARS`) JSON or prose, and an over-long (`MAX_PRIORITY_REASON_CHARS`) / control-char reason. An **empty** `order` array is accepted and means HOLD (take no action this tick) — but only honoured as a hold when the output is otherwise valid (`llm_used`). Any rejection → deterministic discovery order with an honest mode.
  - **Tick refactor (`prime_driver::autonomous_prime_tick`).** Discovery now builds ONE deterministic candidate queue (the fallback order, byte-for-byte the legacy order: standing-approvable `proposed` proposals first — offered ONLY when the Guild holds live `prime.proposal.approve` — then approved proposals, then bare Mandates deduped against proposals). A READ-ONLY classify pass (`candidate_menu_entry`/`menu_from_target`/`attemptable_action`) computes the same next step / intended action that would run today **without mutating state**, and offers the model only candidates with a positive **attemptable** action (an approval-category action — hire/clearance/strategy — is "attemptable" only with the matching live standing grant + known Rig; a pure human gate / running / done candidate is recorded deterministically but never offered). With the flag on, a live decider wired, and ≥2 attemptable candidates, the model is asked once for an order; the validated order (listed keys first, any un-listed menu candidates appended in deterministic order) is executed until `max` actions are spent (remaining attemptable candidates record `skipped` "tick action budget reached" with their rank). An **empty** order holds the whole queue (every offered candidate recorded `skipped` "model chose to hold the queue", **zero side effects**). Invalid/unavailable/disabled output (or <2 candidates) executes the byte-for-byte legacy deterministic order. Each executed step still flows through the SAME governed handler + standing authority + budget + Claim + adapter + tenant gates (the model never invents a candidate, widens an action, or bypasses a gate). `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `priority_ai_mode`/`priority_ai_reason`/`priority_rank` (distinct from the action-choice `ai_mode` and strategy-body `strategy_ai_mode`), surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`.
  - **Env controls + wiring (`controller_runtime.rs`).** `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_PRIORITIZATION` (`1|true|yes|on`, default OFF, `parse_prime_llm_prioritization`). Both the background timer and the manual `prime.autonomy_tick_now` (Run Prime now) re-read it each tick and thread it through `autonomous_prime_tick`/`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`. The live `MeshAiDecider` (the SAME one the deliberation + strategy layers build, reusing `RELIX_PRIME_AI_PEER` / `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_SESSION` and the populated coordinator outbound mesh client) is now built when **any** of the three switches is on — so prioritization works even with deliberation/strategy off. **No provider key enters the coordinator / web bridge / dashboard.**
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx`: the Prime-LLM copy now documents **three** opt-in switches — Deliberation (confirm/hold the legal action), Strategy Draft authoring (author the proposed strategy text), and Prioritization (choose the queue order among legal actions) — all off by default, all fall back deterministically, none approves a gate. The Run-Prime-now tick table Provenance column now also shows `ord:<priority_ai_mode>#<rank>` (with the reason on hover) beside `act:`/`strat:`. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.
  - **Tests.** Pure (`prime_priority::tests`): parser accepts a valid reorder / strict subset / empty-as-hold; rejects unknown / duplicate / prose / array / missing-order / non-array-order / non-string-key / too-many-keys / over-long output + reason; strips a code fence; prompt is bounded/pipe-free/lists the keys and clamps for many candidates; mode strings stable. Loop (`prime_driver::tests`, scripted prioritization decider): `prioritization_model_picks_second_only_second_advances` (max=1, the model elevates the second candidate ⇒ only it advances, the first is left unchanged + `skipped` on budget, records `llm_used` with clear ranks), `prioritization_invalid_output_falls_back_to_first` (`fallback`, deterministic first advances), `prioritization_unavailable_model_falls_back_deterministic` (decider error and no-decider ⇒ `unavailable`, deterministic), `prioritization_empty_order_holds_zero_side_effects` (`llm_used` hold, no Mandate planned), `prioritization_is_tenant_scoped` (a Guild-scoped tick only offers/acts on its own Guild; another Guild's Mandate is never discovered/touched and the model cannot select a cross-tenant key), `prioritization_offers_proposal_only_with_standing` (a proposed proposal is offered ONLY with the `prime.proposal.approve` grant — without it stays proposed and unoffered; with it the model may prioritize it), `prime_llm_prioritization_flag_parsing`. All pre-existing Prime deliberation / strategy / standing-authority tests unchanged + green. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (pre-existing unrelated `controller_runtime.rs`/`maintenance.rs` warnings only); dashboard rebuilt + parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This is **queue prioritization among already-computed legal candidates**, NOT freeform goal invention or arbitrary tool-calling: the model only reorders (or holds) the deterministic classifier's attemptable menu — it cannot invent a candidate, add an action, widen any candidate's allowed action, approve a gate it lacks a standing grant for, or bypass budget/Claim/adapter/tenant scope. With the flag off (or <2 attemptable candidates) the discovery order is byte-for-byte the legacy behaviour. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip is **not** integration-tested in CI (it needs a real provider; the prompt builder + parser + deterministic fallback that bound it are fully unit/loop tested with scripted output). Reuses the deliberation layer's `MeshAiDecider`/session rather than a separate prioritization session.

- **Prime Orchestration Authoring (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked "the orchestrated Brief tree's text is mechanical / rule-based only (fixed role→title map; no authored content)" gap.
