When the operator opts in, a model may **author the TEXT** — titles, dossiers, checklists — of the orchestration Brief skeleton the deterministic readiness logic has ALREADY computed, while the security invariant holds: **the model is NOT the permission system** (company-model §4.6 the Mandate→Brief materialisation; §12.5/§12.5A the Prime planner / model-assisted seam, applied to the orchestration work-object text). **Default OFF.** The skeleton (roles, agents, assignments, ids, source markers, gates) is unchanged; the model only writes human-facing text for already-allowed items.
  - **Pure orchestration module (`nodes/coordinator/agent/prime_orchestration.rs`).** Dependency-light snapshot → prompt → parse, fully unit-tested without a mesh/provider. `PrimeOrchestrationMode` (`deterministic_only`/`llm_used`/`fallback`/`unavailable`); `PrimeOrchestrationSnapshot { mandate_title, mandate_status, strategy_excerpt (bounded approved-strategy excerpt), active_roles: [{role_key, agent_id}], gap_roles: [(role_key, reason)] (context only), max_briefs }` — a bounded, **secret-free** snapshot (no repo/file/secret dump); `PrimeOrchestrationBlueprint { parent, roles: BTreeMap<role_key, item>, subjects: BTreeMap<agent_id, item> }` with `PrimeOrchestrationItem { title?, dossier?, checklist[] }`. `build_orchestration_prompt` renders a length-capped (`MAX_ORCH_PROMPT_CHARS`), pipe-/control-sanitized prompt listing ONLY the offered role/subject keys and asking for strict JSON keyed by those keys; it tells the model the skeleton is fixed and it may author text only.
  - **Strict parser/validator (`parse_orchestration_blueprint`).** Accepts ONLY the offered role keys + subject (agent) keys + the `parent` key + the `roles`/`subjects` sections; rejects an unknown top-level key, an unknown role/subject key, more entries than offered, an array where an object is expected, a non-string title/dossier/checklist item, an over-long title (`MAX_ORCH_TITLE_CHARS`) / dossier (`MAX_ORCH_DOSSIER_CHARS`) / checklist item (`MAX_ORCH_CHECKLIST_ITEM_CHARS`), too many checklist items (`MAX_ORCH_CHECKLIST_ITEMS`), non-object/array/scalar/over-long (`MAX_ORCH_OUTPUT_CHARS`) JSON or prose. Pipe → `/`; control chars stripped (titles + checklist items collapse newlines; dossiers keep `\n`/`\t`). Any rejection → deterministic titles + dossiers with an honest mode.
  - **Handler integration (`handlers::handle_orchestrate_with_blueprint`).** `handle_orchestrate` now delegates to `handle_orchestrate_with_blueprint(…, blueprint: Option<&PrimeOrchestrationBlueprint>)` with `None` (the public `mandate.orchestrate` capability + the manual `prime.advance` route stay deterministic). The blueprint is **text-only** and applied ONLY to NEWLY-created Briefs (a parent/role-track title from the blueprint, a role-track/subject Dossier when authored, the subject title); `ensure_marked` sets a title only on creation, so an existing/hand-edited Brief title is **never** clobbered on rerun. The roles/agents/assignments/reviewer stamping/`max_briefs` cap/source-marker idempotency are byte-for-byte the deterministic path, and **placeholder-track text stays deterministic** so the placeholder→active title promotion (which keys on the machine `… track blocked:` prefix) is preserved. With `blueprint = None` the behaviour is byte-for-byte the deterministic v1.
  - **Driver integration (`prime_driver`).** On an `orchestrate_assign_ready` advance the autonomous/manual tick calls `author_orchestration_blueprint` (which builds the SAME active/gap role computation `handle_orchestrate` uses, so the offered keys match) and passes the VALIDATED blueprint (never raw model output) to `handle_orchestrate_with_blueprint`. Off / no-decider / snapshot-unavailable / invalid output ⇒ `None` + honest mode + deterministic text. `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `orchestration_ai_mode`/`orchestration_ai_reason` (set only on the orchestrate row; distinct from the action-choice `ai_mode`, strategy-body `strategy_ai_mode`, and queue-order `priority_ai_mode`), surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`.
  - **Env controls + wiring (`controller_runtime.rs`).** `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_ORCHESTRATION` (`1|true|yes|on`, default OFF, `parse_prime_llm_orchestration`). Both the background timer and the manual `prime.autonomy_tick_now` re-read it each tick and thread it through `autonomous_prime_tick`/`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`. The live `MeshAiDecider` (the SAME one the other Prime LLM layers build) is now built when **any** of the four switches is on. **No provider key enters the coordinator / web bridge / dashboard.**
  - **Dashboard.** `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx`: the Prime-LLM copy now documents **four** opt-in switches — Deliberation, Strategy Draft authoring, Prioritization, and Orchestration authoring — all off by default, all fall back deterministically, none approves a gate. The Run-Prime-now tick table Provenance column now also shows `orch:<orchestration_ai_mode>` (reason on hover) beside `act:`/`strat:`/`ord:`. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist` + dist parity.
  - **Tests.** Pure (`prime_orchestration::tests`): parser accepts a valid / partial blueprint; rejects unknown role/subject/top-level key, array-top-level, array-where-object-expected, item-that-is-an-array, prose, over-long output/title/dossier, too-many/non-string checklist items; sanitizes pipe→`/` + control chars (collapsing title newlines, keeping dossier newlines); prompt is bounded/pipe-free/lists only offered keys + clamps for many roles; mode strings stable. Loop (`prime_driver::tests`, scripted orchestration decider): `orchestration_llm_authors_brief_text` (same 3-Brief skeleton + assignment, but model titles/dossier on the new parent/role/subject; `orchestration_ai_mode=llm_used`, action choice deterministic), `orchestration_llm_bad_output_falls_back_deterministically` (`fallback`, deterministic titles, tree still created), `orchestration_llm_no_decider_is_unavailable`, `orchestration_llm_off_is_deterministic_only`, `orchestration_llm_rerun_is_idempotent_and_preserves_hand_edits` (no duplicate Briefs; a hand-edited title is never clobbered by a rerun blueprint), `orchestration_llm_is_tenant_scoped`, `prime_llm_orchestration_flag_parsing`. All pre-existing Prime tests unchanged + green. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime`/`heartbeat` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; dashboard rebuilt + parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This authors the **text** of an already-computed Brief skeleton only — the model cannot invent a role, agent, Brief id, source marker, dependency, assignee, approval, budget change, or tool, and the direct one-click `mandate.orchestrate` / `prime.advance {action:"orchestrate_assign_ready"}` route stays **deterministic** by design (it never builds a blueprint). Placeholder/gap-track text is deterministic (not model-authored) to preserve the placeholder→active title promotion. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip is **not** integration-tested in CI (it needs a real provider; the prompt builder + parser + deterministic fallback that bound it are fully unit/loop tested with scripted output). Reuses the existing `MeshAiDecider`/session rather than a separate orchestration session.

- **Prime Plan-Package Authoring (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked "the plan-package composer is manual-only / there is no autonomous LLM planner / no model-chosen `create_document`+`create_interaction`" gap, in a bounded, governed, product-spine way (execution-and-issue §1.7/§1.8/§3.1 the planner pattern; company-model §12.5/§12.5A the Prime planner / model-assisted seam). When the operator opts in, the autonomous/manual Prime tick may OPEN a *proposed* Brief decomposition (a plan package) on a single un-decomposed Brief and **leave the confirm OPEN for a human** — it never approves it, never assigns agents, and never creates children directly. **Default OFF.** **The model is NOT the permission system.**
  - **Pure plan-package module (`nodes/coordinator/agent/prime_plan_package.rs`).** Dependency-light snapshot → prompt → validate, fully unit-tested without a mesh/provider. `PrimePlanPackageMode` (`deterministic_only`/`llm_used`/`fallback`/`unavailable`); `PrimePlanPackageSnapshot { brief_title, brief_status, mandate_title }` — a bounded, **secret-free** snapshot; `ValidatedPlanPackage { plan_title, plan_body, summary, prompt, children: Vec<brief::ChildSpec> }`. `build_plan_package_prompt` renders a length-capped (`MAX_PLAN_PACKAGE_PROMPT_CHARS`) prompt asking for STRICT JSON. `validate_plan_package` bounds output (`MAX_PLAN_PACKAGE_OUTPUT_CHARS`), strips a code fence, secret-redacts + length-bounds every string (reusing `prime_plan::sanitize_text`), caps children at `MAX_AUTONOMOUS_CHILDREN` (8, tighter than the store's 20), keeps only valid priorities, and remaps each `after` to a strictly-earlier KEPT sibling (dropping forward/self/unknown/dropped-target refs) so the store's own `brief::normalize_proposal` always accepts the result; empty body / no usable child → reject → deterministic fallback. `deterministic_plan_package` is a safe generic plan→build→verify chain (carrying the DRAFT/not-approved language) used on disabled/unavailable/rejected output. Children NEVER carry assignee hints (open unassigned).
  - **Driver integration (`prime_driver`).** A new `plan_package_eligibility(task_store, tenant, mandate_id)` returns `Eligible{brief_id,title,status}` / `Blocked(reason)` / `NotApplicable`: it acts ONLY when the Mandate has a SINGLE Brief that is non-terminal (`done`/`cancelled` excluded), childless (no Sub-briefs), has **no** `plan` Dossier (so a human/Prime/stale plan is never overwritten), is not `plan`-locked, and has no open `suggest_tasks`/plan-`confirm` (no duplicate). `author_plan_package_content` mirrors `draft_strategy_doc` (model when the switch is on AND a decider is wired, else deterministic). A new **(B5)** step in `process_candidate_inner`, placed AFTER every advance/start/governance/disposition phase and BEFORE the human-gate tail, opens the package through the EXISTING `TaskStore::open_plan_package` (author = `AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_AUTHORITY`), counts one tick action, and Chronicles `prime.autonomous_plan_package` (ids/counts/mode only — never the body). `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `plan_package_ai_mode`/`plan_package_ai_reason`/`plan_doc_id`/`suggestion_id`/`confirm_id`/`child_count` (set only on the plan_package row), surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`.
  - **Env controls + wiring (`controller_runtime.rs`).** `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_PLAN_PACKAGE` (`1|true|yes|on`, default OFF, `parse_prime_llm_plan_package`). Both the background timer and the manual `prime.autonomy_tick_now` re-read it each tick and thread it through `autonomous_prime_tick`/`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`; the live `MeshAiDecider` (the SAME one the other Prime LLM layers build) is now built when **any** of the five switches is on. **No provider key enters the coordinator / web bridge / dashboard.**
  - **Tests.** Pure (`prime_plan_package::tests`, 11): accepts a well-formed package; rejects empty/overlong/malformed and missing-body/no-usable-child; caps child count; drops invalid priority + forward/unknown `after`; remaps `after` across dropped children; strips fence + redacts secrets; deterministic fallback is safe/bounded; mode strings stable; prompt bounded/steers/clamps. Loop (`prime_driver::tests`, 7, scripted decider): `plan_package_opens_one_and_leaves_confirm_open`, `plan_package_no_duplicate_on_second_tick`, `plan_package_malformed_or_unavailable_falls_back_safely`, `plan_package_does_not_clobber_existing_plan`, `plan_package_tenant_isolation`, `plan_package_approval_materializes_exactly_once` (approve via `respond_plan_confirm` → children created; second accept → `already_approved`, same ids, exactly-once ledger), `plan_package_off_by_default_authors_nothing`. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` green (4262); `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing warnings only — `maintenance.rs:227`, `controller_runtime.rs` collapsible-if — both untouched); `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This is bounded plan-package *authoring*, NOT freeform document editing or blanket self-approval: the authoring layer never accepts its own confirm — materialization happens only when an approval accepts through `brief.plan_confirm_respond` / `respond_plan_confirm`, either a human **or** (under the explicit `prime.plan_package.approve` standing grant — *Prime Plan-Package Approval — Standing Authority v1*, below) the loop accepting its OWN Prime-authored package. By default (the `tail` trigger) it is a deliberate **gap-filler at the tick tail**, firing only for a candidate the existing flow leaves idle (e.g. a Mandate whose lone Brief is `blocked`); **the `before_execute` trigger (Prime Active Planner Trigger v2, below) makes it also pre-empt a raw start.** Even then it does **not** decompose multi-Brief / orchestrated Mandates, scan every leaf Brief, or interrupt higher-priority governance gates. The model authors plan content only (title/body/summary/children) — never a method, capability, tool, assignment, agent, or approval. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip is **not** integration-tested in CI (the validator + deterministic fallback + eligibility/dedup/tenant/exactly-once paths are fully unit/loop tested with scripted output). Reuses the existing `MeshAiDecider`/session rather than a separate plan-package session. No dashboard change in this slice.

- **Prime Active Planner Trigger v2 — IMPLEMENTED.** Makes WHEN Prime authors a plan package configurable so it can propose a decomposition *before* starting raw undecomposed work, not only as an idle-tail gap-filler (execution-and-issue §1.7/§1.8/§3.1; company-model §12.5/§12.5A). **Layered on top of** the master `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_PLAN_PACKAGE` opt-in — with the master switch OFF nothing is authored in any mode. **Still no self-approval, no agent/tool assignment, no child creation.**
  - **Trigger parsing (`prime_plan_package::PrimePlanPackageTrigger`, pure + unit-tested).** `RELIX_PRIME_PLAN_PACKAGE_TRIGGER`: `tail`/`gap_fill`/blank → `Tail` (v1 idle gap-fill only); `before_execute`/`plan_before_execute` → `BeforeExecute` (also pre-empt a raw start); any **unknown** value safely falls back to `Tail`. Parsed via `parse_prime_plan_package_trigger`, threaded (like the other Prime switches) from both the background timer and the manual `prime.autonomy_tick_now` through `autonomous_prime_tick`/`handle_prime_autonomy_tick_now_with_ai`/`process_candidate(_inner)`.
  - **Shared open path + (B0) preemption (`prime_driver`).** The v1 (B5) tail-open logic is extracted into one helper `try_open_plan_package_for_mandate(...)` (same `plan_package_eligibility`, same `TaskStore::open_plan_package`, same author/validate/deterministic-fallback content, same budget/tenant/dedup guards). A new **(B0)** step at the TOP of the `ready_to_start` arm calls it when the trigger is `before_execute` AND the Mandate has exactly one **eligible** un-decomposed leaf Brief: it opens the proposed package and **holds** the raw start (returns the `plan_package` record instead of starting). It preempts ONLY a lone eligible leaf start — governance gates (proposal/strategy approval, team plan, hire/Clearance) classify to different phases and never reach (B0). `PlanPackageEligibility::Blocked` now carries `pending_package`: a PENDING package keeps the start held across ticks (the interactions check runs first, so Prime's own just-opened package is recognised as pending, never duplicated and never letting the raw Brief slip past); a mere existing/locked plan Dossier (not pending) lets the already-planned Brief start normally rather than stalling. The tail (B5) still runs as the catch-all in every mode. `PrimeAutonomyRecord` gains `plan_package_trigger` (`tail`/`before_execute`, set on the plan_package row, surfaced on `prime.autonomy_tick_now`).
  - **Tests.** Pure (`prime_plan_package::tests`, +4): trigger parses tail/gap_fill/blank → tail, before_execute/plan_before_execute → before_execute, unknown → tail, trigger strings stable. Loop (`prime_driver::tests`, +7, scripted decider): `plan_package_tail_trigger_does_not_preempt_a_ready_start`, `plan_package_before_execute_preempts_a_ready_start` (one package, confirm open, start held, `plan_package_trigger=before_execute`), `plan_package_before_execute_second_tick_holds_without_duplicate` (pending package holds, no dup, no extra budget), `plan_package_before_execute_respects_existing_plan_dossier` (no authoring; already-planned Brief still starts), `plan_package_before_execute_tenant_isolation`, `plan_package_before_execute_inert_when_master_switch_off` (legacy start), `plan_package_before_execute_falls_back_safely` (fallback/unavailable still open + held). `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` green (4273); `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing warnings only — `maintenance.rs:227`, `controller_runtime.rs` collapsible-if — both untouched); `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This changes only the WHEN (trigger), not the WHAT: it is still bounded plan-package authoring with the confirm left OPEN for a human. The authoring layer never self-approves; acceptance is now possible **only** under the separate, grant-gated `prime.plan_package.approve` standing authority (*Prime Plan-Package Approval — Standing Authority v1*, below), it is **not** freeform LLM control of the company, and `before_execute` preempts ONLY a lone eligible leaf Brief's raw start. No bridge/dashboard change in this slice.

- **Prime Plan-Package Approval — Standing Authority v1 — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the honestly-tracked "self-approval is not implemented" caveat for plan packages: the autonomous/manual Prime tick may now ACCEPT/materialize a plan package it ITSELF authored — but ONLY under the explicit, default-OFF `prime.plan_package.approve` standing grant, through the EXISTING confirm/decomposition-ledger path. **This is not blanket self-approval:** Prime-authored packages only, single-Brief + tenant-scoped, existing primitive + exactly-once ledger only (company-model §12.5/F-quater; execution-and-issue §1.7/§1.8).
  - **Seventh category (`prime_driver`).** `CATEGORY_PLAN_PACKAGE_APPROVE = "prime.plan_package.approve"`, added to `STANDING_AUTHORITY_CATEGORIES` (so the `prime.standing_authority` read surface + dashboard Settings grant/revoke it like the others — no new mutation route; the synthetic authority reuses `agent.standing_approval.*`). Default OFF; acts only while a live `standing_approvals` row exists for `__relix_autonomous_prime__` in that Guild. A seventh `descriptions[]` entry keeps the read surface honest; `apps/dashboard/src/pages/Settings.tsx` gains the label "Approve Prime-authored plan packages" (the category otherwise renders from the backend list verbatim).
  - **Approval gate (`try_approve_prime_plan_package_for_mandate`).** A shared helper called at the TOP of the `ready_to_start` arm (before the (B0) active-planner open) AND before the (B5) tail open, so a pending Prime-authored package is the next actionable governance gate the moment the grant exists — *before* opening a duplicate package and *before* any raw start. It acts only on a **single-Brief** candidate Mandate whose Brief is **in this Guild** (`task_in_tenant`), finds the OPEN `confirm` bound to a `plan` Dossier with a linked `suggest_tasks` proposal **authored by `__relix_autonomous_prime__`** (a human/other-actor package is invisible), and — only if `standing_active(CATEGORY_PLAN_PACKAGE_APPROVE)` — accepts it through the EXISTING `TaskStore::respond_plan_confirm` (the SAME primitive the human `brief.plan_confirm_respond` handler calls), so the linked proposal materializes once through the exactly-once decomposition ledger. Children open unassigned (empty resolved-assignee slice — an autonomous package sets no hints). With no grant it is a no-op (returns `None`, no side effect, no grant consumed) and the prior hold/report behaviour is unchanged. One bounded grant call is consumed via `consume_standing` ONLY on a real materialization (`approved`); once accepted the confirm is `resolved`, so a re-tick finds no OPEN Prime confirm and neither duplicates children nor consumes a second grant. A stale/refused accept records `blocked` honestly with no consume. Action `plan_package_approve`, outcome `advanced` on success (carries `suggestion_id`/`confirm_id`/`child_count`); Chronicles `prime.autonomous_plan_package_approve`. Independent of the authoring switch — approval authority is separate from authoring.
  - **Tests (`prime_driver::tests`, +6).** `plan_package_approve_without_standing_leaves_confirm_open` (no grant → confirm stays open, no children, no consume), `plan_package_approve_with_standing_materializes_through_ledger` (grant → accepted through the ledger, children created, confirm resolved, bounded `max_calls=1` grant consumed once), `plan_package_approve_is_idempotent_on_retick` (re-tick → no duplicate children, no second consume), `plan_package_approve_is_tenant_isolated` (a Guild-A grant never approves a Guild-B package), `plan_package_approve_refuses_human_authored_package` (a non-Prime-authored package is never auto-approved even with the grant), `plan_package_before_execute_then_standing_approval_then_proceed` (tick 1 opens under `before_execute` + holds; tick 2 with the grant approves/materializes; tick 3 proceeds without duplicating the package or re-approving). `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` green; `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; clippy clean on touched code; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This is explicit, bounded standing authority for **Prime-authored packages only**, through the existing confirm/decomposition-ledger path only — NOT blanket self-approval, NOT approval of another actor's package, NOT freeform LLM control. With no `prime.plan_package.approve` grant every plan-package gate stays human exactly as before. The live bridge→model→coordinator round trip and a live HTTP grant→tick→materialize smoke are **not** integration-tested in CI (the gate / author-match / tenant / idempotency / before-execute-pipeline paths are fully loop-tested in-process). No new mutation route; reuses `agent.standing_approval.*` and `respond_plan_confirm`.

- **Prime Autonomy End-to-End Smoke v1 + two gaps it found — IMPLEMENTED.** A release-grade backend smoke that drives the REAL `autonomous_prime_tick` repeatedly across the WHOLE new active-planner chain (not isolated helper tests), proving it moves work through the governed chain on the safe `echo` Rig — and the two backend gaps it surfaced, fixed with the smallest safe change (execution-and-issue §1.7/§1.8/§3.1; company-model §12.5/§12.5A).
  - **The E2E tests (`prime_driver::tests`, +2).** `prime_autonomy_e2e_plan_package_to_execution`: ready bare Mandate + lone leaf, `before_execute` trigger, plan-package authoring on, `prime.plan_package.approve` granted (bounded `max_calls=1`). Tick 1 OPENS the package before the raw start and HOLDS it (confirm open, 0 children, 0 runs); tick 2 ACCEPTS/materializes the Prime-authored package through the existing confirm + exactly-once decomposition ledger (children appear **exactly once**, the bounded grant is consumed **exactly once**, confirm resolved); a re-tick duplicates neither the package, the approval, nor the children; with the `prime.brief.assign_decomposed` grant a further tick **autonomously assigns** the unassigned Prime-decomposed children to the parent's own active `echo` assignee (no human assignment — the assignment grant consumed **exactly once**, a re-tick neither reassigns nor consumes again), then the loop STARTS them as **durable Shifts on `echo`** (heartbeat-trigger runs, `rig=echo`), and HONESTLY STOPS at the run-review gate (no `prime.run.review_accept` grant) opening no duplicate run; the Chronicle records `prime.autonomous_plan_package` / `…_plan_package_approve` / `…_assign_decomposed` / `…_mandate_start` **exactly once each**. `prime_autonomy_e2e_orchestration_no_op_is_honest`: the autonomous-only path (children left unassigned) — orchestration does real work **once**, every further tick is an honest **`skipped`** no-op (the loop parks at the assignment gate), children stay exactly two, no raw undecomposed leaf is ever run, and the Chronicle carries **exactly one** `prime.autonomous_advance` (no livelock spam).
  - **Gap 1 — autonomous orchestration livelock (FIXED, `prime_driver` `ADVANCE_ORCHESTRATE` arm).** After a Prime-decomposed package materializes unassigned children, the Mandate sits at `needs_orchestration`; `orchestrate_assign_ready` builds its own skeleton once but cannot adopt the decomposed children, so the loop re-ran orchestration **every tick** — taking false `advanced` credit, spending an action, and appending a Chronicle event each time. The arm now detects an **idempotent no-op** (the run created no Brief AND reduced no unassigned count — compared via `brief_counts` before/after, because the result body's `assigned_briefs` also reports an already-assigned subject as a re-assert and is not a reliable progress signal) and records it as **`skipped`** with no action consumed and no Chronicle event, parking honestly at the assignment gate instead of spinning. The first, real orchestration is unaffected (it advances).
  - **Gap 2 — non-deterministic Chronicle anchor (FIXED, `prime_driver::mandate_chronicle_anchor`).** `chronicle_autonomous` anchored an action's event on `list_briefs_by_mandate(mandate, 1)`, which is ordered `updated_at DESC` with arbitrary intra-second tie-breaking — so an event scattered onto whatever Sub-brief was touched most recently (e.g. a just-materialized decomposition child), making provenance non-deterministic (a flaky read under load). It now resolves a **stable anchor Brief** — a top-level (non-Sub-brief) Brief, lowest `task_id` (immutable) — so every autonomous event for a Mandate lands on the SAME Brief across decomposition/orchestration. No existing test asserted on these events; the change is provenance-only.
  - **What it still does NOT prove.** A **live** provider/bridge round trip (the smoke uses the safe `echo` Rig + a scripted decider, never a real model or remote Rig). Autonomous assignment of Prime-decomposed children is now proven **under the narrow `prime.brief.assign_decomposed` grant** (see *Prime-Decomposed Child Assignment — Standing Authority v1*, below) — with no grant, or a parent with no valid active assignee, the loop still parks honestly at the assignment gate. Run via `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib prime_driver::tests::prime_autonomy_e2e`. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` green (4281); `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; clippy clean on touched code (2 pre-existing warnings only — `maintenance.rs:227`, `controller_runtime.rs` collapsible-if — both untouched); `git diff --check` clean.

- **Prime Governed Dossier Authoring (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the broad "no autonomous authoring — no agent/LLM authors or revises a document on its own" caveat for the **company orchestration path** (company-model §12.5F; execution-and-issue §1.8). The orchestration parent / role-track / subject-execution / placeholder plan Dossiers were previously persisted with the legacy author-less `add_dossier` (author = NULL, no lock check). They now route through a single governed helper so Prime's own generated plan text is first-class, lock-aware, idempotent document state — **without** opening any freeform agent document editing.
  - **Store helper (`TaskStore::author_prime_dossier`, `coordinator/mod.rs`).** Input `(task_id, kind, title, body)`. It pre-reads the current latest revision of `(brief, kind)`: a Prime-owned latest → `AlreadyPresent` (no duplicate appended, rerun-idempotent); a human/editor or legacy author-less latest → `SkippedHumanOwned` (never clobbered); no latest yet → writes the FIRST revision through the EXISTING governed `author_dossier` (mode `revise`, no `expected`), stamped author = `agent::prime_driver::AUTONOMOUS_PRIME_AUTHORITY` (`__relix_autonomous_prime__`). A kind locked by a different subject is refused by `author_dossier` and surfaced as `LockedByOther`; a concurrent stale write surfaces as `Stale`. Outcome type `brief::PrimeDossierOutcome` (`Authored`/`AlreadyPresent`/`LockedByOther`/`SkippedHumanOwned`/`Stale`) with a stable `.label()`. Only the first Prime-owned `create` revision is ever written (no agent overwrite of stored text); kinds (`orchestration`/`execution`/`blocker`) are the flow's existing names, unrenamed.
  - **Handler integration (`handlers::handle_orchestrate_with_blueprint`).** The four `add_dossier` writes (parent `orchestration`, role-track `orchestration`, subject `execution`, placeholder `blocker`) now call `author_prime_dossier` and push a per-doc `prime_dossier_note` (`{task_id, kind, outcome, …}`) onto a new `dossier_notes` array on the orchestration result body — so a locked / human-owned doc Prime declined to overwrite is reported honestly, not silently dropped. All four remain guarded by `!was_existing` (create-on-new-Brief only), so a rerun on a reused Brief still writes nothing; the helper's idempotency is an additional backstop. No document body is dumped into any event (the success path's `brief.dossier_authored` Chronicle from `author_dossier` is unchanged).
  - **Tests.** Store (`coordinator::tests`): `author_prime_dossier_creates_prime_owned_then_idempotent` (first write Prime-stamped `create`; rerun `already_present`, single revision, original body kept), `author_prime_dossier_preserves_human_and_legacy_docs` (`skipped_human_owned` over a human `author_dossier` row AND a legacy author-less `add_dossier` row; bodies preserved), `author_prime_dossier_refuses_lock_held_by_other` (`locked_by_other`, nothing written). Handler (`handlers::tests`): `orchestrate_parent_dossier_is_prime_authored_and_idempotent` (parent `orchestration` Dossier stamped `__relix_autonomous_prime__`, `dossier_notes` carries the `authored` entry, rerun appends no duplicate revision). `cargo fmt --check` clean; `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` green (4244); `cargo check -p relix-runtime -p relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy -p relix-runtime` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing warnings in `maintenance.rs:227` + `mod.rs:10947`, both untouched); `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** This governs **Prime's own** generated orchestration/plan text only. It does NOT add a model-chosen `create_document`/`create_interaction` action, does NOT let any agent author or revise an *operator's* Dossier, and does NOT write raw model JSON to a doc — those remain out of scope (freeform agent document editing is deliberately not built). The bridge is untouched (no new route; `dossier_notes` rides the existing `mandate.orchestrate` response). No dashboard change.

- **Issue document authoring / per-doc revision-locking / forking (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Implements `docs/relix-execution-and-issue-design.md §1.8` (Dossier documents are revisioned with optimistic concurrency + lockable) for the durable `task_documents` Dossier surface. Closes the honestly-tracked "full issue document authoring / per-doc revision-locking / forking" gap. **Bounded v1, append-only, safe by construction — NOT** a rich-text editor, markdown overhaul, collaborative cursor, external document store, or autonomous LLM planner.
  - **Schema (additive, nullable).** Three columns on `task_documents` (CREATE + additive `ALTER`): `author TEXT`, `revision_of_doc_id TEXT`, `forked_from_doc_id TEXT`. Legacy / `brief.dossier_add` / plan-package rows carry NULLs. `revision_number` is **derived in the read** (a correlated-subquery 1-based position within Brief+kind, `created_at`/`rowid` ordered — `DOSSIER_REVNUM_SQL`), never stored, so every row (incl. legacy) has one; `list_dossiers` now orders by `rowid` (insert order) so the list order matches the revision number. `brief.dossiers` / `dossier_get` / `dossier_latest` carry the new metadata (additive — existing clients unaffected).
  - **Store method (`author_dossier`, optimistic-locked).** Input `(task_id, kind, title, body, author, mode, expected_latest_doc_id?, base_doc_id?)`. `mode=revise` (default): when `expected_latest_doc_id` is given it MUST equal the current latest of that kind, else a typed `DossierStale` is returned and **nothing is written** (Dossiers stay immutable/append-only); when none is given it appends on top of the latest (linking `revision_of_doc_id`) or creates the first revision. `mode=fork`: requires `base_doc_id` on the **same Brief+kind** and writes a new append-only row carrying `forked_from_doc_id` **even if the latest moved** (the explicit branch-from-stale escape hatch, never an accidental overwrite). Validation: safe short `kind` token (`[a-zA-Z0-9_-]`, ≤40), non-empty length-bounded `title`/`author`, non-empty `body` ≤64 KiB. The whole read-latest-then-insert runs under the store's single connection mutex (effectively atomic). Each write Chronicles `brief.dossier_authored` (create) / `brief.dossier_revised` / `brief.dossier_forked`.
  - **Capability + bridge.** `brief.dossier_author` (JSON arg) is tenant-scoped on the owning Brief like every Dossier surface; a stale result is an `Ok` `{stale:true,…}` body (not an error). Bridge `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/dossiers/author` maps that stale discriminant onto an honest **409 Conflict** carrying the structured body (`dossier_author_response`, mirroring `run_report_response`; "never retry a 409"); every successful author is 200. A companion `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/dossiers/latest?kind=` (proxying `brief.dossier_latest`) loads a body for editing. Both behind boot-policy allow rules (`spine_brief_dossier_author` / `spine_brief_dossier_latest`) + coverage.
  - **Dashboard.** The Brief workroom (`apps/dashboard/src/components/BriefDetail.tsx`) gains a compact **Documents** section: each kind's latest revision (kind/title/rev/author/forked badge) with **Edit latest** (loads under the optimistic lock, keeping the loaded doc_id as `expected_latest_doc_id`), a kind/title/body **textarea** editor (no rich text), **Save revision** (a 409 keeps the draft + flags it stale), and **Fork from loaded revision**. Saving a new `plan` revision naturally makes any plan-bound approval stale (the approval binds the latest plan id). `apps/dashboard/src/api.ts` gains `Dossier`/`DossierMeta`/`DossierAuthored` types + a `briefDossiers.{latest,author}` client. Rebuilt `dashboard-dist`.
  - **Tests.** Runtime: `dossier_author_revise_lock_and_fork` (create→revise→stale-refusal→fork + the three Chronicle events), `dossier_author_validation_and_fork_base_guards`, `dossier_reads_carry_revision_metadata` (derived revnum incl. legacy rows), `brief_dossier_author_denied_across_tenant`, and `plan_confirm_stale_after_authored_plan_revision` (the existing plan-confirm stale protection still holds when the new plan revision is written through `author_dossier`). Bridge: `dossier_author_stale_is_a_409_authored_is_200`. Targeted `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib dossier`/`plan_confirm` green; `relix-web-bridge` green; `cargo clippy` clean on the touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `maintenance.rs` warnings only); `npm run build` + dist parity; `git diff --check` clean.
  - **Honest scope / not done.** Textarea + append-only v1 only — **no** rich-text editor, **no** markdown renderer overhaul, **no** collaborative cursor, **no** external document store. The **dashboard** plan-package **composer** remains a manual surface; autonomous (LLM) plan-package authoring is now shipped on the **Prime tick** (see *Prime Plan-Package Authoring (v1)* above) — bounded, governed, confirm-left-open.

- **Document locking (v1) — IMPLEMENTED (closes the §1.8 locking gap; one explicit deviation).** Adds explicit, owner-or-nobody locking on top of the optimistic revision lock, for the durable Dossier surface. **Backend-only** (no dashboard work in this slice).
  - **Schema (additive).** A new `task_document_locks` table keyed `(task_id, kind)` — `locked_by`, `locked_at`, optional bounded `reason` — created via `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` (fresh + existing DBs; no ALTER needed).
  - **Store methods.** `lock_dossier(task_id, kind, subject, reason?)` upserts the lock (a same-owner re-lock is idempotent and refreshes the reason; a different owner returns a no-write `DossierLockConflict`); `unlock_dossier(task_id, kind, subject)` is **owner-or-nobody** (a different subject is a `DossierLockConflict`; an absent lock is an idempotent `DossierUnlocked`); `list_dossier_locks(task_id)` lists active locks (oldest first). `author_dossier` now reads the lock **first** and returns a no-write `DossierLocked` (`Ok` body) when the kind is locked by someone other than the author — checked before the stale/lineage decision, so a locked-by-other write is refused regardless of base. Validation reuses `is_safe_dossier_kind` + a `MAX_DOSSIER_LOCK_REASON_LEN` (280) bound. Lock/unlock Chronicle `brief.dossier_locked` / `brief.dossier_unlocked` (bounded payloads, no content).
  - **Capabilities + bridge.** `brief.dossier_lock` (`task_id|kind|subject|reason`) / `brief.dossier_unlock` (`task_id|kind|subject`) / `brief.dossier_locks` (`task_id`), all tenant-scoped on the owning Brief via `deny_cross_tenant`. Bridge `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/dossiers/lock` + `…/unlock` map the `{conflict:true,…}` discriminant onto **409** (`dossier_lock_response`); `GET …/dossiers/locks` passthrough; `dossier_author_response` now also maps the author `{locked:true,…}` discriminant onto **409**. Boot-policy allow rules in both `relix-mesh-up.{ps1,sh}` (`spine_brief_dossier_lock|unlock|locks`) + the coverage manifest.
  - **Deviation (recorded).** A locked-document write from a non-owner is **refused** (the caller reloads / waits for unlock / explicitly `fork`s), **not** auto-redirected to a new key — Paperclip's "locked-flag → writes redirect" nicety is **deferred**. No operator force-unlock, no lock lease/expiry in v1.
  - **Tests.** Runtime: `dossier_lock_blocks_other_author_then_unlock_allows`, `dossier_lock_conflict_and_idempotency`, `dossier_lock_validates_inputs`, `dossier_lock_denied_across_tenant`. Bridge: `brief_doc_lock_and_interaction_cancel_routes_round_trip` (lock 200 + wire arg, conflict 409, unlock, locks list, cancel, idempotent create). `cargo test -p relix-runtime --lib` (4240 pass), `relix-web-bridge` bins green, `cargo clippy` clean on touched code (2 pre-existing unrelated `controller_runtime.rs`/`maintenance.rs` warnings only), fmt + `git diff --check` clean.

- **Thread-interaction cancel + idempotent create + continuation wake (v1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Extends the existing §1.9 interaction model (open/respond/expire) with the three v1 gaps. **Backend-only.**
  - **Schema (additive).** `brief_interactions.idempotency_key TEXT` (CREATE column + additive `ALTER`) with a partial `UNIQUE` index `brief_interactions_idem` over `(task_id, author, idempotency_key) WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL` (created after the ALTER; legacy keyless rows exempt).
  - **Store methods.** `open_interaction` now delegates to `open_interaction_idem(…, idempotency_key?)`: with a key, a check-then-insert under the store lock returns the existing card for a repeated `(task_id, author, key)` (durable backstop = the partial UNIQUE index); a keyless create is the unchanged legacy path. `cancel_interaction(task_id, interaction_id, subject)` flips an `open` card to `cancelled` (Chronicles `brief.interaction_cancelled`), is idempotent on an already-cancelled card, and refuses a decided one. `respond_interaction` and `cancel_interaction` both **offer a continuation wake** (`offer_supervisory_wake`, dropping the conn lock first to avoid re-entrant deadlock) — the §1.9 "wake the assignee when answered" policy; no assignee → an honest `brief.wakeup_skipped` note.
  - **Capabilities + bridge.** `brief.interaction_create` (JSON, idempotency-aware) + `brief.interaction_cancel` (`task_id|interaction_id|subject`), tenant-scoped. Bridge `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/interactions` routes through `brief.interaction_create` when an `idempotency_key` is present (else the legacy pipe `brief.interaction_open`); `POST …/interactions/:iid/cancel` is new. Boot-policy rules (`spine_brief_interaction_create|cancel`) + coverage manifest.
  - **Deviations (recorded).** **Supersede-on-comment** is **NOT** implemented for plain ask/confirm cards (only the approval-bound plan confirm expires, via the existing stale-plan path); there is **no per-interaction `expires_at` TTL** (event-driven expiry only); `suggest_tasks` materialization is the pre-existing exactly-once decomposition path, unchanged.
  - **Tests.** Runtime: `interaction_cancel_lifecycle`, `interaction_create_is_idempotent`, `interaction_respond_and_cancel_offer_continuation_wake`, `interaction_cancel_denied_across_tenant` (plus the existing open/respond/duplicate/cross-tenant tests still green). Bridge: covered in `brief_doc_lock_and_interaction_cancel_routes_round_trip`.

- **Prime integration hook (§ Part C) — docs-only, deliberately no autonomy-loop change.** These new governed capabilities (`brief.dossier_lock`/`unlock`/`locks`, `brief.interaction_create`/`cancel`) are the path a future Prime / Operative will use to lock a plan it is drafting, raise an answerable card, or close one — **through the same tenant-scoped, validated, audited capabilities a human uses**. No deliberation/orchestration *action name* (`create_document` / `create_interaction`) was added to the autonomous Prime loop in this slice: the Prime action dispatch is a constrained confirm/hold over a computed menu, and adding a free-form authoring action is out of scope and would need its own governed, validated wiring. Until then, an LLM cannot author a document or interaction by emitting raw JSON — only the governed capabilities can, behind policy + tenant + validation, exactly as today.

## Known Divergences From The Design Docs

This is the honest ledger. Do not describe these as done until the code is actually wired and tested.

### Execution And Issue Design

- Board transitions still use a rigid edge graph. `relix-execution-and-issue-design.md` wants permissive target validation plus guarded side effects. Guarded side effects now exist; the transition validator is still stricter than the design.
- Claim has the two-pointer fields now, but it is not the full Paperclip checkout engine. Implemented: `checkout_run_id`, `execution_run_id`, holder, locked-at, self-refresh, lease/release/admin force-release, lock clearing, persistent wakeup rows, queue/coalesce/defer/skipped decisions, lazy lock stamping from queued wakeups, deferred promotion, **explicit HTTP 409 conflict semantics on the run start path** (roadmap §5 slice 1, see below), **an in-process per-Operative start lock** (below), and **a start-path duplicate-start guard** that refuses a *new* manual/Prime start when the SAME Operative already has a live, actually-running run on the same Brief (below) — so the deliberately-idempotent `claim_brief_for_run` self-refresh can no longer be turned into two run rows/workspaces by a double-start, and **stale-run adoption by terminal-run evidence** (roadmap §5 slice 10, see below) so a dangling live Claim pointing at an already-terminal run is reclaimed — at manual/Prime start time AND as a batch admission step at the top of every autonomous heartbeat tick — instead of waiting for the age-based sweep. Missing: a dedicated queued-run table separate from wakeup rows, and the broader Paperclip stale-run *adoption-in-place* (the new agent inheriting the dead owner's checkout context) — Relix releases+re-claims rather than transferring the prior checkout.
- **Claim HTTP 409 + per-Operative start lock (roadmap §5 slice 1; execution-and-issue §1.4/§7.1 LOCKED two-pointer Claim, §2.6 start lock) — IMPLEMENTED.** The two-pointer Claim already detected a conflict (a live Claim held by another execution → `claim_brief_for_run` returns `Ok(false)`, surfaced by `preflight_run` as a `RunReport{status:"already_running"}`), but the HTTP bridge passed that refusal through as a **200** the dashboard could blindly retry. Closed: (1) **409 surface** — the `brief.run` route (`run_brief` in `relix-web-bridge/src/spine.rs`) now inspects the returned `RunReport` and maps the conflict status `already_running` onto **`409 Conflict`** (`run_report_response` + `json_with_status`), preserving the structured `RunReport` body so the client sees *why*. Every other outcome stays **200**: real runs (`running`/`done`/`failed`/`continued`) and the **precondition** refusals (`unassigned`/`no_adapter`/`adapter_unavailable`/`workspace_error`/`workspace_context_error`) — those describe a fixable setup gap, not a lost race, so a client may legitimately retry after fixing the cause. The 409 is reserved for the one case a blind retry must never be attempted on; the rule is pinned in code + tests: **never retry a 409**. The coordinator `brief.run` contract is unchanged (still returns an `Ok` `RunReport` for all refusals); the HTTP semantics live in the bridge, mirroring the existing `coordinator_err_status` mapping. (2) **Per-Operative start lock** — a new in-process start-lock registry on `TaskStore` (`agent_start_lock(agent_id) -> Arc<Mutex<()>>`, lazily created, keyed per Operative) is acquired across the synchronous claim+commit critical section of `preflight_run` (the shared manual/Prime start chokepoint), so two concurrent start passes for the **same** Operative are serialized — they can't both read the live-run count stale and double-claim a slot / double-start the same Operative/Brief execution path (§2.6). It is **distinct from the live-run claim *count*** (which measures capacity) and from the per-Brief DB Claim (which guards one Brief): the lock orders the check-then-claim itself. Different Operatives get distinct locks → unrelated work runs fully in parallel. The lock is only ever held across the short synchronous start (never across an adapter run), so it **cannot go stale** — no timeout is needed (a poisoned lock is recovered; the guarded state is just a `()` marker). (3) **Same-Operative duplicate-start guard** — the start lock alone only *serializes* the critical section; it does not stop two *sequential* starts by the same Operative from both being accepted, because `claim_brief_for_run` deliberately lets the **same** Operative refresh a live Claim (the wakeup/heartbeat/lease idempotency the lower-level API must keep) and `preflight_run` mints a **new** `run_id` each call — so a double-click / re-start would re-claim and open a SECOND run row + workspace. `preflight_run` now, while holding the start lock and *before* claiming, calls the new read-only `TaskStore::live_run_by_agent(brief, agent)` and refuses `already_running` (→ 409) when it returns a live run. The guard fires only on **both** a live Claim held by that Operative **and** running-run evidence (a `brief_runs` row in `running` whose id matches the Claim's execution/checkout pointer); a stale Claim with no running run does **not** match (that is stale-run adoption's job, slice 10), and once a run finishes (Claim released + run terminal) a fresh start is allowed again — so legitimate continuation is never blocked. The lower-level `claim_brief_for_run` idempotent self-ownership is **unchanged** (the guard lives only in the start path), so wakeup/heartbeat/recovery callers are unaffected. The bridge already maps `already_running` → 409, so no bridge change was needed. Tests: bridge — `already_running` → 409 with the body preserved, real/precondition statuses stay 200; coordinator — start lock is per-Operative + reused (same Operative shares one lock, different get distinct), two concurrent distinct-Operative claims → exactly one wins and the loser conflicts (and a retry by the loser loses again), the manual path refuses `already_running` when another run holds the Claim, two concurrent same-Brief starts against a live external Claim both conflict + a retry loses again, **a sequential same-Brief same-Operative double-start: first Ready+running, second refused `already_running` with no second run row/workspace, and a post-completion start allowed again**, and **a concurrent same-Brief same-Operative race: exactly one wins, the other conflicts, one run row, never-retry-a-409 pinned**. **Now closed (slice 10, see next entry):** stale-run adoption by terminal evidence — a dangling live Claim whose run pointer is already terminal is reclaimed at start time, not only by the age-based sweep. The start lock is wired into the per-run start chokepoint (`preflight_run`), while the heartbeat batch path's slot accounting stays race-free via its single SQLite transaction (atomic count+claim) rather than the per-Operative lock.
- **Claim stale-run adoption by terminal evidence (roadmap §5 slice 10; execution-and-issue §1.4 "stale-run adoption" / §7.1 LOCKED two-pointer Claim) — IMPLEMENTED.** A Brief's Claim can be left **live** (lease not yet expired) even though the run it points at has already reached a **terminal** state — e.g. the owning process died between recording the terminal `brief_runs` row and releasing the Claim, or a long lease outlived a crashed owner. Age-based `recover_stale_runs` never fixed this: it only sweeps rows still `status = 'running'`, and this run is already terminal — so the dangling Claim would block a fresh start (`already_running` → 409) until the lease simply aged out, even though terminal evidence proves the prior Shift ended. Closed by a new store helper `TaskStore::reclaim_terminal_claim(task_id)` (`coordinator/mod.rs`), called inside the start chokepoint `preflight_run` (`coordinator/heartbeat.rs`) **after** the duplicate-start guard and **before** `claim_brief_for_run`, and now ALSO from the autonomous heartbeat (see the heartbeat admission entry below). It reads the Claim's run pointer (`execution_run_id`, else `checkout_run_id`), looks that run up in `brief_runs` for the same Brief, and releases the Claim **only on terminal evidence** — any status other than `running`. It is **safe by construction** and never steals a live owner: a still-`running` pointer → no-op (never releases a Claim backing a live run); a pointer matching no `brief_runs` row for this Brief → no-op (no evidence — never release another actor's live Claim on a guess); the release is a conditional `UPDATE` keyed on the Claim's **own** pointer + holder (the same guard as `release_claim_for_run`), so a **newer** Claim that already re-acquired the Brief is never clobbered. On a real reclaim it promotes the oldest deferred wakeup (like a normal release) and records a `brief.claim_reclaimed` Chronicle note (only on an abnormal dangling Claim — never on normal completion, where the Claim was already released, so no noise). The **409 duplicate-start** behavior from slices 1 is preserved: a still-`running` matching run still refuses `already_running` (the reclaim is a no-op on it), while a terminal matching run now lets a new start proceed. Tests: store helper — releases when the pointed run is terminal (+ chronicle + idempotent), leaves a `running` run alone, needs evidence matching the Claim's own pointer (a different terminal run is not evidence), does not clobber a newer running Claim; start path (`preflight_run`) — adopts a stale Claim with terminal run evidence and a fresh start succeeds (one live run row + the reclaim chronicle), refuses `already_running` (→ 409, never retry) when another worker's run is still `running`. The existing age-based recovery, the duplicate-start guard, and all slice-1 conflict tests still pass unchanged. **Honest remaining edge:** Relix *releases + re-claims* (the new owner mints a fresh checkout/run) rather than transferring the dead owner's checkout context in place — full Paperclip "adopt the prior checkout run" (the new agent inheriting the crashed run's `checkoutRunId`) is not modeled; and adoption fires on terminal evidence where the Claim's run pointer matches a recorded terminal `brief_runs` row. (The heartbeat-origin asymmetry that previously made the autonomous path's pointer *never* match a recorded run is now closed — see "Claim/run id alignment" below — so the only Claim freed by lease expiry instead of this adoption is one lost in the narrow window before its run row was ever written, i.e. a crash between the claim and `record_run_start`.)

- **Claim stale-run adoption — autonomous heartbeat admission step (roadmap §5 slice 10; execution-and-issue §1.4/§7.1) — IMPLEMENTED.** The reclaim above was wired only into the manual/Prime start chokepoint (`preflight_run`); the autonomous heartbeat could not benefit because a Brief whose Claim is still **live** (lease not yet aged out) is excluded from `list_ready_briefs` — so the dispatcher never saw it and it stayed wedged behind the dangling Claim until the lease expired (the documented remaining edge). Closed by a new batch helper `TaskStore::reclaim_terminal_claims_ready(limit)` (`coordinator/mod.rs`) called as the **first step of every `dispatch_batch_with_policy` tick** (`coordinator/heartbeat.rs`), **before** `list_ready_briefs`. It pre-filters (one query) for would-be-ready Briefs (assigned, active board, unblocked) blocked **only** by a live Claim whose run pointer (`execution_run_id`, else `checkout_run_id`) refers to a terminal `brief_runs` row, then reclaims each through the **same** `reclaim_terminal_claim` helper the manual/Prime path uses — so manual/Prime and heartbeat share one tested adoption primitive. All safety lives in `reclaim_terminal_claim` (the candidate query is only a pre-filter): it re-reads each Claim under its own lock and releases only on terminal evidence matching the Claim's **own** pointer + holder, so a Claim that changed between the candidate scan and the release is a no-op; it never releases a still-`running` run or a newer re-acquired Claim. Once reclaimed, the Brief becomes `ready` and the normal queue/claim path (timer wake → `claim_queued_wakeups_with_caps`) dispatches it the **same tick**, and a promoted deferred wake is reused (no duplicate wakeups/runs). It is **idempotent** (a Brief already reclaimed or now re-running is no longer a candidate — a second pass records no further reclaim) and **tenant-safe by construction** (each reclaim touches only that one Brief's own Claim). Tests (`coordinator/heartbeat.rs`): the heartbeat adopts a terminal stale Claim then dispatches it the same tick (one reclaim chronicle, board → `in_review`, Claim released, no duplicate live run); never reclaims a live `running` Claim (untouched, not dispatched); does not reclaim when the pointer moved to a newer running run; the adoption is idempotent (two passes → one reclaim, one promoted wake); and it is tenant-safe (Guild A's terminal-stale Claim adopted while Guild B's live running Claim is untouched). **Honest remaining edge:** still release+reclaim (a fresh checkout/run), not in-place transfer of the dead owner's checkout context. Adoption requires the Claim's run pointer to match a recorded terminal `brief_runs` row; for heartbeat-origin Claims this now holds by construction (the claim/run id alignment below), so the only Claim freed by lease expiry instead of this admission step is one lost before its run row was ever written (a crash between the claim and `record_run_start`).
- **Claim/run id alignment for heartbeat-origin Claims (roadmap §5 slice 10 follow-up; execution-and-issue §1.4/§7.1) — IMPLEMENTED.** Closes the asymmetry the two adoption entries above flagged as their remaining edge for the *autonomous* path: the heartbeat used to stamp the Brief Claim's `execution_run_id` with a `shift_<uuid>` (minted at wakeup-queue time / claim time / deferred-promotion) while the dispatcher minted a **separate** `run_<uuid>` for the `brief_runs` ledger row — so a heartbeat-origin Claim's pointer could **never** match a recorded run, and `reclaim_terminal_claim` (which adopts only on a pointer→terminal-`brief_runs` match) could not adopt it; it waited for lease expiry. Now there is **ONE** durable id end to end: the wakeup mints a `run_<uuid>` when first **queued** (`request_brief_wakeup_with_admission`), when **promoted** from deferred (`promote_oldest_deferred_wakeup_in_conn`), and as the claim-time fallback (`claim_queued_wakeups_with_caps`); that id is stamped onto the Claim's `execution_run_id` and is now **carried on `ClaimedWakeup.run_id`**, which `dispatch_batch_with_policy` uses as the `brief_runs.run_id` (via `prepare_claimed_run`) **instead of minting a fresh one**. So the Claim pointer and the ledger row are the same `run_` id, and a heartbeat-origin Claim left dangling on a terminal run is adopted by terminal evidence exactly like a manual run. The id stays workspace-path-safe (`run_id_is_safe`); `preflight_run`'s manual/Prime path is unchanged (it still mints its own `run_<uuid>` at claim time); the test-only pure helper `claim_ready_batch` was aligned to `run_` for consistency (the live loop claims via the wakeup queue). To make adoption *effective* for this path, `reclaim_terminal_claim` also now **closes the mid-flight wake tied to the reclaimed run** — the dangling state always co-occurs with the spawning wake still `queued`/`running` (the owner died before `finish_wakeup`), and because that wake's `execution_run_id` is now the SAME id as the reclaimed pointer, the reclaim finishes ONLY that wake (status mirrored from the run's terminal status), so the next timer wake is not coalesced into a stale `running` wake and the adopted Brief re-dispatches the same tick with no duplicate run/wake. The cleanup matches only the wake whose id == the reclaimed pointer (an unrelated wake, or a `deferred` wake with no id, is never touched) and is a no-op for the manual/Prime path (which creates no wake under the run id). Tests (`coordinator/heartbeat.rs`): the heartbeat claim pointer is a `run_` ledger id equal to the queued wake's id and the Brief row's `execution_run_id` (`heartbeat_claim_pointer_is_a_run_ledger_id_not_a_shift_id`); a heartbeat-origin Claim dangling on a terminal run is adopted and re-dispatched the same tick with no leftover queued/running wake and no duplicate live run (`heartbeat_origin_dangling_terminal_claim_is_adopted_and_redispatched`); and the reclaim closes only the wake tied to the terminal run, leaving an unrelated queued wake untouched (`reclaim_closes_only_the_wake_tied_to_the_terminal_run`). The existing live-running-not-reclaimed, pointer-moved-not-reclaimed, idempotent, and tenant-safe adoption tests still pass unchanged. **Honest remaining edge (unchanged):** still release+reclaim (a fresh checkout/run), not in-place transfer of the dead owner's checkout context; and a Claim lost before its `brief_runs` row was ever written (a crash between the claim and `record_run_start`) has no terminal evidence to match and is still freed by lease expiry.
- Entry guards are enforced for the current board path: `in_progress` requires an assignee and no unresolved Snags; `in_review` requires `reviewer_agent_id`.
- There is now a Brief-local wakeup queue and coalesce/defer/queue engine for the heartbeat dispatcher. Implemented: timer wake admission, lazy claim stamping, deferred promotion, per-Operative max-running caps on queue claims, and a per-Operative Allowance hard-stop admission gate at dispatch (see the Allowance hard-stop slice above; refused Briefs park in `blocked` with a `brief.budget_refused` event). A true per-Operative start lock separate from claim counts now exists on the per-run start chokepoint (`preflight_run`; see the Claim HTTP 409 + start-lock slice above) — the heartbeat batch path's slot accounting remains race-free via its single SQLite transaction rather than the lock. A Guild-level spend gate now also gates the autonomous path (see the Guild-level spend hard-stop slice above; refused Briefs park in `blocked` with a `guild.budget_refused` event). Still missing: all external triggers funneled exclusively through that chokepoint, and the conservative recovery chain. Failure handling is otherwise still simple failure-to-blocked parking.
- **Brief-run chokepoint audit (TG7), honest finding.** Every path that *actually executes* a Brief funnels through the one shared seam `prepare_claimed_run` (scoped-workspace preflight → board move → `brief_runs` ledger row → cancel-register → lifecycle transcript → bridge-back token → pre-run baseline) → `execute_ready`: the **manual** `brief.run` capability via `preflight_run` (probe → `claim_brief_for_run` single-owner concurrency → `prepare_claimed_run`), **Prime's Start-to-Shift** `prime.start` (company-model §12.5B) over an approved Mandate's ready Briefs, and the **autonomous heartbeat** via `dispatch_batch_with_policy` → `prepare_claimed_run` (after `claim_queued_wakeups_with_caps`). The two operator-initiated paths (`brief.run` + `prime.start`) now share one async seam — `preflight_and_spawn` (`preflight_run` → commit → `execute_ready` on a background thread) — so a Prime-started Shift is byte-identical to a manual run and is likewise treated as a sovereign, *not* Allowance-gated action. `run_brief_now` is only the synchronous wrapper around `preflight_run` + `execute_ready`. The **companion** (`POST /v1/spine/companion`) only *creates/moves/comments* Briefs (no `brief.run` call) and **bridge-back** (`brt_*` token) only lets an in-flight Shift report back (comment / sub-brief / dossier / snag / clearance) — neither is an execution entry point; the work they create is later executed through the same chokepoint. **`scheduled` is a reserved `trigger` value with no scheduler wired today.** Two honest gaps remain: (a) the per-Operative **Allowance hard-stop is enforced only on the autonomous heartbeat path**, not the manual `brief.run` path — an operator-initiated run is treated as a deliberate, sovereign action and is **not** budget-gated; (b) the per-run workspace-preflight + claim + ledger ARE shared, but concurrency caps (`max_concurrent_runs`) are an autonomous-only admission gate, while the manual path relies on the single-owner Claim alone (one run per Brief, but no per-Operative parallel-run cap). Both are intentional-but-undocumented-until-now; fixing either is a behavior change deferred to an explicit decision.
- **Thread interactions (§1.9) — the answerable cards now exist for `ask`/`confirm`.** A net-new Brief-scoped interaction model: a small `brief_interactions` table (modeled on the Dossier `task_documents` pattern — `interaction_id`, `task_id` FK, `kind` ∈ `ask`/`confirm`, `prompt`, `choices` JSON, `author`, `status` ∈ `open`/`resolved`/`rejected`, `response`, timestamps, `resolved_by`), three capabilities (`brief.interaction_open` / `brief.interactions` / `brief.interaction_respond`), bridge routes (`POST`/`GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/interactions`, `POST …/:iid/respond`), boot-policy allow rules in both `relix-mesh-up.{ps1,sh}` + the coverage manifest, and the Brief-workroom **Requests** panel (open cards above the Conversation with inline Yes/No · choice · free-text answer; resolved/rejected listed and marked; section omitted when there are none — honest empty state). Tenant-scoped via the owning Brief (`deny_cross_tenant`; a cross-Guild Brief/interaction id reads as not-found). The response is **idempotent** — a second answer to an already-answered card is a typed `Invalid` refusal (→ HTTP 400), not a silent overwrite — and both the open and the answer are mirrored into the Chronicle (`brief.interaction_opened` / `…_resolved` / `…_rejected`). Tested at the runtime (happy path + event emission, duplicate-response refusal, cross-tenant denial) and the bridge (open→list→respond round-trip with exact wire-arg assertions + duplicate→400). **v1 additions (see the implemented bullet above):** `cancel` (`brief.interaction_cancel`, `status` gains `cancelled`), idempotency-aware create (`brief.interaction_create` + `idempotency_key` column / partial-UNIQUE index), and a continuation wake on respond/cancel. **Still deferred vs. Paperclip:** supersede-on-comment for plain cards and a per-interaction `expires_at` TTL (only the approval-bound plan confirm expires, via the stale-plan path).
- **`suggest_tasks` (§1.9) — the proposed child-Brief tree now exists (first slice).** The third documented kind is built on the same `brief_interactions` table (a new nullable `proposal` column carries the bounded JSON proposal; `kind = 'suggest_tasks'`). An Operative opens a card with a `summary` + a bounded list of child specs (`{title, priority?, after?, assignee_agent_id?|assignee_role?}`); the proposal is validated + size-capped server-side ([`brief::normalize_proposal`]: ≥1 child, ≤20, titles ≤200 chars / summary ≤500 chars truncated, priorities validated, empty titles dropped, **each assignee hint trimmed + ≤128 chars with an id-OR-role-not-both rule** — no path/file execution, no unbounded payload). The optional **`after`** is a simple intra-proposal dependency (§1.6): the 0-based index of an **earlier** sibling this child depends on. `normalize_proposal` remaps it across any dropped (empty) children and **refuses a forward / self / out-of-range / dropped-target reference at open time** (so the proposal is a backward-only, acyclic-by-construction order before any card exists). Two capabilities (`brief.suggest_open` taking a JSON arg like `prime.propose`; `brief.suggest_respond` taking `task_id|interaction_id|responder|verdict` with `verdict ∈ accept/reject`), bridge routes (`POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/suggestions`, `POST …/:iid/respond`; the cards **list through the existing** `GET …/interactions`), boot-policy allow rules + coverage-manifest entries, and the Brief-workroom **Requests** panel render the proposed titles with **Accept N tasks** / **Reject** controls. **Accept** is now **crash-safe and resumable** via a durable **decomposition claim/ledger** (relix-execution-and-issue-design §1.7 — see the dedicated *Exactly-once plan decomposition* bullet below): the claim row (not the card flip) is the linearization point, so a duplicate accept **no-ops** (returning the same ordered ids), a crashed accept **resumes from a durable cursor** (never re-creating an already-made child), and a re-accept whose proposal hashes differently is **refused** (the accepted plan cannot fork). It materializes each child as a real Sub-brief via the existing `create_brief` + `link_subbrief` (tenant-stamped, owner-attributed); the card flips `open → resolved` only once the whole plan has materialized. Each child now **inherits the parent's SAFE spine context** so the children stay company-consistent: the parent's `mandate_id` / `campaign_id` (passed at create) and its `reviewer_agent_id` (set best-effort after create); the **parent's assignee is never inherited** — but a child may now carry an **optional governed assignee hint** (Operative id or role) that is validated through the existing assign-Key gate and assigned on accept (see *governed assignee hints* below). Where a child carries an `after` dependency it is wired as a **Snag (`blocked_on`) on the referenced earlier sibling** (both already exist — children are created in order; `add_snag` re-checks self/cycle and is idempotent), so the dependent starts blocked until its prerequisite reaches `done` (the LOCKED §1.6 rule). It records the created ids on the card's `response` and Chronicles `brief.suggestion_opened` / `…_materialized` (now naming the inherited context + dependency-edge count, with child ids) / `…_rejected`. **Reject** closes the card and creates nothing. Tenant-scoped via the owning Brief (`deny_cross_tenant`; a cross-Guild Brief/card id reads as not-found). The generic `brief.interaction_respond` path refuses a `suggest_tasks` card so it can't be resolved without creating its children. The Requests-panel cards render the proposed children as an ordered list and surface each `after` dependency inline (`↳ after #N: <title>`) so the operator sees the order before accepting; the inherited Mandate/Campaign/reviewer show up on each child's own Brief detail once created. **Governed assignee hints (§1.9).** Each proposed child may carry an **optional, explicit** assignee hint — an Operative id (model A, precise) **or** a role (model B, friendly; resolved to the *oldest active same-Guild* Operative via `list_by_role_for_tenant`), never both. The hint is **never silently inherited** (absent ⇒ the child opens unassigned). On accept the wire handler (`handle_brief_suggest_respond`, now given the `AgentStore`) reads the proposal via the new read-only `TaskStore::suggestion_proposal` and resolves + governance-validates each hint through `agent::handlers::resolve_assignee_hint` **before** the (claiming) accept: same-Guild + active (an explicit check that holds **even for the Founder/operator**, whose assign-Key check is bypassed) then `enforce_assign_key` (the same gate as `brief.set` assignee). Any unhonourable hint (unknown / cross-Guild / inactive / no active role match / unauthorized) refuses the **whole** accept with **no partial creation** — the card stays `open`. `respond_suggestion` takes the pre-validated `&[Option<String>]` and passes each to `create_brief`, so an assigned child is created already-assigned (its own `brief.assigned` Chronicle event); the `…_materialized` event now also names the **assigned vs needs-assignment** split. **Assignment follow-through (workroom):** because a materialized child **without an assignee hint** opens unassigned (and would otherwise be silently inert), the resolved card now renders each created child — read from the card's `response` (the comma-joined ids, in proposal order, zipped with the proposal titles) — as a deep-link to its board card (`/briefs?brief=<id>`, where the existing per-card assign control lives, gated by the Assign-Key) with either an **“assigned: <who>”** badge (a hinted child that passed the gate) or a **“needs assignment”** marker, and the accept banner names how many were assigned vs still need staffing. A proposed hint also shows as a chip on the **open** card (so the operator sees who each child would be assigned to before accepting). No assignee is invented or inherited; assignment flows only through the existing governance gate, and any unassigned children surface in the Action Center as `blocked` “Assign an Operative” items (they open in `todo`, so `list_unassigned_briefs_for_tenant` includes them). Tested at the runtime (accept materializes + links + chronicles, **children inherit Mandate/Campaign/reviewer but NOT assignee**, **a valid `after` materializes a Snag edge that blocks the dependent until the prerequisite is `done`**, **an invalid `after` is refused at open with no card/children created**, reject creates none, duplicate accept **no-ops** with no duplicate Briefs, generic-respond refusal, cross-tenant denial) + `brief::normalize_proposal` unit tests (incl. backward-only `after`, forward/self/out-of-range rejection, remap across dropped children) + a bridge mini-mesh round-trip (open→list→accept with JSON/pipe wire-arg assertions incl. the `after` pass-through + duplicate→400). **Governed assignee-hint tests:** resolver (`resolve_assignee_hint`) — id/role happy paths, unknown/cross-Guild/inactive/no-role-match denied, both-set + over-long rejected, non-operator-without-profile denied; store — pre-validated assignees applied with the assigned/needs split chronicled, absent ⇒ unassigned; wire handler — a role hint assigns the child end-to-end and an unhonourable hint refuses the accept with **no partial creation** (card stays open); `normalize_proposal` — hints trimmed/carried, id-OR-role-not-both + over-cap rejected. **Caveat:** the assignee hint resolves at accept (an id/role can name an Operative hired after the card opened), so a hint that was valid at open can still refuse the accept if the Operative is gone/inactive by then; `after` is a single backward index per child (no multi-dependency lists or forward/cross-proposal edges). **Still deferred:** the "wake the assignee when answered" continuation policy, and live streaming of cards into the thread (the panel refreshes on open/answer + the run-event SSE, not a realtime interaction stream). **(Now shipped — see the *Approval-bound plan confirm* bullet below):** the plan-approval *binding* of a `confirm` to an exact Dossier revision and the supersede-on-comment expiry of a pending plan confirm.
- **Exactly-once plan decomposition (§1.7 — BACKEND SHIPPED, partial).** The `suggest_tasks` accept path is now backed by a durable **decomposition claim/ledger** so an accepted child-Brief plan is **resumable and never duplicates children**, even if materialization crashes mid-way. A new `brief_decomposition_claims` table is keyed by `(task_id, interaction_id)` = (source Brief, accepted-plan identity); for this first slice the accepted-plan identity is the `suggest_tasks` interaction id (no full Dossier revision yet). The row carries: a **fingerprint** — `brief::proposal_fingerprint`, a BLAKE3 (`hex(blake3(…))`, the repo's local hash convention from `db.rs`) over the **normalized** proposal's materialization-affecting fields only (child count + per-child title / priority / `after` / assignee-id / assignee-role), so cosmetic JSON differences and a re-worded `summary` do **not** matter; a **`created_ids`** cursor — the ordered, comma-joined child ids created **so far** (its length is the resume position), bounded (≤ `MAX_SUGGESTED_CHILDREN`) and carrying **no raw prompt text**; `plan_len`; an `owner` (the accepter — used for audit **and** the owner-takeover guard below); and `status` (`in_progress` → `complete`). **Crash-safe materialization** (`respond_suggestion_impl`): the card stays `open` while materializing (so the wire handler can re-resolve assignee hints on a resume); the claim is established with an atomic `INSERT OR IGNORE` (the linearization point); a re-accept with a **different** fingerprint is a typed `Invalid` refusal (no fork), the **same** fingerprint with a `complete` claim **no-ops** (returns the recorded ids, no new children/events), and an `in_progress` claim **resumes from the cursor** (subject to the owner-takeover guard below). Children are created **in deterministic order, one id persisted to the cursor (via a compare-and-swap) before the next is created**, so a retry continues from exactly where it stopped. The **whole** accept materialization (claim establish → create-and-record loop → finalize) runs under a per-decomposition in-process **materialization lock** (`TaskStore::decomposition_lock`, one `Mutex<()>` per `(task_id, interaction_id)`, mirroring the per-Operative start lock), so two concurrent accepts/resumes of the same card cannot interleave a child `create_brief` with its cursor record — the loser blocks, then re-reads the claim and either no-ops (`complete`) or resumes (`in_progress`). Linking + reviewer inheritance + `after`→Snag wiring are done **after** the cursor record and are **idempotent**, so a resume heals any gap a crash left and a re-run never duplicates an edge. On completion the claim is marked `complete`, the card flips to `resolved` with the **full ordered child-id list as its `response` exactly once**, and the Chronicle is honest: a genuine resume emits one `brief.suggestion_resumed` followed by the single `brief.suggestion_materialized` (a no-op duplicate emits neither). All prior governance is preserved unchanged — parent Mandate/Campaign/reviewer inherited (assignee never), assignee hints resolved + assign-Key gated **before any child is created** (an invalid hint refuses the whole accept and **creates no claim**), `after`→`blocked_on` Snags, delegation-depth pre-check, and tenant/Guild isolation. A test-only `respond_suggestion_failing_after` hook (no product-API change) injects a mid-materialization crash to prove resume. Tested: full accept records a `complete` claim with the ordered cursor + one materialized event; duplicate accept no-ops; a partial crash resumes creating only the missing children (reusing the pre-crash ids) with one resume + one materialized event; `after` edges wire correctly across a resume; a changed-fingerprint re-accept refuses without forking; an invalid assignee hint creates no claim and no child; a cross-tenant accept creates neither claim nor child; **two threads racing the same accept behind a barrier create exactly the planned children with no extra unlinked orphan row and converge on one ordered id list** (`decomposition_concurrent_accepts_never_orphan_a_child`); **the same owner resumes its own in_progress claim while still fresh**, **a different responder is refused on a fresh in_progress claim**, **a different responder takes over a stale claim** (reassigning ownership + one `brief.suggestion_taken_over` event, resuming from the cursor with no duplicate children), **a fingerprint mismatch still refuses even after the claim goes stale** (the fork check runs before the takeover logic, so no takeover happens), and **a `complete` claim no-ops for any responder without reassigning ownership**; plus `brief::proposal_fingerprint` unit tests (summary-insensitive, child/priority/after/hint-sensitive, length-stable). **Owner-takeover invariant (now ENFORCED — §1.7).** The `suggest_tasks` accept is an **operator-driven, synchronous** materialization, so the claim's `owner` is the **accepter** (an operator/Founder subject), **not** a long-lived run with a heartbeat/lease — there is no real run-liveness pointer to probe (unlike the two-pointer Brief Claim). The true exactly-once safety remains the in-process materialization lock + durable cursor + fingerprint; on top of that the resume path now enforces a **conservative owner guard with stale-age takeover** (`DECOMPOSITION_OWNER_STALE_SECS`, 15 min): the **same** owner may always resume its own `in_progress` claim; a **different** responder is **refused** while the claim is still **fresh** (touched within the threshold — the owner may be mid-plan or about to retry) and may **take over** only once the claim is **stale** (untouched past the threshold ⇒ the owning process crashed and never resumed) or **terminal** (a `complete` claim no-ops for anyone). A takeover reassigns `owner` and Chronicles `brief.suggestion_taken_over`. The order is **fingerprint-check → complete-no-op → owner-guard/takeover**, so a forked proposal refuses regardless of owner or staleness, and a duplicate accept still no-ops for any responder.
