The threshold is testable without sleeping (a `backdate_claim` direct-DB seed ages `updated_at`). **Honest limits / still a gap:** the accepted-plan identity is the interaction id, **not** an approval-bound Dossier revision — full Dossier document authoring + approval-bound document revisions remain a **separate, unbuilt gap** (this slice does not introduce them); the owner-takeover rule is a **stale-age** policy on `updated_at`, not a real liveness probe — there is no heartbeat for these synchronous operator interactions, so a crashed owner's claim is held for up to `DECOMPOSITION_OWNER_STALE_SECS` before another operator may take it over (correctness never depends on this — the lock + cursor + fingerprint already guarantee exactly-once; the guard only stops a *second* operator from racing in on a decomposition another operator is actively driving). **The prior CAS-loser orphan caveat is now closed:** a true concurrent double-accept no longer leaves any unlinked orphan child Brief — the per-decomposition materialization lock (above) serializes the create-and-record loop so the loser of the race never creates a child for a slot it then loses. The durable claim remains the crash-safe linearization point; the lock only removes the in-process interleave window (and the single-connection store has exactly one writer, so this fully closes it — the in-loop stale-cursor re-adopt is now defensive belt-and-suspenders).
- **Board-card blocker affordance (dashboard-design §6).** The board route (`GET /v1/spine/board/:column` → `brief.board` → `list_briefs_by_board_for_tenant`) now enriches each `BriefCard` with a `blocked_by` field: the Brief's **unresolved** Snags (blockers whose own `board_status != 'done'`), surfaced as the blocker's `human_ref` where set else its id. One batched read over the page's ids; the blocker side is filtered to the **same Guild**, so a cross-tenant blocker is neither shown nor counted (no existence leak), and a resolved blocker drops off. The field is `#[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]` and is populated **only** by the board query (every other `BriefCard` list leaves it empty → omitted from the wire), so the addition is wire-additive for all other card surfaces. The dashboard Brief board renders a compact `⛔ Blocked by <ref>` chip (single blocker) or `⛔ Blocked by N Briefs` (count, full list in the title) on blocked cards only — clear cards stay uncluttered. Tested at the runtime (a card carries only its open same-Guild blocker by ref; resolved + cross-Guild blockers excluded; non-blocked card empty). The detail's own `blocked` flag + Relations counts are unchanged.
- **Approval-bound plan confirm (§1.8 — BACKEND + DASHBOARD SHIPPED, first slice).** A `confirm` interaction card can now be **bound to an exact `plan` Dossier revision**, so a plan approval can only resolve against the plan it was opened for. Each existing Dossier row is treated as an **immutable revision** (Dossiers are append-only — the latest `plan` Dossier id IS the current plan revision; `latest_dossier_id_conn` reads it: newest `created_at`, `rowid` tiebreak). Two additive nullable columns on `brief_interactions` — `bound_doc_id` (the bound revision = a Dossier id) + `bound_doc_kind` (e.g. `plan`) — carry the binding (surfaced on the `Interaction` wire type, omitted when unbound). A new governed capability **`brief.plan_confirm_open`** (`task_id|author|prompt`, prompt optional; boot-policy `spine_brief_plan_confirm_open` allow rule + coverage-manifest entry; tenant-scoped via the owning Brief, `deny_cross_tenant`) opens a `confirm` bound to the Brief's **current latest `plan` Dossier** — it **refuses clearly when no `plan` Dossier exists** (you can't bind an approval to a plan that isn't written), and Chronicles the bound doc id (`brief.plan_confirm_opened`) so the approval thread is auditable. **Staleness on accept (`respond_interaction`):** an *accept* (`resolved`) of a plan-bound confirm re-reads the latest `plan` revision under the same lock; if it no longer equals `bound_doc_id` (a newer `plan` Dossier was attached), the accept is **refused as stale**, the card flips `open → expired`, and a `brief.interaction_expired` event is recorded — it **never resolves as approved** against a superseded plan, and no `brief.interaction_resolved` is written. (A *reject* of a stale card stays on the normal path — only the approval is guarded.) **Supersede-on-comment (`comment_on_brief`):** posting a comment on a Brief expires any **open plan-bound confirm** on it (`kind = confirm` AND `bound_doc_kind = 'plan'` → `expired`, with a `brief.interaction_expired` note per card) — the operator answered by commenting instead of clicking, so the pending plan approval must not later resolve as approved; **only** plan-bound confirms are touched (plain `ask`/`confirm`/`suggest_tasks` cards are untouched). **Duplicate-answer behavior is unchanged** (typed/idempotent: a second response to a `resolved`/`rejected`/`expired` card is a typed `Invalid` refusal). **Plain confirms are fully unaffected** — no binding ⇒ no staleness check, no supersede. **Tenant isolation:** a cross-Guild Brief/card reads as not-found (no existence leak), same convention as plain interactions; the bind/read/accept all scope to the owning Brief's Guild. Tested at the runtime: open refuses without a plan Dossier (and a non-`plan` Dossier doesn't satisfy it); open binds the **latest** plan revision + records it in metadata + Chronicles the bound id; accept succeeds when the plan is unchanged (and a duplicate accept is a typed refusal); a newer plan revision makes the old confirm stale → accept refuses + expires + records no approval; commenting supersedes/expires an open plan confirm and a later accept refuses typed; a plain confirm is unaffected by plan churn + comments and still accepts; cross-tenant open/accept are denied with no leak. **Dashboard/bridge wiring (now shipped):** a dedicated authenticated bridge route **`POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/plan-confirm`** (`spine::open_plan_confirm`, registered in `main.rs` beside the `…/interactions` routes) proxies `brief.plan_confirm_open` — payload `{author?, prompt?}`, the author defaulting to the local bridge identity (`operator`) when absent (mirroring `comment_brief`), returning `{interaction_id}` and mapping the typed coordinator refusals consistently (no-plan-Dossier → 400, cross-tenant → not-found). No new boot-policy rule is needed — the mesh capability + its `spine_brief_plan_confirm_open` allow rule + coverage-manifest entry already shipped in the backend slice; the REST route rides the existing bridge bearer. The **Brief workroom** (`apps/dashboard/src/components/BriefDetail.tsx`) now renders a workroom-native **Plan approval** control (next to Requests): a **Request approval** button that opens the bound confirm against the Brief's latest `plan` Dossier and reloads the thread — disabled when the detail shows no `plan` Dossier locally or when a plan-bound confirm is already open (else the route refuses and the banner surfaces it honestly). The new terminal **`expired`** status now renders **distinctly from `rejected`** (a neutral `todo` tone + a "superseded before approval" tooltip, not the red of a decline), and a plan-bound confirm carries a small **"bound to plan"** cue (with the bound Dossier id in its title) on both the open and closed cards; the `Interaction` wire type now surfaces `bound_doc_id`/`bound_doc_kind`. The bridge round-trip is tested (`brief_plan_confirm_route_opens_and_refuses_without_plan`: explicit-author wire arg `task_id|author|prompt`, absent-author → `operator`, no-plan-Dossier → typed 400 with the reason preserved). **Honest limits / still a gap:** the bound revision is the Dossier *id* (Dossiers are already immutable rows — there is no separate per-doc optimistic-concurrency revision id or document **locking/forking** yet, §1.8); this is **not** wired into the autonomous planner flow (no agent auto-opens the plan confirm or fires decomposition on accept — the exactly-once decomposition above is still keyed on the `suggest_tasks` interaction id, **not** this bound plan revision); and there is still **no full document authoring/editing UI** (the control approves an existing `plan` Dossier; it does not write or revise one). The existing `brief.comment` path also still drives supersede from the dashboard.
- **Plan package — bound-plan approval now triggers decomposition (§1.7/§1.8/§3.1 — BACKEND + BRIDGE SHIPPED, dashboard safe-response path).** This closes the last seam between the two bullets above: a *plan package* binds an approval-bound `confirm` to **both** an exact `plan` Dossier revision **and** the exact `suggest_tasks` proposal it gates, so **accepting the confirm materializes that proposal through the resumable, exactly-once decomposition ledger** — bound-plan approval *is* the decomposition trigger. One new additive nullable column on `brief_interactions` — `bound_interaction_id` (the linked `suggest_tasks` id; surfaced on the `Interaction` wire type, omitted when unset) — carries the proposal link beside the existing `bound_doc_id`/`bound_doc_kind`. A new governed capability **`brief.plan_package_open`** (`TaskStore::open_plan_package`) creates all three artifacts **atomically under one connection lock** so a partial package can never leak: (1) an **immutable `plan` Dossier revision** (`plan_title` defaults to "Plan"; `plan_body` is **required** — a plan package without a plan body refuses); (2) the **`suggest_tasks` proposal**, validated + size-capped by the same `brief::normalize_proposal` governance as a standalone `brief.suggest_open` (a bad proposal refuses **before any row is written** — no orphan plan Dossier); (3) the approval-bound `confirm` linked to both. It Chronicles `brief.dossier_added` (plan) + `brief.suggestion_opened` + `brief.plan_package_opened` and returns `{plan_doc_id, suggestion_id, confirm_id}`. A second governed capability **`brief.plan_confirm_respond`** (`task_id|confirm_id|responder|verdict`, `TaskStore::respond_plan_confirm`) answers the package confirm: on **accept** it (a) re-checks the bound `plan` Dossier is still the **latest** revision — a newer plan, or a comment that already expired the card, refuses **without materializing** (the same stale guard as the plan-confirm above), (b) **materializes the linked proposal exactly once through `respond_suggestion`** — the existing crash-safe `brief_decomposition_claims` ledger (fingerprint + `created_ids` cursor + owner-takeover) — using assignee hints the wire handler pre-validates through the **assign-Key gate before any child is created** (an invalid hint refuses the whole accept with no partial creation, card stays `open`), and (c) only on success flips the confirm `open → resolved` and Chronicles `brief.plan_confirm_approved`. A **duplicate accept is idempotent** (the ledger no-ops, the SAME child ids return as `already_approved`). On **reject** the confirm flips `open → rejected` and the still-open linked proposal is closed (`rejected`); if the proposal had already materialized it is left intact and the outcome says so honestly (`rejected_proposal_already_closed`). The typed result `{outcome, suggestion_id, created:[ids]}` carries *what actually happened* so a caller never infers approval from a bare 200. A **plain/standalone** confirm (no `bound_interaction_id`) is **refused here** — it is still answered through `brief.interaction_respond`, which itself still refuses a `suggest_tasks` card; the two paths don't overlap. Tenant-scoped via the owning Brief (`deny_cross_tenant`) and the materialization is itself tenant-stamped through `respond_suggestion`. **Bridge routes (shipped):** `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/plan-package` (`spine::open_plan_package`, JSON `{author, plan_title?, plan_body, summary?, children:[…], prompt?}` → `{plan_doc_id, suggestion_id, confirm_id}`) and `POST /v1/spine/briefs/:id/plan-confirms/:cid/respond` (`spine::respond_plan_confirm`, `{responder, accept}` → the typed outcome), registered in `main.rs` beside the suggestion routes, mapping typed coordinator refusals consistently and riding the existing bridge bearer. Boot-policy `spine_brief_plan_package_open` + `spine_brief_plan_confirm_respond` allow rules (both mesh-up scripts) + coverage-manifest entries shipped (boot-policy coverage guard passes). **Dashboard (safe-response path only):** the workroom now routes any **plan-package confirm** (a `confirm` carrying `bound_interaction_id`) through the new `briefPlanConfirms.respond` route instead of the generic `brief.interaction_respond`, so clicking **Yes** triggers decomposition **exactly once** (and **No** closes both); the accept banner names the materialized Sub-brief count and is honest about an idempotent re-approve. **Dashboard plan-package composer (now shipped):** the workroom (`apps/dashboard/src/components/BriefDetail.tsx`) now carries a **minimal manual composer** beside the Plan-approval control — a plan title (optional, defaults to "Plan"), a required plan body, an optional approval prompt, and a small child-task list (title per child, optional `low|normal|high|urgent` priority, and an optional `after` dependency offered **only** for an earlier titled sibling so a self/forward/cyclic edge can't be expressed). It validates locally (non-empty plan body, ≥1 child with a title) then calls the existing `briefPlanConfirms.open` (`POST …/plan-package`); on success it reloads the Brief/thread and names the created bound confirm in an honest banner, so the plan-bound confirm card appears in Requests and is approved through the already-safe response path. It is a **manual composer, not a full document editor or LLM planner** — no markdown preview, no revision-locking/forking, no autonomous authoring. There is still **no autonomous LLM planner** (no agent auto-authors the plan or auto-fires this), and still **no per-doc document locking / forking / revision-id** beyond the immutable Dossier row (§1.8). Tested at the runtime: open creates the plan Dossier + linked suggestion + bound confirm and Chronicles the package open; accept re-checks latest-plan then materializes + resolves **both** the confirm and the proposal; accept twice is idempotent (same ids, no second event/child); a stale plan expires the confirm and does **not** materialize; reject after the proposal already materialized reports honestly; an invalid assignee hint refuses with no partial child; the handler refuses an unlinked confirm; cross-tenant open/respond denied with no leak; `after` dependencies wire across the materialization.
- **Issue documents as approval-bound Dossiers remain the open §1.7 gap.** **Exactly-once plan decomposition** is now **backend-shipped (partial)** — see the *Exactly-once plan decomposition* bullet above (the durable `brief_decomposition_claims` ledger: proposal fingerprint, `created_ids` resume cursor, crash-safe resume / no-op duplicate accept / no-fork refusal) — but it is keyed on the `suggest_tasks` interaction id, **not** an approval-bound Dossier revision. **Binding a plan *approval* to an exact Dossier revision is now backend-shipped (first slice)** — see the *Approval-bound plan confirm (§1.8)* bullet above (`brief.plan_confirm_open` binds a `confirm` to the latest `plan` Dossier id; a stale accept after a newer plan revision or a superseding comment expires the card and never resolves as approved). **Tying that bound-plan approval into the decomposition trigger is now backend + bridge shipped** — see the *Plan package* bullet above (`brief.plan_package_open` links the bound confirm to the exact proposal; `brief.plan_confirm_respond` accept materializes it through the resumable ledger exactly once). **Still unbuilt:** full issue-document authoring / per-doc revision-locking / forking (§1.8) and an autonomous LLM planner. The dashboard now has a **minimal manual plan-package composer** (plan title/body + approval prompt + a child-task list) wired to `briefPlanConfirms.open` — see the *Plan package* bullet above — but that is a manual composer, **not** a full document editor or LLM planner. **Child/blocker auto-wake promotion** is now **shipped** too — see the *Supervisory auto-wake at the transition seam* note in the `coordinator/mod.rs` row above (`promote_blockers_resolved` / `promote_children_completed` at the `set_board_status` choke point, routed through the persistent wakeup queue). The issue-tree **cost rollup + billing-code attribution** backend foundation (company-model §6.6) is now **shipped** — see the *Cost rollup / billing attribution* capability above (`brief.cost_rollup`, `tasks.billing_code` + run-start stamping); the **delegation-depth counter + guard** backend is also now **shipped** — see the *Delegation-depth counter + guard* capability above (`MAX_SUBBRIEF_DELEGATION_DEPTH`, `link_subbrief` guard, `brief_delegation_depth`); object-level **Mandate/Campaign/Guild billing codes** are now also **shipped** (see the *Cost rollup / billing attribution* capability above — `billing_code` on each object + the tenant-safe `ObjectBillingResolver` fallback); the **frontend** Costs page is now **shipped (partial)** too (see the Lattice + Costs frontend slice below).

### Company Model

- Spawn governance now has two independent gates: the strategy gate (only on `agent.request_hire_for_mandate`) and the spawn Key (on both `agent.request_hire` and `..._for_mandate`). `agent.create` is operator-only. `spawn_route=lead/founder` now mints a **real typed spawn Clearance** linked to activating the pending hire (decided via `coord.approval.decide`); `route=lead` widens the deciders to the actor's Lead. **Remaining escape hatches / gaps:** the operator/admin paths are deliberately ungated (the Founder/Board is sovereign); spawn Clearances auto-expire after 7 days with no re-notification, and there is no batch "approve this whole team" gate yet.
- **Tenant isolation:** the product agent/governance routes (`agent.get/keys/update/delete/reports/peers/by_role/branch/line/manages/assign_check/allowance_committed`, `coord.approval.pending/get/decide`) are now tenant-scoped — a known id from another Guild resolves to not-found. The unscoped store methods remain only as internal/gate helpers (e.g. the admission gate's `get_by_subject`); these are intentional internal paths, not product routes.
- Per-agent Keys: `rig`, `monthly_allowance_cents`, `max_concurrent_runs`, `wake_on_timer`, `wake_on_demand`, and the org/work Keys (`can_spawn_agents`, `spawn_route`, `can_assign_work`, `assign_scope`, `assign_allowed_agents`, `can_manage_work`, `manage_scope`, `manage_allowed_agents`, `can_configure_agents`, `configure_scope`, `configure_allowed_agents`, `secret_allowlist`, `instruction_bundle`) are stored, validated, and editable from the dashboard. **Enforced:**
  - `wake_on_timer`, `max_concurrent_runs`, the Allowance hard-stop (below), `wake_on_timer`/`wake_on_demand` at the `brief.wakeup` chokepoint;
  - the **spawn Key** (agent-originated hires);
  - the **assign Key** at every assignment path — `brief.set` (assignee), `brief.create` (initial assignee), `brief.move` into `in_progress`/`in_review` — with an assignee-validity layer (cross-tenant / unknown / disabled / pending assignees refused);
  - **`can_manage_work` + `manage_scope` + `manage_allowed_agents`** — gates `brief.move` (all moves), `brief.set` (non-assignee fields), `brief.set_due`, `brief.pin`, `brief.snag`/`brief.unsnag` when the Brief is owned by *another* Operative (`enforce_manage_key`; bypassed for an unowned Brief, the Founder/Board, and owner == actor self-progress; tenant-scoped; non-active owner fails closed);
  - **`can_configure_agents` + `configure_scope` + `configure_allowed_agents`** — gates `agent.update` and `agent.delete` (`enforce_configure_key`); **self-configuration is denied** (no privilege self-escalation); `configure_scope = none` denies even with the boolean on; cross-tenant target fails closed;
  - **`secret_allowlist`** — gates `credentials.get` for Operatives (`enforce_secret_allowlist`), layered on the vault's existing owner/tenant gate; exact-id match, empty = deny-by-default, disabled Operative denied, non-Operative callers pass through to the vault gate;
  - **`instruction_bundle`** — composed into the agent prompt as a trusted, operator-authored charter section (`compose_brief_prompt_with_charter`), placed ahead of and separated from the Brief body / comment thread; edits flow through the configure gate (an agent cannot rewrite its own charter).
- **Remaining Key gaps / intentional bypasses:** all the above gates are skipped when no agent store is wired into `coordinator::register` (some embedded/test configs); the Founder/Board (operator/admin) intentionally bypasses every per-agent gate (the sovereign model); `brief.comment` is intentionally **not** manage-gated (communication, not control); the `secret_allowlist` is only consulted on the explicit `credentials.get` read path (no runtime auto-injection path exists today to gate); any future wake trigger must use `brief.wakeup` or it bypasses the on-demand policy.
- Operative Allowance is now **enforced at Brief dispatch** (not just a stored cap): an Operative with `monthly_allowance_cents = 0` is hard-stopped, and a positive cap stops dispatch once its **current UTC calendar-month** recorded AI spend (the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window`, implicit reset at month start) reaches the cap (best-effort — see the Allowance hard-stop and Allowance calendar-month windowing slices for the exact limits). A **Guild-level spend hard-stop** now also gates the autonomous path (see the Guild-level spend hard-stop slice above). The issue-tree **cost rollup + billing-code attribution** backend foundation is now shipped (`brief.cost_rollup` over the durable `brief_runs` ledger; `tasks.billing_code` + run-start stamping; see the *Cost rollup / billing attribution* capability above), and the **delegation-depth counter + guard** is shipped (`link_subbrief` refuses past `MAX_SUBBRIEF_DELEGATION_DEPTH`; see the *Delegation-depth counter + guard* capability above), and object-level (Mandate/Campaign/Guild) **billing codes** are now shipped (see the *Cost rollup / billing attribution* capability above), and the frontend Costs page is now shipped (partial — see the Lattice + Costs frontend slice below). The positive-cap gate is only as accurate as the metrics ledger's per-Operative spend attribution.
- **Action Center (company-model §5.4/§8.2) — `company.actions` / `GET /v1/spine/company/actions`.** A READ-ONLY feed of the operator's next actions computed from existing live state (no notification table). Implemented categories: `approval` (pending Clearances + proposed-strategy Mandates), `hire` (pending Operatives), **`budget`** (committed-vs-Guild-budget + zero-Allowance hard-stop with waiting work **+ live actual spend** — per-Operative and Guild over/near their Allowance/budget when the metrics ledger is wired), `ready_to_start`, `blocked` (missing-assignee + dependency-blocked), `needs_review`, `failed_or_refused` (now a **recovery-decision card** that prefers the durable per-run diagnosis metadata — failure-class / retryable / retry-budget / action / route — and falls back to the refusal-taxonomy map for legacy rows), `stale`. Ordered + deduped by the pure `agent/action_center.rs` (rank: approval<hire<budget<failed_or_refused<needs_review<ready_to_start<blocked<stale). The Overview card refreshes off the existing run-event SSE + a low-frequency poll. **Live spend-vs-Allowance is now wired** (commit `579fa8c5`, Live Spend Telemetry Pack — supersedes the prior "deferred" note here): the read handler threads the **authoritative month-to-date spend the gate itself enforces** — `MetricsQuery::cost_since` over the **current UTC calendar month** (the canonical `heartbeat::allowance_window`), the `over_allowance` source — through the `action_center::SpendSource` seam (`handlers::MetricsSpendSource::current_month`, wired into `company.actions` in `register_agent_capabilities` from the `MetricsBundle.query`), emitting per-Operative **and** Guild over/near-spend cards (over = at/over the cap = the gate's refusal threshold [High], near = ≥80% [Medium]) carrying the real `spent / limit / percent`, kept DISTINCT from the committed-Allowance planning signals (capacity reserved vs money spent — never double-counted); when metrics are disabled the seam is `None` and **no** spend item is fabricated. **Remaining real-spend gaps:** the near band is a fixed 80%; the production `MetricsSpendSource` is now tested against a **real** in-memory `MetricsStore`/`MetricsQuery` — `company_actions_live_spend_from_real_metrics_store` seeds priced rows (keyed by `agent_id`, the gate's attribution contract), proving the handler SUMS the window, EXCLUDES rows outside the current calendar-month window, and renders the real over/near figures; `company_actions_live_spend_real_metrics_is_tenant_isolated` proves a foreign Guild's recorded spend never leaks (isolation via the handler roster, since `cost_since` does not filter by tenant). What remains *not* covered end-to-end is only the cross-process bridge→coordinator HTTP transport carrying that spend (the spend SOURCE itself is no longer a fake), and `cost_since` attribution still depends on production recording `agent_name == agent_id` (the same best-effort assumption the heartbeat Allowance gate relies on). **Now shipped (was "deferred"):** a **per-run diagnosis layer** — durable `failure_class` / `retryable` / `retry_budget_remaining` / `recovery_action` / `recovery_route` on `brief_runs` with a true retryable-vs-not verdict — see the *Brief/Shift recovery diagnosis* pack above; the `failed_or_refused` card now rides it. **Still deferred / not yet built:** Stage-2 autonomous recovery (auto-retry lane + LLM diagnostic pass + one-click Inbox decision card — this is Stage-1 classification only, no autonomous retry, no provider quota polling); finer `blocked` sub-reasons as distinct reasons; a dedicated "mandates-with-proposed-strategy" index; hard-realtime push of every field (the refresh is event-trigger + poll; the feed is capped at 60 with an honest `truncated` flag).
- **First-run on-ramp (company-model §12.6) — `company.starter_crew` / `POST /v1/spine/company/starter-crew`.** Owner-gated, idempotent, tenant-scoped: ensures the Founder + one active **safe-local echo** starter Operative per role (default engineer+designer; canonicalised, de-duped, capped), so an empty company can reach a real Shift through `prime.propose → approve → start` with **no external coding-agent auth**. Starters are plain workers (no spawn/assign Keys), clearly labelled local/demo (never Claude/Codex), created directly only as the Board's sovereign first-run action (§5.4) — the same trust basis as `ensure_founder`. **Loop proven to its terminal:** the in-process loop test (`starter_crew_closes_the_positive_local_loop_through_prime_start`) now closes the full §12.6 path end to end — empty company → starter crew → `prime.propose → approve → start` → echo Shift reaches `done`/`pending_review` → the run is **review-gated** (`run_apply_eligibility` is `Err` while `pending_review`) → operator **accepts** → eligibility flips to `Ok` → **apply** reaches the durable `apply_status = "applied"` (a safe no-op for echo, which writes nothing). The live HTTP smoke (`docs/live-smoke.md`) documents the same `run.diff` (eligible:false) → `review` accept → `run.diff` (eligible:true) → `run.apply` tail over real routes. **Runnable-on-approval (the missing-role hire path):** `agent.approve_hire` (`POST /v1/agents/:id/approve-hire`) now accepts an optional `{rig}` and binds it **atomically at approval** (`AgentStore::approve_hire_with_rig` — tenant-scoped, pending-only, no-clobber, validated against `rig::is_known_rig`/`KNOWN_RIG_NAMES`), so a greenlit Prime hire is *immediately runnable* by the next `prime.start` **without a separate `PATCH /v1/agents/:id {rig}`**. The JSON response carries `{rig, rig_set, runnable, needs_rig}`; omitting `rig` preserves prior behaviour with `needs_rig:true`. The Action Center hire card carries the machine-actionable `action_api` + `suggested_rig:"echo"`. Proven end-to-end over live HTTP: starter crew → propose ("…with test coverage") → approve (files a qa hire) → start (qa skipped) → **one** `approve-hire {rig:"echo"}` (`runnable:true`) → start (qa reconciled + runs on echo, **no PATCH**) → review/apply tracks → move to board `done` → integrate runs + applies → Action Center calm. **Remaining gap:** echo-only (real provider execution still needs an installed + authenticated CLI, chosen explicitly at approval or via `agent.update {rig}` — never silently); the default roster is engineer+designer (other roles still come from real hires/Clearances unless requested).
- The Prime/CEO flow now spans plan → readiness → **orchestration**: `mandate.team_plan` (persisted), `mandate.team_readiness` (live staffing), and `mandate.orchestrate` (turns an approved + ready Mandate into an idempotent, governance-respecting Brief tree, assigning the active team, persisting each run). A bounded **guided driver v1** (`prime.next_step` / `prime.advance`, see the "Prime guided driver v1" capability entry above) now names the ONE next governed step and can advance **one** safe step at a time on explicit operator click (`propose_strategy` / `create_team_plan` / `orchestrate_assign_ready`, stale-safe via re-read → 409, governance + Keys unchanged). **Prime Strategy Drafting v1 (commit pending):** a Mandate with **no strategy yet** is now classified `needs_strategy_proposal` (`advance_action="propose_strategy"`, `can_advance=true`); the guided one-click `prime.advance {action:"propose_strategy"}` and the opt-in autonomous tick both compose a strategy doc (`prime_driver::draft_mandate_strategy` from the Mandate's title/description/status + the Guild's active work roles, pipe-sanitized + length-bounded — or, in the autonomous/manual-tick loop with `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_STRATEGY_DRAFT` on, **model-authored** for the body via Prime Strategy Authoring v1, below) and propose it through the EXISTING `mandate.strategy.propose` handler. This is **draft, not approval**: the doc lands `proposed`, surfaces in the Action Center `approval` category, and the next governed step becomes the human `mandate.strategy.approve` gate; a strategy already `proposed`/`approved`/`rejected` is **never overwritten** (re-advance refuses `stale_action`, so a human rejection is honoured), it is tenant-scoped + bounded (one tick action), and chronicled `prime.autonomous_strategy_proposed` only when it actually proposes (on the Mandate's parent Brief if one exists). No model, no new provider/key. The manual guided surface is no longer the whole story: autonomous Prime v1 now runs the approved-work loop — there is **no blind loop**, approvals + hire/spawn/budget decisions + Start stay human **by default**, and **absent an explicit standing grant** no driver **approves** a strategy or proposal, greenlights its own hires/Clearances, or stands up + orchestrates a whole team end-to-end on its own; the driver only surfaces, **drafts the strategy proposal**, and one-step-advances through the EXISTING governed routes. The bounded standing-authority layer adds — only inside a Board grant — proposal approval, **proposed-strategy approval** (`prime.strategy.approve`, never reviving a rejected strategy), and planning hire/Clearance greenlights; budget gates are never delegated. The Brief **skeleton** is **deterministic/rule-based, not LLM** (a three-tier parent → role track → per-agent subject execution tree; no model-invented decomposition, dependencies, roles, agents, or assignments); the Brief **text** (titles / dossiers / checklists) is deterministic by default and **opt-in model-authored** in the autonomous/manual Prime tick only under `RELIX_PRIME_LLM_ORCHESTRATION` (Prime Orchestration Authoring v1, below) — the model authors text for the already-computed skeleton and can never change a role/agent/id/assignment/gate, and the direct one-click `mandate.orchestrate` stays deterministic. Idempotency uses **stable, subject-aware source markers** (Mandate-id + role + agent-derived), so renaming a Mandate, hand-editing a Brief title, swapping the active agent, or crashing mid-run no longer orphans or duplicates the tree — a changed agent gets its own subject Brief while the role track is reused, and any missing tier is filled on rerun. Missing/pending/blocked roles now get **durable placeholder role tracks** (a role-track Brief titled `… blocked: <reason>` with a `blocker` Dossier, but no subject execution Brief and no assignee); when the role later activates, the same role track is reused and gains its subject Brief. Work is still **refused per-role** until that role is active — placeholders are never assigned. Every materialised Brief (parent, role track, subject execution) is now **stamped with the Founder/Board reviewer up front** (same `find_founder` resolution as `prime.approve`), so a Mandate-orchestrated echo Shift lands in `in_review` instead of parking in `blocked`, and the operator's `run.review → run.apply` is the review-to-done that advances the Brief to `done` (pinned by `orchestrate_stamps_founder_reviewer_so_shift_is_review_to_apply_able`; the no-Founder honest fallback by `orchestrate_without_founder_leaves_reviewer_unset`). The full higher-level path — Founder creates a Mandate → governed strategy gate (orchestrate **refused** before approval) → `team_plan` staffs via the governed hire + echo-Rig affordance → `orchestrate` assigns the linked Brief tree → one subject Shift runs through echo → review → apply to board `done` — is now **proven over live HTTP** (`docs/live-smoke.md`, "Variant: the Mandate → Strategy gate → Orchestrate path").

### Adapters And Hermes

- Tether / plugin-hook system is unbuilt. The existing plugin host is an out-of-process capability-provider system, not the in-process lifecycle-hook bridge described in `relix-hermes-integration.md`.
- Hermes rich seam is unbuilt. `hermes_rig` is a stdio placeholder and remains `BoxLevel`; real `/v1/runs`, MCP, `relix-bridge`, and PerToolCall governance are future work.
- CLI adapters declare structured-output flags and metadata and DO parse stream-json/JSONL for the run outcome. **Token/cost/session capture now ships (TG6/TG2):** `parse_claude_usage`/`parse_codex_usage` extract per-run usage (tokens, Claude `cost_micros`, model, `session_id`) onto `brief_runs` + the `agent_runtime_state` ledger (accumulated totals + resumable `session_id`), honest-null when the adapter emits nothing. **Codex now replays same-scope sessions** (`codex exec resume [OPTIONS] <session> -`; exact tenant+Operative+Rig+Brief match only). Still missing: Claude session replay (working-dir-keyed and unsafe across fresh scoped workspaces), `$0-but-tracked` subscription cost ledger rows, quota polling/back-off, Codex per-tenant `CODEX_HOME` symlink, and interrupt/stop beyond the existing kill-based cancel.
- Bridge-back exists for the narrow universal floor: comment/Sub-brief/Dossier/Snag/Clearance/claim-holder routes. Thin adapters still have no per-tool-call governance; Clearance is the route for an adapter to ask Relix before crossing a boundary it cannot gate internally.

### Dashboard

- **Standalone Relux local operator login (auth v1) — SHIPPED (closes the "unauthenticated by design" caveat partially).** The standalone `relux-kernel serve` surface previously bound loopback and was **unauthenticated by design** (`docs/RELUX_MASTER_PLAN.md` §22 release caveat); the React shell rendered outside any auth gate. It is now gated by a **single-admin local login** that mirrors the proven legacy bridge design (`crates/relix-web-bridge/src/dashboard_auth.rs`) but is self-contained in the kernel (`crates/relux-kernel/src/auth.rs`): a durable **Argon2id** admin credential at `dev-data/relux/dashboard-admin.json` (next to the DB, gitignored, OS-restricted, never plaintext, never returned) + an **in-memory** session table keyed by a 256-bit random sid. New **public** endpoints `GET /v1/auth/status`, `POST /v1/auth/setup` (first-run only), `POST /v1/auth/login`, `POST /v1/auth/logout`, `GET /v1/auth/me`; a `require_session` middleware (`axum::middleware::from_fn_with_state`, attached via `route_layer`) protects **every** `/v1/relux/*` route except the public `/v1/relux/health`, and the static dashboard stays public so the SPA always renders the setup/login screen (never a blank page). A successful setup/login sets an **HttpOnly** `relux_session` cookie (`SameSite=Lax`, `Path=/`, 12h, **no `Secure`** because the console is loopback `http://` — documented). The dashboard (`apps/dashboard`) already shipped the cookie-based `api.ts` + `AuthProvider`/`Login` for the legacy bridge; this slice **gates the Relux shell on the session** in `App.tsx` and adds a **Sign out** + signed-in-operator control in `ReluxShell.tsx`. Recovery is the local `relux-kernel reset-admin [username] [password]` CLI (filesystem-only, generates+prints a strong password once when omitted, never reads the old secret, no network reset; restart `serve` to drop live sessions). The CLI store path (`prime`/`task`/`tools`/autonomy) is unaffected (direct SQLite, no HTTP). A dev/test-only `RELUX_AUTH_DISABLED` bypass leaves the API open (OFF by default; flagged by `serve` + `doctor`). **Tests:** 10 lib unit tests (Argon2id-not-plaintext, setup-once, verify, sessions, reset, cookie attributes) + 4 bin HTTP tests over the real router via `oneshot` (health public / state 401-without-session / setup→session→logout→relock / wrong-vs-right password / bypass). **Honest remaining caveat:** still a single-operator local console — one admin account, loopback bind, no transport TLS; not a multi-tenant/internet production surface. *(Sessions were in-memory in this v1 slice; they are now restart-persistent — see the **Restart-persistent operator sessions** slice below.)*
- **Sliding/rolling operator sessions (auth v1.1) — SHIPPED.** The fixed 12h cookie lifetime from auth v1 is now an **idle timeout** that rolls forward on activity instead of a hard expiry (`crates/relux-kernel/src/auth.rs`, `server.rs`). The `Session` carries two deadlines: `expires_at` (idle, slid forward) and `absolute_deadline` (set at creation to `created_at + SESSION_ABSOLUTE_MAX_SECS`). `SessionStore::refresh` slides `expires_at` to `now + SESSION_TTL_SECS` **capped at `absolute_deadline`** and returns the cookie `Max-Age`; `validate` is unchanged and **non-mutating** (status polls do not slide). The `require_session` middleware admits via the non-sliding `validate_session`, runs the handler, and **only on a success status** calls `refresh_session` + appends `Set-Cookie` (`set_session_cookie_with_max_age`, same opaque sid — the window slides, the id is not rotated). **Expiry model:** idle timeout = **12h** (`SESSION_TTL_SECS`, the v1 value, preserved); absolute max lifetime = **7 days** (`SESSION_ABSOLUTE_MAX_SECS`) — a continuously active (or stolen) cookie is forced to re-authenticate after a week. **Cookie discipline:** no `Set-Cookie` on the guard's 401 or on a 4xx/5xx handler response; logout (public route, clears the cookie) and change-password (still preserves the caller's own session and invalidates the others) are unaffected — change-password succeeds with a 200, so its response also carries the refreshed cookie. **Tests:** 7 new lib unit tests (slide-forward, absolute cap clamps the slide, idle-expired prune, absolute-expired even with idle time left, validate-does-not-slide, immutable ceiling across repeated refreshes, `set_session_cookie_with_max_age` window + negative clamp) + 2 bin HTTP tests (successful protected request re-emits the cookie with the same sid and full idle `Max-Age`; unauthenticated/bogus session sets no cookie). No dashboard change required — sessions simply last while the console is in use. **Honest caveat (now closed):** this v1.1 slice was still in-memory (a `serve` restart dropped all sessions); both the sliding idle deadline and the absolute cap are **now persisted** across a restart — see the **Restart-persistent operator sessions** slice below.
- **Restart-persistent operator sessions (auth v1.2) — SHIPPED (closes the "sessions are in-memory" caveat from auth v1/v1.1).** The session table in `crates/relux-kernel/src/auth.rs` is no longer purely in-memory: it is mirrored to a durable, gitignored local file so a logged-in operator survives a `serve` restart instead of being forced to re-sign-in. **Storage model:** `SessionStore` is now keyed by `hash_sid(raw id)` (SHA-256, hex) and backed by an optional file path; every mutation (`create`/`refresh`/`remove`/`retain_only`, plus prune-on-`validate`/`meta`) atomically rewrites the file via the shared `atomic_write_restricted` (tmp + rename + `restrict_to_current_user`, the SAME hardening as `dashboard-admin.json`). The file (`dev-data/relux/dashboard-sessions.json` by default — next to the admin credential, under the gitignored `dev-data/` root; `RELUX_SESSION_FILE` overrides via `main.rs::session_path`) is a small versioned envelope of `{ sid_hash, username, expires_at, absolute_deadline }` rows. **Security:** the **raw session id is never written to memory-key or disk — only its SHA-256 hash** (preimage resistance makes a leaked file non-replayable as a cookie; the cookie still carries the raw id and the middleware hashes it to look it up). SHA-256 (not Argon2) is correct here because the sid is a 256-bit CSPRNG token, not a low-entropy password. Expired rows are **pruned on load and on use** (load rewrites the pruned set so the file never accumulates dead rows; persistence itself only ever writes live rows). **Every prior safety property is preserved across a restart:** logout removes the row from disk; a password change still keeps the caller's session and invalidates every *other* one **on disk**; the sliding idle deadline and the immutable absolute ceiling are the persisted values; `RELUX_AUTH_DISABLED` still bypasses entirely (it short-circuits before any session lookup); and `reset_admin_credential` now **clears the session file** (and `run_reset_admin` also clears a `RELUX_SESSION_FILE`-relocated one), so local recovery invalidates old sessions on the next restart. **Wiring:** `DashboardAuth::from_paths(admin_path, session_path)` (new) is used by `serve`; `from_admin_path` keeps deriving the default session path next to the admin file (`session_path_for_admin`); both load still-live sessions at construction. **Tests:** 8 new lib unit tests (survives a simulated restart, expired not reloaded, load prunes an already-expired on-disk row + rewrites, raw sid never on disk / only its hash, logout persists removal, change-password invalidates others durably, refresh persists the slid deadline, reset-admin clears the file, default-path-next-to-admin) + 1 bin HTTP test (login → rebuild the server `AppState` from the same files → same cookie still authenticates → logout persists removal across the rebuild). `cargo test -p relux-kernel` green (lib + bin); `cargo clippy -p relux-kernel --all-targets` clean. **Honest remaining caveat:** a `serve` process *already running* keeps its in-memory copy of sessions until restarted, so an out-of-band `reset-admin` still needs the documented restart to fully take effect; the absolute cap is still wall-clock from mint (now persisted, but still not re-anchored by activity).
- **Canonical surface (Phase 2 Slices 1–3) — React is the ONLY dashboard.** The React SPA in `apps/dashboard` (built to `crates/relix-web-bridge/dashboard-dist`, served at `/dashboard`, assets under `/dashboard/assets/*`) is THE product dashboard, full stop. `dashboard::dashboard_router()` serves the committed React bundle at `/dashboard`. **Slice 3 retired the legacy single-file `dashboard.html` console entirely** — the file and every code path that served it (`page()`, the embedded HTML, `RELIX_DASHBOARD_PATH`) are deleted. There is NO HTML fallback that could serve an old-looking app. If the React bundle is missing (a source-only checkout that never ran the frontend build), `/dashboard` returns an **honest HTTP 503 missing-bundle notice** (`missing_bundle_notice`) that tells the operator to run `npm run build` — this is an explicit build/operator error, not a legacy dashboard. **The committed `dashboard-dist` is the canonical dashboard artifact and MUST be rebuilt + committed whenever `apps/dashboard` source changes** (run `npm run build`; output lands in `dashboard-dist`). Two guards enforce this so a stale bundle can never serve old UI: (1) a Rust dist-parity test (`committed_react_dist_present_and_index_references_existing_assets`) fails `cargo test` if `dashboard-dist/index.html` references a missing bundle asset, and `dashboard_router_serves_react_spa_and_assets` proves `/dashboard` + `/dashboard/assets/*` serve the real bundle; (2) a **dist-parity gate** that rebuilds the dashboard and fails if the committed `dashboard-dist` drifts from a fresh build — `scripts/check-dashboard-dist.ps1` (wired into `scripts/ci-local.ps1`) locally, and the `dashboard dist parity` job in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` on every push to `main` + every PR. The gate is non-destructive locally (it only installs `node_modules` when missing).
- **Spine board RETIRED (Phase 2 Slice 2).** The interim spine board `spine_dashboard.html` and its `legacy_page()` handler + the `RELIX_ENABLE_LEGACY_SPINE` flag are **deleted** — there is no code path that serves the old board. `GET /spine` is now a **permanent (308) redirect to `/dashboard`** (public allowlisted so old bookmarks/docs resolve cleanly). The `/v1/spine/*` JSON routes are unchanged and remain the supported product-spine API. Old-board → React parity: Briefs board + **Brief detail/Chronicle/comment** (`BriefDetail`, `/v1/spine/briefs/:id/thread`), Crew + **Operative Keys + Guild Allowance** (`/v1/spine/keys/:agent`, `/v1/spine/allowance/committed`), **Mandates + Clearances** (Mandates page), Command Center **inbox** (blocked/overdue/unassigned), Activity/Chronicle tail, and the **Runs/Shifts** ledger. Superseded-not-ported: the old board's group-by-priority/assignee toggles and per-Operative Desk drilldown (the Command Center inbox + the Briefs board cover the same needs).
- The dashboard is now the React SPA in `apps/dashboard` (the direction in `relix-dashboard-design.md`). The previous interim single-file HTML shell has been deleted (Slice 3). The **Lattice org chart** (`/lattice`) now ships the product-grade pan/zoom/pinch surface from dashboard-design §9, and the **Costs surface** (`/costs`) is shipped over the real Guild spend + Brief cost-rollup routes (with the per-agent observed-spend nuance documented below). Remaining React work is product depth + polish (componentized router, query cache, fuller route-level detail, richer recovery/approval flows), not another HTML surface. **Surgical realtime invalidation has a first real slice** — the dependency-free client invalidation bus (`invalidate.ts`, §11 seed; see the Dashboard Invalidation Bus pack) — though the full §11 engine (own WebSocket, hierarchical query-key factory, route-aware cache hydration, rate-limited toasts) is still future.
- The page now follows the work-object IA, but it lacks a componentized router, query cache, and tenant-prefix navigation; surgical invalidation now exists in seed form (the §11 client invalidation bus) but not yet the full query-key factory.
- The Desk/Inbox and the Brief live work thread now exist (sectioned needs-attention Desk, claim holder, Chronicle timeline, Operative Desk), but only as request/response reads in the interim shell — there is no websocket-driven realtime, transcript/interaction streaming, or push invalidation; the thread refreshes on open/comment.
- The per-Operative Keys panel exists (enforced spawn/assign Keys + stored-only manage/configure/secrets/charter). Pending Clearances render on the Desk **with inline Approve/Reject** (`POST /v1/spine/clearances/:id/decide`, forwarded as the bridge identity; the runtime cap enforces authorisation). The Mandate panel has a **"Plan team"** action, renders the **persisted latest plan + live team readiness** (`mandate.team_plan.latest` + `mandate.team_readiness`), and gains an **Orchestrate** action (Plan / Create briefs / Create + assign) that renders the latest persisted orchestration run — broken out by tier (parent, role tracks created/reused, placeholder/blocked tracks created/reused with reasons, subject-execution Briefs created/reused, assigned, skipped/blockers, next actions; tiers are derived from each Brief's source marker + `placeholder` flag) — and refreshes the board after a run.
- The **Action Center** (company-model §8.2) now lands on the Overview Command Center: a real next-actions card sourced from `GET /v1/spine/company/actions`, with severity-toned category chips, plain-language reasons, and a button to each item's existing action route (approve hire/Clearance → Agents/Mandates, review/apply → Runs, start/assign/unblock → Briefs, budget → Agents); a calm empty state when nothing needs the operator. It now **refreshes** off the existing run-event SSE (debounced change-trigger) with a low-frequency poll fallback — low-latency, not hard-realtime websocket push of every field.
- The Brief workroom now renders **answerable interaction cards** (§1.9 `ask`/`confirm`/`suggest_tasks`) in a **Requests** panel above the Conversation — `ask`/`confirm` cards get inline Yes/No · choice · free-text controls; `suggest_tasks` cards list the proposed child titles as an ordered list — surfacing any `after` dependency inline (`↳ after #N: <title>`) and any **proposed assignee/role hint** as a chip — with **Accept N tasks** / **Reject** controls (accept materializes them as real Sub-briefs server-side, inheriting the parent's Mandate/Campaign/reviewer, wiring the dependency Snags, and assigning each hinted child through the assign-Key gate). After accept the resolved card shows each child's state — **assigned: <who>** or **needs assignment**. Answering writes a Chronicle event and flips the card. **Live work in the workroom (dashboard-design §7/§8) — SHIPPED (partial):** the Brief detail now embeds the **run transcript renderer** (`RunTranscript`) as a *Live work* block in the Latest-Shift section, so the active/latest Shift's transcript (block-grouped, live-tailed) is visible *inside* the Brief, not only on the Runs page. Interaction cards now refresh on a **dedicated interaction-card SSE** (dashboard-design §7/§11): `GET /v1/spine/briefs/:id/interactions/stream` (bridge `interactions_stream`) tenant-scopes exactly like the list route by proxying the same `brief.interactions` capability, emits an initial snapshot, then pushes `event: interactions` (the same JSON array as the list route) **only when the card list's fingerprint changes** (pure, unit-tested `interactions_fingerprint`; terminal `event: not_found` on an unknown/cross-Guild Brief, transient `event: error` keeps trying, keep-alive `ping`). BriefDetail subscribes via `subscribeBriefInteractions` and updates the cards **directly** (§11 surgical update, with a subtle "live" cue on the Requests header); the run-event SSE `reload()` still owns the rest of the workroom, and a `txKey` bumps the embedded transcript after a Shift mutation. So a card raised by an agent *without* an accompanying run transition now surfaces within the poll window, not only on the next run event / manual Refresh. **Honest caveat:** the card stream is **polling-backed SSE** (~2.5s, fingerprint-gated) like the Prime status stream — not a true backend event source / full websocket push.
- **Run transcript renderer (dashboard-design §8) — FRONTEND SHIPPED.** `apps/dashboard/src/components/RunTranscript.tsx` is a standalone, reusable renderer over the durable `/v1/runs/:id/events` transcript, used on the Runs page (expanded run) and embedded in the Brief workroom. It folds the flat adapter stream into typed blocks — a **lifecycle rail** (`accepted`/`workspace_prepared`/`process_*`/`artifacts.*`/`apply.*`/terminal, source `relix`; plus codex `thread`/`turn` lifecycle), **assistant/result message** cards (adapter `assistant_message`/`result`), **collapsible grouped tool actions** (`tool_use`/`command`/`file_change`, with the bounded `payload_json`), **permission-denied** + **error/stderr** callouts, and a **usage/cost** chip (`usage` / source `cost`) — with a **nice↔raw** segmented toggle (raw = compact verbatim dump for debugging, never the only UI). It fetches its own events and **live-tails** an in-flight run with an **efficient incremental `?since=` cursor**: while the run is `running` it polls only the new tail on a steady **2.5s** cadence (the lifecycle run-event SSE carries only coarse transitions, NOT per-transcript frames, so it's used as an *immediate nudge*, not the tail source) and **merges** the new events on (deduped by `event_id`) — it never re-reads the whole transcript per tick. It shows an honest **live/reconnecting/polling** chip plus a real **in-flight summary** (event count · current phase · last-event clock, e.g. `12 events · tool call · 3s ago`) — **no fabricated progress bar**. It also shows an **honest stalled / no-activity cue** (parity with the Relux Work Run Detail): a once-a-second wall clock ages the bar between tail polls, and when an in-flight Shift goes quiet (no new transcript event for **≥ 10s**) it shows a **`◌ No activity for Xs`** badge — measured directly off the last event's real wall-clock `run_events.ts` (the legacy `ts` is real time, unlike the Relux **logical** clock, which is aged against a client wall clock instead). The threshold + the `No activity for Xs` copy are a **single shared pure helper** (`noActivityLabel` / `RUN_STALL_SECS` in `apps/dashboard/src/runstall.ts`), re-exported by both `runtranscript.ts` (legacy) and `reluxruntranscript.ts` (Relux) so both surfaces read identically without coupling their (different) event models. The pure merge/cursor/phase + stall helpers live in `apps/dashboard/src/runtranscript.ts` + `runstall.ts` (unit-tested). Color is semantic-only; all data is the real, redacted transcript — no fabricated cards. The Runs page dropped its flat per-event dump + local event state/loader in favour of this component; the shared `RunEvent` type + `runControls.events` helper live in `api.ts`.
- The **Briefs surface now reads as a goal-facing plan** (dashboard-design §6; roadmap DoD): a **Board / Plan** toggle (`?view=plan`) renders the loaded board cards as a numbered workflow checklist with sub-brief nesting, status/priority/assignee/mandate + blocker chips, latest-run state/deep-link, and per-parent progress strips — bounded to the visible window (relation detail fetched for the first 80 cards; the rest flat + labelled), no backend change (see the Briefs Plan view slice above). Still partial: no whole-tree (beyond the loaded board) rollup, no realtime progress push, session-cached relations.
- Missing or partial surfaces: the Lattice org chart now has full drag-pan, cursor-anchored wheel zoom, touch pinch, Fit, Reset, and persisted per-browser viewport preferences; the Costs surface is shipped, with an honest remaining nuance that the per-Operative "observed spend" table remains metrics-window operational telemetry explicitly labelled distinct from the canonical Guild month-to-date ledger; the **run transcript renderer** (nice/raw, live-tailed) is now **shipped** and the Brief workroom **embeds it inline**, and interaction cards now refresh on a **dedicated interaction-card SSE** (`…/interactions/stream`, polling-backed + fingerprint-gated); the **Approvals hub now has its own dedicated live Clearance stream** (`…/clearances/stream`, polling-backed + fingerprint-gated, with a bounded refresh fallback); the Operative workbench now has **charter editing** (Instructions tab), a **read-only Skills tab** (`/v1/skills?agent=…`), and the per-Operative **model lane** (model + reasoning/effort) is both editable and consumed by supported CLI Rigs through `RigRunRequest` (`--model` for Claude/Codex and Codex `model_reasoning_effort`). Still missing/partial: full Approvals with spend enforcement controls (and a live backend source for the direct-hire/budget action feed — still refresh/polling), per-Operative skill-assignment / create-update-deprecate editor (Skills are read-only), and a true backend event source / websocket-driven realtime (today's streams are polling-backed SSE).

## Remaining External-Infra Work

- Smarter companion: the rule parser is now a **company-aware action spine** — it reads live company state (`company.actions` / `brief.blocked_list` / `brief.runs` / `agent.operatives`) and opens **governed plan packages** (`brief.plan_package_open`), all through the same mesh capabilities + approvals the dashboard uses (see the `companion.rs` row above). An **opt-in `mode:"ai"`** now adds model-assisted **action *selection*** (commit `ee09e05e`): the model may pick ONE action from a fixed allowlist, the bridge **validates** that choice into the existing `CompanionAction` enum and runs it through the **same governed handler** as the deterministic path (falling back to the rule parser on unavailable/invalid/disallowed, with an honest `ai_mode`). It is **AI-assisted, one-turn / one-action — NOT autonomous**: the model never calls a tool, never has freeform text executed, and never bypasses an approval (the plan-package confirm is still operator-approved). The remaining future work is a fuller planner that drives the SAME governed spine APIs (no new write path needed).
- Sandboxed Cell: container/VM isolation before exposing powerful Macro/Rig execution broadly.
- Persistent Keeper and Bench backends behind the in-memory ledgers.
